- The `spring.profiles.include` 'per-property-source, not list-merged' rule is a PROPERTY-STACK semantic (includes are processed per source, NOT subject to relaxed-binding collection-merge/last-wins) — it cannot be expressed by a pure `resolve_active` over an already-flattened `Vec<Name>`. Either the harvested `ProfileLevers` must carry per-source structure (leaking transport into the profile algebra) or the rule lives upstream in `property-sources`/`config-data`. Spring's flat mutable property model blends these concerns; Rust's cleaner layering forces an explicit boundary decision about who owns this rule.
- 'A profile-excluded bean's definition never even exists' (invisible to autowiring/post-processors, not merely lazy) depends entirely on the conditions SPI's graceful-no-bean semantics. Rust's bias toward `Result`/early-failure tempts collapsing 'profile not active' (silent no-bean now) and 'something needed that bean' (loud failure later) into one eager error. These are DISTINCT, time-separated outcomes Spring keeps separate; profiles must preserve that separation via condition-report (drop silently, fail loudly only if later needed), inheriting the conditions clash.
- Profile activation as a Cargo FEATURE would be the wrong reflex (features only OR-on, can't be un-set, and a sibling can flip one on via unification) — profile activation is intrinsically a RUNTIME, ops-replaceable, mutually-exclusive-capable choice (dev XOR prod), exactly the case the cross-crate doc says must stay a runtime/profile decision, NOT a cfg. So unlike the OnClass-as-cfg analogue (a sibling condition feature), profiles are firmly on the RUNTIME side of the conditional-strategy blend — a clarifying boundary, not a tension to resolve here.

### Interactions
- **conditions** — The substrate this feature IS built on — `@Profile` is just a `@Conditional`. Profiles contributes a single registered `OnProfile` Condition (a `ConditionId`/`Leaf(ON_PROFILE, ...)` preset) and consumes the SPI's two-phase model (profiles are PARSE-phase: depend only on the sealed environment, not on what-beans-exist), AND-fold (a `#[profile]` stacked with another condition just ANDs), and graceful-no-bean semantics. Profiles owns NO bespoke registration path; it is the most-ergonomically-named preset. Co-review acid test: `OnProfile` is the canonical example proving the SPI serves parameterized presets.
- **environment** — Deep unification + hard dependency. The environment OWNS the canonical active-profile set (`active_profiles()`/`ActiveProfiles`) as a derived read over the property stack (`spring.profiles.active` is just a property), and is where `accepts_profiles`/`profiles()` lives; profiles OWNS the grammar evaluator that delegate calls into (`profiles::matches`) and (R3) the `resolve_active` ALGEBRA that turns levers into the sealed set. The env's open question 'is matching a method or a free fn over a derived ActiveProfiles' is answered by profiles' free-fn factoring. The env seal timing is profiles' key happens-before.
- **property-sources / property-resolution** — The three levers (`active`/`include`/`group`/`default`) are READ as properties from the ordered first-source-wins stack (a CLI override beats a file). property-resolution supplies the read path; property-sources supplies the ordering and the never-blend rule. The buried `include` 'per-property-source, not list-merged' semantic is genuinely a property-stack concern (see rustClashes) — boundary must be drawn so profiles owns the algebra, not the per-source harvesting.
- **config-data** — The leaf analogue of Boot's Config Data + EnvironmentPostProcessor is the ORDERED INFRASTRUCTURE that harvests `ProfileLevers` into the environment during the cold seal phase, including a cross-crate library 'insisting on' an included profile. config-data also carries the `on-profile`/`activate.on-profile`-document analogue (profile-conditional config documents) which reuses this feature's `ProfileExpr` grammar+evaluator. Profiles supplies the grammar; config-data supplies the document-activation hook and the harvesting.
- **relaxed-binding** — The activation keys themselves are relaxed-bound: `SPRING_PROFILES_ACTIVE` (env-var UPPER_SNAKE), `spring.profiles.active` (kebab), etc. map to one canonical lever. Profile NAME validation (letters/digits/`-_.+@`, start/end alphanumeric) is a guard against names colliding with the expression operators — a Boot-layer concern this feature exposes as a gated `validate` flag, coordinated with relaxed-binding's key-form mapping.
- **condition-report** — Every profile match/no-match threads a `ConditionOutcome{matched, reason}` into the report as a non-error side channel ('bean X dropped: profile expression `prod & us-east` not satisfied; active={dev}'). R2 enriches this with a group-level entry ('group prod dropped, 4 members; activated-via=none'). Profiles produces the verdict+reason; condition-report owns accounting/presentation. The separation of condition-not-met (silent now) vs wiring-broken (loud later) is preserved here.
- **annotation-model** — Upstream dependency for the second condition input: the `#[profile("...")]` attribute's parsed `ProfileExpr` is materialized as const metadata ONTO the element's annotation-model descriptor, read without constructing the bean. Whatever annotation-model picks (compile-time-merged const vs runtime engine) determines when the profile expression is parsed/available; profiles' compile-time parse fits the const-metadata model. Profiles can also be a meta-annotation (custom stereotype `@Production`), which annotation-model's attribute-forwarding must support.
- **configuration-classes / component-stereotypes / component-scanning** — Profiles sit type-level (gating all nested `@Bean` methods — the class-level-short-circuit), method-level (gating one bean), or as a meta-annotation on a custom stereotype. Discovered components and config-class `@Bean` methods are gated by the `OnProfile` condition before becoming live definitions, riding the SAME cross-crate discovery substrate as the components. R2's profile-GROUP is conceptually the analogue of a profiled `@Configuration` class.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — Imposes two ordering edges on the bring-up state machine: (1) the Environment must be SEALED with `ActiveProfiles` fully resolved (active + include-prepend + group-fan-out + default-fallback) BEFORE the profile/condition pass; (2) that pass runs during definition registration, before eager instantiation. The seal-then-evaluate ordering IS a sub-step of refresh; profiles must slot in, not run ad hoc.
- **container-hierarchy** — Hierarchical contexts de-dup profile names and a child may layer additional active profiles over the parent (one-directional visibility). The immutable `ActiveProfiles` (R3) realizes child activation as deriving a child set from the parent's, not mutating the parent — honoring the DAG without a back-reference, consistent with the environment design's structural-sharing/merge model.
- **auto-configuration** — Auto-configured beans can themselves be profile-gated, and profiles are a structural complement to the OnMissingBean back-off: profiles answer 'which beans exist per environment' while auto-config answers 'opinionated defaults that back off'. Both ride the conditions SPI; profiles being PARSE-phase prune early, auto-config OnMissingBean is REGISTER-phase — the two-phase model keeps them composable.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- THE conditional strategy (charter §3, deferred): profiles land firmly on the RUNTIME side of the cfg-vs-codegen-vs-runtime blend (activation is an ops-replaceable, mutually-exclusive-capable runtime choice, NOT a cfg/feature) — but the per-bean profile GUARD rides whatever the conditions SPI picks (runtime descriptor table vs the R3 CondExpr seam). Phase 2 must confirm profiles are always runtime-evaluated even if other conditions (OnClass) are static, and that this asymmetry is coherent.
- Where exactly is `ActiveProfiles` PRODUCED and what owns it — is the lever-harvesting (`active`/`include`/`group`/`default` read from the property stack, incl. the per-property-source-not-list-merged `include` rule and relaxed-binding) a `config-data`/`property-sources` responsibility, with profiles owning only the pure `resolve_active` ALGEBRA over already-harvested levers? The boundary between TRANSPORT (harvesting) and ALGEBRA (resolution) is unresolved and cross-cuts environment/config-data/relaxed-binding.
- Does the buried `spring.profiles.include` 'per-property-source, NOT list-merged' semantic force `ProfileLevers` to carry per-source structure (leaking transport into the profile algebra), or does that rule live entirely upstream in the property-stack layer? This is the sharpest concrete instance of the transport-vs-algebra boundary above.
- Is profile MATCHING a method on the environment (`accepts_profiles`) or a free function over a derived `ActiveProfiles` view (the factoring R1/R3 assume)? This was left open by BOTH the conditions and environment designs and must be decided ONCE so profiles, conditions, and environment agree on the seam.
- How is late/additive activation (Boot's `setAdditionalProfiles` augment-not-replace, programmatic `addActiveProfile`) realized against an immutable-after-seal `ActiveProfiles` — a pre-seal lever merge, a child-derived set, or a re-seal? This is an instance of the deferred scope/lifetime/ownership keystone applied to profiles and is coupled to the environment design's builder-consumed/capability-token seal seam.
- Should profile group fan-out be ONE level (Spring's documented behaviour) or TRANSITIVE with cycle detection (R3's defensible improvement)? A faithfulness-vs-robustness call that also decides whether a `ProfileGroupCycle` is even a possible error.
- Is a first-class named profile-GROUP scope (R2) worth its conceptual-debt risk (a near-parallel-engine, plus the 'group'-scope vs 'group'-lever name collision), or do profiles stay purely a per-element condition preset with group-as-introspection being a condition-report view? Decides how literally the 'named groups of beans' catalog framing is taken structurally.
- How do cross-crate profile-ACTIVATION contributions (a library insisting on an included profile) get discovered and ordered — they must ride the SAME env-customizer / EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue discovery substrate as everything else (const descriptors, runtime-evaluated, topo-ordered by data), NOT a bespoke profiles channel — and how does that reconcile with the deferred cross-crate composition model?
- Does the optional dynamic/WASM-module 'second classpath' contribute profile-gated definitions and/or profile activations that have no compile-time literal expression — forcing the runtime profile evaluator + runtime grammar parser to ALWAYS exist (even though the native-crate common case parses at compile time)? Decides whether the runtime parser is a mere escape hatch or a mandatory layer for origin-agnosticism.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated `profiles` STRICTLY as (a) the most-ergonomically-named CONDITION PRESET (`@Profile` is a `@Conditional`), (b) the EXPRESSION GRAMMAR + evaluator (`!`/`&`/`|`, no-mix-without-parens, array=OR, negation=absence), and (c) the ACTIVATION-LEVER ALGEBRA (active/include/group + reserved-`default` fallback). I deliberately did NOT design: the condition SPI itself (two-phase/AND-fold/graceful-no-bean → `conditions`, already designed), the active-profile-set source-of-truth and read view (`environment`, already designed — I build on its sealed `ActiveProfiles`/`active_profiles()` and its open 'matching method vs free fn' question), the property stack/ordering/relaxed-binding that TRANSPORTS the levers (`property-sources`/`property-resolution`/`config-data`/`relaxed-binding`), or the report accounting (`condition-report`).

The genuinely divergent axis for THIS feature is WHERE the design's center of gravity sits and HOW a profile-group is REPRESENTED: R1 minimizes profiles to a thin condition preset + grammar (maximal unification, faithful to 'profiles are just a condition'), R2 makes the named bean-GROUP a first-class introspectable structural unit (literal to the 'named groups of beans' catalog framing, richer diagnostics, but risks a near-parallel-engine + a 'group' name collision), R3 puts the weight on the ACTIVATION ALGEBRA as a sealed `ActiveProfiles` value object owning the buried lever rules + transitive group fan-out with cycle detection (strongest guard against the notorious default-suppression gotcha, single canonical 'active' set). They are COMPOSABLE, not exclusive — the likely hybrid is R1's thin preset for the per-bean gate + R3's `resolve_active`/`ActiveProfiles` algebra for activation, with R2's group-as-introspection as a condition-report VIEW rather than a registration scope.

Two intents to keep distinct in later phases: 'which beans EXIST per environment' (the structural profile gate — a condition) vs 'how the active set is COMPUTED from levers' (the activation algebra — owned here). The hardest, most-surprising intent is the latter (default-suppression, include-prepend, per-property-source-not-merged, group fan-out), which is why R3 elevates it.

Critical constraints from grounding, all honored: profile/feature/condition logic is RUNTIME evaluation over const descriptors (cross-crate doc's hard rule — never pre-main, never link/section/constructor order). Profiles invent NO bespoke discovery channel — gated definitions ride the shared definition-descriptor substrate (linkme default + optional dynamic/WASM source) inheriting its DCE/Layer-0/generics hazards and self-check; cross-crate activation contributions ride the env-customizer substrate. The `ProfileExpr`/`ActiveProfiles`/`ON_PROFILE` ABI lives in the stable kernel and stays minimal (emitted const data hard-codes paths). Profiles are SYNCHRONOUS COLD-PATH (the seal + condition pass in refresh-lifecycle; no async, no blocking, no hot-path cost). Nightly review: nothing here needs nightly — const grammar parsing/`ProfileExpr` trees, runtime tree evaluation, `Set<Name>` membership, and inventory/linkme are all stable; profiles are sync cold-path so no async-trait boxing tax. Charter alignment: fail-fast-on-ambiguity becomes a COMPILE error for literal expressions (#9, earliest legible), graceful-no-bean preserved (condition-not-met ≠ wiring-broken), thin macro (#10, emits one const entry), unification (#11, a condition preset not a parallel engine). Co-review partners: `conditions` (the substrate — `OnProfile` is its canonical parameterized-preset acid test), `environment` (the sealed `ActiveProfiles` and the matching-seam open question), and `config-data` (lever harvesting + the `on-profile`-document analogue reusing this grammar).

## Environment Abstraction  `[environment]`

Spring's `Environment` is the single object that answers "what is true about where I'm running," fusing the two facets of deployment context: (1) active/default **profiles** and (2) an ordered, first-source-wins **property-source stack**. The unification is deliberate and conceptual — `spring.profiles.active` is itself just a property, so the same read mechanism drives both, and developers get one mental anchor for all deployment-context reasoning. The API is split along a least-privilege seam: `PropertyResolver` (the read view: `getProperty`, `getRequiredProperty`, `containsProperty`, `resolvePlaceholders`, `acceptsProfiles`) is handed to application beans, while `ConfigurableEnvironment` (the mutate view: `setActiveProfiles`, `getPropertySources()`, `merge(parent)`) is reserved for the bootstrap/infrastructure layer so business code can consume config but never reshape precedence. The container owns exactly ONE environment and it is reachable everywhere (Spring: `EnvironmentAware` or `@Autowired Environment`). Hierarchical contexts merge child-wins for identically-named sources and de-dup profile names. For leaf, the intent to replicate is: ONE owned, read/mutate-segregated, reachable-everywhere abstraction that unifies profiles + properties — NOT Spring's interface-inheritance mechanism. leaf must own the façade/seam; the stack mechanics live in `property-sources`, the read/placeholder walk in `property-resolution`, and conditional bean-group activation in `profiles` — this feature is the unifying anchor those three plug into.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Two-trait seam over an owned snapshot handle (read/mutate as distinct Rust types)
Model the read/mutate split as two Rust traits over one owned value. `trait PropertyResolver { fn get(&self, key:&str)->Option<Cow<str>>; fn get_required(&self,key:&str)->Result<Cow<str>,EnvError>; fn contains(&self,key:&str)->bool; fn resolve_placeholders(&self,tpl:&str)->Result<String,EnvError>; fn accepts_profiles(&self, expr:&ProfileExpr)->bool; fn active_profiles(&self)->&[ProfileName]; }` is the everywhere-shared READ view. `trait ConfigurableEnvironment: PropertyResolver { fn sources_mut(&mut self)->&mut PropertySourceStack; fn set_active_profiles(&mut self,&[ProfileName]); fn merge_parent(&mut self,&dyn PropertyResolver); }` is the MUTATE view, only the bootstrap layer holds `&mut`. One concrete `Environment` struct implements both; the container stores it as a single owned field and hands out `&dyn PropertyResolver` (or `Arc<dyn PropertyResolver>`) to beans, never `&mut`. Profiles are NOT a separate subsystem: `active_profiles()` reads the resolved value of the reserved key (leaf's analogue of `spring.profiles.active`) through the SAME source stack, so a CLI/env-var source can override a file — the unification falls out of the read path for free. `accepts_profiles` delegates to the `profiles` neighbour's expression evaluator over the active set. Borrow-discipline (`&` vs `&mut`) IS the least-privilege seam — no runtime guard needed because application code is only ever given the shared-reference trait object.

**Pros:** Read/mutate segregation is enforced by Rust's own borrow checker / trait-object split — the strongest possible 'application code cannot reshape precedence' guarantee, at zero runtime cost (charter #5: no locks, memory discipline).; Thin macros: the whole abstraction is plain traits + a struct; nothing needs a macro (charter #10). Fully hand-writable; `#[derive(EnvironmentAware)]`-style sugar, if any, only emits a trait impl.; Unification is structural and cheap: profiles ride the property read path, exactly mirroring Spring's 'profiles-active is just a property' intent with no parallel machinery (charter #11).; Single owned value, stack-friendly: the Environment lives as one field on the container, no gratuitous Arc churn for the mutate side (only the read view is shared).

**Cons:** 'Reachable everywhere' for async beans typically forces `Arc<dyn PropertyResolver + Send + Sync>` to survive `.await` across threads — so the zero-Arc ideal holds only for synchronous/borrowed access; cross-task reach reintroduces an Arc (deferred to T2 / scope model).; A pure borrow-based `&mut` seam means mutation is only legal where someone holds `&mut Environment`; if a later bean wants to push a source after refresh has frozen the env, the type system blocks it (matches Spring's intent that the stack freezes, but needs an explicit escape hatch).; `Cow<str>` return type leaks a representation choice into the public read API that may clash with the eventual type-conversion neighbour (typed `get::<T>()`).

**Mechanisms considered:** plain traits + one owning struct (borrow-checked read/mutate seam); RPITIT/AFIT for an async `get` only if a source can be async — but property reads should stay sync (cold/in-memory); keep reads sync; trait upcasting (1.86) so a `&dyn ConfigurableEnvironment` can coerce to `&dyn PropertyResolver` cheaply for the everywhere-handout

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This feature is a foundational kernel type: the `PropertyResolver`/`ConfigurableEnvironment` traits + the `Environment` struct live in `leaf-core`, so every downstream crate names them by absolute path. No cross-crate registration is needed for the abstraction ITSELF — it is a single owned object the container constructs, not a discovered set. Cross-crate enters only via WHO contributes property sources and profile activations (the `property-sources` / `config-data` / `EnvironmentPostProcessor`-analogue layer): those contributors are the discovered set and inherit the link-time-registry-vs-build-codegen duality (default link-time `linkme` slice of source-providers PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned source). The Environment itself must be origin-agnostic: it holds `Box<dyn PropertySource>` so a native source, a config-file source, or a future WASM-module-provided source all slot in identically. Risk: if profile activations are themselves contributed cross-crate (a crate that insists on a profile, à la `spring.profiles.include`), that contribution rides the same DCE-hazard substrate as component discovery — must be a `const` descriptor, evaluated at runtime, never pre-main.

**T2 — execution context:** The Environment is built during the cold bootstrap path (before any async bean work) — mutation happens here, single-threaded, holding `&mut`. After bootstrap it is frozen and only the read view escapes. Reads MUST be synchronous and non-blocking (in-memory stack walk, charter #4 — never poll/await on a hot read path). The mutate seam's `&mut` lifetime confines all reshaping to the bootstrap task. Cross-task reach for async beans: the read view must be `Send + Sync` to cross `.await` boundaries, which is the pressure toward `Arc<dyn PropertyResolver>` noted in cons. Errors (missing required key, unresolvable placeholder, malformed profile expr) are returned as a rich `EnvError` carrying key, the source stack consulted, and candidates — surfaced at the bootstrap validation pass for env-derived failures (charter #9), or at the call site for late `get_required`. No cancellation concern on the read path; bootstrap mutation is not cancellable mid-refresh.

#### 
Keep one `Environment` value, but make the read/mutate seam a runtime *capability* rather than a borrow distinction, so mutation can be granted to specific infrastructure phases without requiring exclusive `&mut` ownership. The read view `EnvRef` (cheap clone, `Arc`-backed, `Send+Sync`) is what everything holds. Mutation requires a `MutationToken` minted once by the bootstrap owner and consumed by infrastructure hooks (the leaf analogue of `EnvironmentPostProcessor`): `fn customize(env:&Environment, tok:&MutationToken) -> ...`. The token is non-`Clone`, non-`Send`-by-default, and is dropped at the refresh boundary — after which the stack is sealed and mutation APIs return `Err(Sealed)`. Internally the stack is an ordered `Vec<Box<dyn PropertySource>>` guarded by a single fine-grained lock that is only ever taken during the bootstrap/customize window (never on the steady-state read path: once sealed, reads go through an immutable snapshot `Arc<SealedEnv>` with no lock). Profiles unify the same way as R1 (active = resolved reserved key), but the active-profile SET is itself recomputed reactively when a source is added during customize (a notification, not a poll), so `include`/`group` fan-out (the `profiles` neighbour) is resolved as sources land rather than in a second pass.

**Pros:** Decouples 'who may mutate' from 'who owns the value' — lets ordered infrastructure hooks (the EnvironmentPostProcessor lineage, and `post-processor-spi` neighbour) mutate the env in a defined sequence without threading a single `&mut` through the whole bootstrap call graph (better DX for the boot layer, charter #1).; The seal-then-snapshot model gives a genuinely lock-free steady-state read path (charter #4/#5): the lock exists only in the cold customize window; hot reads hit an immutable `Arc<SealedEnv>`.; Capability token is a self-documenting, auditable mutate seam — and is the natural home for the child-wins `merge_parent` rule when contexts are hierarchical (`container-hierarchy` neighbour).; Origin-agnostic by construction: sources are `Box<dyn PropertySource>` added through the token, so dynamic/WASM sources slot in during customize identically to native ones.

**Cons:** Introduces a lock (even if cold-path-only) and an `Arc<SealedEnv>` snapshot — more machinery and heap than R1's pure borrow seam; must justify the lock 'with intent' per charter #5.; The MutationToken is a hand-built capability rather than a language-enforced guarantee — a misbehaving infrastructure crate that captures the token could mutate out of phase; weaker than R1's borrow-checked guarantee (mitigated by token being non-Clone/non-Send and dropped at seal).; Reactive recomputation of the active-profile set on every source-add is more complex than a single resolve-at-end pass and risks subtle ordering bugs in `include`/`group` interaction — must define recompute semantics carefully.; Two representations (mutable-during-customize vs sealed-immutable) doubles the env's internal states.

**Mechanisms considered:** capability token (non-Clone, phase-scoped) for the mutate seam; seal + immutable `Arc<SealedEnv>` snapshot for lock-free steady-state reads; one fine-grained Mutex/RwLock taken only during the cold customize window; reactive recompute (notification/signal, not poll) of the active-profile set as sources are added — honouring charter #4 reactive-on-hot, poll-on-cold; trait upcasting for `EnvRef` -> read-only sub-views

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same kernel-residency as R1 (traits + struct in `leaf-core`). The capability-token model maps cleanly onto cross-crate EnvironmentPostProcessor-style contributors: each contributor crate registers a `const EnvCustomizer` descriptor (fn pointer `fn(&Environment,&MutationToken)`) into a link-time slice; the bootstrap owner mints the token, topo-sorts the customizers by declared order, and invokes them — so cross-crate property-source/profile contribution rides the SAME discovery substrate (link-time `linkme` default + dynamic directory-scanned source as the optional WASM 'classpath') as component scanning, with the same DCE guardrails (const descriptors, runtime evaluation, force-link of opted-in crates, self-check for empty registry). The token never crosses a crate boundary as data — only the customize fn is invoked with a borrowed token — so there is no 'token smuggling' across the link boundary. Ordering of customizers is data on the descriptor, resolved at runtime (never link order).

**T2 — execution context:** All mutation runs in the cold bootstrap/customize phase on the bootstrap task; the token's drop marks the seal boundary. Customizers are synchronous and must not block on IO — if a contributor needs IO (e.g. fetch remote config), that is an async pre-step that produces an in-memory source BEFORE customize (mirrors Spring's BootstrapContext for pre-container expensive clients). After seal, `EnvRef` is `Arc<SealedEnv>`: cheap-clone, `Send+Sync`, lock-free reads on hot paths. Reactive profile recompute fires via an internal notification during customize only — never a steady-state poll. Errors during customize are aggregated and reported at the bootstrap validation gate with full provenance (which customizer, which source, which key); a customizer panic is caught and turned into a rich diagnostic rather than aborting bring-up silently. Cancellation: the customize phase is a bounded cold step, not cancellable mid-flight; the async pre-steps that feed it are where cancellation/timeout live.

#### R3 — Profiles-and-properties as a unified typed query surface (one resolver, two question shapes)
Push the unification further than Spring's API does: expose a single read object `Env` whose surface answers BOTH question shapes through one engine, with profiles modeled as a *derived view* over properties rather than a co-equal facet. `Env` offers `prop(key) -> Option<Cow<str>>`, `prop_typed::<T>(key) -> Result<T,_>` (delegating to the `type-conversion` neighbour), `resolve(tpl)`, AND `profiles() -> ActiveProfiles` where `ActiveProfiles` is computed lazily/memoized from the reserved active+include+group keys read through the very same stack. Profile MATCHING is not on `Env` at all — it is a free function `profiles::matches(expr, &ActiveProfiles)` (the `profiles` neighbour owns the grammar), so `Env` stays a pure property surface and the 'profiles are just properties' intent is literal: there is no `accepts_profiles` method, only `env.profiles()` feeding the profile evaluator. The read/mutate seam is expressed as two newtype wrappers around the same backing `Arc<EnvCore>`: `Env(Arc<EnvCore>)` is the everywhere read handle (Clone, Send+Sync); `EnvBuilder` is a distinct owned type that BUILDS the `EnvCore` and is consumed (`.build() -> Env`) at the end of bootstrap — mutation literally cannot exist after build because the builder is moved. Post-build, an 'override' is only possible by constructing a child `Env` that layers a new top source over the parent's `Arc<EnvCore>` (structural sharing), which directly realizes the hierarchical child-wins merge as a persistent-data-structure layering rather than an in-place mutate.

**Pros:** Cleanest possible unification (charter #11): one engine, profiles are a derived read, no second subsystem and no `accepts_profiles` surface — matching Spring's deepest intent more literally than Spring's own API.; Builder-consumed-on-build is the simplest correct read/mutate seam: mutation is structurally impossible after `build()`, no token, no lock, no `&mut` threading — strong guarantee + great DX (charter #1).; Hierarchy/merge becomes persistent-structural layering: a child `Env` shares the parent's `Arc<EnvCore>` and adds a top layer, giving child-wins + de-dup for free and zero copy (charter #5 memory discipline; serves `container-hierarchy`).; Typed reads (`prop_typed::<T>`) integrate `type-conversion` and `value-injection` neighbours at the resolver seam, where Spring does conversion-at-injection-point.

**Cons:** Diverges from Spring's explicit two-interface API — though that is mechanism not intent, a reviewer expecting a recognizable `Environment`/`PropertyResolver` mapping may find the 'profiles as derived view' framing surprising; needs clear docs.; Builder-consumed model makes the EnvironmentPostProcessor-style 'mutate the live env in ordered phases' pattern awkward: customizers must run AGAINST THE BUILDER (so they take `&mut EnvBuilder`), reintroducing an ordering/threading question the token model (R2) handled more directly.; Lazy/memoized `profiles()` over a mutable builder needs careful invalidation if a source is added after first compute during build — a cache-coherence concern.; Structural-sharing child Envs are elegant but make 'what is the effective stack here' harder to introspect/diagnose than one flat ordered Vec (tension with `origin-tracking` neighbour's self-documenting goal).

**Mechanisms considered:** builder consumed on `.build()` as the mutate seam (move-based, no token/lock); persistent/structural-sharing `Arc<EnvCore>` layering for hierarchical child-wins merge; profiles as a derived memoized view over the property stack (not a co-equal facet); typed `prop_typed::<T>` delegating to type-conversion at the read seam; generics vs `dyn` for `PropertySource` — keep `Box<dyn PropertySource>` for origin-agnostic (incl. future WASM) sources

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Kernel-resident traits/types in `leaf-core`, same as R1/R2. The builder model changes the cross-crate contribution shape: customizer crates contribute `fn(&mut EnvBuilder)` descriptors (link-time slice or build-time codegen) invoked in topo-sorted order during the build phase, before `.build()` consumes the builder. This is structurally the same discovery duality (static link-time registry default + optional dynamic directory-scanned source for the WASM 'classpath') with the same DCE guardrails. The persistent `Arc<EnvCore>` layering means hierarchical contexts in different crates can share one base Env cheaply across the crate graph without re-collecting sources. Origin-agnostic: `Box<dyn PropertySource>` layers accept native, file, or dynamically-loaded sources identically; a WASM-module source is just another boxed layer added to the builder.

**T2 — execution context:** Build phase is the cold bootstrap path; `&mut EnvBuilder` confines mutation to it; `.build()` moves the builder and produces the immutable `Env(Arc<EnvCore>)`. Steady-state reads are lock-free (immutable structurally-shared core), synchronous, hot-path-safe (charter #4). `Env` is Clone+Send+Sync so it crosses `.await` and threads freely — the Arc is the deliberate, single, justified shared handle (charter #5). Lazy `profiles()` memoization post-build is read-only and safe to compute once under a `OnceCell`/`OnceLock` (cold, computed at first access). Typed `prop_typed::<T>` may fail with a rich conversion error (key, raw value, source origin, target type) at the call site or hoisted to the bootstrap validation gate (charter #9). Child-Env construction is a cheap cold-path operation (clone an Arc, push a layer). No cancellation on reads; build-phase async pre-steps (remote config fetch) own timeout/cancellation upstream of the builder.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `Environment` is a GC'd object reachable from anywhere via `EnvironmentAware`/`@Autowired` with no ownership question. In Rust 'reachable everywhere' collides with ownership/lifetimes: a single owned value can't be borrowed by many async beans across `.await`/thread hops without either an `Arc<dyn PropertyResolver + Send + Sync>` or a scoped handle — so the zero-Arc memory-discipline ideal (charter #5) is in direct tension with the reachability intent. The aware-callbacks neighbour's injection model and the eventual scope/ownership model (Phase 2 keystone) decide how this resolves.
- Spring's read/mutate seam is interface inheritance (`ConfigurableEnvironment extends PropertyResolver`) enforced only by which type a caller is handed — a soft, reflection-era guarantee. Rust offers a STRONGER seam (borrow `&` vs `&mut`, or a consumed builder, or a capability token) but each strong option constrains WHEN mutation can happen far more than Spring (Spring lets infra mutate the live env almost anytime pre-refresh). Matching Spring's flexible-mutation DX while keeping a Rust-strong seam is the core tension across R1/R2/R3.
- Spring `EnvironmentAware` injects the env reflectively into beans the container creates. Rust has no reflection-based field injection; 'reachable everywhere' must be realized by passing the read handle explicitly (constructor param) or via the leaf injection mechanism — which means the aware-callbacks neighbour can't be a magic side-channel and must be ordinary dependency injection of an `Env`/`PropertyResolver` handle.
- Spring resolves profiles via `Environment.acceptsProfiles` as an instance method co-located with property reads. In Rust the cleaner factoring may separate the profile EXPRESSION grammar/evaluator (the `profiles` neighbour) from the env's property surface, so the unification 'profiles are just properties' is expressed by profiles being a derived READ over the stack rather than by co-locating a matching method — a structural divergence that is intent-preserving but API-shape-diverging.
- Spring's `merge(parent)` mutates a child env in place with child-wins semantics. Rust ownership pushes toward either persistent/structural-sharing layering (R3) or an explicit token-mediated merge (R2) rather than in-place mutation of a shared parent — the `container-hierarchy` neighbour's one-directional visibility must be realized without a back-reference that violates the DAG.
- `null` never overrides in Spring (absence is the only fall-through). Rust's `Option<&str>` models this naturally — `None` = absent — but leaf must be explicit that a source returning `Some("")` is NOT absence, preserving Spring's monotonic-override invariant; the type makes the distinction sharper than Java's null, which is a clarity win but a behavior contract that must be stated.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — This feature OWNS the ordered first-source-wins stack as the `ConfigurableEnvironment`/builder's backing structure; `property-sources` owns the stack's mechanics (named sources, addFirst/addLast/addBefore/addAfter/replace/remove, never-blend rule, `Box<dyn PropertySource>` origin-agnostic source trait). The Environment is the holder and the mutate-seam gatekeeper; property-sources is the held thing. Hard dependency.
- **property-resolution** — The Environment's READ view (`PropertyResolver`/`Env::prop`/`resolve`) IS the entry point that property-resolution implements: key lookup, `${...}` placeholder resolution, defaults, strict-vs-lenient, recursive resolution over the source stack. This feature defines the read trait surface; property-resolution provides the walking/resolving engine behind it.
- **profiles** — Deep unification point. `profiles` owns the `!`/`&`/`|` expression grammar, the array-is-OR rule, the reserved `default` profile, and the active/include/group three-lever model; this feature supplies the ACTIVE-profile set (read as a property through the same stack — `spring.profiles.active` analogue) and is where `accepts_profiles`/`profiles()` lives. `@Profile` is just a `@Conditional` over `env.profiles()`, so the conditions neighbour reads through this feature.
- **aware-callbacks** — Spring's `EnvironmentAware` is the 'reachable everywhere' delivery mechanism. In leaf this becomes ordinary injection of an `Env`/`PropertyResolver` read handle into beans that need deployment-context access — the aware-callbacks neighbour must treat the Environment as one of the injectable infrastructure handles, fired as a group before init, NOT as reflective field magic.
- **value-injection** — `${property}` placeholder injection at the bean injection point resolves through this feature's read view (and property-resolution). The Environment is the source of truth `@Value`-equivalents read from; typed reads (R3 `prop_typed::<T>`) are where type-conversion meets value-injection.
- **config-data** — The leaf analogue of Boot's Config Data engine + EnvironmentPostProcessor is the ORDERED INFRASTRUCTURE that populates the source stack during the cold bootstrap/customize phase (R2 token customizers / R3 builder customizers). config-data loads application/profile files into property sources; this feature provides the mutate seam (token/builder/&mut) it mutates through, and the seal/build boundary it must finish before.
- **container-hierarchy** — Hierarchical contexts need child-wins merge of identically-named sources and profile-name de-dup. This feature realizes that via structural-sharing layering (R3) or token-mediated merge (R2), honouring the neighbour's one-directional visibility (child sees parent, not vice versa) without a DAG-violating back-reference.
- **type-conversion** — Typed property reads (`getProperty(key, Class<T>)` analogue / R3 `prop_typed::<T>`) coerce string source values to typed values at the read seam, delegating to the central ConversionService/formatter registry the type-conversion neighbour provides.
- **origin-tracking** — For rich diagnostics (charter #9), resolved values should carry provenance (which source, file/line). This feature's read path must be able to surface origin alongside value so a deep precedence stack stays self-documenting; tension noted in R3 where structural-sharing layering complicates 'show the effective flat stack'.
- **post-processor-spi** — The EnvironmentPostProcessor-equivalent customizers (R2/R3) are ordered infrastructure that edit the environment blueprint before the container is built — conceptually the same 'edit the blueprint vs decorate the product' separation the post-processor-spi neighbour formalizes; env customizers are the env-stack analogue of BFPPs.
- **conditions** — `@Conditional`-equivalents (incl. the OnProperty/OnExpression members of condition-family) evaluate as pure predicates over Environment state. This feature is a primary input to condition evaluation; conditions read the frozen read view at registration-decision time.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — The Environment must be fully built/sealed at a defined point in the bring-up state machine (Spring: prepareEnvironment before refresh). This feature's seal/build boundary is a fixed step in the refresh-lifecycle ordering; reads after that point are immutable.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Reachability vs memory discipline: is the everywhere-shared read handle an `Arc<dyn PropertyResolver + Send + Sync>`, a scope-bound borrow, or a cheap-clone `Env(Arc<EnvCore>)` newtype? This is the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (charter §3 deferred) applied to the env — unresolved here on purpose.
- Which read/mutate seam mechanism wins framework-wide: borrow `&`/`&mut` (R1), a phase-scoped capability token (R2), or a consumed builder (R3)? This should be decided once for ALL blueprint-editing infrastructure (env customizers, BFPP-analogues, definition rewriting), not per-feature — a unification question for Phase 2.
- How is the EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue (env-stack customizer) discovered cross-crate, and does it share ONE substrate with component scanning / auto-config discovery? The static link-time-registry-vs-build-codegen duality plus the optional dynamic directory-scanned (WASM 'classpath') source must be decided uniformly across all discovery features.
- Where does the bootstrap/'BootstrapContext' phase live for env contributors that need async IO (remote config fetch) BEFORE the synchronous customize/seal step — i.e. the async-pre-step → in-memory-source → sync-customize pipeline (charter §3 async execution model, deferred)?
- Is profile MATCHING a method on the env (`accepts_profiles`) or a free function over a derived `ActiveProfiles` view (R3)? This decides how literally 'profiles are just properties' is realized and must be coordinated with the `profiles` and `conditions` neighbours.
- Does typed property reading (`prop_typed::<T>`) belong on the env read surface or strictly in `value-injection`/`binder`? Decides whether type-conversion is wired at the env seam or only at injection/binding points.
- How is value provenance (`origin-tracking`) threaded through the read path without bloating the hot read or breaking the structural-sharing layering — i.e. is origin attached to every returned value, or queryable on demand?

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated this feature strictly as the UNIFYING FAÇADE/SEAM — the one owned, read/mutate-segregated, reachable-everywhere abstraction — and deliberately did NOT design the stack mechanics (`property-sources`), the resolution/placeholder engine (`property-resolution`), or the profile grammar/levers (`profiles`), which are distinct catalog neighbours. The three realizations differ primarily on HOW the read/mutate seam and reachability are expressed (borrow-checked traits vs capability token vs consumed builder + structural-sharing hierarchy), which is the genuinely divergent design axis for THIS feature. All three keep the property-source trait as `Box<dyn PropertySource>` to stay origin-agnostic (native / file / future WASM-module sources slot in identically), per the guardrail. The cross-crate env-customizer discovery (EnvironmentPostProcessor analogue) is the only part of this feature that touches the link-time-registry/DCE substrate, and I flagged that it should share ONE discovery mechanism with component scanning rather than inventing a bespoke one — left UNRESOLVED as a Phase 2 question. Nightly review: nothing here needs nightly — stable async traits, `Arc<dyn>` upcasting (1.86), `TypeId`/`dyn Any`, and `OnceLock` cover everything; reads stay synchronous (cold, in-memory) so no async-trait boxing tax on the env surface. Charter alignment: read path is lock-free/reactive-safe in all three (R2/R3 explicitly seal-then-immutable-snapshot); the only `Arc` is the deliberate everywhere-handle, justified per charter §5.

## PropertySource Stack & Precedence  `[property-sources]`

This feature owns the *held thing* the `environment` façade wraps: an ordered, NAMED, first-source-wins stack of key/value backing sources. Spring's intent (docs section "PropertySource and the 'first source wins' rule") has four load-bearing parts to replicate as INTENT, not mechanism: (1) **A `PropertySource` is a named wrapper over ANY key/value backing** — a Map, env vars, a command line, a servlet/JNDI context, a file. The NAME is its identity, used by ordering mutation and parent-merge. Concrete subtypes (`MapPropertySource`, `SystemEnvironmentPropertySource` with relaxed UPPER_SNAKE matching, `CommandLinePropertySource`, the enumerable `EnumerablePropertySource`) all conform to one shape. (2) **First-source-wins resolution**: lookup iterates the stack in order and returns the FIRST source that *contains* the key; earlier entries have higher precedence. (3) **Explicit ordering mutation**: `addFirst()` (highest), `addLast()` (lowest), `addBefore(name, src)`, `addAfter(name, src)`, `replace(name, src)`, `remove(name)` — ordering is a deliberate, named-relative operation, never implicit. (4) **Determinism over merging — NEVER BLEND**: a property has exactly ONE effective value with ONE traceable origin; a preceding source's value *entirely replaces* a later one; there is NO key-level deep merge. Two corollaries: **null never overrides** — a source returning "absent" falls through to the next source, but a present value (even empty) does NOT, so "unset" and "set" stay distinguishable and overrides stay monotonic; and **child-wins parent merge** — for hierarchical contexts, an identically-NAMED source in the child keeps the child's instance and discards the parent's (so common sources like system-env aren't searched twice). SCOPE BOUNDARY: the upstream `environment` design owns the façade/seam (read/mutate segregation, reachability, who-may-mutate) and `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` placeholder walk; THIS feature owns only the stack data structure, the `PropertySource` source trait (origin-agnostic, so native/file/WASM sources slot in identically), the ordering-mutation vocabulary, the first-source-wins lookup primitive, and the never-blend + null-never-overrides + name-as-identity invariants. The genuinely divergent design axis here is HOW the ordered named stack and its mutation/lookup are represented in Rust (flat ordered Vec + name index, vs persistent immutable layering, vs an enumerable-vs-on-demand source dichotomy).

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Flat ordered Vec of boxed sources + name index (the literal MutablePropertySources transcription)
Model the stack as the most direct Rust transcription of `MutablePropertySources`. A source is one object trait, origin-agnostic so any backing slots in:

```rust
pub trait PropertySource: Send + Sync {
    fn name(&self) -> &SourceName;          // identity for ordering + merge
    fn get(&self, key: &str) -> Option<PropertyValue>;  // None == ABSENT (fall through)
    // optional enumerable facet for relaxed-binding / origin listing:
    fn as_enumerable(&self) -> Option<&dyn EnumerablePropertySource> { None }
}
pub struct PropertyValue { raw: Cow<'static,str>, origin: Origin } // raw, not blended; carries provenance
```
The stack is `struct PropertySourceStack { sources: Vec<Box<dyn PropertySource>>, index: HashMap<SourceName, usize> }`. **First-source-wins** is a hot, allocation-free linear walk: `for s in &self.sources { if let Some(v) = s.get(key) { return Some(v) } } None` — the `None`-is-absent contract IS null-never-overrides, and the early-return IS never-blend (we return the whole `PropertyValue`, never merge fields). **Ordering mutation** is the literal vocabulary: `add_first(src)` inserts at index 0, `add_last(src)` pushes, `add_before(name, src)`/`add_after(name, src)` look up the anchor in `index` and splice, `replace(name, src)` swaps in place preserving position, `remove(name)` extracts; every name-relative op returns `Err(NoSuchSource{ name, present: [..] })` with the current names when the anchor is missing (charter #9). The `index` is rebuilt or patched on each mutation (mutation is cold-path, so O(n) reindex is fine). **Child-wins merge**: `merge_parent(&parent)` iterates the parent's sources and appends only those whose name is NOT already present locally — child instance kept, parent dup discarded, child sources stay on top. The whole thing is the backing field of the `environment` façade's mutate view; after seal/build the façade hands out a read-only borrow/snapshot of this Vec and the walk is lock-free.

**Pros:** Most literal intent parity: every Spring method (`addFirst`/`addLast`/`addBefore`/`addAfter`/`replace`/`remove`) maps to one obvious Vec operation; a Spring developer recognizes it instantly (charter #1 DX, #2 intent-shape).; Hot read path is a stack-local linear scan over a contiguous `Vec` with early return — zero allocation, no locks, cache-friendly; first-source-wins and never-blend fall out of `Option` short-circuit (charter #4 reactive/no-poll on hot path, #5 memory discipline).; `Box<dyn PropertySource>` is rigorously origin-agnostic: a `MapPropertySource`, an env-var source with relaxed matching, a config-file source, or a future WASM-module source are all just boxed trait objects added the same way (guardrail).; Name index makes `addBefore`/`addAfter`/`replace`/`remove` O(1)-anchor-lookup and gives instant loud collision/`NoSuchSource` diagnostics — name-as-identity is a real `HashMap` key, mirroring Spring exactly.; `None`=absent makes the null-never-overrides invariant a TYPE-LEVEL guarantee, sharper than Java's null: a source returning `Some(empty)` provably does not equal absence, so 'unset' vs 'set-empty' cannot be confused.

**Cons:** Mutating the `Vec` + rebuilding/patching the `index` requires exclusive access; works only while the `environment` mutate-seam holds the stack mutably (fine pre-seal, but means no in-place reorder after freeze — matches Spring's intent but needs the env's escape hatch).; A flat shared `Vec` does not naturally express hierarchical child-wins as structural sharing — `merge_parent` copies/clones parent source handles (or moves boxed sources), so deep context hierarchies re-collect rather than share (heap churn vs R2).; Linear walk is O(n_sources) per key; for a 15-layer stack queried in a tight loop this is fine, but an enumerable 'list all keys' (needed by relaxed-binding / origin listing) must union across sources with first-wins dedup, which this minimal trait pushes onto the caller unless `as_enumerable` is widely implemented.; `Cow<'static,str>` in `PropertyValue` couples the source trait to a string representation; a source whose backing yields borrowed-with-shorter-lifetime values (a memory-mapped file) can't return a borrow and must own/clone.

**Mechanisms considered:** `Vec<Box<dyn PropertySource>>` for the ordered stack + `HashMap<SourceName,usize>` name index; one object-safe `PropertySource` trait (origin-agnostic), reads kept synchronous (in-memory, cold-data) — no AFIT/RPITIT needed on the read path; optional `EnumerablePropertySource` sub-trait via `as_enumerable()` downcast facet for key-listing/relaxed-binding without forcing every source to enumerate; `Option<PropertyValue>` return where `None`==absent encodes null-never-overrides; early-return encodes never-blend; trait upcasting (1.86) considered for enumerable facet but `as_enumerable()` default-None is simpler and stable everywhere

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The `PropertySource` trait + `PropertySourceStack` are kernel types in `leaf-core`, named by absolute path everywhere; the stack ITSELF is a single owned object the container constructs, so it needs NO cross-crate registration. Cross-crate enters only through WHO contributes sources (the `config-data` / EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue layer): those source-contributors are the discovered set and inherit the link-time-registry-vs-build-codegen duality — a default link-time `linkme` distributed-slice of `const SourceProvider` descriptors (fn pointers `fn(&BootContext) -> Box<dyn PropertySource>` + a declared default-position hint: first/last/before(name)/after(name)) PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned source-provider directory (the WASM-module 'classpath'). DCE guardrails apply to the contributor slice exactly as for component scanning: const descriptors, runtime evaluation, force-link of opted-in crates, and a self-check that warns when an expected source-provider crate yields zero contributions (silent-empty-registry is the worst failure mode). CRITICAL: ordering must NEVER come from link/section order (unspecified) — each descriptor carries its desired position as DATA, and the stack assembler applies add_first/add_last/add_before/add_after at runtime in a deterministic descriptor-sorted pass. The stack is origin-agnostic by construction: a `Box<dyn PropertySource>` from a native crate, a file loader, or a dynamically loaded WASM module are indistinguishable to the Vec.

**T2 — execution context:** The stack is mutated only during the cold bootstrap/customize phase, single-threaded, under the `environment` mutate-seam's exclusive access; all `add_*`/`replace`/`remove`/`merge_parent` ops run there. After the env seals, the `Vec` is frozen and only a shared read view escapes. **Reads MUST be synchronous and non-blocking** — an in-memory linear scan, never an `.await` or poll on the hot read path (charter #4); a `PropertySource` backed by remote/async data is NOT allowed to block in `get()` — such a source must have been materialized into an in-memory snapshot during an async pre-step BEFORE it was added to the stack (mirrors Spring's BootstrapContext for expensive clients). Errors are local and rich: `add_before`/`replace`/`remove` on a missing name return `NoSuchSource{ name, present_names }`; a `get()` returns `Option` (absence is not an error). No cancellation concern on reads; the cold mutation phase is a bounded, non-cancellable step. Cross-task reach is the `environment` façade's concern (its `Arc<SealedEnv>`), not the stack's — the stack itself stays a plain owned `Vec`.

#### R2 — Persistent immutable layered stack (structural-sharing cons-list of source layers)
Model the stack as a persistent immutable data structure so hierarchical child-wins merge becomes zero-copy structural sharing and post-seal reads are lock-free by construction. The stack is an `Arc`-linked layered chain: `struct Layer { source: Arc<dyn PropertySource>, name: SourceName, below: Option<Arc<Layer>> }`, walked top-to-bottom. `struct PropertySourceStack { top: Option<Arc<Layer>>, names: Arc<HashMap<SourceName, ()>> }`. **First-source-wins** walks the chain from `top` down, returning the first `Some(PropertyValue)` — identical short-circuit semantics, but the chain is the order. **Ordering mutation** is functional: `add_first(src)` conses a new top layer over the existing chain (cheap, shares the tail); `add_last`/`add_before`/`add_after`/`replace`/`remove` are persistent rebuilds (rebuild only the layers above the splice point, share everything below) returning a NEW `PropertySourceStack` value — the env mutate-seam swaps its handle, so 'mutation' is really controlled replacement. **Child-wins hierarchical merge is the headline win**: a child context's stack is `child_layers` consed ON TOP OF the parent's `Arc<Layer>` chain — the parent chain is SHARED, not copied, and child layers naturally shadow identically-named parent layers (first-wins during the walk handles 'child instance kept'); de-dup is enforced by skipping a child layer push when the name resolves to the same instance. Never-blend and null-never-overrides are unchanged (`Option` short-circuit per layer). The persistent structure means many sibling/child contexts across the crate graph share one base chain with O(1) layering.

**Pros:** Hierarchical child-wins merge is zero-copy structural sharing: child stack = child layers consed over the SHARED parent `Arc<Layer>` chain, directly realizing `container-hierarchy`'s one-directional visibility (child sees parent via the tail link; parent has no child reference — no DAG violation) with minimal heap (charter #5).; Post-seal reads are lock-free with no snapshot copy: the immutable chain is already a safe-to-share value; `Arc<Layer>` clone is cheap and `Send+Sync`, so the read handle crosses `.await`/threads for free (charter #4/#5, serves the env's reachability need).; Functional mutation (return a new stack) makes the 'frozen after seal' invariant structural — you literally cannot mutate the old value in place; an out-of-phase mutation just produces a new value the sealed env ignores (strong correctness, charter #9 fail-clear).; First-source-wins handles child-shadows-parent for free: the walk hits the child layer first, so identically-named child sources win without any explicit replace step — the merge rule emerges from the order invariant.; Excellent for many-context topologies (test contexts, child contexts per integration) where re-collecting a flat Vec per context would be wasteful.

**Cons:** Persistent rebuild for `add_before`/`add_after`/`replace`/`remove` in the MIDDLE of a deep chain rebuilds all layers above the splice — O(depth-above) Arc allocations per mutation; cheaper than full copy but more `Arc` churn than R1's in-place Vec splice (cold-path, but still heap), and `add_first` is the only truly O(1) op.; 'Show me the effective flat ordered stack' (needed by `origin-tracking` self-documentation and diagnostics) requires walking and flattening the chain — the elegant sharing makes introspection less direct than R1's literal `Vec` (explicit tension with origin-tracking neighbour).; More `Arc` than R1: every layer is `Arc`-wrapped even within a single non-hierarchical context, so the zero-Arc ideal is abandoned up front for the sharing benefit — must be justified 'with intent' per charter #5.; The mutation vocabulary (`addBefore`/`replace`/`remove`) is less literal than Spring's in-place ops; reviewers see a functional rebuild rather than a recognizable mutate-this-list, a (intent-preserving) shape divergence.; Name-collision/`replace`/`remove` need either a maintained `names` set (rebuilt on each functional update) or an O(depth) chain scan — slightly more bookkeeping than R1's `HashMap<name,usize>`.

**Mechanisms considered:** persistent/structural-sharing `Arc<Layer>` cons-chain for the ordered stack; functional mutation (return-new-stack) as the realization of addFirst/addLast/addBefore/addAfter/replace/remove; child stack = child layers consed over shared parent chain for zero-copy child-wins merge (serves container-hierarchy); optional `im`/`rpds`-style persistent vector considered but rejected — a hand-rolled Arc cons-chain keeps the dependency surface minimal and the layering semantics explicit; `Arc<dyn PropertySource>` (not `Box`) so a single source instance can be shared across child contexts without cloning the backing data — still origin-agnostic

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same kernel-residency as R1 (trait + stack type in `leaf-core`). The persistent layering specifically helps cross-crate hierarchical composition: a base `Arc<Layer>` chain assembled at the root can be shared cheaply into child contexts living in different crates without re-collecting sources across the crate graph. Cross-crate source CONTRIBUTION is identical to R1 — a link-time `linkme` slice of `const SourceProvider` descriptors (default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned provider set (the WASM 'classpath'), each descriptor carrying its position-hint as DATA (never link order), assembled at runtime by consing layers in a deterministic descriptor-sorted pass. Same DCE guardrails (const descriptors, runtime eval, force-link, zero-contribution self-check). Origin-agnostic: an `Arc<dyn PropertySource>` layer is identical whether the source is native, file-backed, or WASM-module-provided. One extra cross-crate nicety: because layers are `Arc`, an integration crate can contribute a source that the root context AND every child share by reference.

**T2 — execution context:** All stack construction/layering happens in the cold bootstrap/customize phase; functional mutation produces new `PropertySourceStack` values the env mutate-seam swaps in, all single-threaded pre-seal. After seal the `Arc<Layer>` chain is immutable and shared — reads are lock-free synchronous top-down walks, hot-path-safe (charter #4), and the chain is `Send+Sync` so it crosses `.await`/threads as a cheap `Arc` clone (the deliberate shared handle, charter #5). A `PropertySource` backing must still be in-memory/non-blocking in `get()` — async data is materialized into a layer during an async pre-step before consing (same discipline as R1). Errors: name-relative ops on a missing anchor return `NoSuchSource{ name, present_names }` computed by walking the chain (rich diagnostics, charter #9). Child-context construction is a cheap cold-path op (clone the parent's `Arc<Layer>` tail, cons child layers). No cancellation on reads; layering is a bounded cold step. Diagnostic 'flatten the effective stack' is a cold, on-demand walk — never on the hot read path.

#### R3 — Enumerable/on-demand source dichotomy with a precomputed effective-key index (read-optimized, provenance-first)
Split the `PropertySource` abstraction along Spring's own `EnumerablePropertySource` vs non-enumerable seam, and exploit it to flip the read path from per-key linear scan to an O(1) precomputed lookup, with provenance baked in. Two source shapes:

```rust
trait PropertySource: Send + Sync { fn name(&self)->&SourceName; fn get(&self,k:&str)->Option<PropertyValue>; }
trait EnumerablePropertySource: PropertySource { fn keys(&self)->&dyn Iterator<...>; } // can list its keys
```
The stack still records the ordered `Vec` of sources (the source of truth for ordering mutation, exactly as R1), but at SEAL TIME it computes an **effective index**: `HashMap<CanonicalKey, (PropertyValue, SourceName)>` built by walking ENUMERABLE sources top-to-bottom and recording the FIRST occurrence of each key (first-source-wins, materialized once). Reads of enumerable-covered keys become an O(1) map hit that returns value+origin together. NON-enumerable sources (e.g. a 'random.*' or a JNDI-like source that can't list keys) are kept as an ordered fallback chain consulted ONLY on index-miss, preserving on-demand semantics. **Ordering mutation** is the literal R1 vocabulary over the pre-seal `Vec`; the effective index is (re)built at seal and is the post-seal read structure. **Never-blend** is enforced by 'record first occurrence only — never combine'; **null-never-overrides** by 'a source contributing `None`/absent for a key does not create an index entry, so a lower source's present value is what lands'. **Child-wins merge** rebuilds the child's effective index by layering child enumerable sources first; provenance (`SourceName` + `Origin`) is stored IN the index, so 'why is this value X' is a direct lookup — this realization treats `origin-tracking` as a first-class read-path output, not an afterthought.

**Pros:** Hot read path is O(1) for the common (enumerable-source) case instead of O(n_sources) linear scan — meaningfully faster for deep stacks queried hot, while still honoring first-source-wins (materialized once at seal) (charter #4).; Provenance is a first-class read output: the effective index stores `(value, SourceName, Origin)` so `origin-tracking`'s 'why is this value X / which source / file+line' is a direct map hit — the deepest service to the origin-tracking neighbour of the three realizations.; Honestly models Spring's enumerable-vs-non-enumerable distinction (relaxed-binding NEEDS key enumeration; `random.*`/JNDI-like sources canNOT enumerate) — `relaxed-binding` and 'list all keys for binding' get a real `keys()` surface instead of being pushed onto callers.; Building the index once at seal naturally produces a flat, self-documenting effective view (the diagnostic 'show the resolved stack' is just the index) — solving R2's introspection tension.; Mutation pre-seal stays the recognizable literal Vec vocabulary (R1's DX) while the read path is optimized post-seal — best-of-both on the read/mutate split.

**Cons:** Two read paths (O(1) index for enumerable + ordered fallback for non-enumerable) is genuinely more machinery and more states than R1/R2 — must justify the index 'with intent' (charter #5) and carefully define the index-miss → fallback ordering so first-source-wins holds ACROSS the boundary (a non-enumerable high-precedence source must shadow an enumerable lower one, which the naive index-first read would get WRONG — needs a precedence-cutoff rule).; Materializing the effective index eagerly copies every enumerable key's value into the index — heap cost proportional to total key count, and a value-clone unless `PropertyValue` is `Arc`/`Cow`-shared; for large config sets this is real memory the linear-scan approaches avoid.; Index must be rebuilt on ANY pre-seal mutation that changes ordering/sources, or computed strictly once at seal; supporting post-seal late additions (Spring's `@PropertySource`-added-at-refresh, env customizers running late) means re-materializing — a cache-coherence concern R1/R2 don't have.; The enumerable/non-enumerable split leaks a capability distinction into the source trait that source authors must understand (which shape to implement), slightly higher authoring overhead than R1's single trait.; Relaxed-binding's many-forms-of-one-key (kebab vs UPPER_SNAKE vs camel) means the index key must be CANONICALIZED before insertion, coupling this feature's index to the `relaxed-binding` neighbour's canonicalization — an ordering dependency at seal time.

**Mechanisms considered:** pre-seal ordered `Vec` for mutation (R1 vocabulary) + post-seal precomputed `HashMap<CanonicalKey,(PropertyValue,SourceName,Origin)>` effective index for O(1) reads; `EnumerablePropertySource: PropertySource` sub-trait for key-listing (relaxed-binding + index build); non-enumerable sources kept as an ordered on-demand fallback chain; record-first-occurrence-only at index build = materialized first-source-wins + never-blend; provenance (`SourceName`+`Origin`) stored in the index row so origin-tracking is a direct read; `Cow`/`Arc`-shared `PropertyValue` to avoid cloning every value into the index; precedence-cutoff rule so a high-precedence NON-enumerable source correctly shadows lower enumerable entries (the cross-path first-wins correctness fix)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Kernel-resident traits + stack/index types in `leaf-core`, same as R1/R2. Cross-crate source contribution is identical (link-time `linkme` slice of `const SourceProvider` descriptors as default 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned provider set as the WASM 'classpath'; position carried as descriptor DATA, assembled in a deterministic runtime pass; same DCE guardrails + zero-contribution self-check). The enumerable/non-enumerable distinction adds a per-descriptor capability flag so the assembler knows whether a contributed source can feed the effective index or must join the on-demand fallback chain. Origin-agnostic: native, file, and WASM-module sources all implement `PropertySource` (and optionally `EnumerablePropertySource`) identically; a WASM source that cannot cheaply enumerate simply omits the enumerable impl and joins the fallback chain. The index is computed at the root/binary's seal point where the full resolved source set is known — consistent with 'the final binary is the only point that sees the whole graph'.

**T2 — execution context:** Pre-seal mutation (the literal Vec ops) runs in the cold bootstrap phase under the env mutate-seam, single-threaded. **Index materialization runs once at the seal boundary** — a cold, bounded step that walks enumerable sources and builds the `HashMap`; this is allowed to be O(total-keys) because it is cold-path (charter #4 permits cold-path work). Post-seal reads: enumerable keys are O(1) lock-free map hits, non-enumerable keys fall back to a lock-free ordered walk of the (small) non-enumerable chain — both synchronous, hot-path-safe, no `.await`/poll. The index is `Send+Sync` (immutable after seal) and shareable for cross-task reach via the env's `Arc`. A `PropertySource::get()`/`keys()` must be non-blocking in-memory; async data materializes into a source before the seal-time index build (same discipline as R1/R2). Errors: name-relative mutation ops return `NoSuchSource{name,present_names}`; index build surfaces relaxed-binding canonicalization conflicts (two source-specific forms of one canonical key within the SAME source) as rich diagnostics at the seal validation gate (charter #9). No cancellation on reads; index build is a non-cancellable cold step. Late post-seal additions trigger a re-materialization (cold) rather than a hot-path mutation.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `PropertySource` is a GC'd object held by reference in a mutable `MutablePropertySources` list that infra can reshape almost anytime pre-refresh. In Rust, who-may-mutate-when collides with ownership: an in-place mutable `Vec` (R1) needs exclusive `&mut` access confined to the env's pre-seal phase, while a persistent layered structure (R2) makes mutation 'replace the handle' — neither matches Spring's loose 'mutate the live shared list whenever'. The flexible-mutation DX vs Rust-strong-seam tension is inherited from the `environment` neighbour's mutate seam, and resolving it framework-wide is a Phase 2 keystone, not this feature's call.
- `null` as 'property absent' is Spring's monotonic-override mechanism (a null in a high source does NOT mask a lower non-null). Rust's `Option<PropertyValue>` models this MORE sharply — `None` is provably distinct from `Some(empty_string)` — which is a clarity win, but leaf must STATE the contract loudly: a source returning `Some(PropertyValue{raw:""})` is a PRESENT empty value that DOES win first-source-wins and does NOT fall through. Java's null blurred 'unset' and 'set-to-null'; Rust forces the distinction, so the never-override-on-absence rule becomes a type invariant rather than a documented convention.
- Spring's `addBefore(name, src)`/`addAfter`/`replace`/`remove` mutate a shared list in place by name. Rust ownership pushes either toward (a) an in-place `Vec` splice needing `&mut` + a name→index map (R1), or (b) a persistent functional rebuild returning a new stack (R2), or (c) keeping the mutable Vec only pre-seal and freezing into a read-optimized index (R3). The literal in-place semantics are most faithful in R1 but least amenable to cheap hierarchical sharing; the divergence is intent-preserving (ordering vocabulary identical) but shape-diverging.
- Spring's `merge(parent)` mutates the child env's list in place, keeping child instances for duplicate NAMES. Rust ownership and `container-hierarchy`'s one-directional visibility (child sees parent, never the reverse) push toward structural-sharing layering (R2: child layers consed over a SHARED parent chain, parent holds no back-reference) or a copy-on-merge append (R1) — never an in-place mutation of a shared parent that would create a back-edge violating the DAG. The child-wins rule must be realized WITHOUT the child mutating the parent's list.
- Spring resolution is a per-key linear walk that is 'fast enough' on the JVM and never questioned. In async-first Rust on a hot read path, the same O(n_sources) walk is acceptable for in-memory sources (R1/R2) but tempts a precomputed index (R3) — which then collides with the never-blend invariant (the index must record first-occurrence only) and with non-enumerable sources (which cannot be indexed and must remain an on-demand fallback), reintroducing an ordering-correctness subtlety the linear walk never had.
- Spring's `PropertySource<T>` is generic over its backing type `T`, relying on erasure to store heterogeneous sources in one list. Rust has no erasure: the stack must be `Box<dyn PropertySource>`/`Arc<dyn PropertySource>` (object-safe, origin-agnostic) and the per-source backing type stays hidden behind the trait. This is the right move for origin-agnosticism (native/file/WASM all conform) but means the source trait's method signatures (`get(&str)->Option<PropertyValue>`) must be chosen to NOT leak `T`, and a typed/generic source convenience would be a separate ergonomic wrapper, not the stored form.
- Spring sources can lazily consult a live backing (servlet context, JNDI) at read time, on the JVM where blocking IO mid-read is tolerated. leaf's async-first + hot-path-no-block discipline forbids a `PropertySource::get()` that blocks or awaits — so any source whose backing is remote/async must be materialized into an in-memory snapshot during a cold async pre-step BEFORE it joins the stack. This narrows what 'any key/value backing' can mean at read time: the backing must be synchronously, non-blockingly readable, or pre-snapshotted.

### Interactions
- **environment** — INVERSE of a hard dependency: `environment` is the HOLDER/seam, this feature is the HELD thing. The `PropertySourceStack` is the backing field of `environment`'s `ConfigurableEnvironment`/builder mutate view; `environment` gatekeeps WHO may mutate the stack and WHEN (the &mut/token/builder seam) and seals it. This feature provides the stack data structure, the ordering-mutation vocabulary, and the first-source-wins lookup primitive that `environment`'s read view delegates to. We deliberately do NOT design the seam or reachability — those are `environment`'s already-completed call.
- **property-resolution** — `property-resolution` is the primary CONSUMER of this feature's first-source-wins lookup: its key resolution and `${...}` placeholder walk call into the stack's `get(key)` primitive. This feature owns the single-key first-source-wins/never-blend/null-never-overrides semantics; property-resolution layers defaults, recursive placeholder expansion, and strict-vs-lenient modes ON TOP of that walk. Hard dependency (resolution needs the stack).
- **origin-tracking** — Tight coupling: every value this feature returns is a `PropertyValue { raw, origin }` carrying provenance, so origin-tracking's 'which source / file+line set this' is answerable from the value itself. The `PropertySource` name is the coarse origin; the per-value `Origin` is the fine one. R3 elevates this to a first-class read-path output (origin stored in the effective index); R2 notes the tension that structural-sharing layering makes 'show the effective FLAT stack' an explicit walk rather than a direct list. Provenance must survive the never-blend short-circuit untouched (we return the winning source's origin, never a merged one).
- **config-data** — `config-data` (the Boot Config Data + EnvironmentPostProcessor analogue) is the dominant cross-crate CONTRIBUTOR of sources: it loads application/profile config files and pushes them into this stack via the ordering-mutation API during the cold bootstrap/customize phase, with the deterministic precedence order. This feature provides the named-source abstraction and the add_first/add_last/add_before/add_after vocabulary config-data uses to place each loaded document at its correct precedence; config-data owns the file-format loading and the precedence ORDER policy.
- **relaxed-binding** — relaxed-binding maps one canonical kebab-case key to many source-specific forms (UPPER_SNAKE env vars, camelCase, snake_case, list/map index conventions). It needs to ENUMERATE a source's keys (the `EnumerablePropertySource` facet) and canonicalize them; this feature must expose key enumeration (R1's optional `as_enumerable`, R3's first-class `EnumerablePropertySource` sub-trait + canonicalized index). The relaxed UPPER_SNAKE matching of an env-var source is realized by that source's `get()` trying canonical-form lookups — a per-source concern, but the enumerable surface this feature defines is what relaxed-binding binds over.
- **container-hierarchy** — Hierarchical contexts need child-wins merge of identically-NAMED sources (child instance kept, parent discarded) and profile-name de-dup, honoring one-directional visibility (child sees parent, never the reverse). This feature realizes that as either copy-on-merge append (R1's `merge_parent` skipping locally-present names) or zero-copy structural-sharing layering (R2's child layers consed over a SHARED parent chain) — in all cases WITHOUT a parent->child back-reference that would violate the hierarchy DAG.
- **profiles** — The active-profile set is read as a property (leaf's `spring.profiles.active` analogue) THROUGH this stack via the same first-source-wins walk — so a command-line/env source can override a file-declared active-profiles, falling out of the order invariant for free. `profiles` owns the expression grammar and the active/include/group levers; this feature is merely the stack those reserved keys resolve through. Note Spring's subtlety: `spring.profiles.include` processing is per-property-source, NOT list-merged — consistent with this feature's never-blend rule (no cross-source list extension).
- **value-injection** — `@Value`-equivalent `${property}` injection ultimately resolves through this stack's first-source-wins lookup (via property-resolution). This feature is the source-of-truth the injected value comes from; the single-traceable-origin guarantee means an injected value is attributable to exactly one source for diagnostics.
- **type-conversion** — This feature returns RAW string `PropertyValue`s (never blended, single origin); typed reads (`get::<T>()` at the env/binder seam) coerce that raw string to a typed value via type-conversion. The stack stays string-typed and origin-agnostic; conversion is a downstream concern layered at the read seam, so this feature's never-blend invariant is preserved before any coercion happens.
- **post-processor-spi** — The EnvironmentPostProcessor-equivalent source-contributors (config-data and friends) that mutate this stack pre-seal are the env-stack analogue of BFPPs — 'edit the blueprint (the source stack) before the product (the resolved config) exists'. This feature provides the mutation surface those ordered infrastructure contributors edit through; post-processor-spi formalizes the 'edit blueprint vs decorate product' separation and the ordering of those contributors.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Stack representation framework-wide: does the ordered named stack want to be an in-place mutable `Vec`+index (R1), a persistent `Arc`-layered cons-chain (R2), or a mutable-Vec-frozen-to-a-precomputed-index (R3)? This couples to the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (how much Arc, how hierarchies share) and to the read/mutate seam decision inherited from `environment` — must be decided once, not per config feature.
- Is the hot read path a per-key linear scan (acceptable for in-memory sources, simplest, R1/R2) or a precomputed effective-key index (O(1) but adds materialization cost, cache-coherence on late mutation, and a non-enumerable-fallback correctness rule, R3)? This is a performance-vs-machinery tradeoff that should be settled against the actual hot-path read frequency and the binder/relaxed-binding enumeration needs — and coordinated with `property-resolution`'s placeholder walk which is the real consumer.
- How are cross-crate source-CONTRIBUTORS (the EnvironmentPostProcessor/config-data analogue) discovered, and does that share ONE substrate with component scanning / auto-config discovery?
