**T2 — execution context:** COLD-PATH like R1, but the execution context is cleanly bisected: `plan(..)` is the async half (all file/dir/network IO via the injected `ConfigFs`, on the bootstrap executor, materializing everything to in-memory props — permitted cold-path async, charter #3) and holds NO borrow of the property-sources stack; `apply(..)` is the synchronous half (a pure fold that takes `&mut stack` briefly, no awaits, no IO) — this separation eliminates R1's long-lived `&mut`-across-`.await` borrow and makes the awaiting phase and the mutating phase non-overlapping. Same happens-before edges: early-control keys + sealed `ActiveProfiles` (from `profiles`) must precede planning; the stack seals after `apply`. The one execution subtlety: placeholders in import locations force the planner to maintain a provisional in-memory lookup over accumulated contributions — a synchronous, non-blocking read (no IO), so it stays hot-path-clean even though it runs inside the cold planner. Cancellation: `plan` is a cancellable awaited task tree (startup timeout, abort on first hard error); `apply` is uncancellable and infallible-by-construction (ordering can't fail) so a partial stack is never observed. Errors are rich `ConfigDataError` values carrying location/prefix/import-chain/IO-cause/optional-flag, aggregated at the startup validation gate; the `ConfigDataPlan` doubles as the failure context ('planned contributions so far'). Explicit RAII closes IO resources within `plan` (no async Drop).

#### R3 — Lazy resolver-graph: locations/imports modeled as a memoized DAG of resolver nodes pulled on demand, snapshotted to the stack at seal
Model the config-data universe as a directed graph of RESOLVER NODES (a location, an import edge, a multi-doc document, a configtree directory) and resolve LAZILY with memoization, only materializing what the active-profile set + import graph actually reach — then snapshot the reached subgraph to the `property-sources` stack at seal. This treats 'which documents exist and import what' as a pull-based dependency graph rather than a forward worklist.

```rust
enum ResolverNode { Location(ConfigDataLocation), Document { props, activate_on, imports }, ConfigTree(PathBuf), EnvVar(String) }
struct ConfigDataGraph { nodes: Slab<ResolverNode>, edges: Vec<(NodeId, ImportEdge)>, memo: HashMap<ConfigDataResource, NodeId> }
impl ConfigDataGraph {
    async fn resolve(&mut self, root: NodeId, profiles: &ActiveProfiles) -> Result<(), ConfigDataError>;  // memoized DFS, dedup via memo
    fn snapshot(&self, stack: &mut PropertySourceStack);   // topological flatten → ordered sources
}
```
Resolution is a memoized depth-first traversal from the root locations: visiting a `Location` node loads+splits it (async), each resulting `Document` node is activation-filtered (`profiles::matches`) and, if admitted, its `spring.config.import` edges are added and followed; the `memo` map keys on the resolved canonical resource so a node visited twice is reused (idempotency = memoization, structurally). The reached subgraph is then TOPOLOGICALLY FLATTENED into the precedence order (import-below-importer = child-below-parent in the topo order; profile-specific and location-group last-wins applied as edge/node weights) and `snapshot` folds it onto the stack. The divergence: idempotency and import-position become GRAPH properties (memoized nodes, topo order) rather than a loaded-set + worklist-insertion; unreached documents (skipped profiles, unfollowed optional imports that nothing references) are never materialized, so lazy memory is minimal.

**Pros:** Import idempotency and 'keep first-discovery position' become STRUCTURAL graph properties (memoized node + topological order) rather than imperative bookkeeping — a chained/diamond import graph (A imports B and C, both import D) resolves D once and places it correctly by construction, the cleanest model for complex import webs.; Lazy memoized resolution materializes ONLY the reached subgraph: documents for inactive profiles and optional imports nothing pulls are never loaded/parsed, minimizing cold-path IO and peak memory for large multi-location/multi-profile setups (charter #2 low overhead, #5).; The graph is a first-class diagnostic/visualization artifact: 'show the import graph, which nodes were reached, which were skipped and why' is a direct dump — the richest provenance story for 'why is my config what it is' across a deep import web (charter #9), and a natural origin-tracking complement.; Topological flatten cleanly separates 'discover the structure' (async DFS) from 'impose precedence order' (sync topo sort with weights) — like R2's plan/apply split but with idempotency/position handled by graph identity rather than a sort tiebreak.; Naturally extensible to the dynamic/WASM 'second classpath': a WASM-provided loader contributes nodes/edges into the same graph; the resolver doesn't care whether a node's loader is native or sandboxed (origin-agnostic by construction).

**Cons:** Heaviest machinery of the three: a node/edge graph + memo map + topological flatten with precedence weights is substantially more than Boot's documented single-pass worklist — risks OVER-MODELING a problem Boot deliberately made a simple deterministic pass (a faithfulness-vs-cleverness tension; the intent is 'single pass', not 'arbitrary DAG').; Topological order is only a PARTIAL order; the full externalized-config precedence is a TOTAL order, so the topo flatten still needs the same `PrecedenceRung`-style total comparator as R2 to break ties — the graph buys idempotency/position elegance but does NOT remove the need for an explicit precedence ladder, so it's R2's complexity PLUS a graph.; Lazy resolution interacts badly with Boot's actual semantics in one place: Boot's last-wins-at-location-GROUP with multiple active profiles is fundamentally an ORDERED-pass concept ('resolved per config-location group during the deterministic import traversal'); reconstructing exact Boot order from a graph topo sort + weights is subtle and easy to get wrong vs R1/R2's direct worklist order — higher risk of a precedence-order divergence bug.; A cycle in the import graph (A imports B imports A) is possible to express and must be detected (loud `ConfigDataImportCycle` error) — Boot's worklist+idempotency makes cycles a non-issue structurally; the graph REINTRODUCES cycle-detection as a concern the simpler models don't have.; Memoization across `.await` with a `&mut self` graph during async DFS recreates a borrow/ownership tangle (the resolver mutates `memo`/`nodes` while awaiting loads) similar to R1's, partially negating R2's clean async/sync bisection unless the DFS is carefully structured to load-then-insert.

**Mechanisms considered:** resolver-node DAG (`Slab<ResolverNode>` + edge list) with `HashMap<ConfigDataResource, NodeId>` memo for idempotency-as-memoization; memoized async DFS from root locations, following only admitted documents' import edges (lazy: unreached nodes never loaded); topological flatten of the reached subgraph + a `PrecedenceRung`-style total comparator for tie-breaking into the full externalized-config order; import-cycle detection during DFS (loud `ConfigDataImportCycle` error) — a concern only this model introduces; activation filter via `profiles::matches` at each Document node (delegated to profiles); graph dump as the import-web diagnostic / origin-tracking complement; same shared link-time loader-descriptor substrate as R1/R2 for cross-crate format loaders, and WASM loaders contributing nodes (candidate, not decision)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same kernel residency and same shared link-time loader-descriptor substrate as R1/R2 (linkme default 'classpath' + optional dynamic/WASM 'classpath', selection by `handles` DATA, DCE/zero-contribution guardrails). The graph model's cross-crate angle: because nodes/edges are data, a cross-crate loader (or a WASM module) can contribute arbitrary nodes/edges into the SAME graph, and the topological flatten treats them uniformly — the most natural fit for a future dynamic 'second classpath' that contributes whole config subtrees. But the precedence TOTAL order still must be co-owned across features (profiles/auto-config/test layers) via the same `PrecedenceRung`-analogue comparator, so the cross-feature precedence-ownership question (T1 of R2) is unchanged — the graph adds structure within the config-data layer but does not change WHO owns the global ladder. The graph is built at the final binary's env-seal point (the only place the full loader set + real FS are visible); unreached subgraphs are deterministic given the resolved feature set + active profiles, and (per the cross-crate doc) must be documented to differ between `-p` and `--workspace` builds since the loader set can differ.

**T2 — execution context:** COLD-PATH. The async DFS (`resolve`) does all IO (file/dir/network loads) on the bootstrap executor, memoizing into the graph — permitted cold-path async/poll for flaky remote nodes (charter #3/#4). Each loaded document materializes to in-memory props before snapshotting, preserving the synchronous-read invariant. `snapshot` is the synchronous topo-flatten + fold onto the stack (no awaits, brief `&mut stack`). Same happens-before edges as R1/R2: early-control keys + sealed `ActiveProfiles` precede resolution; stack seals after snapshot. The execution risk noted in cons: the DFS holds `&mut self` (memo/nodes) across `.await` while loading — must be structured as load-into-owned-then-insert to avoid a borrow tangle, or the async/sync bisection R2 achieves is lost. Cancellation: the DFS is a cancellable awaited traversal (startup timeout); a cycle is detected synchronously during DFS and raised as a rich `ConfigDataImportCycle` (the chain of nodes) BEFORE further IO; other failures are `ConfigDataError` with the node/edge/location/import-chain context, aggregated at the startup validation gate (charter #9). The graph itself is the failure context ('reached nodes, pending edges'). Explicit RAII closes IO resources within the DFS (no async Drop); unreached nodes hold no resources because they were never opened.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's Config Data engine runs as an EnvironmentPostProcessor that MUTATES a live, GC'd `MutablePropertySources` in place during a loosely-ordered bootstrap, freely interleaving 'load a file' and 'reshape the stack'. Rust ownership collides: an eager loader (R1) needs `&mut EnvBuilder` held across every `.await` of file IO — a long-lived exclusive borrow that fights the borrow checker the moment a loader must also READ the partially-built stack (e.g. `import: ${DIR}/x.yaml`). The plan-then-apply split (R2) and the load-into-owned-then-insert DFS (R3) are Rust-native responses that separate the awaiting (IO, no stack borrow) phase from the mutating (sync fold, no awaits) phase — an intent-preserving restructuring with no Spring analogue, and the cleanness of that bisection is the real divergence axis.
- Spring does config-file IO synchronously on the JVM main thread during bootstrap, where blocking on disk/network mid-load is normal and unquestioned. leaf is async-first with explicit execution-context discipline: ALL config IO (file reads, configtree directory walks, remote/Vault loaders) must be cold-path async on the bootstrap executor, and crucially EVERY loaded document must be MATERIALIZED to an in-memory `PropertySource` BEFORE it joins the synchronous-read stack — because property-sources mandates non-blocking `get()`. So a remote config source that Spring would lazily re-read becomes, in leaf, an async-fetch→in-memory-snapshot→sync-add pipeline confined to the cold seal phase; a flaky remote source's retry/backoff is a PERMITTED cold-path poll loop (charter #4), but it must never leak an `.await` onto the read path.
- Spring's `spring.config.import` resolves 'fixed vs import-relative' locations against a live filesystem with GC'd path objects and lazy class loading, and idempotency is a runtime `Set` of visited resources mutated during the pass. In Rust the 'visited set' is fine (a `HashSet`), but the import-position rule ('inserted immediately below the importer, keeping first-discovery position') collides with how each realization represents order: R1 makes it worklist-insertion order (emergent, hard to introspect), R2 makes it a `discovery_index` sort-key tiebreak (declarative data), R3 makes it topological child-below-parent (structural). Spring's GC-and-mutate model hides this representational choice; Rust forces an explicit decision about whether import position is emergent, sorted, or structural — and only R2/R3 make it inspectable for the 'why this precedence' diagnostic.
- Spring's full externalized-config precedence is a 15-rung order maintained by mutating the property-sources list in a fixed sequence inside the bootstrap, with `PropertySourceOrderingBeanFactoryPostProcessor` re-ordering late. In Rust the question 'is the precedence ladder emergent insertion calls (R1) or declarative data co-owned across features (R2/R3's `PrecedenceRung` enum + comparator)' has no Spring counterpart because Spring's reflection/mutation model lets any post-processor reach in and reorder. leaf's stronger ownership pushes toward a declarative ladder that profiles/auto-config/test-support can CO-OWN by contributing rungs — but WHO owns the total order (config-data vs a shared precedence-policy authority spanning profiles+auto-config) is a cross-feature decision Spring never had to make because mutation was ambient.
- Spring's `spring.config.activate.on-profile` is evaluated at load time against a `Profiles` object built from a live, still-mutable Environment, and the HARD RULE banning self-activation is enforced by throwing during the mutate. leaf's `profiles` design seals `ActiveProfiles` into an IMMUTABLE value object BEFORE the config-data pass (the 'decide profiles up front, then filter documents' rule becomes a literal happens-before edge: profiles seal, THEN config-data filters). Rust's immutability is an ASSET here — the active set provably can't change mid-load, so the circular/late-activation paradoxes Boot 2.4 banned are structurally impossible, not just rule-checked. But the document-may-not-set-profiles.active rule must still be a loud inline check (the document CAN syntactically contain the key; admitting it is the error), raising a rich `IllegalActivationDocument` rather than silently ignoring it.
- Spring's `configtree:` and `env:` prefixes lean on the JVM treating any directory/env-var as a lazily-readable backing with GC'd wrappers. In Rust, a configtree directory walk is async cold-path IO that must be fully materialized into an in-memory `MapPropertySource` (one key per file, contents as value, fine origin = the file path) at load time — there is no lazy re-read of a mounted secret without an explicit refresh primitive. The 'your platform's config IS a property source' mental model survives, but the directory/env-var must be snapshotted, not lazily consulted, narrowing 'any backing' to 'synchronously-readable-after-cold-materialization' (the same constraint property-sources imposed on its sources).
- Spring's early-control keys (`spring.config.name/location/additional-location`) are read from a partially-built Environment before files are located, relying on the mutable-stack-already-has-env/sysprops/cmdline ordering. In Rust this is a clean two-phase bootstrap: the high-precedence sources (env vars, system properties, command-line) must be seeded into the stack FIRST (a deterministic pre-step), then the early-control keys are read from that partial stack via the same first-source-wins lookup, then file location begins. The 'silently ignored if placed in application.properties' gotcha becomes a structural consequence (files aren't loaded yet, so a file-declared control key simply isn't present when the keys are read) — Rust's explicit phase ordering makes the gotcha a provable property rather than a documented surprise.
- Spring multi-document split (`---` / `#---` / `!---`) is done by its YAML/properties parsers producing an ordered list of documents, with GC'd intermediate structures. In Rust the chosen format-loader (an async trait, AFIT stable) must parse-and-split into an owned `Vec<LoadedDocument>` carrying per-value fine `Origin` (file+line/column, captured by the parser) — and because async Drop is unavailable, the parser's file handle / mmap must be closed by explicit RAII within the cold load, not relied upon to drop asynchronously. The split itself is faithful; the constraint is that origin capture and resource cleanup are eager and explicit, not GC-deferred.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — PRIMARY DOWNSTREAM TARGET (hard dependency): config-data is the dominant CONTRIBUTOR of sources to the property-sources stack. Every loaded/admitted document is wrapped as an in-memory `MapPropertySource` and placed via property-sources' explicit ordering vocabulary (add_first/add_last/add_before/add_after). config-data owns the file-format LOADING and the precedence-ORDER POLICY (which document lands at which rung); property-sources owns the stack data structure, first-source-wins, never-blend, and name-as-identity. The deterministic single-pass + import-below-importer + last-wins-at-group semantics are realized THROUGH that vocabulary (R1 eager calls, R2 a sorted plan folded with add_last, R3 a topo-flattened snapshot). We do NOT redesign the stack.
- **profiles** — BIDIRECTIONAL, two distinct couplings. (a) config-data DEPENDS on profiles having SEALED `ActiveProfiles` BEFORE the load pass — the active set drives which `application-{profile}.*` files load and which location-group wins (last-active-profile-wins), realizing Boot's 'decide profiles up front, then filter documents'. (b) config-data REUSES profiles' `ProfileExpr` grammar + `profiles::matches` evaluator for `spring.config.activate.on-profile` multi-document gating (the Boot-level analogue of @Profile for property documents). The two profile layers share ONE active set but run at different phases (properties first, beans later). config-data also ENFORCES the hard rule that an activate.on-profile document may not set profiles.active/include/group/default (loud IllegalActivationDocument). profiles owns the grammar+activation algebra; config-data owns the document-activation hook and the file harvesting of the activation levers.
- **origin-tracking** — PRIMARY PRODUCER of fine origins: config-data is the ONLY layer that knows file + line/column at parse time, so its format loaders STAMP `Origin::TextResource{resource, location}` (or intern it / build the key→location index, per origin-tracking's chosen representation) onto each value as they parse each document. A configtree loader stamps the file path as origin; an env: loader stamps the env-var name; SAJ stamps the JSON path. config-data defines WHEN/WHERE origins are captured (eagerly during the cold parse); origin-tracking defines the `Origin` TYPE and how it rides the never-blend short-circuit. The deterministic precedence rank is orthogonal — origin records WHERE a value came from, the stack position records its precedence.
- **property-resolution** — CONSUMER coupling at two points: (a) `spring.config.import` locations and `spring.config.location`/`name` control keys may contain `${...}` placeholders that must be resolved DURING the load pass against the partial stack (env/sysprops/cmdline already seeded, plus contributions-so-far) — R1 reads the live partial builder, R2/R3 maintain a provisional lookup view; (b) after the stack is sealed, the loaded values are read through property-resolution's first-source-wins + placeholder walk like any other source. property-resolution owns the `${...}` grammar and strict/lenient modes; config-data is a consumer of that walk for its own location/import placeholders and a producer of the values it later resolves.
- **environment** — HOST/SEAM (upstream, complete): the environment façade owns the mutate-seam config-data runs inside and the seal boundary after which the stack is frozen. config-data's whole load pass is a cold-path step within environment's customize phase, taking the `&mut EnvBuilder` mutate view (R1) or producing a plan/snapshot the env applies (R2/R3). environment gatekeeps WHO may mutate and WHEN and seals; config-data is the dominant EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue customizer that runs there. We do not design the seam.
- **relaxed-binding** — KEY-FORM coupling: the early-control keys and activation levers are relaxed-bound (`SPRING_CONFIG_LOCATION` env-var UPPER_SNAKE, `spring.config.location` kebab, `SPRING_PROFILES_ACTIVE`, etc.) — config-data reads them through the relaxed lookup. configtree: filenames map directly to canonical keys (dotted filename → dotted property); the bracketed `my.map.[key-with-dashes]` literal-key escape applies when a loaded document declares map keys. relaxed-binding owns canonicalization; config-data must read its control/activation keys via the canonical form and produce loaded keys that relaxed-binding can later canonicalize.
- **auto-configuration** — PRECEDENCE-LADDER CO-OWNER and ordering peer: auto-config contributes a `setDefaultProperties`-analogue (the lowest rung, below config-data files) and is itself a deferred ordered layer that backs off. In R2/R3's declarative `PrecedenceRung` model, auto-config and config-data CO-OWN the externalized-config ladder by each contributing rungs rather than config-data privately hard-coding all 15. Both run in the cold bootstrap; config-data resolves the property stack FIRST (auto-config's OnProperty conditions read the resolved stack), so config-data is a happens-before of auto-config's condition evaluation. The two-phase model (properties resolved, then conditional bean registration) keeps them composable.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — Imposes a fixed sub-ordering on bring-up: (1) seed the high-precedence sources (env/sysprops/cmdline) and read early-control keys; (2) seal `ActiveProfiles` via profiles; (3) run the config-data single-pass load (async cold IO); (4) seal the property-sources stack; THEN (5) the condition/profile bean-registration pass and eager instantiation. config-data is the cold IO-heavy step that must complete and materialize all sources before the stack seals — it slots into refresh's environment-preparation phase, not ad hoc.
- **resource-loading** — DEPENDENCY for the loaders' backing: configtree directory walks, classpath-vs-external location resolution, the `optional:`/`file:`/`classpath:` prefix scheme, and `*` wildcard expansion are resource-loading concerns the config-data loaders sit on top of. The fixed-vs-import-relative location determination and `optional:` tolerance map onto resource-loading's pattern/URL abstraction. config-data owns the config-specific prefix semantics and the import-relative resolution; resource-loading owns the underlying classpath/file/URL access the loaders call.
- **config-properties / binder** — DOWNSTREAM CONSUMERS (via the sealed stack): @ConfigurationProperties-analogue binding reads the resolved, ordered, origin-stamped stack config-data produced. config-data guarantees the single-traceable-origin and never-blend invariants hold from load through to the binder, so a binding/validation failure can name the exact file+line (origin) of the offending value. config-data owns producing the resolved stack; binder owns coercing/validating it and rendering origin in failures.
- **post-processor-spi** — ARCHITECTURAL ANALOGUE: config-data IS the EnvironmentPostProcessor-equivalent — an ordered infrastructure contributor that 'edits the blueprint (the property-source stack) before the product (resolved config) exists'. Its cross-crate format-loaders are discovered the same way other post-processors/infrastructure beans are. post-processor-spi formalizes the edit-blueprint-vs-decorate-product separation and the ordering of these contributors; config-data is the canonical environment-stack instance of that pattern, running pre-seal during the cold customize phase.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- WHO owns the full externalized-config PRECEDENCE-ORDER POLICY (Boot's 15-rung ladder + the PropertySourceOrderingBeanFactoryPostProcessor reordering)? Is it config-data-private (R1's emergent insertion calls) or a SHARED declarative ladder (a `PrecedenceRung` enum + comparator, R2/R3) co-owned by config-data + profiles + auto-config + a test-support layer? This is a cross-feature concern spanning config-data/profiles/auto-config/property-sources and was flagged unresolved by property-sources too — it must have ONE owner and one canonical total order, decided once.
- Is config-data's engine an EAGER imperative loader that mutates the stack as it walks (R1, max Boot fidelity, but `&mut EnvBuilder`-across-`.await` borrow tension), a PURE plan-then-apply split (R2, clean async/sync bisection, declarative precedence, more machinery), or a LAZY resolver-graph (R3, structural idempotency, lazy materialization, over-modeling risk + cycle detection)? This couples to the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (how much the mutate-seam borrow can span awaits) and to the environment mutate-seam decision — and determines how introspectable the 'why this precedence' diagnostic is.
- WHERE does the async config-IO pipeline live and how does it fence remote/network loaders (Vault, remote config server) off from the synchronous-read stack — the async-fetch→in-memory-snapshot→sync-add pipeline (the BootstrapContext analogue) shared with property-sources and environment? Including: is a flaky-remote-source retry/backoff poll loop a sanctioned cold-path activity, and does config-data own a refresh primitive for re-snapshotting a changed configtree/remote source, or is that strictly out of scope (Boot reloads only on restart)?
- How are cross-crate FORMAT LOADERS (.toml, remote, Vault, configtree variants) discovered, and does that share ONE substrate with property-sources' source-contributors, component scanning, and auto-config discovery? The link-time-registry (linkme default 'classpath') vs build-time-codegen duality PLUS the optional dynamic directory-scanned (WASM 'second classpath') loader set, with the DCE/Layer-0/zero-contribution-self-check guardrails (a `configtree:` prefix with no registered loader MUST fail loudly), must be decided uniformly across all discovery features — left unresolved here on purpose.
- Does the optional dynamic/WASM 'second classpath' contribute config DOCUMENTS or whole config SUBTREES (not just loaders) — i.e. a WASM module that resolves a sandboxed configtree or a remote source as nodes in R3's graph / contributions in R2's plan? This decides whether config-data's `ConfigFs`/loader abstraction must always admit an origin-agnostic dynamic source, and how its precedence rung is assigned when its origin is not a compile-time-known crate.
- How do the two profile LAYERS (config-data `activate.on-profile` document gating vs profiles' `@Profile` bean gating) share the single sealed `ActiveProfiles` across the phase boundary, and is the happens-before edge (profiles seal → config-data filters documents → stack seals → bean conditions evaluate) owned by refresh-lifecycle or negotiated pairwise? The 'properties resolved first, then beans filtered' ordering is load-bearing and cross-cuts profiles/config-data/refresh-lifecycle/auto-configuration.
- Should `spring.config.import` placeholders (`import: ${DIR}/x.yaml`) be resolvable against the PARTIAL stack during loading, and if so does that force every plan/graph model (R2/R3) to maintain a provisional in-memory lookup view (partially reconstructing the stack it deferred building)? This is the sharpest concrete instance of the load-time-read-vs-mutate tension and couples to property-resolution's placeholder engine and the ownership-borrow decision.
- Is the deterministic-single-pass guarantee (Boot's deliberate simplicity) worth preserving literally (R1/R2 worklist), or is R3's richer DAG model (better for complex import webs, but a partial order needing the same total comparator PLUS cycle detection) a net win or an over-model? This is a faithfulness-vs-power call that also decides whether `ConfigDataImportCycle` is even a possible error and how the import-position rule is represented (emergent / sorted / structural).

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated config-data STRICTLY as the file/format LOADING + deterministic single-pass LOCATION/IMPORT-traversal + multi-document SPLIT/activation + early-control-key bootstrap + ownership of the externalized-config PRECEDENCE-ORDER POLICY. I deliberately did NOT redesign: the property-source stack/lookup/never-blend/ordering-vocabulary (property-sources, complete — config-data is its dominant CONTRIBUTOR), the profile grammar+activation algebra+sealed ActiveProfiles (profiles, complete — config-data REUSES its evaluator for activate.on-profile and DEPENDS on its seal), the Origin type (origin-tracking, complete — config-data is the fine-origin PRODUCER at parse time), the ${...} engine (property-resolution), key canonicalization (relaxed-binding), the env façade/seam (environment), or binding/validation (binder/config-properties).

The genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is HOW the single-pass engine is structured and how async IO is fenced from the synchronous stack: R1 = eager imperative worklist mutating the stack via add_* as it walks (max Boot fidelity, simplest mental model, but `&mut EnvBuilder`-held-across-`.await` borrow tension and an emergent/implicit precedence policy); R2 = pure plan-then-apply (async planner emits an ordered `ConfigDataPlan` of rung-tagged contributions, sync applier folds it — clean async/sync bisection, exhaustively unit-testable via injected `ConfigFs`, DECLARATIVE co-ownable precedence ladder, at the cost of more machinery + transient double-buffering + a provisional lookup for import placeholders); R3 = lazy memoized resolver-graph (idempotency-as-memoization, import-position-as-topological-order, lazy materialization of only the reached subgraph, richest import-web diagnostics — but heaviest, over-models Boot's deliberate single-pass, still needs a total-order comparator on top of the partial topo order, and reintroduces cycle detection). They are partly COMPOSABLE: the likely hybrid is R2's plan/apply bisection (for the clean async-IO/sync-mutate separation and the declarative co-owned precedence ladder) with R1's straightforward worklist traversal as the planner's internals, reserving R3's graph only if real import webs prove complex.

Critical constraints from grounding, all honored: ALL config IO is cold-path async on the bootstrap executor, with every document MATERIALIZED to an in-memory PropertySource before it joins the synchronous-read stack (the async-pre-step discipline property-sources/environment mandate, charter #3); a flaky-remote retry/backoff is a permitted COLD-path poll loop (charter #4); the read path stays synchronous/non-blocking. Format loaders are discovered via the SAME shared link-time descriptor substrate as property-sources' contributors and component scanning (linkme default 'classpath' + optional dynamic/WASM 'second classpath'), inheriting the DCE/Layer-0/generics/zero-contribution-self-check guardrails — a `configtree:` prefix with no registered loader MUST fail loudly, never produce a silent empty stack; loader SELECTION is by descriptor DATA (the `handles` predicate), never link/section order (the cross-crate doc's hard rule). The engine + loader trait + plan/graph types live in the stable kernel; emitted descriptors hard-code absolute paths (proc-macro hygiene). Macros stay thin (a loader registers via one const descriptor, charter #10). The 'decide profiles up front, then filter documents' rule becomes a literal happens-before edge (profiles seal → config-data filters), and Rust's immutable sealed ActiveProfiles makes Boot 2.4's banned late-activation paradoxes STRUCTURALLY impossible. The early-control-key 'silently ignored in application.properties' gotcha becomes a provable consequence of explicit phase ordering (files aren't loaded when the keys are read).

Nightly review: NOTHING needs nightly — AFIT/RPITIT (stable 1.75) for the async `ConfigDataLoader` trait, async closures (1.85) for loader factories, const TypeId / const-eval for descriptors, linkme/inventory (stable) for the loader substrate, and `proc_macro::Span` (stable 1.88) for compile-time origins of inline config literals all cover it. The one first-class design CONSTRAINT (not a gap) is the absence of async Drop: the cold load pass must close file handles / mmaps / dir iterators / network connections via explicit RAII guards within the bounded cold step, never relying on async-deferred drop. Co-review partners: property-sources (the stack config-data fills + the precedence-ladder ownership question), profiles (the sealed ActiveProfiles + the reused activate.on-profile grammar + the two-profile-layers phase boundary), origin-tracking (fine-origin production at parse time), and auto-configuration (the precedence-ladder co-ownership + the properties-first-then-beans phase ordering). The biggest UNRESOLVED cross-cutting tension flagged for Phase 2 is who OWNS the total externalized-config precedence order (config-data-private vs a shared declarative ladder co-owned with profiles/auto-config/test-support) — left open on purpose, consistent with what property-sources flagged.

## Origin Tracking  `[origin-tracking]`

Spring intent (doc §"Origin tracking", lines 1525-1529): wrap every loaded config value in an `OriginTrackedValue` (value + `Origin`) so a deep precedence stack stays self-documenting. `TextResourceOrigin` records file + line/column; `PropertySourceOrigin` records the owning source; sources implement `OriginLookup<String>` to answer "where did this key come from." The load-bearing intent to replicate (NOT mechanism): (1) PROVENANCE IS A FIRST-CLASS PROPERTY OF A VALUE — every effective value is attributable to exactly one place, turning the Environment from an opaque map into a debuggable structure. (2) TWO ALTITUDES OF ORIGIN — a COARSE origin (which named source owns the key, the `PropertySourceOrigin` analogue) and a FINE origin (file + line/column for text-backed sources, the `TextResourceOrigin` analogue); the fine origin is optional (env vars, programmatic maps, random.* have only a coarse origin). (3) ORIGIN SURVIVES THE PRECEDENCE WALK UNTOUCHED — because the upstream `property-sources` stack NEVER BLENDS (first-source-wins returns the WHOLE winning value), the origin returned is the WINNING source's origin, never a merged/synthesized one; null-never-overrides means a fell-through source contributes no origin. (4) ORIGIN POWERS DIAGNOSTICS — precise error messages ("property X was set in application.yaml line 12"), an env-dump/actuator-env analogue, and binding/validation failure messages all read the origin off the value. SCOPE BOUNDARY: the upstream `property-sources` design already fixed the carrier shape `PropertyValue { raw, origin }` and owns the stack/lookup/never-blend invariants; `config-data` owns file-format LOADING (and is the producer that knows file+line); `binder`/`config-properties` own how a binding FAILURE renders the origin; `relaxed-binding` owns key canonicalization. THIS feature owns ONLY: the `Origin` type itself (its two altitudes, origin-agnostic across native/file/env/WASM sources), the contract for HOW a source attaches an origin to each value it returns (the `OriginLookup` analogue), the rule that provenance rides the never-blend short-circuit unmodified, and the rendering/introspection surface that turns an origin into a human-readable "where did this come from." The genuinely divergent Rust axis: HOW the origin is represented and carried so that (a) the hot read path stays cheap and (b) rich file+line diagnostics are available — owned-inline vs interned-handle vs lazily-recomputed-on-demand.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Owned inline Origin enum carried by value (the literal OriginTrackedValue transcription)
The most direct Rust transcription of `OriginTrackedValue` + the `Origin`/`TextResourceOrigin`/`PropertySourceOrigin` family. `Origin` is one owned enum, sized to cover both altitudes, carried INLINE inside the `PropertyValue` the upstream stack already returns:

```rust
pub enum Origin {
    /// coarse: only the owning source is known (env vars, programmatic Map, random.*)
    Source { source: SourceName },
    /// fine: text resource with location (the TextResourceOrigin analogue)
    TextResource { resource: ResourceRef, location: TextLocation, source: SourceName },
    /// chained: a value produced by another value (placeholder expansion / property-source-of-a-property-source)
    Derived { from: Box<Origin>, via: DerivationKind },
    Synthetic,            // programmatic / defaulted
}
pub struct TextLocation { line: u32, column: u32, span_len: u32 }
pub struct ResourceRef { uri: Arc<str> }      // shared file path/URI, one Arc per file
// upstream carrier (already defined by property-sources):
// pub struct PropertyValue { raw: Cow<'static,str>, origin: Origin }
```
A source ATTACHES origin at load time: a text loader (config-data) records `TextResource{resource, location}` per key as it parses; an env/map source records `Source{name}`; a programmatic override records `Synthetic`. Because the upstream stack's first-source-wins returns the WHOLE winning `PropertyValue` and never blends, the `Origin` rides along untouched for free — the winning source's origin IS the answer, no extra walk. `Derived` is the chaining case: when `property-resolution` expands `${a}` into a value, it wraps the result origin as `Derived{from: origin_of_a, via: PlaceholderExpansion}` so the causal chain (charter #9 'full causal chain') is preserved. Rendering is a `Display`/diagnostic method on `Origin` that produces 'application.yaml:12:5' or 'env var APP_MODE' or 'app.mode (from ${...} in application.yaml:12)'. The whole thing is plain owned data: no registry, no side table, no cross-crate machinery — the origin is born with the value and dies with it.

**Pros:** Maximum intent fidelity: `Origin::TextResource{file,line,column}` and `Origin::Source{name}` map one-to-one onto `TextResourceOrigin`/`PropertySourceOrigin`; a Spring developer reads it instantly (charter #1 DX, #2 intent-shape).; Provenance rides the never-blend short-circuit for FREE: the upstream stack already returns the whole winning `PropertyValue`, so the winning origin is the answer with zero extra work — no second walk, no lookup (serves property-sources' never-blend invariant directly).; `Derived{from: Box<Origin>}` captures the full causal chain for placeholder expansion / source-of-a-source, exactly the 'full causal chain... and where' the charter #9 diagnostics invariant wants.; Self-contained: no side table, no interning, no registry — the origin is owned data born with the value; trivially `Send+Sync`, crosses `.await`/threads as part of the value, no lifetime entanglement (charter #5 simplicity, #3 async-safe).; Origin-agnostic by construction: native, file, env, and a future WASM-module source all just construct an `Origin` variant; the enum doesn't care who built it (guardrail).

**Cons:** Heap/size cost on the HOT read path: every returned `PropertyValue` carries a full `Origin` even when nobody asks for provenance — `ResourceRef{uri:Arc<str>}` is an Arc clone per text value, `Box<Origin>` for `Derived` is a heap node; for a hot loop reading thousands of keys this is real churn the diagnostics-only path doesn't need (tension with charter #5 'avoid gratuitous Arc/boxing').; Memory proportional to total key count even in production where origins are rarely read: the origin is materialized eagerly at load for EVERY value, paying for diagnostics that may never run.; File path duplicated logically across every key from the same file unless `ResourceRef` Arc-shares the URI (it does here) — but the per-value `Arc<str>` clone is still a refcount bump per value.; `Derived` chaining can grow unbounded for deeply nested placeholders (`${a}`→`${b}`→`${c}`), each a `Box` allocation; needs a depth bound shared with property-resolution's recursion guard.; Couples the upstream `PropertyValue` size to the full `Origin` enum — widens the carrier the whole stack passes around, even for sources that only ever produce the coarse `Source` variant.

**Mechanisms considered:** owned `Origin` enum (two altitudes: coarse `Source`, fine `TextResource`) carried inline in the upstream `PropertyValue`; `Arc<str>` for the file URI so the path is shared across keys from one file (one Arc per resource, cloned per value); `Box<Origin>` recursive `Derived` variant for placeholder-expansion / source-of-a-source causal chaining; `proc_macro::Span` location APIs (stable 1.88: line/column/file/source_text) considered for COMPILE-TIME origin of inline `#[value("${...}")]` literals — a value-injection-site origin that this enum can also represent via a `Synthetic`/code variant; `Display`/diagnostic-render method on `Origin` rather than a separate formatter type

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** `Origin` + `PropertyValue` are kernel types in `leaf-core`, named by absolute path everywhere; the origin is plain owned data constructed by whoever loads the value, so it needs NO cross-crate registration of its own. Cross-crate enters only via the PRODUCERS of origins — the `config-data`/EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue source-contributors discovered through the SAME link-time-registry-vs-build-codegen substrate as `property-sources`' contributors (a default `linkme` distributed-slice of `const SourceProvider` descriptors = the 'classpath', PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned provider set = the WASM-module 'classpath'); each contributor, when it materializes a `Box<dyn PropertySource>`, is responsible for stamping the correct `Origin` onto each value it yields. DCE guardrails apply to those contributors exactly as for `property-sources`/component-scanning (const descriptors, force-link of opted-in crates, zero-contribution self-check) — but `Origin` itself adds NO new registry. Origin-agnostic: a native source stamps `Source{name}`, a file loader stamps `TextResource{...}`, a future WASM-module source stamps whatever altitude it can supply — all just enum construction, indistinguishable to consumers. The `ResourceRef` URI is a string the producing crate owns; no path-reference/link-order concern because origins are data, not link-time-collected items.

**T2 — execution context:** Origins are CONSTRUCTED during the cold bootstrap/load phase, single-threaded, by source loaders as they parse (config-data's file parse records line/column then; an async-fetched source materializes its snapshot AND its origins during the cold async pre-step BEFORE joining the synchronous stack — same discipline property-sources mandates). On the HOT read path the origin is merely CARRIED along with the value it's attached to — a move/clone of owned data, never an `.await`, never a lock, never a recomputation (charter #4 reactive/no-poll on hot path). The origin is `Send+Sync` (owned data + `Arc<str>`) so it crosses task/thread boundaries as part of the value. Errors: origin construction is infallible (worst case `Synthetic`/unknown); RENDERING an origin for a diagnostic is a cold, on-demand `Display` call that touches no IO. No cancellation concern — origin attachment is part of the bounded cold load step; `Derived` chaining shares property-resolution's depth bound so a pathological placeholder cycle fails with a rich diagnostic rather than unbounded `Box` allocation.

#### R2 — Interned origin table: values carry a cheap Copy OriginId, the table holds the rich data
Separate the cheap value-carrier from the rich provenance. Every `PropertyValue` carries only a `Copy` `OriginId` (a `u32`/`NonZeroU32` handle); the rich `Origin` data lives once in a per-environment `OriginTable` (a side arena/`Vec<OriginEntry>` indexed by `OriginId`). Interning de-duplicates: all keys from `application.yaml` share ONE `ResourceRef` entry, and identical coarse origins collapse to one id.

```rust
#[derive(Copy,Clone)] pub struct OriginId(NonZeroU32);
struct OriginEntry { source: SourceId, location: Option<TextLocation>, derived_from: Option<OriginId> }
pub struct OriginTable { entries: Vec<OriginEntry>, resources: Vec<ResourceRef>, sources: Vec<SourceName> }
// carrier shrinks: PropertyValue { raw: Cow<'static,str>, origin: OriginId }
impl OriginTable { pub fn resolve(&self, id: OriginId) -> ResolvedOrigin<'_> { ... } }
```
A source, while loading, calls `table.intern_text(resource, line, col)` / `table.intern_source(name)` and stamps the returned `OriginId` on each value. First-source-wins is unchanged: the winning value carries its `OriginId`, which rides the never-blend short-circuit (a `u32` copy, even cheaper than R1's Arc). `Derived` chaining is `derived_from: Option<OriginId>` — a flat index link, no `Box`. Diagnostics resolve LAZILY: when an error needs to render provenance, it borrows the `OriginTable` (reachable via the sealed environment) and walks `id → entry → resource/source` to build 'application.yaml:12:5'. The table is built during the cold load phase and frozen at seal alongside the property-source stack; after seal it's an immutable shared `Arc<OriginTable>` the env hands out for read-only resolution.

**Pros:** Cheapest possible hot read path: the carrier shrinks to a `Copy` `u32` `OriginId` — first-source-wins moves/copies a 4-byte handle with zero Arc bump and zero allocation, the leanest of the three (charter #2 low-overhead, #4 hot-path, #5 memory discipline).; Interning de-duplicates aggressively: one `ResourceRef`+`SourceName` per file/source regardless of key count, and identical coarse origins collapse — memory is O(distinct origins) not O(total keys), a real win over R1 for large config sets.; `Derived` chaining is a flat `Option<OriginId>` index link — no recursive `Box`, no unbounded heap; the causal chain is a cheap pointer-chase through the table (still charter #9 full-chain).; The frozen `Arc<OriginTable>` is exactly the data structure an `/actuator/env`-analogue / startup env-dump wants: one place to enumerate every origin, render the whole resolved stack with provenance, cross-check counts — diagnostics introspection is first-class and centralized.; Origin-agnostic: any source (native/file/env/WASM) interns through the same `OriginTable` API and gets back an opaque `OriginId`; consumers never see who produced it (guardrail).

**Cons:** Indirection: rendering a diagnostic REQUIRES the `OriginTable` in hand — a value's `OriginId` is meaningless without it, so the diagnostics path must thread the (sealed-env) table everywhere an origin might be rendered (binder errors, validation), a coupling R1's self-contained owned origin avoids.; An `OriginId` is only valid against the table that minted it — if a value escapes its environment (a test that copies a `PropertyValue` out, a child-context value rendered against a parent table) the id can be stale/wrong; needs a discipline that ids never cross table boundaries (or a table-generation tag), extra correctness burden.; The table is mutable during the cold load phase (interning appends entries) — needs exclusive `&mut` confined to the bootstrap phase, then frozen; if a source is added post-seal (late env customizer) the frozen table must be re-opened/extended, a cache-coherence concern R1 doesn't have.; Hierarchical contexts complicate id-space: a child env's table either re-interns parent origins (defeating sharing) or references the parent table by an outer id-space — must define how `container-hierarchy`'s child-wins values render their (parent-minted) origins; cross-table id resolution is the subtle part.; Slightly less literal than Spring's `OriginTrackedValue` (which owns its `Origin`): a reviewer sees a handle + side table rather than a value that knows its own origin — intent-preserving but shape-diverging.

**Mechanisms considered:** interned `OriginId` (`NonZeroU32`, `Copy`, niche-optimized so `Option<OriginId>` is free) on the value; rich data in a side `OriginTable` arena; de-dup interning of `ResourceRef`/`SourceName`/identical coarse origins so memory is O(distinct origins); flat `derived_from: Option<OriginId>` index link for placeholder chaining (no recursive Box); frozen `Arc<OriginTable>` at seal as the env-dump / actuator-env introspection surface; table-generation tag / id-space scoping considered to make stale-id misuse detectable across hierarchy boundaries; `proc_macro::Span` compile-time locations (1.88) could be pre-interned as `Synthetic`/code entries for inline value-injection literals

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** `OriginId` + `OriginTable` are kernel types in `leaf-core`; the table is a single owned object the environment constructs during bootstrap, so the table needs NO cross-crate registration. Cross-crate is, again, only the PRODUCERS: the same `property-sources`/config-data source-contributor substrate (link-time `linkme` slice = default 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned set = WASM 'classpath', position-as-data, DCE/zero-contribution guardrails). Each contributor interns its origins THROUGH the env-provided `OriginTable` handle during load — so a cross-crate source must be HANDED the table (passed into the source-materialization step), which is a deliberate, scoped capability, not an ambient global (honors 'scope discovery, don't make it implicitly global'). Origin-agnostic: native/file/env/WASM contributors all call the same `intern_*` API and receive opaque ids. One cross-crate subtlety the table adds over R1: the id-space must be owned by ONE table per environment, so a contributor cannot mint ids against its own private table and expect them to resolve in the env's table — the env's table is the single id authority, which the bootstrap wiring must enforce.

**T2 — execution context:** Interning happens in the cold bootstrap/load phase under exclusive `&mut OriginTable` access, single-threaded, alongside property-source loading; an async-backed source materializes its snapshot AND interns its origins during the cold async pre-step before joining the sync stack. The table is FROZEN at the seal boundary into an immutable `Arc<OriginTable>` shared by the env. Hot read path: the value carries only a `Copy` `OriginId` — moving/copying it across first-source-wins is allocation-free and lock-free (charter #4/#5). Diagnostic resolution (`table.resolve(id)`) is a cold, on-demand, lock-free read of the frozen `Arc<OriginTable>` (immutable → safe to share across tasks/threads, charter #3) — no IO, no `.await`. Errors: interning is infallible (unknown → a reserved `OriginId` for `Synthetic`); a stale/cross-table id is a programming error the generation-tag discipline can turn into a loud panic/diagnostic rather than silent wrong-origin (charter #9). Late post-seal source additions trigger a cold table re-open + re-freeze, never a hot-path mutation. No cancellation on reads; interning is a bounded cold step.

#### R3 — Lazy source-delegated OriginLookup: values carry source+key identity, fine origin recomputed on demand
Mirror Spring's `OriginLookup<String>` literally: a value's ATTACHED origin is only the COARSE (source identity); the FINE origin (file+line/column) is NOT carried on the value at all but ANSWERED ON DEMAND by asking the owning source 'where did key K come from?'. The hot path stays maximally lean; the expensive fine-origin computation happens only when a diagnostic actually needs it.

```rust
pub trait OriginLookup {                  // implemented by sources that can locate keys
    fn origin_of(&self, key: &str) -> Option<Origin>;   // fine origin, computed on demand
}
pub trait PropertySource: Send + Sync {
    fn name(&self) -> &SourceName;
    fn get(&self, key: &str) -> Option<PropertyValue>;   // PropertyValue carries ONLY coarse SourceName + the key it answered
    fn as_origin_lookup(&self) -> Option<&dyn OriginLookup> { None }   // optional fine-origin facet
}
// carrier stays minimal: PropertyValue { raw, source: SourceName, key: KeyRef }
```
First-source-wins returns the winning value carrying its coarse `SourceName` + the resolved key (cheap, the never-blend short-circuit carries identity only). When a diagnostic needs the fine origin, it looks up the owning source by name in the (sealed) stack, calls `source.as_origin_lookup()?.origin_of(key)` to RECOMPUTE 'application.yaml:12:5' lazily (a text source keeps a key→location index it built at parse time; a source that can't locate keys simply returns the coarse origin). `Derived` chaining is reconstructed on demand by re-walking the resolution that produced the value. This trades per-value memory for per-diagnostic computation: production reads carry almost nothing; only the rare error path pays to reconstruct provenance.

**Pros:** Leanest steady-state memory: production values carry only a coarse `SourceName` + key reference; NO per-value file/line is materialized, so memory is independent of whether diagnostics ever run — best for the common 'origins are read approximately never' case (charter #5).; Honest transcription of Spring's `OriginLookup<String>` SPI — the fine origin is a CAPABILITY a source optionally offers, not a value field; sources that genuinely can't locate keys (env, random.*, JNDI-like) cleanly return only coarse origin, matching Spring exactly.; Hot read path carries minimal data and never touches IO/locks; fine-origin reconstruction is confined to the cold diagnostic path where its cost is irrelevant (charter #4 — keeps the hot path pristine).; No interning table to thread, no id-space/staleness/hierarchy-id-space problems (R2's costs avoided); the source itself is the single authority on its own keys' origins, so hierarchical contexts 'just work' — ask the source that won.; Origin-agnostic: any source can implement `OriginLookup` (file → line index; WASM module → whatever it can supply) or omit it (→ coarse only); the facet is optional and uniform (guardrail).

**Cons:** Fine origin requires the OWNING SOURCE to still be alive and queryable at diagnostic time — fine on the sealed in-memory stack, but a source that dropped its parse-time key→location index (to save memory) CAN'T reconstruct, silently degrading to coarse origin; the 'keep the index' decision reintroduces R1/R2's memory cost where fine origin is wanted.; The value must carry enough IDENTITY (source name + the exact resolved key) to re-query — and relaxed-binding means the key the source indexed may differ from the canonical key the consumer used, so the re-lookup must canonicalize consistently (coupling to relaxed-binding's UNIFORM form at BOTH index-build and lookup time, a correctness subtlety R1/R2 sidestep by capturing the origin at load).; Two-step diagnostics (find source by name in stack, then `origin_of`) is more machinery on the error path and can FAIL to find a fine origin (source removed/replaced post-resolution), making provenance non-deterministic relative to when you ask — weaker than R1/R2's capture-at-load guarantee.; `Derived` placeholder chaining is hardest here: reconstructing 'this came from ${a} which came from application.yaml:12' on demand means re-running or recording the resolution path, which the lean value didn't keep — so chaining either needs a recorded trail (defeating leanness) or can't be reconstructed (weaker charter #9 chain).; Spring actually carries `OriginTrackedValue` (value+Origin) on the value AND has `OriginLookup` — leaning purely on lazy lookup is LESS faithful than R1; it optimizes memory at the cost of the 'value knows its own origin' guarantee Spring's binder relies on.

**Mechanisms considered:** optional `OriginLookup` facet trait (the literal `OriginLookup<String>` analogue) on sources; value carries coarse `SourceName`+key only; on-demand fine-origin RECOMPUTATION by re-querying the owning source's parse-time key→location index; optional downcast facet `as_origin_lookup()` (default-None) vs a required method — default-None keeps non-locating sources simple, stable everywhere; relaxed-binding UNIFORM-form canonicalization shared between the source's key index build and the re-lookup so the re-query hits; recorded resolution trail (opt-in) for `Derived` chaining, vs accepting coarse-only chains when no trail kept; trait upcasting (1.86) considered for the facet but `as_origin_lookup()` default-None is simpler/stable

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** `OriginLookup` + `Origin` are kernel traits/types in `leaf-core`. The fine-origin capability is a per-source trait impl, so cross-crate it inherits the `property-sources` source-contributor substrate (link-time `linkme` 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath', DCE/zero-contribution guardrails) — a contributed source from any crate optionally implements `OriginLookup` exactly like a native one. CRITICAL cross-crate property: because fine origin is RECOMPUTED by the source itself, the source object must REMAIN in the sealed stack (the env owns it) for diagnostics to work — which the property-sources stack already guarantees (it holds the `Box/Arc<dyn PropertySource>`). No id-space or table to thread cross-crate (R2's cost avoided); the only cross-crate contract is 'if your source can locate keys, implement `OriginLookup`'. A WASM-module source that can supply line info implements the facet; one that can't omits it and degrades to coarse — uniform and origin-agnostic. No new registry beyond the shared source-contributor one.

**T2 — execution context:** The source's key→location index is BUILT during the cold load/parse phase (config-data parsing the file), single-threaded, and kept inside the source object that lives in the sealed stack. Hot read path: `get()` returns a value carrying only coarse identity — allocation-free, lock-free, no `.await` (charter #4); the fine origin is NOT computed on the hot path. Diagnostic path (cold): `origin_of(key)` is a synchronous, non-blocking lookup into the source's in-memory index — MUST NOT block or `.await` (a source whose location data is remote must have materialized the index during the cold async pre-step, same discipline as property-sources). Resolution reads the sealed, immutable stack — `Arc`-shared, `Send+Sync`, crosses tasks/threads safely (charter #3/#5). Errors: `origin_of` returns `Option<Origin>` (None → degrade to coarse, never an error); the two-step find-source-then-lookup can yield coarse-only if the source can't locate the key — a graceful degradation, but the binder/validation diagnostic must state 'origin: <source>, exact location unavailable' rather than fail (charter #9 partial-but-honest context). No cancellation on reads; index build is a bounded cold step. `Derived` chaining, if supported, requires an opt-in recorded trail captured during the cold resolution, not the hot path.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `OriginTrackedValue` is a GC'd wrapper object freely referenced and passed around; an `Origin` can be held, cached, and rendered anywhere with no lifetime concern. In Rust, WHERE the rich origin data lives collides with ownership: owned-inline (R1) makes the value self-contained but fattens the carrier and churns Arc/Box; an interned handle (R2) shrinks the value but ties the `OriginId` to a specific table's lifetime/id-space (stale-id hazard); lazy lookup (R3) keeps values lean but requires the owning source to outlive every diagnostic. Spring's 'origin is just another object on the heap' has no single Rust translation — the carry-vs-lookup, owned-vs-interned tradeoff is real and couples to the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone, a Phase 2 decision.
- Spring records file+line via `TextResourceOrigin` at YAML/properties PARSE time using its own parsers; the location is whatever the parser tracked. In Rust, two distinct location sources exist and must not be conflated: RUNTIME parse locations (config-data's file parser tracking line/column — the dominant case) vs COMPILE-TIME `proc_macro::Span` locations (stable 1.88: line/column/file/source_text) for inline `#[value("${...}")]` literals in source code. The `Origin` type must represent BOTH a runtime-parsed file location AND a compile-time source-code location — Spring only has the former because config is never compiled in; leaf's macro-driven value-injection introduces a second altitude of 'where' that has no Spring analogue.
- Spring's `null`-means-absent (a fell-through source contributes no value AND no origin) interacts with origin tracking: only the WINNING source's origin is attached, and an absent source provably contributes nothing. Rust's `Option<PropertyValue>` models this sharply (None = no value = no origin), which is cleaner than Java — BUT leaf must state the contract loudly: a `Some(PropertyValue{raw:"", origin})` is a PRESENT empty value WITH a real origin that wins; 'set-to-empty in application.yaml:12' is distinct from 'unset' and the origin must survive to say so. The never-blend short-circuit returning the whole value (origin included) is what makes single-traceable-origin a type-level guarantee rather than a convention.
- Spring chains origins implicitly via heap references (`OriginTrackedValue` whose value came from another tracked value); GC handles the graph. Rust's `Derived` chaining for placeholder expansion (`${a}`→`${b}`) collides with ownership: a recursive `Box<Origin>` (R1) allocates per link and needs a depth bound; a flat `Option<OriginId>` index (R2) needs the table; on-demand reconstruction (R3) needs a recorded trail the lean value didn't keep. The 'full causal chain' charter-#9 wants for diagnostics has a concrete heap/representation cost in Rust that Spring's GC hides — and it couples to property-resolution's recursion-depth guard.
- Spring's `OriginLookup<String>` lets a source LAZILY answer 'where is key K' at any time on the JVM, where re-reading a parsed structure mid-diagnostic is free and the source object is always alive (GC). leaf's async-first + hot-path-no-block discipline plus explicit ownership means: lazy lookup (R3) requires the source to stay in the sealed stack AND keep its key→location index in memory (no GC to keep a dropped parser tree alive), and `origin_of` must be synchronous/non-blocking — so a source whose location data is remote/async cannot lazily fetch it mid-diagnostic; it must have materialized the index during a cold pre-step. What Spring gets 'for free' lazily, leaf must decide to PAY FOR at load (R1/R2) or constrain to in-memory-already (R3).
- Spring's origin is type-erased provenance attached uniformly regardless of source type (`PropertySourceOrigin` for any source, `TextResourceOrigin` for text). Rust's origin-agnostic guardrail pushes the same way — `Origin` must NOT leak the source's concrete backing type — but the FINE-origin capability is genuinely heterogeneous (text sources have line/column; env vars/random.*/programmatic maps do not). This forces an explicit two-altitude `Origin` (coarse always, fine optional) rather than Spring's single `Origin` interface with subtypes; the optionality of the fine altitude must be modeled as data (an `Option<TextLocation>`), not as a downcast, to stay origin-agnostic for future WASM sources.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — DIRECT BUILD-ON (upstream dependency, already designed): property-sources already fixed the carrier `PropertyValue { raw, origin }` and owns the never-blend / first-source-wins / null-never-overrides invariants. THIS feature defines the `origin` field's TYPE (the two-altitude `Origin`) and the contract that a source stamps an origin on every value. The headline coupling: provenance rides property-sources' never-blend short-circuit UNTOUCHED — because the stack returns the WHOLE winning value, the winning source's origin IS the answer with no extra walk and no merging. R2's `OriginTable` is the natural home for property-sources' 'show the effective flat stack' introspection that property-sources' R2 (persistent layering) flagged as awkward. We do NOT redesign the stack, lookup, or ordering — those are property-sources' completed call.
- **config-data** — PRIMARY PRODUCER of fine origins: config-data loads application/profile files and is the only layer that knows file + line/column at parse time, so it is responsible for stamping `Origin::TextResource{resource, location}` (R1) / interning it (R2) / building the key→location index (R3) as it parses each document. This feature defines the `Origin` shape and the stamping contract; config-data owns the file-format parsing and thus the actual line/column capture. The deterministic precedence order config-data assigns is orthogonal — origin records WHERE a value came from, not its precedence rank (the rank is the stack position).
- **property-resolution** — CONSUMER + chaining producer: property-resolution performs the `${...}` placeholder walk over the stack's first-source-wins lookup; when it EXPANDS a placeholder it produces a derived value whose origin must chain (`Origin::Derived{from, via: PlaceholderExpansion}` in R1 / `derived_from: Option<OriginId>` in R2 / recorded trail in R3) so a diagnostic can say 'value came from ${a} resolved in application.yaml:12'. The `Derived` chaining depth must share property-resolution's recursion-depth guard. property-resolution owns the placeholder grammar and strict/lenient modes; this feature owns how the resulting value's provenance records the expansion.
- **binder** — PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC CONSUMER: binder binds ConfigurationPropertySources onto a Bindable target and is THE place a binding/conversion failure must render provenance ('failed to bind app.timeout: expected Duration, found "xyz" set in application.yaml:14'). binder reads the origin off the winning value (R1: directly; R2: resolves the `OriginId` against the env's `Arc<OriginTable>`; R3: calls `origin_of` on the owning source). This feature must guarantee the origin is available at the binder's error site — which is exactly the indirection cost R2/R3 must pay and R1 avoids. binder owns the bind-method/result-monad and error rendering; this feature owns the provenance the error embeds.
- **config-properties** — DOWNSTREAM DIAGNOSTIC CONSUMER (via binder): @ConfigurationProperties-analogue binding onto a typed POJO/record surfaces validation failures that should name the offending property's origin ('app.pool.size must be > 0; was 0, set in application.yaml:9'). It consumes origin transitively through binder; this feature's job is that the origin survived from load through the never-blend walk to the validation failure point intact and single-traceable.
- **relaxed-binding** — CORRECTNESS COUPLING on key identity: relaxed-binding maps one canonical kebab key to many source-specific forms (UPPER_SNAKE env, camelCase, etc.). For origin tracking this matters most in R3 (lazy lookup): the key a source INDEXED at parse time may differ from the canonical key the consumer queries, so the re-lookup must canonicalize to the UNIFORM form at BOTH index-build and lookup — a coupling R3 must honor. In R1/R2 the origin is captured at load against whatever key the source used, so the form-mismatch is sidestepped. relaxed-binding owns canonicalization; this feature must ensure the origin attaches to the value regardless of which source-specific form matched.
- **environment** — HOST/REACHABILITY (upstream seam): the environment façade holds the sealed property-source stack and (in R2) the frozen `Arc<OriginTable>`; it is the reach point through which diagnostics obtain the table / the live sources for origin resolution. environment owns read/mutate segregation and reachability; this feature relies on its sealed read-view to expose origins (R1: carried in values the env returns; R2: the env hands out the `Arc<OriginTable>`; R3: the env exposes the sealed stack so the owning source can be re-queried). We do not design the seam.
- **value-injection** — COMPILE-TIME ORIGIN CONSUMER: `@Value`-equivalent `${property}` injection resolves through the stack, so an injection failure should name BOTH the runtime config origin (where the value came from) AND the compile-time injection-site origin (which struct field / source line requested it, captured via `proc_macro::Span` line/column/file, stable 1.88). This feature's `Origin` must represent the compile-time source-code altitude (a clash with Spring, which has no compiled-in injection sites) so the diagnostic can say 'injected at MyService::timeout (src/svc.rs:20), value set in application.yaml:14'.
- **container-hierarchy** — PROVENANCE ACROSS THE HIERARCHY: child-wins merge keeps the child's identically-named source, so a value's origin must name the WINNING (child or parent) source correctly. R3 'just works' (ask the source that won, whoever owns it). R1 carries the right origin inline. R2 has the subtle id-space problem: a child env's `OriginTable` must be able to resolve origins minted against the parent (cross-table id-space or re-interning) — the one place hierarchy adds real cost to origin tracking. Honors one-directional visibility: rendering a child value's origin never needs a parent→child back-reference.
- **type-conversion** — ORDERING/PRESERVATION: this feature's value is RAW string + origin; type-conversion coerces the raw string to a typed value at the read/binder seam. The origin must survive the conversion step so a CONVERSION failure can still name where the raw string came from ('expected u16 for server.port, found "-1" at application.yaml:8'). type-conversion owns coercion; this feature ensures provenance is attached to the raw value before any coercion and is available when coercion fails.
- **config-metadata** — COMPLEMENTARY (design-time vs run-time provenance): config-metadata emits compile-time metadata describing ACCEPTED config keys (a self-documenting API surface for tooling); origin tracking answers WHERE an ACTUAL loaded value came from at runtime. Together they make config fully debuggable — metadata says 'app.timeout is a Duration, default 30s, declared in MyProps' and origin says 'the active value was set in application-prod.yaml:5'. No dependency; they meet in tooling/diagnostics (an env-dump that shows both the declared schema and the live origin).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Origin representation framework-wide: owned-inline `Origin` (R1, self-contained, fattens the carrier), interned `OriginId` + side `OriginTable` (R2, lean carrier, table lifetime/id-space coupling), or lazy source-delegated `OriginLookup` (R3, leanest steady-state, source must outlive diagnostics)? This is the same carry-vs-lookup, owned-vs-interned tension property-sources flagged for value representation, and it couples directly to the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone — must be decided ONCE across the whole config model, not per-feature.
- Should provenance be carried on EVERY value (R1/R2, hot-path-present, memory ~O(keys) or O(distinct origins)) or reconstructed ON DEMAND only on the diagnostic path (R3, near-zero steady-state memory, source must keep its key→location index)? This is the same hot-path-memory-vs-diagnostic-latency tradeoff property-sources raised for origin; it must be settled against actual diagnostic frequency and whether production builds want origins at all (a build-time 'strip origins in release' lever is a candidate).
- Two altitudes of 'where' with no single Spring analogue: how does `Origin` unify a RUNTIME parsed file location (config-data) with a COMPILE-TIME `proc_macro::Span` source-code location (value-injection sites)? Both feed diagnostics; the unified `Origin` type and the macro→runtime hand-off of compile-time spans is a cross-cutting decision spanning value-injection, the macro/codegen-boundary keystone, and the unified-diagnostics model.
- The causal-chain cost: how rich should `Derived` provenance be (placeholder expansion, source-of-a-source), and where is its depth bound shared with property-resolution's recursion guard? Recursive `Box` (R1), flat index links (R2), or recorded trail (R3) all have different heap costs the GC hid in Spring — the 'full causal chain' charter-#9 ambition must be priced against representation, coordinated with property-resolution and the unified-diagnostics model.
- Does origin attachment reuse the SAME cross-crate source-contributor substrate as property-sources/config-data (link-time `linkme` 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath', DCE/zero-contribution guardrails), and does a cross-crate source need to be HANDED a capability (R2's `OriginTable` handle) to stamp origins — i.e. how is the origin-stamping capability scoped without becoming an ambient global? This shares the unresolved cross-crate composition keystone with property-sources, environment, and component-scanning; do NOT invent a bespoke origin registry.
- How do origins compose across `container-hierarchy`: a child env resolving a child-won value's origin (R1 carries it; R3 asks the winning source) vs R2's need for a child `OriginTable` to resolve parent-minted `OriginId`s (cross-table id-space or re-interning)? The hierarchy origin-resolution rule must align with the scope/lifetime/ownership decision and container-hierarchy's one-directional visibility, and is the one place hierarchy adds non-trivial cost to provenance.
- Where does the async pre-step live that materializes a remote/async-backed source's origin data (its key→location index, R3) or interned origins (R2) into in-memory form BEFORE the source joins the synchronous-read stack? This is the same async-fetch→snapshot→sync-add pipeline (BootstrapContext analogue) property-sources and environment flagged for sources/customizers — origin data must ride the same pipeline since `origin_of`/resolution must be non-blocking.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated origin-tracking strictly as PROVENANCE MECHANICS layered on the ALREADY-DESIGNED property-sources carrier `PropertyValue { raw, origin }` — namely the `Origin` type (two altitudes: coarse owning-source + optional fine file/line/column, origin-agnostic across native/file/env/WASM), the contract for HOW a source attaches an origin per value, the rule that provenance rides the never-blend short-circuit UNMODIFIED (winning source's origin, never merged), `Derived` chaining for placeholder expansion, and the rendering/introspection surface. I deliberately did NOT redesign: the property-source stack/lookup/never-blend invariants (property-sources, complete), file-format parsing + precedence order (config-data, which is the actual fine-origin PRODUCER), the `${...}` engine (property-resolution), binding-error rendering (binder/config-properties), key canonicalization (relaxed-binding), or the env façade/seam (environment). The genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is HOW the origin is represented and carried: R1 = owned inline `Origin` enum on the value (max intent fidelity, self-contained, but fattens the carrier and churns Arc/Box, memory O(keys)); R2 = interned `Copy` `OriginId` + side `Arc<OriginTable>` (leanest carrier, aggressive de-dup memory O(distinct origins), natural env-dump surface, but id-space/staleness/hierarchy-id coupling); R3 = lazy source-delegated `OriginLookup` (the literal `OriginLookup<String>` analogue, near-zero steady-state memory, but source must outlive diagnostics + keep its key→location index, weaker chaining, relaxed-binding re-lookup coupling). All three keep `Origin` origin-agnostic (an enum/handle constructed by any source, never leaking the backing type — so future WASM sources slot in), all three model the fine altitude as OPTIONAL DATA (`Option<TextLocation>`) not a downcast, and all three keep the HOT read path allocation-free + lock-free + non-blocking (R1 carries owned data, R2 a `u32`, R3 coarse identity) per charter #4. Charter alignment: hot-path discipline honored in all three; the only Arc is deliberate (R1's shared `ResourceRef`, R2's frozen `Arc<OriginTable>`) and justified per charter #5; no new macro logic beyond thin stamping/`proc_macro::Span` capture per charter #10; intent parity is literal in the `TextResourceOrigin`/`PropertySourceOrigin`/`OriginLookup` shapes while the carry strategy is rust-native (charter #2/#11). Nightly review: NOTHING needs nightly — owned enums, `NonZeroU32` niche-optimized handles, `Arc`, `Vec` arenas, and crucially `proc_macro::Span` location APIs (line/column/file/source_text) are ALL STABLE (1.88) for compile-time injection-site origins; `error_generic_member_access`/Provider was explicitly evaluated and REJECTED (nightly, FCP cancelled) in favor of a bespoke typed origin in the diagnostics struct. The ONE genuinely Rust-specific addition over Spring is the compile-time source-code origin altitude (value-injection sites via `proc_macro::Span`) that Spring lacks because config is never compiled in. The cross-crate touchpoint (which sources stamp origins, and R2's capability-handing of the `OriginTable`) shares the SAME unresolved link-time-registry substrate as property-sources/environment/component-scanning — flagged UNRESOLVED for Phase 2, not reinvented here.

## Relaxed Binding  `[relaxed-binding]`

This feature decouples a property's IDENTITY from each transport's SYNTAX: one canonical key, authored once, is matched against every source-specific form it may appear in (kebab `context-path`, camelCase `contextPath`, snake_case `context_path`, `UPPER_SNAKE` env `CONTEXT_PATH`, and the list/map index conventions env vars and files use). Spring's intent (docs §"Relaxed binding") has FIVE load-bearing parts to replicate as INTENT, not mechanism:

(1) **A canonical name with three comparison Forms.** Spring's `ConfigurationPropertyName` carries `ORIGINAL` (as written), `DASHED` (lowercase alphanumeric + dashes), and `UNIFORM` (lowercase alphanumeric only — `foo-bar`, `foo_bar`, `fooBar` all collapse to `foobar`). Matching happens on the UNIFORM form; that single normalization is the WHOLE reason `first-name`, `firstName`, `first_name`, `FIRSTNAME` collide onto one target. The canonical authoring form is lowercase kebab-case. leaf must replicate the equivalence relation (a normalization to a comparison form) — not necessarily three eager strings.

(2) **The env-var mapping rule (subtle, asymmetric).** Canonical→env: replace dots with underscores, **REMOVE dashes** (NOT convert to `_`), uppercase: `spring.main.log-startup-info` → `SPRING_MAIN_LOGSTARTUPINFO`. Spring's `SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` produces up to **four candidate names** (current + legacy formats × upper/lower) so a single env var can match both `foo.bar-baz` and `foo_bar_baz`. This is shaped by OS env-name restrictions (letters/digits/underscore only) — env vars are the source whose syntax is MOST constrained and therefore the form that drives the design.

(3) **List/map index conventions per transport.** Indexed list elements from env use a numeric index wrapped in underscores (`MY_SERVERS_0`, `MY_SERVERS_1` → `List servers`); in files, `[index]` brackets. Map binding from env **lowercases the env-var NAME (not the value)** — `MY_PROPS_VALUES_KEY=Value` → `{"key": "Value"}` (key lowercased, value case preserved). To preserve an original map key containing dashes/dots/uppercase in files, wrap it in brackets `my.map.[key-with-dashes]=value` — the bracket-escape disables relaxed normalization for that one segment.

(4) **The asymmetric-placeholder gotcha (a hard interaction contract).** Always reference the canonical kebab form in `${...}`: `${demo.item-price}` resolves via relaxed lookup across `.properties` and env, but `${demo.itemPrice}` will NOT pick up `demo.item-price`.
