Relaxed lookup only fully works *from* the canonical form — i.e. the placeholder engine must canonicalize a placeholder's KEY before lookup, and authoring a non-canonical key in a placeholder is the documented foot-gun.

(5) **Optional env-var namespacing prefix.** `setEnvironmentPrefix("input")` namespaces ONLY system-env vars (`remote.timeout` → `INPUT_REMOTE_TIMEOUT`); it deliberately does NOT prefix system properties or file-based properties — so the prefix is a per-source (env-only) concern, not a global one.

DESIGN INTENT (the why): different transports impose different naming rules (env can't have dots; properties prefer dots; code prefers camelCase). Rather than force users to know which form each source needs, bind them all to one canonical name — name a property once, set it however your platform allows.

SCOPE BOUNDARY (what THIS feature owns vs neighbours): `property-sources` owns the ordered stack + first-source-wins + never-blend LOOKUP PRIMITIVE; `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` placeholder walk + strict/lenient + read interface; `config-properties`/`binder` own the prefix-rooted tree binding onto a typed target; `type-conversion` owns string→T; `origin-tracking` owns provenance. THIS feature owns ONLY the **key-identity layer**: the canonical-form definition + the normalization/equivalence relation (UNIFORM-form matching), the per-transport name-mapping rules (env-var four-candidate rule, dash-removal, list/map index conventions, the bracket-escape), and the contract that a relaxed `get(canonical)` consults a source's many syntactic forms. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: WHERE canonicalization lives (an eager canonical-name value type vs source-side mappers that expand a canonical query into candidate concrete keys vs a normalized index/trie over enumerable sources), and HOW it slots between the stack's `get(key)` and the resolver/binder without re-deciding ordering or never-blend.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Canonical name value type with a uniform comparison form (the literal ConfigurationPropertyName transcription)
Model relaxed binding as a first-class KEY value type — leaf's `ConfigPropertyName` — that owns the equivalence relation, exactly as Spring's `ConfigurationPropertyName` does. A canonical kebab key is parsed once into an immutable, segmented name; matching is defined on a derived UNIFORM form.

```rust
pub struct ConfigPropertyName { segments: Box<[Segment]> }            // parsed canonical name
enum Segment { Named(Box<str>), Indexed(u32), MapKey(Box<str> /*bracket-escaped, literal*/) }
impl ConfigPropertyName {
    pub fn parse(canonical: &str) -> Result<Self, NameSyntaxError>;    // validates kebab canonical form
    pub fn uniform(&self) -> UniformName<'_>;                          // borrowed lowercase-alnum-only view per segment
    pub fn matches(&self, candidate: &str) -> bool;                    // normalize candidate, compare segment-wise on uniform form
}
// A source-agnostic equivalence: two raw keys are 'the same property' iff their uniform forms are equal segment-by-segment.
pub fn uniform_eq(a: &str, b: &str) -> bool;                          // foo-bar == foo_bar == fooBar == FOOBAR
```
Normalization is a `const fn`-friendly char fold: lowercase, drop every non-alphanumeric separator EXCEPT inside a bracket-escaped `[..]` segment (which is preserved verbatim, matching Spring's literal-map-key escape). A relaxed lookup is `RelaxedGet`: given a canonical `ConfigPropertyName`, ask each source in stack order whether it contains a key whose uniform form equals the canonical's — the source answers `get_relaxed(&name) -> Option<RawValue>`. For a NON-enumerable source (raw env, where you cannot list keys) the name produces its **candidate concrete forms** to probe directly: the env mapper emits the up-to-four candidates (`FOO_BARBAZ` dash-removed + `FOO_BAR_BAZ` legacy, each upper/lower), list/map index forms (`MY_SERVERS_0`). For an ENUMERABLE source (a parsed `.properties`/file map) the source can normalize-and-compare its own keys. The canonical name is the SINGLE source of truth; every transport derives its probes/comparisons from it. The asymmetric-placeholder contract is honored by construction: `property-resolution` hands the placeholder KEY through `ConfigPropertyName::parse` before lookup, so a non-canonical placeholder simply fails to canonicalize the same way (the documented gotcha is preserved as intent).

**Pros:** Most literal intent parity: a `ConfigPropertyName` with a uniform comparison form is a line-for-line transcription of Spring's `ConfigurationPropertyName`/Forms; a Spring developer recognizes the exact equivalence (`first-name`==`firstName`==`FIRSTNAME`), and the kebab-canonical authoring rule is identical (charter #1 DX, #2 intent-shape).; ONE source of truth for identity — the canonical name — from which env candidates, file comparisons, and list/map index forms all derive, so the asymmetric-placeholder gotcha and the bracket-escape fall out naturally rather than being special-cased per consumer (charter #11 unification of the key model).; Normalization is a pure `const fn`-style char fold over already-materialized strings: no allocation on the borrowed `uniform()` fast path, stack-friendly, lock-free, synchronous (charter #4 hot path, #5 memory).; `Segment` enum makes list-index and bracket-escaped-literal-map-key STRUCTURAL, so the file `[index]`/`[key-with-dashes]` and env `_0_` conventions are represented in the name type itself, not smeared across string hacks (charter #9 legible model, easier to test).; Origin-agnostic: a source only needs to answer `get_relaxed(&ConfigPropertyName)` (or expose enumerable keys for self-normalization) — native, file, or a future WASM-module source implements the same tiny seam; the relaxed layer never assumes how a source is backed.

**Cons:** A canonical name that probes a non-enumerable env source by emitting up to four candidate strings per segment-combination risks combinatorial probe counts for deeply nested names (each segment independently dash-removed vs underscored) — must bound/short-circuit the candidate set (Spring caps at four whole-name candidates, not a cartesian product), a correctness subtlety that is easy to get wrong.; Two lookup paths (enumerable source self-normalizes its keys; non-enumerable env source is probed by generated candidates) means the equivalence relation lives in TWO places (the source's normalize-compare and the name's candidate-generator) that must stay in lockstep, or `${demo.item-price}` could match in files but miss in env — exactly Spring's asymmetry, but now a maintenance hazard rather than a deliberate doc note.; Parsing every canonical key into a segmented `Box<[Segment]>` allocates per distinct name; for a binder walking hundreds of leaf keys under a prefix this is real heap churn unless names are interned/cached (charter #5) — pushes toward a name cache, which is extra machinery.; The `uniform_eq` free function is tempting to call ad hoc from neighbours (resolver, binder), which would scatter the normalization rule; discipline is needed to route ALL identity questions through `ConfigPropertyName` so the rule has one owner.; Bracket-escape semantics (preserve a segment verbatim, disabling normalization) is a parser special-case that interacts with the placeholder engine and the binder's map handling — the boundary of who strips/keeps brackets must be pinned, or a literal map key with dashes round-trips wrong.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `ConfigPropertyName` value type with segments + a derived UNIFORM comparison form (literal Spring transcription); `const fn` char-fold normalization (lowercase, drop non-alnum separators) producing a borrowed `UniformName` view; no eager three-string ORIGINAL/DASHED/UNIFORM materialization; candidate-form generation for non-enumerable sources (env four-candidate rule: dash-removed + legacy-underscore, upper/lower) vs self-normalization for enumerable sources; `Segment` enum encoding Named / Indexed(u32) / bracket-escaped literal MapKey to model list/map conventions structurally; optional name interning/cache to amortize per-key parse for the binder's many-leaf-key walk (a memory-vs-recompute tension, surfaced not resolved); stable-only: enums, `Box<[T]>`, `Cow`, `Result`, `const fn` folds; synchronous so no async-trait machinery on the identity layer

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** `ConfigPropertyName`, the normalization fold, and the `get_relaxed` source seam are kernel types in `leaf-core`, named by absolute path; the relaxed layer needs NO cross-crate registration for its CORE behavior — it is a pure transformation between a canonical name and a source's keys, and ships fully self-contained. Cross-crate enters ONLY through one OPTIONAL extension point, carrying the static-link-registry-plus-optional-dynamic-directory duality as CANDIDATES (not decisions): a pluggable **PropertyMapper / name-mapping policy** — an integration that introduces a new transport with its own naming rule (e.g. a future secrets store using a different separator, or a platform with a legacy env convention) would contribute a `const NameMapperDescriptor { applies_to_source_kind, canonical_to_candidates_fn, candidate_to_uniform_fn }`. These would be discovered (CANDIDATE) as a link-time `linkme` distributed-slice of const descriptors (the default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned mapper set (the WASM-module 'classpath'); DCE guardrails apply exactly as for component scanning (const descriptors, runtime selection, force-link of opted-in crates, a zero-contribution self-check warning when a mapper-providing crate yields nothing). CRITICAL: mapper SELECTION must come from descriptor DATA (which source-kind it applies to), never link/section order. By default leaf ships the two stock mappers (default kebab/dotted + system-env) and is otherwise cross-crate-inert. Generics caveat: mappers are concrete `const` fn-pointer descriptors (no generic monomorphization-registration hazard).

**T2 — execution context:** The whole identity layer runs on the **synchronous, non-blocking read path** — both cold (bootstrap: canonicalizing a placeholder key in a config-data location, binding a config tree at startup) and hot (steady-state relaxed reads). Normalization and candidate-generation are pure CPU over already-materialized strings; `get_relaxed` MUST NOT `.await` or block (charter #4) — any source whose backing is remote/async must have been snapshotted into the stack BEFORE the relaxed layer probes it (discipline inherited from `property-sources`). Errors are local, rich, synchronous values, never panics: `NameSyntaxError { input, span, reason: NonKebabCanonical|EmptySegment|UnclosedBracket }` at parse time (charter #9, earliest legible), and the lookup itself returns `Option` (relaxed-miss is absence, falling through the stack — NOT an error here; strict/lenient is the resolver's call, not this feature's). No cancellation concern (bounded pure CPU: bounded by name length × bounded candidate count). `ConfigPropertyName` is immutable + `Send + Sync`, so a parsed name can be cached on a bean/binding and crossed across `.await`/threads freely; the `get_relaxed` source borrow lives only for the call.

#### R2 — Source-side relaxed mappers: each transport translates a canonical query into its own candidate keys (the PropertyMapper direction)
Invert R1's centre of gravity: instead of a rich name type that consumers compare against, push the relaxed knowledge INTO each source as a `RelaxedMapper`, mirroring Spring's `SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` / `DefaultPropertyMapper` split. A source is a thin key/value backing; a mapper wraps it and knows how to turn one canonical query into the concrete keys THAT source actually uses.

```rust
pub trait RelaxedMapper {
    // canonical -> the concrete key forms to probe in THIS source's syntax (ordered, first-hit wins)
    fn candidates(&self, canonical: &CanonicalKey) -> CandidateForms;   // SmallVec of &str/Cow, bounded
    // for diagnostics / reverse: which canonical does a raw source key map to?
    fn to_canonical(&self, raw_key: &str) -> Option<CanonicalKey>;
}
struct DottedKebabMapper;   // files/properties: dots+kebab canonical, accepts camel/snake via uniform compare
struct SystemEnvMapper { prefix: Option<Box<str>> }   // env: dots->_ , REMOVE dashes, uppercase, 4 candidates, _N_ list, lc map-name
// The stack's relaxed get composes mapper + source:
fn relaxed_get(stack: &PropertySourceStack, key: &CanonicalKey) -> Option<RawValue> {
    for entry in stack.iter() {                 // first-source-wins (inherited, NOT re-decided)
        for cand in entry.mapper.candidates(key) {        // bounded candidate list, in priority order
            if let Some(v) = entry.source.get(cand) { return Some(v); }
        }
    }
    None
}
```
The `CanonicalKey` is a thin parsed kebab name (lighter than R1's full Segment model — it need only expose its parts to mappers). Each source declares its mapper at registration; the env mapper owns the four-candidate rule, dash-removal, the optional env-only prefix, and the `_0_` list / lowercase-map-name conventions; the file mapper owns `[index]`/`[bracket-escape]` and accepts camel/snake by normalizing-comparing its own enumerable keys. The asymmetric-placeholder contract is honored because mappers expand FROM the canonical form: a non-canonical placeholder key, fed in, generates the wrong candidates for env (so it misses) — preserving the documented gotcha precisely. Spring's reality maps directly: `PropertyMapper` is per-source, and `SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` vs `DefaultPropertyMapper` is exactly this `RelaxedMapper` split.

**Pros:** Direct transcription of Spring's actual architecture (per-source `PropertyMapper`, with `SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` the special one) — the env four-candidate rule, dash-removal, and prefix live in ONE place (the env mapper) where they belong, instead of leaking into a central name type (charter #2 intent-shape, #11 the mapper is the reusable primitive).; Cleanly origin-agnostic and EXTENSIBLE by construction: a new transport (secrets store, WASM-provided source, a platform with odd env rules) ships its OWN `RelaxedMapper` and slots in without touching the core — the relaxed rule is a property of the source, which is exactly where transport-specific syntax knowledge should live (charter #6 pluggable, origin-agnostic provider requirement).; Per-source prefix (env-only namespacing) is natural: it's a field on `SystemEnvMapper`, not a global concern — matching Spring's intent that the prefix touches ONLY system-env, never files/properties.; Bounded candidate generation is local and auditable per mapper (env caps at four whole-name forms; file mapper compares uniform-normalized enumerable keys), making the combinatorial-probe hazard of R1 a per-mapper contract that each mapper enforces and tests in isolation.; First-source-wins is preserved untouched — the relaxed layer only changes WHICH keys a source is probed with, never the stack order or never-blend (clean separation from `property-sources`).

**Cons:** The relaxed equivalence is now distributed across N mappers; ensuring `foo-bar`==`fooBar`==`FOO_BAR` consistently across the file mapper AND the env mapper AND any third-party mapper is a cross-implementation invariant with no single enforcer — divergence is silent and source-specific (the same asymmetry Spring has, now multiplied by extensibility).; `trait RelaxedMapper` introduces dynamic dispatch (`entry.mapper: &dyn RelaxedMapper`) on a path R1/R3 can keep monomorphic for the stock cases — a hot-path indirection that must be justified by the extensibility win (charter #5); stock sources could use a static enum dispatch to avoid it, adding a fast-path/slow-path split.; `candidates()` returning an ordered list that the stack probes one-by-one against `source.get` turns one logical lookup into up-to-four physical `get`s per source per stack level — fine for a hashmap-backed source, but a per-`get` cost multiplier that R3's pre-normalized index avoids.; A reverse `to_canonical` (needed for diagnostics, `config-metadata`, and 'list all keys' tooling) is awkward for non-enumerable env sources (you cannot enumerate the OS environment's relation to canonical names cheaply) — so the reverse direction is partial, a real gap for the discoverability/diagnostics story.; More moving parts than R1 for the 95% case (two stock mappers behind a trait) — risks over-abstracting when most apps only ever use files + env (charter #2 don't build mechanism for its own sake), unless the trait is justified purely by the third-party-transport extension goal.

**Mechanisms considered:** per-source `RelaxedMapper` trait (Spring `PropertyMapper`) with `candidates(canonical)->bounded forms` + `to_canonical(raw)` reverse; stock `DottedKebabMapper` (files: uniform-compare enumerable keys) + `SystemEnvMapper` (env: 4-candidate, dash-removal, prefix, `_N_` list, lowercase map-name) — the `DefaultPropertyMapper`/`SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` split; static enum dispatch for stock mappers + `dyn RelaxedMapper` only for third-party transports (fast-path/slow-path to avoid gratuitous dynamic dispatch on the hot path); `SmallVec`/`Cow` bounded candidate list probed in priority order against the source's plain `get` (preserving first-source-wins); per-mapper config (env-only prefix as a field on `SystemEnvMapper`) rather than a global prefix; stable-only: object-safe trait, enum dispatch, `SmallVec`, `Cow`; synchronous mappers (no blocking/await in `candidates`)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the MOST cross-crate-relevant realization because `RelaxedMapper` is an explicit extension point: a transport integration (e.g. a secrets-backend crate, or a platform-specific env convention) CONTRIBUTES a mapper across crates. It inherits the full static-link-registry-vs-build-codegen duality as a CANDIDATE: a default link-time `linkme` distributed-slice of `const MapperDescriptor { source_kind, ctor_fn -> Box<dyn RelaxedMapper> }` (the default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned mapper set (the WASM-module 'classpath'). DCE guardrails are important here (a silently-missing mapper means a whole source's keys stop resolving relaxed-style): const descriptors, runtime SELECTION keyed by source-kind DATA (never link/section order), force-link of opted-in transport crates, and a zero-contribution self-check that loudly warns when a transport crate registered no mapper. The two stock mappers (DottedKebab + SystemEnv) ship in `leaf-core` and are NOT cross-crate-discovered — they are always present — so the discovery substrate is only exercised by third-party transports, keeping the common case inert. `RelaxedMapper` being origin-agnostic is the explicit point: a native file source, a system-env source, and a future WASM-module source each ship a mapper through the identical seam. Shares the SAME discovery substrate question as `property-sources` (which discovers source kinds) — flagged as a Phase-2 unification opportunity, not decided.

**T2 — execution context:** All mapper work runs on the synchronous, non-blocking read path (cold during bootstrap config-data/profile/location resolution, hot during steady-state relaxed reads). `RelaxedMapper::candidates` and `to_canonical` are pure CPU, MUST NOT block or `.await` (charter #4): a source backed by a remote secrets service is FORBIDDEN to fetch in `candidates`/`get` — it must have been materialized into an in-memory snapshot during a cold async pre-step before its mapper joins the stack (the BootstrapContext discipline, same as `property-sources`/`property-resolution`). Errors are synchronous rich values; a relaxed miss is `None` (fall-through, not an error). Cancellation: none on the read path (bounded pure CPU; any async pre-materialization of a source's backing is a separate cold async step with its own cancellation, BEFORE mapping). Mappers are `Send + Sync` when their (snapshotted) backing is, so a relaxed stack view can cross `.await`/threads as long as the borrowed stack outlives it — stack reachability remains the `environment` neighbour's concern, not this feature's. The dynamic-dispatch `dyn RelaxedMapper` is the one place an indirection enters the hot path; stock sources use static dispatch to keep it off the common path.

#### R3 — Pre-normalized relaxed index over enumerable sources (build a uniform-keyed lookup table once)
For sources that CAN be enumerated (parsed files, an env snapshot, a JSON blob), trade a little startup work for O(1) relaxed reads: when the source is materialized, build a `RelaxedIndex` keyed by the UNIFORM form, so a canonical query is one normalize-then-hashmap-hit, no per-read candidate generation.

```rust
pub struct RelaxedIndex {
    // uniform-form hash -> (original_raw_key, value-ref or origin); collisions are a hard, reported error
    by_uniform: HashMap<UniformKey, IndexedEntry>,
}
struct UniformKey(Box<str>);   // e.g. 'foo.barbaz' segment-joined uniform form (alnum-only per segment)
impl RelaxedIndex {
    pub fn build(raw_pairs: impl Iterator<Item=(RawKey, RawValue, Origin)>) -> Result<Self, RelaxedCollision>;
    pub fn get(&self, canonical: &CanonicalKey) -> Option<&IndexedEntry>;   // normalize canonical -> uniform -> hashmap
}
```
Each enumerable source is wrapped once at materialization into a `RelaxedIndex`; `relaxed_get` over the stack becomes: normalize the canonical to its uniform form ONCE, then for each source in stack order do a single hashmap lookup (first-source-wins preserved). **Collision detection is first-class**: if one source contains BOTH `first-name` and `firstName` (which collapse to the same uniform key), that is a genuine ambiguity Spring tolerates last-write-style but leaf can surface as a rich `RelaxedCollision { uniform, raw_keys: [..], origins: [..] }` (charter #9 — a silent collapse is exactly the kind of foot-gun the charter wants caught early, ideally at a startup validation pass). The env case is handled by FIRST projecting the (non-enumerable in general, but on most platforms enumerable) env map into uniform keys using the env rule (dots/underscores collapse, dashes already gone), so `SPRING_MAIN_LOGSTARTUPINFO` and `spring.main.log-startup-info` land on the same uniform key. List/map index forms are normalized into the uniform key (`MY_SERVERS_0` → `myservers[0]` uniform), and bracket-escaped literal map keys are stored UN-normalized (preserved). This is the most read-optimized realization, at the cost of an eager index build and a memory footprint per source.

**Pros:** Fastest steady-state relaxed read: one normalize + one hashmap hit per source, no per-read candidate fan-out (R1/R2 both probe multiple candidate strings per source per read) — the strongest hot-path story (charter #4) when the same keys are read repeatedly (binder walking a prefix, `@Value` re-reads).; Makes the relaxed COLLISION (`first-name` AND `firstName` in one source collapsing to one identity) a first-class, detectable, richly-reported condition at index-build time rather than a silent last-wins — turning Spring's quiet tolerance into the early, complete diagnostic the charter wants (#9), ideally surfaced in a startup validation pass.; The uniform key is computed ONCE per source key at build time, so the normalization rule executes at materialization (cold) not per-read (hot) — amortizes the fold and naturally interns the keys, avoiding R1's per-name parse churn on the read path (charter #5).; 'List all accepted keys / reverse-map a raw key to canonical' for `config-metadata`/diagnostics tooling is trivial — the index already holds the raw key alongside the uniform key and origin, giving the discoverability story R2 struggles with for env.; First-source-wins and never-blend are preserved exactly: the index changes only intra-source lookup (uniform-keyed), the stack walk and ordering are untouched (clean separation from `property-sources`).

**Cons:** Requires the source to be ENUMERABLE to index; a genuinely non-enumerable source (a live, unlistable backing) cannot be pre-indexed and must fall back to R1/R2-style candidate probing — so R3 is not universal and needs a hybrid path, splitting the design (most env sources ARE enumerable on real platforms, but the abstraction must not assume it).; Eager index build per source costs startup time and a `HashMap` per source of memory (charter #5) — proportional to total key count; for a huge env / large config tree this is a real footprint that R1/R2 (which compute lazily) avoid. The trade only pays off if keys are read more than ~once.; Collision detection forces a policy decision leaf cannot dodge: is `first-name` + `firstName` in one source a HARD build error, a warning, or last-wins-with-diagnostic? Spring tolerates it; the charter pushes toward catching it — but making it a hard error could break configs that work in Spring (a parity-vs-safety tension this feature surfaces but must not resolve here).; Index invalidation if a source is mutable/refreshable (a hot-reloaded file, a dynamic source) — the pre-built index must be rebuilt on change, adding a refresh hook and a staleness concern that the lazy R1/R2 designs don't have (couples to any future config-refresh feature).; The env-rule projection into uniform keys must replicate the SAME asymmetry as the lazy path (dash-removal, four-candidate equivalence) at build time, or `${demo.item-price}` resolves differently through the index than through a fallback probe — the equivalence rule still has to be perfectly shared between the index builder and any non-enumerable fallback.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `RelaxedIndex` (HashMap keyed by segment-joined UNIFORM form) built once per enumerable source at materialization; O(1) relaxed read after; first-class relaxed-COLLISION detection at build time (`RelaxedCollision{ uniform, raw_keys, origins }`) — turning Spring's silent collapse into an early rich diagnostic / startup-validation-pass candidate; uniform-key interning at build time (amortizes the normalization fold off the read path; avoids per-name parse churn); hybrid fallback: enumerable sources use the index, genuinely non-enumerable sources fall back to candidate-probing (R1/R2 style) — same equivalence rule shared; env-rule projection (dots/underscores collapse, dashes-already-gone, `_N_`->[index], bracket-escape preserved) applied at index build so env and file land on the same uniform key; stable-only: `HashMap`, `Box<str>`, `Result`, const-fn normalization; build is synchronous; a refresh hook for mutable sources (cold path, polling-allowed per charter #4)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The `RelaxedIndex`, `UniformKey`, and normalization live in `leaf-core`; like R1 the CORE relaxed-index behavior needs NO cross-crate registration — it is a transformation applied to whatever (key,value) pairs an enumerable source yields, so it is origin-agnostic by construction (a native file source, an env snapshot, or a WASM-module-provided source all hand the indexer an iterator of pairs). Cross-crate touches only the OPTIONAL custom-name-mapping policy (same as R1/R2): if a third-party transport needs a different normalization/candidate rule, it would contribute a `const NormalizerDescriptor`/`MapperDescriptor` discovered via the SAME candidate substrate — link-time `linkme` slice (default 'classpath') PLUS optional dynamic directory-scanned set (WASM 'classpath'), selection by source-kind DATA, with DCE guardrails + a zero-contribution self-check. The non-enumerable fallback path reuses R1/R2's candidate generation, so the cross-crate surface is identical. A distinctive T1 nuance: because the index is built at the FINAL point where a source is materialized (often the binary/bootstrap, the only place that sees the whole resolved config), the build-time collision self-check naturally lives where whole-graph visibility exists — consistent with the cross-crate doc's 'anchor whole-graph awareness at the final binary' guidance. No generic-registration hazard (the index is data, not a registered generic type).

**T2 — execution context:** Index BUILD runs on a COLD path (synchronous CPU at source materialization / bootstrap; for a mutable source, on an explicit refresh — a cold/background path where polling is permitted per charter #4). Index READ runs on the synchronous, non-blocking hot path: normalize canonical once + a hashmap hit per source, no `.await`, no blocking (charter #4). Any source whose backing is remote/async must be fetched-and-snapshotted in a cold async pre-step BEFORE its pairs are indexed (BootstrapContext discipline, shared with `property-sources`/`property-resolution`) — the indexer only ever sees already-materialized in-memory pairs. Errors are synchronous rich values: `RelaxedCollision { uniform, raw_keys, origins }` at build time (charter #9, earliest legible — a strong startup-validation-pass candidate that lists EVERY collision at once), and a relaxed-miss is `None` at read time (fall-through, not an error). Cancellation: none on the read path; an async pre-materialization step (separate, cold) carries its own cancellation. A refresh/rebuild on a mutable source is a cold, cancellable background task — never on the hot read path. The built `RelaxedIndex` is immutable + `Send + Sync` (for an immutable source), so it can be shared across tasks/threads behind the stack's reachability handle (the `environment` neighbour's concern); a mutable/refreshable index needs a swap discipline (e.g. arc-swap-style atomic replace) that is a Phase-2 concurrency call, flagged not decided.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `ConfigurationPropertyName` leans on JVM string handling and GC'd intermediate Forms; it freely materializes ORIGINAL/DASHED/UNIFORM and tolerates per-lookup allocation. In Rust, eagerly materializing three normalized strings per name is gratuitous heap churn (charter #5) — leaf wants a borrowed `UniformName` view / `const fn` fold computed on demand, or an interned uniform key built once. The clash: faithful Form-transcription (R1) vs Rust's pressure to compute-once-and-borrow (R3's interned index). No free lunch — lazy folds re-compute on the hot path, eager indexes cost memory + a build step.
- Spring's relaxed equivalence SILENTLY collapses `first-name`, `firstName`, `FIRSTNAME` onto one identity and, if a single source defines two of them, quietly resolves one (last/precedence-wins). Rust's charter #9 (fail with rich, complete context, as early as the richest diagnostic allows) is in direct TENSION with silent collapse: leaf CAN detect the collision (R3 does so at index-build) and surface `RelaxedCollision{ raw_keys, origins }` — but making it a hard error risks rejecting a config that works in Spring (intent parity #2). Whether the relaxed collision is a hard error, a startup-validation-pass warning, or last-wins-with-diagnostic is an intent-vs-safety tension this feature exposes but must not resolve.
- Spring's env-var rule produces up-to-four CANDIDATE names and probes them; this is an asymmetric, lossy mapping (dashes are REMOVED, not encoded, so `foo-bar` and `foobar` and `foo.bar` can all collide via env). In Rust this asymmetry must be made explicit and BOUNDED: a naive per-segment candidate cartesian product explodes; leaf must cap candidate generation (Spring caps at four whole-name forms) — a correctness/robustness decision Spring's JVM never had to bound explicitly, and one that, if the index path (R3) and the probe path (R1/R2) compute it differently, silently breaks the asymmetric-placeholder contract.
- Spring blurs 'property absent' and 'no relaxed match' as the same fall-through (a `null`/None). Rust forces two distinct concepts that must not be conflated: a NameSyntaxError (a non-canonical or malformed canonical key — a programmer error, surfaced early) vs a relaxed MISS (the canonical key is well-formed but no source's uniform form matches — ordinary absence, falls through the stack). Conflating them would either swallow malformed-key bugs or turn ordinary absence into errors; leaf must keep parse-error (`Result`) and lookup-miss (`Option`) as separate layers.
- Spring's per-source `PropertyMapper` and `SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper` are dynamically discovered/wired on the JVM. Rust has no classpath: a third-party transport's custom relaxed mapper (R2's extension point) must be discovered via link-time registration (DCE-hazardous, silent-empty failure) or build-time codegen, and selection cannot come from link/section order — it must come from descriptor DATA (which source-kind it applies to). A silently-missing mapper means a whole source stops matching relaxed keys with NO error — the same silent-DCE hazard component-scanning faces, here with config-correctness stakes, arguing for ONE shared discovery substrate (a Phase-2 keystone, not this feature's call).
- Spring's bracket-escape `[key-with-dashes]` disables normalization for one segment so a literal map key survives verbatim. In Rust this is a parser special-case whose ownership boundary is unclear: does relaxed-binding strip/keep the brackets, or does the binder's map handler? If both touch it, a literal map key with dashes/dots round-trips wrong. The clash is that one syntactic escape spans this feature (name normalization), the binder (map binding), and property-resolution (placeholder of a bracketed key) — Rust's explicit ownership pushes leaf to pin exactly ONE owner for the escape semantics, which Spring's shared mutable name object never forced.
- Spring can index/scan env lazily and tolerate enumerating `System.getenv()` per lookup on the JVM. leaf's hot-path-no-block discipline and the desire for an O(1) relaxed read (R3) push toward snapshotting + indexing env ONCE at bootstrap — but a non-enumerable or mutable source (a live secrets backing, a hot-reloaded file) breaks the 'index once' assumption and forces a hybrid lazy fallback + a refresh/atomic-swap story. Async-first means any remote-backed source must be pre-materialized in a cold async step before the relaxed layer (index or probe) ever touches it — narrowing what a 'relaxed source' can do at read time and pushing async into the shared BootstrapContext pipeline.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — HARD DEPENDENCY and the layer THIS feature sits directly on top of. property-sources owns the ordered named stack, first-source-wins, and never-blend. THIS feature does NOT re-decide ordering or blending — it changes only WHICH key(s) a given source is consulted with: a relaxed `get(canonical)` either probes a source with the canonical's candidate forms (R1/R2) or hits a pre-built uniform-keyed index over that source (R3), then returns the first source's single match exactly as first-source-wins dictates. The relaxed equivalence must NEVER cause a value to be assembled from multiple sources (never-blend is preserved); it only widens the syntactic forms one source is matched against. Each source may carry a relaxed capability (an enumerable key list to self-normalize, or a mapper) — the seam between this feature and property-sources is 'how is a single source probed/indexed relaxed-style', inheriting the stack walk unchanged.
- **property-resolution** — TIGHT COUPLING at the lookup boundary, and the home of the asymmetric-placeholder contract. property-resolution owns the `${...}` walk and the read interface; at its `stack.get(key)` step it must route the placeholder's KEY through THIS feature's canonicalization before lookup, so `${demo.item-price}` resolves via relaxed matching while `${demo.itemPrice}` does NOT (Spring's documented asymmetry — relaxed lookup only works from the canonical kebab form). This feature provides the canonical-name parse + relaxed `get`; property-resolution decides strict/lenient and owns the placeholder syntax. CRITICAL boundary question (flagged): is the placeholder's key ALWAYS canonicalized (preserving Spring's asymmetry as intent) or does leaf relax that too — a cross-cutting policy call. The two features compose: resolver walks placeholders, relaxed layer answers each key lookup.
- **binder** — PRIMARY CONSUMER. The binder walks a prefix-rooted property tree onto a typed target; every leaf key it seeks is a canonical kebab name resolved through THIS feature's relaxed matching, and the list (`servers[0]`/`MY_SERVERS_0`) and map (lowercase-env-name, `[bracket-escape]` literal key) index conventions are EXACTLY where relaxed binding earns its keep. R1's `Segment` model (Named/Indexed/MapKey) is the natural representation the binder consumes to descend the tree; R3's reverse index gives the binder 'all keys under this prefix' cheaply. Boundary: the binder owns tree descent, collection/map replacement (not deep-merge), and typed-target assembly; this feature owns the per-segment name identity + index conventions + the bracket-escape. The bracket-escape ownership (this feature vs binder map handler) is a flagged tension.
- **config-properties** — DOWNSTREAM consumer via the binder. A `#[config_properties(prefix="my.main-project.person")]`-style typed config object roots a kebab prefix; each field name (`first_name` in Rust) maps to a canonical kebab leaf (`first-name`) that relaxed binding matches across camel/snake/UPPER_SNAKE/env forms — so a Rust struct field can be populated from `FIRST_NAME` env, `firstName` JSON, or `first-name` file transparently. This feature defines how the field's canonical name is derived (the kebab canonicalization rule) and matched; config-properties owns the prefix-rooting, validation, and the typed projection. The field-name→canonical-key derivation rule (snake_case Rust idents → kebab canonical) is a small but load-bearing convention this feature must define for config-properties to rely on.
- **type-conversion** — DOWNSTREAM and ORTHOGONAL. Relaxed binding resolves a canonical key to a single raw winning value (one source, never blended); type-conversion THEN coerces that raw string to the target type. The two are independent: identity-matching (this feature) happens entirely before coercion. One subtle touchpoint: the env list convention (`MY_SERVERS_0`, `MY_SERVERS_1`) produces multiple raw leaves that the binder + type-conversion assemble into a `Vec`; this feature only establishes that those indexed env keys map to the canonical `servers[0]`, `servers[1]` identities — the collection assembly and element coercion belong to binder + type-conversion.
- **origin-tracking** — COMPLEMENTARY. Every relaxed match returns the winning source's provenance (raw key actually matched + source/file+line), and relaxed binding ADDS a provenance subtlety origin-tracking must represent: the canonical key the user authored (`demo.item-price`) may differ from the RAW key that matched (`DEMO_ITEMPRICE` env). A complete diagnostic should report BOTH ('canonical demo.item-price matched env var DEMO_ITEMPRICE') — so the resolved value's origin should carry the matched raw key alongside the canonical. R3's index naturally stores both (raw key + uniform key + origin); R1/R2 must thread the matched candidate back. This feeds origin-tracking's 'why is this value X' story with the extra relaxed hop.
- **profiles** — CONSUMER. The active-profiles key (leaf's `spring.profiles.active` analogue) is read relaxed: `SPRING_PROFILES_ACTIVE` env binds to the same canonical identity as `spring.profiles.active` in a file (Spring's documented relaxed-binding equivalence for the profile activation key). This feature provides the canonicalization that makes the env form and file form land on the same key; profiles owns the activation grammar and levers. Note property-sources' per-source `include` subtlety (not list-merged) is a profiles+property-sources concern, NOT relaxed binding's — this feature only ensures the activation key's many transport forms match one identity.
- **config-data** — COLD-BOOTSTRAP interaction. config-data resolves `${...}` in file LOCATIONS and import directives; those placeholder keys are canonicalized through THIS feature (via property-resolution) before lookup, and config-data contributes the enumerable file sources that R3 would index relaxed-style. The env:/configtree: prefixed sources config-data mounts are themselves relaxed-matched (a configtree directory of files, or an env-derived source, both expose keys this feature normalizes). config-data owns file-format loading + precedence; this feature owns the relaxed identity of the keys those files contribute. Ordering: relaxed indexing/probing happens AFTER config-data materializes a source into the stack.
- **config-metadata** — DISCOVERABILITY consumer. config-metadata emits compile-time metadata describing accepted properties; the canonical kebab form THIS feature defines is the form metadata should advertise (and IDE autocompletion should suggest), since that is the form from which relaxed lookup fully works (the asymmetric-placeholder lesson). R3's reverse index ('list all accepted canonical keys, with the raw forms each source provides') is exactly the data config-metadata + tooling want; R2's per-source `to_canonical` is the weaker reverse story. This feature defines the canonical surface config-metadata documents; config-metadata owns the emission + hint format.
- **environment** — UPSTREAM reachability/handle owner. environment owns the read/mutate seam, who-can-reach the relaxed-aware resolver, and the handle shape (borrowed vs Arc-rooted) + lifetime across `.await`/threads. THIS feature's relaxed `get` is part of the READ view environment exposes; environment decides where a relaxed resolver/index is reachable from and how it crosses execution contexts. environment also owns the optional env-only namespacing PREFIX configuration (Spring's `setEnvironmentPrefix`), which this feature consumes as a per-(env-)source mapper field — environment sets it, this feature applies it only to the system-env source, never files/properties.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Relaxed COLLISION policy: when one source defines two keys that collapse to the same uniform identity (`first-name` AND `firstName`), is that a hard build/startup error, a startup-validation-pass warning (collect all collisions, report once), or last-wins-with-diagnostic? Spring silently tolerates it; charter #9 pushes to catch it; intent-parity #2 warns against rejecting configs that work in Spring. This is one framework-wide policy, cross-cutting binder, config-properties, and the unified diagnostics model — must not be per-source.
- WHERE does canonicalization live — an eager canonical-name value type the consumers compare against (R1), per-source mappers that expand a canonical query into candidate keys (R2, Spring's actual PropertyMapper architecture), or a pre-normalized uniform-keyed index built per enumerable source (R3)? This couples to the type-erasure/registry substrate and the memory/lifetime model (interned uniform keys vs per-read folds vs per-source indexes), and to environment's read-view handle shape. A keystone representation question that biases the binder and resolver, deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- Is a placeholder's key ALWAYS canonicalized before relaxed lookup (faithfully preserving Spring's documented asymmetry that `${demo.itemPrice}` does NOT match `demo.item-price`), or should leaf relax even the placeholder key (safer DX, breaks parity)? Spans property-resolution, value-injection, and this feature; needs ONE owner for the canonicalize-the-placeholder-key decision and the dispatch ordering with the expression engine.
- Who OWNS the bracket-escape `[key-with-dashes]` semantics (disable normalization for one literal segment) — this feature (name normalization), the binder (map binding), or property-resolution (a bracketed key inside `${...}`)? The escape spans three features; Rust's explicit ownership forces exactly one owner, or a literal map key with dashes/dots round-trips wrong. A cross-cutting boundary question, not this feature's unilateral call.
- Does the relaxed name-mapping extension point (R2's third-party `RelaxedMapper`, R1/R3's optional custom normalizer) SHARE one cross-crate discovery substrate with `property-sources` (source-kind discovery), component-scanning, and auto-config — or stay self-contained with only the two stock mappers? This is the charter #11 unification question and the cross-crate-composition keystone (link-time registry + DCE hazard + optional WASM directory source); adopting a shared substrate in Phase 1 would pre-bias the meta-architecture, so it is deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- How is candidate-form generation BOUNDED for the env four-candidate rule across nested/indexed names so it never explodes combinatorially, and is that bound a configurable knob? Spring caps at four whole-name forms on the JVM without thinking about it; leaf must choose an explicit cap and ensure the index path (R3) and the probe path (R1/R2) compute the SAME bounded equivalence, or the asymmetric-placeholder contract silently diverges between paths. A correctness/robustness decision with no Spring precedent.
- For mutable/refreshable sources (hot-reloaded files, dynamic sources), how is a pre-built relaxed index (R3) invalidated/rebuilt and atomically swapped without a hot-path lock (charter #5) — and does that align with whatever config-refresh story leaf adopts? Spans property-sources, environment, and any future config-refresh feature; the atomic-swap/staleness model is a Phase-2 concurrency call, not this feature's.
- Where does the async pre-materialization pipeline live for a relaxed source whose backing is remote/async (a secrets store exposed as a relaxed source), given `candidates`/`get`/index-build MUST be synchronous non-blocking? This is the same BootstrapContext-analogue (async fetch → snapshot → sync relaxed use) that property-sources, property-resolution, and environment already flagged — must align framework-wide, not be re-invented here.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated relaxed-binding strictly as the KEY-IDENTITY layer that sits between the `property-sources` first-source-wins stack (upstream, not reinvented) and its consumers (`property-resolution`, `binder`, `config-properties`). This feature owns ONLY: the canonical kebab-case form definition; the normalization/equivalence relation (Spring's UNIFORM-form matching — `foo-bar`==`foo_bar`==`fooBar`==`FOOBAR`); the per-transport name-mapping rules (the env-var four-candidate rule with dash-REMOVAL + uppercase + optional env-only prefix; the `_N_`/`[index]` list conventions; the lowercase-env-map-name + `[bracket-escape]` map conventions); and the contract that a relaxed `get(canonical)` consults a source's many syntactic forms while PRESERVING first-source-wins + never-blend. I deliberately did NOT redesign the stack/ordering/never-blend (property-sources), the `${...}` walk / strict-lenient / read interface (property-resolution), the prefix-rooted tree binding (binder/config-properties), string→T coercion (type-conversion), provenance internals (origin-tracking), profile grammar (profiles), or file-format loading (config-data).

The genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is WHERE canonicalization lives and HOW a source's many forms reconcile to one identity: R1 = a `ConfigPropertyName` value type with a derived UNIFORM comparison form (max intent fidelity to Spring's ConfigurationPropertyName/Forms, one source of truth for identity, const-fn fold, borrowed fast path, but per-name parse churn + a two-path enumerable/non-enumerable split); R2 = per-source `RelaxedMapper`s that expand a canonical query into bounded candidate keys (Spring's ACTUAL PropertyMapper/SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper architecture, cleanest extensibility + per-source prefix, origin-agnostic by construction, but distributes the equivalence rule across N mappers + dynamic dispatch + a per-`get` candidate multiplier + a weak reverse-map for env); R3 = a pre-normalized uniform-keyed `RelaxedIndex` built once per enumerable source (fastest hot read, first-class collision detection turning Spring's silent collapse into an early rich diagnostic, trivial reverse-mapping for tooling, but eager build + memory footprint + an enumerability requirement forcing a hybrid fallback + index-invalidation for mutable sources).

All three: keep relaxed reads SYNCHRONOUS and non-blocking (charter #4 — normalization/candidate-gen/index-hit are pure CPU over already-materialized strings; any remote/async-backed source must be pre-snapshotted in a cold async BootstrapContext step before the relaxed layer touches it); preserve first-source-wins + never-blend untouched (only WIDEN which forms one source matches, never assemble across sources); keep the source seam ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a source answers relaxed-get or yields enumerable pairs — native, file, or future WASM-module source slot in identically, charter #6); encode parse-error (`Result`/`NameSyntaxError`) and relaxed-miss (`Option`, fall-through) as DISTINCT layers; and surface rich diagnostics (NameSyntaxError early, RelaxedCollision at index-build, matched-raw-key threaded into origin) per charter #9. Macros stay thin (charter #10): at most a `#[config_properties]`/field-name macro emitting a call to a hand-writable canonicalization API (snake_case Rust ident → kebab canonical), never the normalization logic itself.

Nightly review (against rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md): nothing needs nightly — const-fn char folds, enums/`Box<[T]>` for a segmented name, `HashMap` for an index, `Cow`/`SmallVec`, object-safe `RelaxedMapper`, `Result`/`Option` are all stable; reads are synchronous so no AFIT/RPITIT boxing tax on the identity layer; `const TypeId`/upcasting are irrelevant here. The cross-crate touchpoint (optional custom `RelaxedMapper`/normalizer for a third-party transport) is OPT-IN — the core ships two stock mappers (default dotted-kebab + system-env) and is otherwise cross-crate-inert — and where present it shares the SAME link-time-registry/DCE substrate concern (linkme default 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath', selection by source-kind DATA, zero-contribution self-check) as component-scanning and as `property-sources`' own source-kind discovery; whether they SHARE one substrate is flagged UNRESOLVED for Phase 2, consistent with Phase 1 staying implementation-agnostic. The sharpest Phase-2-flavored tensions I surfaced but did not resolve: the relaxed-collision policy (silent-tolerate vs early-error vs validation-pass), the bracket-escape ownership across three features, whether the placeholder key is always canonicalized (preserving Spring's asymmetry), and bounding the env candidate fan-out identically across the index and probe paths.

## @ConfigurationProperties Type-Safe Binding  `[config-properties]`

This feature is the DECLARATIVE FRONT-END for type-safe externalized-config binding — Spring's `@ConfigurationProperties` annotation surface that turns a strongly-typed POJO/record rooted at a kebab-case prefix into a cohesive, validated, documented, fail-fast config OBJECT, replacing scattered `@Value`. It is deliberately NOT the binding engine (that is the `binder` neighbour, already designed) nor the key-identity layer (`relaxed-binding`) nor the coercion layer (`type-conversion`) nor the constraint engine (`validation`) — it is the thin opinionated layer that DECLARES a target, ROUTES it into the container as a managed bean, and INVOKES the binder/validation machinery at the right lifecycle moment with the right policy. Spring's intent (docs §"@ConfigurationProperties: type-safe binding", lines 1553-1624) has SEVEN load-bearing parts to replicate as INTENT, not mechanism:\n\n(1) **Prefix-rooted typed-target DECLARATION.** `@ConfigurationProperties(\"my.main-project.person\")` declares that this type's tree binds under a canonical kebab-case prefix; `value()` aliases `prefix()`; the prefix MUST be canonical kebab-case. The Rust-divergent question: how a target carries its prefix + opts into being a config-properties type (an attribute macro emitting a trait impl + a registration descriptor vs an explicit builder registration vs a derive that only carries metadata).\n\n(2) **Two leniency flags as POLICY this feature owns.** `ignoreUnknownFields` (default TRUE — a stray key under the prefix is silently ignored) and `ignoreInvalidFields` (default FALSE — a coercion failure throws). These map onto binder `BindHandler` decisions (the binder neighbour flagged exactly this: ignoreUnknownFields = on_start skip-unknown; ignoreInvalidFields = on_failure recover-vs-rethrow), but THIS feature owns the default policy + the per-type override surface.\n\n(3) **Config is data, not code — INERT binding.** Unlike `@Value`, `@ConfigurationProperties` does NOT evaluate expressions (no SpEL/`#{}` analogue) — values are externalized config, bound whole-object, relaxed + validated + documented. The philosophical split this feature must instill: a config object is a pure projection of the Environment, not an expression-evaluating bean. Crucially, Spring DISCOURAGES injecting OTHER beans into a config-properties type — it should be a pure projection, bound very early, trivially testable/serializable.\n\n(4) **Two binding MODES surfaced to the user.** JavaBean/setter binding (default — no-arg construct then set; pre-initialized nested/collections mutated in place) vs constructor/value-object binding (immutable records — implicit when a single non-private, non-injected constructor exists; `@DefaultValue` supplies param defaults; an EMPTY `@DefaultValue` on a nested param forces a non-null nested instance). v4 removed public-field binding. THE rule: an existing/supplied value forces JavaBean. This feature surfaces the mode CHOICE to the user (which the binder then executes) and must define the Rust convention for it.\n\n(5) **Three enabling ROUTES — and why constructor binding is restricted.** (a) explicit registration (`@EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProps.class)` analogue — ideal for conditional/auto-config + third-party types leaf cannot annotate); (b) scan-like auto-discovery (`@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` analogue); (c) plain component stereotype (works but JavaBean-only). CRUCIAL RULE: constructor/value-object binding works ONLY via routes (a)/(b), because (c) and other bean-creation routes instantiate the bean THEMSELVES, leaving no seam for the binder to supply constructor args from config. Auto-registered beans get a deterministic derived name (`<prefix>-<fully.qualified.type>` analogue).\n\n(6) **Fail-fast at startup, bound VERY EARLY.** Binding + validation run at a defined early refresh point (before eager singletons that consume the config), failing the whole bring-up with a rich `BindValidationException`-equivalent naming the offending PROPERTY KEY (with origin/provenance) rather than a deferred NPE — \"config is data, fail at boot.\"\n\n(7) **Self-documenting config-metadata seam.** The same target declaration powers compile-time config-metadata emission (the `config-metadata` neighbour) for IDE autocompletion/docs — \"what properties does this app even accept?\" — at no runtime cost.\n\nSCOPE BOUNDARY (what THIS feature owns vs neighbours): `binder` owns the bind(prefix, Bindable) engine + tree-descent + bind-method execution + the BindResult monad + the BindHandler chain; `relaxed-binding` owns canonical-key identity + per-transport forms + the snake_case-field→kebab-key derivation rule; `type-conversion` owns string→T; `validation` owns the constraint engine; `config-metadata` owns metadata emission; `environment` owns the resolver/source-stack reachability handle; `refresh-lifecycle` owns WHEN refresh steps run; `conditions`/`profiles` own conditional gating; `container-core`/`bean-registry` own bean storage. THIS feature owns ONLY: the declaration surface (the prefix-carrying typed-target marker), the THREE enabling routes + the constructor-binding-restriction rule, the leniency-flag default POLICY + override surface, the bind-mode CHOICE surface (delegating execution to binder), the \"pure projection / discourage-injecting-other-beans\" rule, the derived bean-NAME convention, the WIRING that registers the bound config object as a resolvable bean and invokes binder+validation at the early refresh step, and the BindValidationException-equivalent's property-key framing. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: HOW a type opts in and carries its prefix (attribute macro → trait impl + descriptor vs explicit programmatic registration vs derive-only-metadata), HOW the three enabling routes map onto Rust's no-classpath reality (link-time descriptor registry vs explicit enable-list vs scan-codegen), and HOW the bound config object is exposed as a bean WITHOUT it being able to inject other beans (a least-privilege construction seam).

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Attribute-macro front-end emitting a ConfigProperties trait impl + a link-time registration descriptor (the literal @ConfigurationProperties + @ConfigurationPropertiesScan transcription)
Model config-properties as a thin attribute macro `#[config_properties(prefix = "my.main-project.person")]` on a struct/record that emits ONLY hand-writable artifacts: (a) an impl of a tiny marker trait carrying the prefix + leniency policy as const data; (b) a `const ConfigPropsDescriptor` registered into a link-time distributed slice (the `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` 'classpath' analogue) so the container can discover-and-bind it at refresh without the call site naming it; (c) delegation to the `binder` neighbour's `#[derive(BindTarget)]` (R1 of binder) for the actual tree-shape schema. The macro itself holds NO binding logic — it forwards to binder + carries declaration metadata.

```rust
#[config_properties(prefix = "my.app", ignore_unknown_fields = true, ignore_invalid_fields = false)]
#[derive(BindTarget)]                          // binder neighbour supplies the tree schema
pub struct AppProperties {
    name: String,                               // binds my.app.name (kebab via relaxed-binding)
    #[config(default = "USER")] roles: Vec<String>,
    #[config(default)] security: Security,      // empty-default forces non-null nested
}
// emitted (hand-writable):
impl ConfigProperties for AppProperties {
    const PREFIX: &'static str = "my.app";
    const POLICY: BindLeniency = BindLeniency { ignore_unknown: true, ignore_invalid: false };
    const BIND_METHOD: BindMethod = BindMethod::ValueObject; // derived from type shape
}
#[distributed_slice(leaf_core::CONFIG_PROPS)]
static __LEAF_APP_PROPS: ConfigPropsDescriptor = ConfigPropsDescriptor {
    type_id: TypeId::of::<AppProperties>(), name: "my.app-AppProperties",
    prefix: "my.app", policy: AppProperties::POLICY,
    bind: |env, h| Box::new(leaf_core::bind::<AppProperties>(env, h)), // erased binder call
    conditions: &[], origin: leaf_macros::decl_site!(),
};
```
THREE ROUTES map cleanly: (route a, explicit) a `register_config_properties::<T>()` programmatic call or a `#[leaf::enable_config_properties(MyProps, ThirdPartyProps)]` on the app root — used for third-party types leaf can't annotate and for conditional/auto-config registration; this is the hand-writable escape hatch and does NOT need the slice. (route b, scan) the distributed-slice descriptor IS the `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` analogue — auto-discovered within each linked crate, opted-in per-crate via the cross-crate force-link discipline. (route c, stereotype) a `#[component]`-marked config type is registered JavaBean-only (the descriptor sets `BIND_METHOD: JavaBean` and the macro refuses ValueObject for this route — replicating Spring's restriction). The container, at the early refresh step, walks the descriptor slice (plus explicitly-enabled types), runs conditions, calls the binder + validation per descriptor, and publishes each bound value as a resolvable bean under the derived name. The 'pure projection' rule is enforced structurally: the bind fn pointer receives ONLY `&Environment` (the resolver/source view) + a BindHandler — NEVER the bean container — so a config-properties type CANNOT inject another bean (it is constructed by the binder from config alone, not by the autowiring engine).

**Pros:** Most literal intent parity (charter #1 DX, #2 intent-shape): a Spring developer sees `#[config_properties(prefix=...)]` + the three enabling routes + the leniency flags + the constructor-vs-JavaBean restriction transcribed almost verbatim; the mental model transfers wholesale.; Thin macro (charter #10): emits only a trait impl (const data) + one descriptor static + a forwarding bind fn-pointer — every line hand-writable; `cargo expand` shows exactly the prefix, policy, and the binder call; the programmatic `register_config_properties::<T>()` escape hatch exists for hand-wiring.; The 'pure projection / no other beans' rule (Spring's discouraged-injection intent) becomes a STRUCTURAL guarantee, not a lint: the construction seam hands the binder only `&Environment`, so a config-properties type is physically incapable of injecting a sibling bean — Rust's type system enforces the philosophy the JVM only documents.; Constructor-binding-restricted-to-routes-a/b falls out naturally: the macro sets `BIND_METHOD` per route (ValueObject allowed for explicit/scan descriptors; forced JavaBean for the stereotype route), exactly replicating why Spring forbids value-object binding on self-instantiating beans — the seam where leaf owns construction is the descriptor's bind fn-pointer.; The same descriptor carries the declaration metadata config-metadata wants (prefix, field set via the BindTarget schema, defaults, origin) so config-metadata can co-emit from one source of truth (charter #11) — no duplicate declaration of the property surface.; Origin-agnostic + cross-crate-honest: the descriptor's bind fn-pointer erases the concrete type to a uniform `(env, handler) -> BoxedBound` signature, so a future WASM-module-sourced config type could contribute a descriptor identically; native and dynamic sources slot into one slice.

**Cons:** The distributed-slice scan route inherits the FULL cross-crate DCE hazard (cross-crate doc Layer 0/A/B): a config-properties type in a crate the binary never path-references contributes NO descriptor and binds NOTHING — silently, with no error, so a whole config object is just absent. Needs the force-link discipline + a zero-contribution self-check (a config-props type expected-but-absent is worse than a missing component because the app may run with default/empty config), an obligation this feature must inherit, not invent.; Generics-can't-register (cross-crate doc line 153): a generic config type `Foo<T>` has no single monomorphized descriptor for the slice, so the scan route can't auto-discover it — it must be explicitly registered per concrete instantiation (route a). A real limitation vs Spring's runtime-reflective registration, though config types are rarely generic.; Pre-judges (lightly) toward a link-time registry substrate for the scan route, which is a Phase-2 keystone (the cross-crate composition model) — presenting the slice as THE scan mechanism biases that signal; must stay a CANDIDATE alongside build-time-codegen scan (Architecture C) and explicit-enable (Architecture D).; The bind-METHOD choice (ValueObject vs JavaBean) is inherited from the binder's unresolved 'no Rust JavaBean convention' problem (binder's openNotes): this feature surfaces the choice but cannot resolve how an immutable record vs a Default+setter struct is distinguished — it depends on the binder's bind-method model, a cross-feature dependency.; Two registration paths (slice scan + explicit enable) means the 'which config-properties types exist' question has two sources that must reconcile — and conditional/profile gating (route a's strength) must compose with the slice's runtime condition evaluation without double-registration, an ordering subtlety.; An attribute macro that BOTH carries config-properties metadata AND requires `#[derive(BindTarget)]` is two macros on one type; if not unified ergonomically (one macro forwarding to the other) the DX frays — and pre-deciding whether config_properties subsumes the BindTarget derive touches the metadata/codegen boundary (charter §3).

**Mechanisms considered:** `#[config_properties(prefix, ignore_unknown_fields, ignore_invalid_fields)]` attribute macro emitting a `ConfigProperties` marker-trait impl (const PREFIX/POLICY/BIND_METHOD) + a `const ConfigPropsDescriptor` static; link-time `linkme` distributed slice `CONFIG_PROPS` of descriptors as the `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` analogue (the default 'classpath'), force-linked per opted-in crate; explicit `register_config_properties::<T>()` / `#[leaf::enable_config_properties(..)]` app-root list as the `@EnableConfigurationProperties` analogue (route a, third-party + conditional) and the universal escape hatch; stereotype route: a `#[component]` config type registered JavaBean-only (macro refuses ValueObject), transcribing Spring's restriction; an erased bind fn-pointer `|&Environment, &dyn BindHandler| -> Box<dyn Any>` so the descriptor is generic-free and the construction seam denies bean-container access (pure projection enforced structurally); delegation to binder's `#[derive(BindTarget)]` const SCHEMA for tree shape; delegation to validation's stock ValidationBindHandler for fail-fast; optional dynamic directory-scanned / WASM-module descriptor source feeding the SAME slice (the dynamic 'classpath') — a CANDIDATE; stable-only: const descriptors, `const TypeId::of` (1.91), distributed slice, fn-pointers, enums; the bind fn is synchronous so no async-trait tax on the descriptor

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the cross-crate HEART of the feature, because the scan route (`@ConfigurationPropertiesScan`) IS a discovery mechanism. It carries the full static-link-registry-plus-optional-dynamic-directory duality as CANDIDATES (not decisions): the default is a `linkme` distributed slice of `const ConfigPropsDescriptor` (the static 'classpath') populated by the attribute macro in each defining crate, PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned / WASM-module descriptor source (the dynamic 'classpath') feeding the same slice — both origin-agnostic via the erased bind fn-pointer. DCE guardrails are CRITICAL and arguably higher-stakes than for component-scanning: a silently-dropped config-properties descriptor means the app boots with DEFAULT/absent config (not a loud missing-bean), so the mandatory anti-DCE measures apply — const descriptors, runtime SELECTION/ordering by descriptor DATA (prefix/conditions) never link/section order, force-link of opted-in crates (`use crate as _;` from the app root), and a zero-contribution self-check that loudly warns when an expected config-props-providing crate registered nothing (a `leaf doctor` line: 'crate X enabled but contributed 0 config-properties'). The explicit-enable route (route a) is the Layer-0-safe escape hatch (the app root path-references the type, so it always links) and the ONLY route for third-party types leaf cannot annotate and for generic config types (generics-can't-register, line 153). The macro must HARD-ERROR on a generic config-properties target for the scan route, directing the user to explicit registration. CRITICALLY this SHARES the same discovery-substrate question as `component-scanning`, `auto-configuration`, and the `binder`/`property-resolution` handler discovery — flagged as a Phase-2 unification keystone, NOT decided here (whether config-properties scanning rides ONE substrate with component scanning, or stays a parallel slice). The descriptor's bind fn-pointer hard-codes `::leaf_core::bind::<T>` paths (proc-macro hygiene, absolute paths). The umbrella facade + app root are where the full config-props graph is visible (cross-crate doc line 260), so the bind-everything sweep + the self-check anchor at the binary.

**T2 — execution context:** Config-properties binding runs on the COLD bootstrap path at a defined early refresh step (refresh-lifecycle), 'bound very early' per Spring intent — AFTER the property-source stack is materialized (so the resolver/relaxed layer can be probed) but BEFORE eager singletons that consume the config are instantiated. The descriptor-slice walk + per-descriptor binder call + validation are SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking CPU over already-materialized, placeholder-resolved raw strings (the bind fn-pointer MUST NOT `.await`/block, charter #4 — and it is synchronous so it carries no async-trait/RPITIT boxing tax). Any source whose backing is remote/async MUST have been snapshotted into the stack during a cold async pre-step BEFORE this refresh step (the shared BootstrapContext discipline all the config neighbours flagged — property-sources/property-resolution/relaxed-binding/binder/environment). FAIL-FAST: a bind or validation failure on any descriptor aborts refresh ALL-OR-NOTHING (no partially-built graph published) with a rich `ConfigBindError` carrying prefix + property key + matched raw key + origin (origin-tracking) + the target field path + candidates — ideally aggregating EVERY config-props failure across the whole sweep into one startup-validation report (charter #9 richest diagnostic), not first-fail-abort. The Unbound state (nothing matched the prefix) is NOT an error here — it composes with the type's defaults / `bind_or_create` (binder's three-state monad), distinct from a coercion/validation FAILURE. The bound config object is OWNED + `Send + Sync` if its fields are, published as a singleton that crosses `.await`/threads freely (concurrency-contract's safe-publication guarantee). No cancellation concern on the synchronous sweep (bounded CPU by descriptor count × schema size); the async pre-materialization is a separate cold step with its own cancellation. A future config-REFRESH re-bind is a cold, cancellable background task producing a fresh owned value atomically swapped for the live one (charter #5 no hot-path lock) — a Phase-2 concurrency call, flagged not decided.

#### R2 — Explicit programmatic registration via a typed AppConfig builder (the bevy-plugin / dill-catalog style; no scan, maximal predictability)
Invert R1's auto-discovery: there is NO scan, NO link-time slice for config-properties by default. Config types are registered EXPLICITLY on the application builder, exactly as Spring's `@EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProps.class)` lists types — but as the PRIMARY (not fallback) route, mirroring the Rust ecosystem's explicit-composition camp (bevy `add_plugins`, dill `Catalog::builder().add()`).

```rust
let app = leaf::App::builder()
    .config_properties::<AppProperties>()            // prefix read from the type's ConfigProperties impl
    .config_properties::<DataSourceProperties>()
    .config_properties_with::<ThirdPartyProps>(      // third-party type leaf can't annotate: prefix + policy supplied here
        "vendor.widget", BindLeniency::default())
    .build()?;
```
A config type still carries its prefix + policy via a `#[derive(ConfigProperties)]` (derive-ONLY: emits the `ConfigProperties` trait impl with const PREFIX/POLICY + the BindTarget schema, NO descriptor static — so it is pure metadata, zero link-time footprint), OR a third-party type's prefix/policy is supplied at the registration call site (the `_with` form, the `@EnableConfigurationProperties`-for-foreign-types analogue). The builder accumulates a `Vec<ConfigPropsRegistration>` (each = TypeId + prefix + policy + an erased bind fn-pointer), and the early refresh step binds each. A `config_properties_scan!{ crate_a, crate_b }` macro is offered as SUGAR over the explicit route — it expands to a sequence of `.config_properties::<T>()` calls for the types a crate publicly exports via a hand-writable `pub fn leaf_config_props() -> &'static [ConfigPropsRegistration]` convention (the bevy `PluginGroup` analogue), so 'scan-like' discovery is build-time-explicit, not link-time-magic. The 'pure projection' rule is enforced identically to R1 (the bind fn-pointer gets only `&Environment`). Conditional/profile gating is a `.config_properties_if::<T>(condition)` builder method — conditions evaluated at the registration sweep, the `@Profile`-on-config analogue.

**Pros:** Maximum predictability + reliability (cross-crate doc's explicit-composition lesson, Architecture D): NO DCE hazard, NO silent-empty-registry, NO linker-choice-as-correctness-variable — a config type binds iff it was named on the builder, which is the ONE thing guaranteed on every target including wasm/embedded; the 'which config exists' question has a single, inspectable answer (the builder chain).; Directly transcribes Spring's `@EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProps.class)` as the PRIMARY route — which the docs call out as 'explicit, ideal for conditional/auto-config and third-party classes' (line 1587) — and handles third-party types leaf cannot annotate FIRST-CLASS via `config_properties_with`, the cleanest answer to the orphan-rule-adjacent 'I can't put an attribute on a foreign type' problem (vs R1 where third-party is a secondary escape hatch).; Generics-friendly: `.config_properties::<Foo<Concrete>>()` registers a concrete instantiation at a known call site with no monomorphized-registration wall (cross-crate doc line 153) — a real advantage over R1's slice for generic config types.; Thinnest macro story (charter #10): the `#[derive(ConfigProperties)]` is metadata-only (no descriptor, no link section), and the builder methods are ordinary typed Rust a user could write by hand — `cargo expand` is trivial, and the whole wiring is a value-level, type-checked composition (dill/teloc/axum style) with compile-time `T: ConfigProperties + BindTarget` bounds catching mistakes at compile time (charter #9 earliest legible).; Conditional/profile gating is natural and explicit (`.config_properties_if(cond)`), composing cleanly with conditions/profiles WITHOUT the two-source reconciliation R1 needs (slice + explicit) — one registration list, conditions evaluated over it.; Aligns with the cross-crate doc's tracing-style role separation (line 233): contribution crates only DECLARE config types (the derive, no global side effect); the single app/binary crate OWNS assembly (the builder) — clean ownership, no transitive dependency silently injecting a config object.

**Cons:** Sacrifices 'auto' — the headline Spring DX of `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` (annotate-and-forget, the convention-over-configuration feel) is LOST; a large app with dozens of config-properties types becomes a long builder chain, more ceremony than Spring's scan (charter #1 DX cost, the explicit tradeoff bevy accepts but Spring users may miss).; The `config_properties_scan!{ crate_a }` sugar still requires each crate to publish a hand-written `leaf_config_props()` registry fn and the app to list crates — so 'scan' is really 'list crates once + each crate lists its own types', which is MORE boilerplate than Spring's package scan and pushes work onto integration-crate authors (though it is honest about what Rust can actually do).; Auto-configuration (the `auto-configuration` neighbour — opinionated defaults from libraries) becomes awkward: a library that wants to contribute a config-properties type the app DIDN'T explicitly name (the whole point of auto-config) can't, unless auto-config crates inject registrations via their own enable-list — re-introducing a discovery need R2 tried to avoid, so R2 may be incomplete for the auto-config story (a real gap vs Spring where auto-config classes carry their own `@EnableConfigurationProperties`).; More verbose third-party-vs-own-type asymmetry: own types use the derive + `.config_properties::<T>()`; third-party types use `.config_properties_with::<T>(prefix, policy)` — two call shapes the user must learn, vs Spring's uniform `@EnableConfigurationProperties` list.; Pushes the 'opinionated base, auto-discovered' charter value (#1, the Spring-grade feel) toward 'explicit base' — defensible for reliability but a philosophical step away from the DX north-star; risks feeling less like Spring and more like a manual DI crate.; Loses the single-source-of-truth-for-metadata convenience unless the derive ALSO emits a config-metadata descriptor — and without a slice, gathering 'all config-properties types in the workspace' for tooling/`config-metadata` is harder (you'd have to read the builder, which is runtime, or a build-time codegen pass).

**Mechanisms considered:** `leaf::App::builder().config_properties::<T>()` explicit registration as the PRIMARY route (Architecture D, bevy/dill style); `#[derive(ConfigProperties)]` metadata-ONLY (const PREFIX/POLICY + BindTarget schema, NO link-time descriptor) — zero cross-crate footprint; `config_properties_with::<T>(prefix, policy)` for third-party/foreign types (the @EnableConfigurationProperties-for-foreign analogue, first-class); `config_properties_scan!{ crate_a, crate_b }` sugar expanding to explicit `.config_properties::<T>()` calls over each crate's hand-written `pub fn leaf_config_props() -> &[ConfigPropsRegistration]` (bevy PluginGroup analogue); `config_properties_if::<T>(condition)` builder method for conditional/profile gating, evaluated over the explicit registration list; an erased bind fn-pointer per registration denying bean-container access (pure projection, same as R1); build-time codegen (`cargo metadata`-driven, sqlx style, Architecture C) as an OPTIONAL way to auto-generate the builder chain for opted-in crates — a CANDIDATE bridging explicit + auto; stable-only: typed builder, generics at call sites, fn-pointers, derive-emitted const data; no link sections, no nightly, fully portable incl. wasm

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The MOST cross-crate-reliable realization and the universal escape hatch (Architecture D): a config type binds iff the binary's builder names it (or names a crate's `leaf_config_props()` group), so there is NO Layer-0/DCE exposure, NO linker-choice variability, and FULL wasm/embedded support — the same reliability the cross-crate doc grants explicit composition. The `#[derive(ConfigProperties)]` is metadata-only and travels with the type (like serde's Deserialize — no registration, visible wherever the type is imported), so cross-crate coherence is trivial and generics are fine (registered per concrete instantiation at the call site). The genuine T1 GAP is auto-configuration: a downstream/auto-config crate wanting to contribute a config-properties type the app didn't explicitly name needs SOME discovery — so R2 either (a) accepts that auto-config crates expose a `leaf_config_props()` group the app's `config_properties_scan!` lists (still explicit per-crate opt-in, honoring the 'scope discovery' guardrail), or (b) layers R1's link-time slice ONLY for the auto-config path (a hybrid). This makes R2 cleanest for app-authored config and weakest for library-contributed config — the exact inverse of R1. The optional build-time-codegen variant (Architecture C: a `build.rs`/`cargo leaf prepare` reads `cargo metadata`, emits the builder chain for opted-in crates into the binary) is the deterministic middle path and the recommended wasm/embedded path, sharing the SAME `ConfigPropsRegistration` runtime shape so the substrate is swappable. Shares the Phase-2 cross-crate-substrate question with component-scanning/auto-config but resolves it toward the explicit/codegen end — flagged, not decided. No proc-macro-state hazard (derive is stateless, metadata-only). The app/binary crate is the single assembly point (cross-crate doc role separation, line 233/260).
