**T2 — execution context:** Identical cold-bootstrap execution model to R1: the registration sweep runs at the early refresh step (refresh-lifecycle), after property-source materialization, before consuming eager singletons. The difference is the SOURCE of the registration list (an explicit `Vec<ConfigPropsRegistration>` built at builder time on the bootstrap context, vs R1's slice walk) — but the per-registration work is the same SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking binder + validation call over already-materialized strings (no `.await`/block, charter #4; remote/async sources pre-snapshotted in a cold async BootstrapContext step). Builder construction itself is cold synchronous setup (no I/O, no await — just accumulating registrations). FAIL-FAST + aggregation are identical (abort refresh all-or-nothing with a rich aggregated `ConfigBindError`; Unbound composes with defaults, distinct from Failed). The bound config objects are owned + `Send+Sync` singletons, safely published (concurrency-contract). A `config_properties_if` condition is evaluated synchronously during the sweep (conditions are pure predicates over container state — conditions neighbour). No cancellation on the synchronous sweep; async pre-materialization is a separate cold step. Config-refresh re-bind is a cold cancellable background task with an atomic-swap (Phase-2). Because there is no link-time machinery, there is also no pre-main/life-before-main execution at all (vs R1's slice which, if backed by inventory rather than linkme, would run pre-main constructors — R2 avoids that entirely), a cleaner async-first startup story (charter #2/#4).

#### R3 — Config-properties as a first-class BEAN-DEFINITION role: the type IS a bean whose factory is a binder-backed instance-supplier, unifying with the container's bean model
Question whether config-properties needs a SEPARATE registration channel at all, or whether a config-properties type is simply a BEAN whose construction strategy is 'bind from the Environment' instead of 'autowire collaborators' — unifying config-properties into the `bean-definition`/`bean-registry`/`programmatic-registration` model (charter #11) rather than building a parallel pipeline. A `#[config_properties(prefix=...)]` type produces a `BeanDefinition` whose `instance_supplier` is a binder-backed factory: when the container needs the bean, it binds it from config; when another bean injects `AppProperties`, it resolves through the SAME autowiring-resolution path as any singleton.

```rust
// config-properties type contributes a BeanDefinition like any other bean, but with a special factory:
BeanDefinition {
    type_id: TypeId::of::<AppProperties>(),
    name: "my.app-AppProperties",            // derived <prefix>-<type> name (bean-naming neighbour)
    role: Role::ConfigProperties,             // a role hint (post-processor-spi / bean-definition)
    scope: Scope::Singleton,
    // the construction seam: NOT autowiring — a binder-backed supplier that sees only the Environment
    instance_supplier: InstanceSupplier::ConfigBind {
        prefix: "my.app",
        policy: AppProperties::POLICY,
        bind: |env, h| Box::new(leaf_core::bind::<AppProperties>(env, h)),
    },
    init_order: InitOrder::Early,             // bound before ordinary eager singletons (fail-fast)
}
```
The THREE enabling routes become THREE ways a config-props BeanDefinition reaches the registry, reusing existing machinery: (route a, explicit) a `#[bean]`-method-style or `programmatic-registration` call contributes the definition (the `@EnableConfigurationProperties` analogue, leaning on the existing programmatic-registration AOT-analyzable contract); (route b, scan) the same component-scanning / auto-detection that finds `#[component]` beans ALSO detects `#[config_properties]` types (ONE scan, the `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` analogue riding component-scanning's substrate — charter #11 unification); (route c, stereotype) `#[component]` on a config type yields a config-props definition forced to JavaBean mode. The leniency policy + bind-mode live on the definition. The 'pure projection / no other beans' rule is the `InstanceSupplier::ConfigBind` variant DENYING autowiring access (it gets `&Environment`, not the bean-resolution context) — distinct from `InstanceSupplier::Autowire` which gets collaborators; the bean DEFINITION model already separates 'how is this constructed' from 'what is it', so config-properties is just a new construction strategy, not a new subsystem. Validation rides the binder's ValidationBindHandler. Because it is a real bean, it participates in container-hierarchy, conditions (definition-level), lifecycle-callbacks (a config object could have a post-bind init), and is injectable as `AppProperties` / `ObjectProvider<AppProperties>` (deferral-primitives) anywhere.

**Pros:** Maximal charter #11 unification: config-properties stops being a parallel pipeline and becomes ONE more bean-construction strategy on the existing bean-definition/bean-registry/autowiring machinery — the scan route reuses component-scanning, the explicit route reuses programmatic-registration, injection reuses autowiring-resolution, naming reuses bean-naming, conditions reuse the definition-level condition model. Far less bespoke machinery than R1/R2.; A config object becomes a FIRST-CLASS bean: it is injectable anywhere (`AppProperties`, `&AppProperties`, `ObjectProvider<AppProperties>` via deferral-primitives), participates in container-hierarchy (a child context can shadow a parent's config-props), can have lifecycle-callbacks (a post-bind `@PostConstruct`-style init/normalize step), and benefits from the same primary/fallback + collection-injection semantics — strictly more capable than R1/R2's side-table of bound values.; The 'pure projection / no other beans' rule maps PRECISELY onto the bean-definition model's existing separation of construction strategy from identity: `InstanceSupplier::ConfigBind` (Environment-only) vs `InstanceSupplier::Autowire` (collaborators) is the structural seam — and it explains Spring's restriction (constructor binding only via routes a/b) as 'the container owns construction via the ConfigBind supplier; a self-instantiating @Component can't, so it falls back to JavaBean post-construction binding' — the cleanest articulation of the Spring rule.; Conditional/profile gating is FREE and consistent: a config-props definition carries definition-level conditions exactly like any bean (conditions/profiles neighbours), with NO bespoke `config_properties_if` — the `@Profile`-on-a-config-class intent (docs line 1329) is just a conditional bean definition.; Fail-fast + early binding fit the refresh-lifecycle template naturally: `InitOrder::Early` config-props definitions are instantiated (bound) in an early refresh layer before ordinary eager singletons, so a consuming bean that injects `AppProperties` is guaranteed it exists and is valid — the dependency ordering is the container's existing job, not a special config phase.; AOT/codegen-friendly: leaning on programmatic-registration's AOT-analyzable instance-supplier contract means config-props definitions can be build-time-analyzed alongside all other beans (one graph), and the construction seam is a plain fn-pointer — composing with whatever compile-vs-runtime split Phase 2 picks.

**Cons:** DEEPLY entangles config-properties with the container/bean-model keystones that are explicitly Phase-2-deferred (the type-erasure & registry substrate, the scope/lifetime/ownership model, the bean-definition representation) — presenting config-properties AS a bean-definition role pre-judges how beans are stored/keyed/constructed, the single biggest charter §3 deferral; this realization is the most architecturally presumptuous and must stay strictly a CANDIDATE.; Risks violating the 'pure projection, bound very early, trivially testable/serializable' intent (docs line 1593): making a config object a full bean (injectable, lifecycle-bearing, hierarchy-participating) RE-OPENS the door to it injecting other beans or running lifecycle logic — the exact thing Spring DISCOURAGES — unless the `ConfigBind` supplier rigidly forbids it; the capability R3 adds is partly capability Spring deliberately withholds (a philosophical tension: more unified, but less aligned with 'config is inert data').; Early-binding a config-props bean within the general eager-singleton instantiation order risks ordering hazards the side-table approaches (R1/R2) avoid: a config object must be bound BEFORE any bean that consumes it, but if it is 'just a bean' the container's dependency ordering must special-case config-props as a distinct early layer anyway (`InitOrder::Early`) — so the unification leaks a special case back into refresh-lifecycle, partly undercutting the 'no separate pipeline' claim.; Heavier coupling surface for testing: Spring's intent is that a config object is trivially constructable/serializable OUTSIDE the container (a pure POJO bound from a map); if config-properties is fundamentally a bean-definition, the 'bind this struct from a property map with zero container' path (which R1/R2 keep as a plain `binder::bind::<T>()` call) must be carefully preserved as a non-bean escape hatch, or the testability intent regresses.; The bean-NAME convention (`<prefix>-<type>`) and the role hint must be threaded into bean-naming + bean-definition's existing model, and config-props beans must be EXCLUDED from ordinary by-type autowiring ambiguity rules in a sane way (two config types both injectable as their own type is fine, but the role hint must keep them out of, e.g., collection-injection of unrelated beans) — integration subtleties R1/R2's side table sidesteps entirely.; Whether config-properties SHOULD be a bean at all is itself a design question this realization answers prematurely; Spring makes it a bean, but leaf might deliberately keep config objects as a SEPARATE inert layer for clarity — so R3 forecloses a legitimate alternative (config as a non-bean projection) that R1/R2 preserve.

**Mechanisms considered:** config-properties as a `BeanDefinition` with `role: Role::ConfigProperties` and a binder-backed `InstanceSupplier::ConfigBind` (Environment-only) vs `InstanceSupplier::Autowire` (collaborators) — construction strategy as the seam; reusing component-scanning's auto-detection for the scan route (ONE scan finds beans AND config-props types — charter #11); reusing programmatic-registration's AOT-analyzable instance-supplier contract for the explicit route (the @EnableConfigurationProperties analogue); reusing autowiring-resolution / deferral-primitives so a config object is injectable as `T` / `ObjectProvider<T>` anywhere; definition-level conditions/profiles for gating (no bespoke config_properties_if); bean-naming for the derived `<prefix>-<type>` name; `InitOrder::Early` in the refresh-lifecycle template so config-props bind before consuming eager singletons (fail-fast ordering); a preserved non-bean `binder::bind::<T>()` escape hatch so config objects stay testable/serializable outside the container; stable-only: bean-definition data + fn-pointer suppliers + TypeId keying (1.91) + Any/downcast; binder call synchronous

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Cross-crate behavior is INHERITED from whatever substrate the bean-model/component-scanning uses — which is precisely the point and the risk. The scan route rides component-scanning's discovery (the SAME link-time-slice-vs-build-codegen-vs-explicit substrate, the SAME Layer-0/DCE hazard, the SAME force-link + zero-contribution self-check obligations) rather than a parallel CONFIG_PROPS slice — strongly advancing the charter #11 'one discovery substrate' unification, but making config-properties' cross-crate reliability entirely dependent on the (Phase-2) bean-discovery decision. The explicit route rides programmatic-registration (Layer-0-safe, the app names the definition). Generics-can't-register applies via the bean model (a generic config-props bean needs a concrete registration shim, line 153) — consistent with how generic beans are handled generally. The erased `ConfigBind` supplier fn-pointer (`|&Environment, &dyn BindHandler| -> Box<dyn Any>`) is origin-agnostic and could be contributed by a WASM-module source as a dynamic bean definition (the dynamic 'classpath' duality), identical to how a dynamic bean would slot in. The DECISIVE T1 consequence: R3 does NOT introduce a config-properties-specific cross-crate mechanism — it FOLDS config-properties into the bean-graph cross-crate model — so the Phase-2 cross-crate-composition keystone and the type-erasure/registry-substrate keystone now BOTH gate config-properties, which is why R3 is the most unified and the most deferral-entangled. Flagged, not decided.

**T2 — execution context:** Config-props beans are bound at an EARLY layer of the refresh-lifecycle eager-instantiation phase (InitOrder::Early), on the COLD bootstrap path, before ordinary eager singletons — the binder-backed `ConfigBind` supplier runs SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking binding over already-materialized strings (no `.await`/block, charter #4; remote/async sources pre-snapshotted in the cold async BootstrapContext step, shared discipline). Because it is a bean, its construction participates in the container's bean-instantiation creation lock + three-level cache + safe-publication (concurrency-contract / bean-instantiation neighbours) — but a config-props bean has NO collaborators to wait on (it binds from the Environment, not other beans), so it cannot participate in a construction CYCLE (a structural simplification: config-props beans are always leaves in the dependency graph for construction purposes, even though other beans depend on THEM). FAIL-FAST: a bind/validation failure aborts refresh all-or-nothing through the container's existing instantiation-failure path, with the rich aggregated `ConfigBindError` (property key + origin + candidates, charter #9). If a config object has an optional post-bind lifecycle-callback (a normalize/derive-computed-field step), it runs synchronously after binding in the bean's init phase (lifecycle-callbacks neighbour) — but it MUST NOT block/await and MUST NOT reach for other beans (the pure-projection constraint), a discipline the `ConfigBind` role enforces. Injection of `AppProperties` into a consuming bean rides the normal (cold, synchronous-resolution) autowiring path; the bound singleton is `Send+Sync` and crosses `.await`/threads freely once published. Config-refresh re-bind is a cold cancellable background task that must atomically swap the bean instance in the singleton cache without a hot-path lock (charter #5) — a Phase-2 concurrency call entangled with the scope/lifetime model, flagged not decided.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's THREE enabling routes (`@EnableConfigurationProperties` list, `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` package scan, plain `@Component`) all rest on the JVM classpath: scanning reads bytecode annotations at runtime, and `@EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProps.class)` names a `Class<?>`. Rust has no classpath and no runtime annotation reflection — so the SCAN route must be synthesized from a link-time descriptor registry (DCE-hazardous, silent-empty failure) or build-time codegen or an explicit enable-list, and the EXPLICIT route names a concrete `T` at a known call site. The deepest clash: Spring's scan is 'discover all config-props types in these packages' (a runtime query against a global registry); leaf's nearest honest equivalent is 'discover within each crate the binary force-links' (per the cross-crate doc), with a silently-dropped descriptor meaning a config object is ABSENT with no error — higher-stakes than a missing component because the app may boot with default/empty config and misbehave subtly.
- Spring's two binding MODES (JavaBean setter-mutation vs value-object constructor binding) rest on JVM conventions Rust lacks: 'JavaBean' = no-arg construct + getters/setters + in-place mutation; 'value-object' = a single non-private, non-injected constructor (records get it free). Rust has NO universal setter/getter convention and NO uniform field-mutation of an existing instance — an immutable struct simply cannot be JavaBean-bound. This feature must SURFACE a mode choice the user understands, but the underlying convention (Default+`&mut` fields = JavaBean vs a constructor = value-object) is something leaf must INVENT (delegated to the binder neighbour's unresolved bind-method model), not transcribe. Spring's 'an existing/supplied value forces JavaBean' rule is especially awkward — Rust can't field-mutate an arbitrary existing `T`.
- Spring's 'discourage injecting OTHER beans into a config-properties class' is a documented GUIDELINE (a lint/convention) on the JVM, where a config object is a full bean that COULD inject collaborators but shouldn't. Rust lets leaf make this a STRUCTURAL guarantee — the construction seam hands the binder only `&Environment`, never the bean container — so a config-props type is PHYSICALLY incapable of injecting a sibling bean. The clash is inverted: Rust can ENFORCE the philosophy the JVM only suggests, but only if config-properties is kept OUT of the general autowiring construction path (R1/R2's side table) or rigidly role-gated within it (R3's ConfigBind supplier) — a design decision Rust forces that Spring never had to make.
- Spring's `@ConfigurationProperties(prefix)` + the relaxed snake/camel/kebab/UPPER_SNAKE equivalence means a Rust struct field `first_name` must derive a canonical kebab key `first-name` under the prefix — but the field-name→canonical-key derivation is a CONVENTION leaf must define (delegated to relaxed-binding), and Rust idioms (snake_case fields) map to kebab differently than Java's camelCase fields. There is no free reflective field-name access at runtime; the field names must be captured AS DATA at macro-expansion time (the BindTarget schema), so a refactor that renames a field silently changes the bound property key unless the macro pins it — a fragility Spring's runtime reflection partly masks.
- Spring binds onto MUTABLE bean instances and re-binds freely on the JVM's GC'd heap. Rust's ownership/immutability pushes config-properties toward 'bind produces a fresh OWNED value, published as an immutable singleton' — and a config-REFRESH (re-bind on file change, an Actuator-style feature) cannot mutate a shared `&AppProperties` in place without a lock or atomic swap (charter #5 no global locks). The refresh/staleness/atomic-swap model is a Rust-specific concurrency concern (shared with relaxed-binding's index-invalidation and binder's re-bind) that Spring's mutable beans never forced — and it interacts with whether a config object is a bean (R3, must swap in the singleton cache) or a side-table value (R1/R2, simpler swap).
- Spring's fail-fast `BindValidationException` typically surfaces ONE failure at a time through exceptions; Rust's charter #9 wants the RICHEST diagnostic — ideally a startup-validation pass aggregating EVERY config-props bind/coercion/constraint failure across ALL registered types at once, naming each property key + origin + candidates. Aggregation across multiple config-properties objects (not just within one) is a cross-type concern this front-end owns (it orchestrates the whole sweep), with a Rust-specific aggregation cost (collecting Results instead of throwing on first) that Spring's exception model never optimized for — and it must resist the `?`-fail-first reflex.
- Spring makes a config-properties type a BEAN (named `<prefix>-<fqn>`, injectable, lifecycle-bearing) — leaf must decide whether a config object IS a bean (R3, maximally unified but re-opens the inject-other-beans door Spring discourages and entangles the deferred bean-model keystones) or a SEPARATE inert projection layer (R1/R2, aligned with 'config is inert data, trivially testable outside the container' but a parallel pipeline). Spring's GC'd object model never forced this either/or; Rust's explicit construction + ownership makes 'is config a bean?' a load-bearing question with no free default — and it is entangled with the type-erasure/registry substrate and scope/lifetime keystones (charter §3) this feature must NOT resolve.
- Spring's config-metadata is emitted by an annotation processor reading the same `@ConfigurationProperties` declaration at compile time. In Rust, emitting the self-documenting property surface needs the field set + defaults + descriptions AS DATA at build time — which a proc-macro can produce for its OWN invocation (the declaring crate) but NOT across crates (cross-crate doc line 89), and a `#[derive(Deserialize)]`-style binder (binder's R2) that leaf doesn't own makes metadata harder. So whether config-properties' declaration is the single source of truth for BOTH binding AND metadata, and whether that lives in a proc-macro vs build.rs codegen, is a metadata/codegen-boundary clash (charter §3) Spring's unified annotation processor never had to split.

### Interactions
- **binder** — HARD DEPENDENCY and the engine THIS feature drives. config-properties is the DECLARATIVE front-end; the binder is the machinery (Spring's 'the binder @ConfigurationProperties uses internally', docs line 1606). This feature DECLARES a prefix-rooted typed target + the leniency policy + the bind-mode choice, then INVOKES `binder::bind::<T>(prefix, bindable)` at the early refresh step and consumes the BindResult three-state monad (Bound/Unbound/Failed). The two leniency flags map directly onto binder BindHandler decisions (ignore_unknown_fields = on_start skip-unknown; ignore_invalid_fields = on_failure recover-vs-rethrow) — the binder OWNS the handler chain + tree-descent + bind-method execution + collection-replacement; this feature owns the POLICY defaults + the declaration surface that produces the Bindable. The bind-mode model (JavaBean vs value-object, and the no-Rust-JavaBean-convention problem) is the binder's to resolve; this feature surfaces the choice to the user.
- **relaxed-binding** — HARD DEPENDENCY (transitively, via the binder). The prefix MUST be canonical kebab-case, and each Rust field name (`first_name`) derives a canonical kebab leaf (`first-name`) under the prefix via relaxed-binding's snake_case-ident→kebab rule — so a field binds from `FIRST_NAME` env, `firstName` JSON, or `first-name` file transparently. This feature DEFINES that the prefix is canonical kebab and relies on relaxed-binding's field-name→canonical-key derivation; relaxed-binding owns the equivalence relation + per-transport forms. The bracket-escape `[key-with-dashes]` ownership tension (relaxed-binding vs binder vs property-resolution) flagged by both neighbours is inherited, not resolved here.
- **validation** — DOWNSTREAM seam, invoked via the binder's handler chain. A `#[validated]`-marked config-properties type runs JSR-303-analogue constraints on the bound object via validation's stock ValidationBindHandler (riding the binder), failing fast at startup with the property-key-framed error — the canonical reuse the intent calls out ('config constraints look like every other validated bean', docs line 1616). This feature OWNS the policy that config-props validation runs at the early refresh step + fails the whole bring-up; validation owns the constraint engine; the binder owns the handler hook. `@Valid` cascades into nested config objects via the engine's cascade.
- **type-conversion** — DOWNSTREAM (transitively, via the binder per leaf). Each leaf value is coerced to the target field type via type-conversion (Duration/DataSize/Period suffixes, case-insensitive enums, comma-split collections); config-properties does NOT evaluate expressions (no SpEL analogue — config is INERT, the deliberate split from @Value), so its path is pure config→type with no expression engine. The binder orchestrates per-leaf conversion; this feature only establishes the inert-binding contract.
- **environment** — UPSTREAM reachability/handle owner. The binder is constructed FROM the Environment (Spring's `Binder.get(environment)`), which exposes the resolver + the ordered first-source-wins property-source stack; this feature's bound config object is a pure PROJECTION of that read view. environment owns who-can-reach the resolver + the handle shape (borrowed vs Arc-rooted) + lifetime across `.await`/threads; the early refresh step borrows the read view to bind. CRUCIALLY the 'pure projection / no other beans' rule means the construction seam gets the Environment read view ONLY — never the bean container.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — ORDERING dependency — owns WHEN config-properties binding runs. config-properties is 'bound very early' (docs line 1593): the binding+validation sweep is a fixed refresh step AFTER property-source materialization (so the resolver is ready) and BEFORE eager singletons that consume the config (so a consuming bean is guaranteed valid config exists). A bind/validation failure aborts refresh ALL-OR-NOTHING (no partially-built graph). refresh-lifecycle owns the fixed-order template + the step's position; this feature provides the binding that step performs. (Spring's warning that custom converter beans must be `static` because binding precedes full post-processor registration — docs line 1612 — is the same precede-the-rest ordering concern.)
- **conditions** — CONSUMER — config-properties registration is conditionally gateable. A config-props declaration can carry definition-level conditions (the `@ConditionalOnProperty`/`@Profile`-on-a-config-class analogue, docs line 1329 noting @Profile placement rules for @EnableConfigurationProperties vs scanned config types), so a config object is registered/bound only when its condition holds. conditions owns the pure-predicate evaluation; this feature owns where the condition attaches to a config-props registration (and the route-dependent placement rule Spring documents: on the enabling @Configuration for explicit route, on the type itself for the scan route).
- **profiles** — CONSUMER (a specialization of conditions). Profile-gated config-properties (active only under a named profile) is just a conditional config-props registration — and the active-profiles key itself (`leaf`'s `spring.profiles.active` analogue) is read relaxed (env `SPRING_PROFILES_ACTIVE` ≡ file `spring.profiles.active`), which this feature's binding consumes. profiles owns the activation grammar; this feature owns that a config-props type can be profile-gated and that profile-specific config files contribute to the bound object.
- **config-metadata** — DOWNSTREAM producer-side coupling — the self-documenting seam. The same prefix + field set + defaults + descriptions that this feature DECLARES is exactly what config-metadata emits at compile time (groups/properties/hints powering IDE autocompletion, 'what properties does this app accept?', docs lines 1618-1624 incl. the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` for reusable types in separate modules). A leaf-owned declaration macro can co-emit metadata from one source of truth (charter #11); this feature defines the declared surface, config-metadata owns the emission format + per-type metadata location. The canonical kebab form is the form metadata advertises (the relaxed-binding asymmetric-placeholder lesson).
- **component-scanning** — CANDIDATE-SHARED discovery substrate (the `@ConfigurationPropertiesScan` analogue). The scan enabling route discovers config-properties types the way component-scanning discovers `#[component]` beans — and R3 explicitly proposes ONE scan finding both (charter #11 unification). Whether config-properties scanning rides component-scanning's discovery substrate (one link-time slice / build-codegen / explicit enable-list) or stays a parallel CONFIG_PROPS slice is a flagged Phase-2 keystone, NOT decided here. component-scanning owns the discovery primitive + include/exclude filters; this feature owns the config-props-specific descriptor content + the stereotype-route JavaBean-only restriction.
- **auto-configuration** — CONSUMER — auto-config classes carry config-properties. The opinionated-defaults layer (libraries shipping `@EnableConfigurationProperties` for their own config types) is a PRIMARY user of the explicit enabling route: an auto-config registers a third-party/library config-properties type that the app didn't name (docs line 1587 'ideal for conditional/auto-config and third-party classes'). This is exactly where R2's explicit-only model has a gap (a library can't contribute a config type the app didn't list) and where R1's slice / R3's bean-definition discovery shine — a real tension surfaced. auto-configuration owns the deferred-import + backoff ordering; this feature owns the config-props registration auto-config emits.
- **bean-definition / bean-registry** — INTEGRATION point — how the bound config object becomes resolvable. The bound value must be published as a resolvable bean under the derived `<prefix>-<type>` name (bean-naming) so consumers can inject `AppProperties`. R1/R2 publish it as a side-table singleton wired into the registry; R3 makes config-properties a first-class BeanDefinition with a binder-backed instance-supplier (the deepest unification, charter #11, but entangles the deferred bean-model keystones). bean-definition/bean-registry own the definition representation + singleton cache; this feature owns the construction STRATEGY (bind-from-Environment, not autowire-collaborators) and the role hint that keeps a config object a pure projection.
- **programmatic-registration** — BACKBONE of the explicit enabling route (the `@EnableConfigurationProperties` analogue). The explicit route (register a named config-props type, ideal for third-party types leaf can't annotate + conditional/auto-config) leans on programmatic-registration's functional, AOT-analyzable instance-supplier contract — a config-props registration is a special instance-supplier (bind-from-Environment). programmatic-registration owns the imperative/conditional registration contract + the instance-supplier model; this feature owns the config-props-flavored supplier + the third-party-prefix-supplied call shape (`config_properties_with`).
- **bean-naming** — CONSUMER — the derived name convention. Auto-registered config-props beans get a deterministic derived name (`<prefix>-<fully.qualified.type>`, docs line 1591) so they don't collide and are resolvable. bean-naming owns the default-name derivation + collision-as-loud-error rule; this feature owns the specific `<prefix>-<type>` convention for config-props beans (distinct from the decapitalized-class-name default for ordinary beans).
- **deferral-primitives** — DOWNSTREAM (if R3 — config-props is a bean). When a config object is a first-class bean (R3), a consumer can inject it as `ObjectProvider<AppProperties>` / lazily / optionally via deferral-primitives, and a config-refresh story interacts with whether consumers hold the value or a provider. R1/R2's side-table value is injected eagerly as `AppProperties`; the provider/lazy access is a capability R3's bean model grants. deferral-primitives owns the 0..1/0..N/lazy access types; this feature only notes that config-as-a-bean unlocks them.
- **origin-tracking** — COMPLEMENTARY — diagnostics provenance. A config-props bind/validation failure must name the offending PROPERTY KEY with its origin (file/line, owning source) AND the matched raw key (the canonical `my.app.item-price` may have matched env `MY_APP_ITEMPRICE`) — so the BindValidationException-equivalent reports 'my.app.timeout must be ≥1 (was 0, from application.yaml:12, matched env MY_APP_TIMEOUT)'. origin-tracking owns the provenance representation; the binder threads the matched raw key; this feature frames the whole-config-object fail-fast error around the property key the user can fix (not the Rust field).
- **value-injection** — SIBLING + contrast (the deliberate philosophical split). @Value (value-injection) is the per-field, expression-capable, eager scalar mechanism; @ConfigurationProperties is the whole-object, INERT (no expressions), relaxed+validated+documented mechanism for groups/hierarchies of settings (docs line 1567). This feature exists partly to REPLACE scattered value-injection for cohesive config. They share the upstream property-resolution read path but differ sharply: value-injection evaluates expressions and converts at the injection point; config-properties binds an inert tree. The contrast IS the design intent.
- **concurrency-contract** — COMPLEMENTARY — safe publication of the config singleton. A bound config object is typically a shared immutable singleton; concurrency-contract guarantees safe publication of the fully-built, validated value so consumers across threads/tasks see a complete object. This feature's bind-then-publish (and R3's bean-instantiation safe-publication) reinforces that a published config is provably valid; a config-refresh atomic-swap (Phase-2) must preserve safe publication without a hot-path lock.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is a config-properties object a first-class BEAN (R3 — maximally unified onto bean-definition/bean-registry/autowiring/lifecycle, injectable + hierarchy-participating, but re-opens the inject-other-beans door Spring discourages and ENTANGLES the deferred bean-model + type-erasure/registry + scope/lifetime keystones) or a SEPARATE inert projection layer (R1/R2 — a side-table of bound values aligned with 'config is inert data, trivially testable outside the container', but a parallel pipeline)? This is THE keystone representation question for the feature and it cross-cuts the type-erasure/registry substrate, the scope/lifetime/ownership model, and the bean-definition representation — all explicitly Phase-2-deferred. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- Which cross-crate substrate backs the SCAN enabling route (`@ConfigurationPropertiesScan`), and does it SHARE one substrate with component-scanning + auto-configuration + the binder/property-resolution handler discovery (charter #11), or stay a parallel CONFIG_PROPS slice? A link-time slice (zero-cost, DCE-hazardous, silent-empty), build-time codegen (deterministic, portable, a build step), or explicit-enable-only (predictable, but loses 'auto' and gaps the auto-config story)? The silent-DCE stakes are HIGHER than for components (a missing config object may boot with default/empty config and misbehave subtly). This is the cross-crate-composition keystone; adopting a shared substrate in Phase 1 would pre-bias the meta-architecture. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- How is the 'pure projection / discourage injecting other beans' rule ENFORCED — structurally (the construction seam hands the binder only `&Environment`, never the bean container, making injection physically impossible) or by convention/lint (Spring's approach)? Structural enforcement requires keeping config-properties OUT of the general autowiring construction path (R1/R2) or rigidly role-gating it within (R3's ConfigBind supplier) — a decision entangled with whether config is a bean (Q1) and with the construction-seam design in the bean-model. Spans bean-definition, autowiring-resolution, and this feature. UNRESOLVED.
- Which bind-METHOD model does leaf adopt given Rust has no JavaBean setter/in-place-mutation convention — faithfully replicate both JavaBean (invent a Default+`&mut`-field convention) and value-object (constructor), or lean value-object-only? And how is the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule honored when Rust cannot field-mutate an arbitrary existing `T`? This feature SURFACES the mode choice but the model is the binder's to resolve; the two features must agree on one convention. Cross-cuts binder + config-properties. UNRESOLVED (deferred to the binder's flagged question).
- Is config-properties diagnostics fail-on-FIRST or an AGGREGATED startup-validation pass collecting EVERY bind/coercion/constraint failure across ALL registered config-props types at once (charter #9 richest diagnostic)? This feature orchestrates the whole sweep, so cross-TYPE aggregation (not just within one object) is its concern — but it cross-cuts validation (constraint failures), the binder (per-leaf failures), property-resolution (a shared validation pass observing placeholder resolution + binding), and the unified diagnostics/error model (charter §3). Whether to aggregate framework-wide must be one policy. UNRESOLVED.
- Where does the metadata/codegen boundary fall for config-properties — does ONE declaration macro emit BOTH the binding artifacts AND the config-metadata (proc-macro, visible only to its own crate) OR is metadata emitted by a separate build.rs/codegen pass that sees the resolved graph (needed for the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` cross-module-reusable-type case where the consuming crate can't see the source)? A proc-macro can't see other crates (cross-crate doc line 89); cross-module metadata reuse needs build-time codegen. Cross-cuts config-metadata, the metadata/codegen boundary (charter §3), and the binder's BindTarget-schema source of truth. UNRESOLVED.
- How is the auto-configuration story served if the SCAN route is explicit-only (R2)? A library/auto-config crate contributing a config-properties type the app didn't name is the WHOLE point of auto-config (libraries shipping their own `@EnableConfigurationProperties`), but R2's explicit-builder model can't express it without the library injecting registrations via its own enable-list — re-introducing a discovery need. This couples the config-properties enabling-route decision to whether dependency-based auto-configuration exists at all (charter §3 deferral) and how auto-config crates contribute beans/config. UNRESOLVED.
- For config-REFRESH (re-bind a config object on source change — an Actuator-style capability), how is a freshly-bound, re-validated config object atomically SWAPPED for the live one without a hot-path lock (charter #5), and does it swap a side-table value (R1/R2) or a singleton-cache bean instance (R3)? Binding produces a fresh owned value (Rust can't mutate a shared `&T` in place); the swap/staleness model spans environment, the binder's re-bind, relaxed-binding's index-invalidation, the scope/lifetime model, and any future config-refresh feature. A Phase-2 concurrency call, entangled with Q1. UNRESOLVED.
- Where does the async pre-materialization pipeline live for a config-properties type whose source backing is remote/async (config bound from a secrets store or remote config server), given the binder + the early-refresh bind sweep MUST be synchronous non-blocking? This is the SAME BootstrapContext-analogue (async fetch → snapshot → sync bind) that property-sources, property-resolution, relaxed-binding, binder, and environment ALL flagged — it must align framework-wide, not be re-invented here, and config-properties is a downstream consumer of whatever that pipeline becomes. UNRESOLVED.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated config-properties strictly as the DECLARATIVE FRONT-END that sits ON TOP of the binder (the engine, already designed, built on concretely not reinvented), which in turn sits on relaxed-binding (key identity), property-resolution (the read path), property-sources (the stack), type-conversion (coercion), and validation (constraints) — and that publishes a bound, validated config object into the container's bean model (container-core/bean-registry). This feature owns ONLY: the prefix-rooted typed-target DECLARATION surface; the THREE enabling routes (explicit / scan / stereotype) + the constructor-binding-restricted-to-explicit-and-scan rule; the leniency-flag DEFAULT POLICY (ignore_unknown_fields=true, ignore_invalid_fields=false) + per-type override; the bind-MODE choice surface (delegating execution to the binder); the 'pure projection / discourage injecting other beans' rule; the derived `<prefix>-<type>` bean-name convention; the WIRING that registers the bound object as a resolvable bean and invokes binder+validation at the early refresh step; and the property-key framing of the fail-fast BindValidationException-equivalent. I deliberately did NOT redesign the bind engine / Bindable / BindResult / BindHandler / tree-descent / collection-replacement (binder), canonical-key identity + per-transport forms + the snake→kebab rule + bracket-escape (relaxed-binding), the ${...} walk + strict/lenient (property-resolution), the stack ordering + never-blend (property-sources), string→T coercion (type-conversion), the constraint engine (validation), metadata emission format (config-metadata), profile/condition grammar (profiles/conditions), bean storage/naming internals (bean-registry/bean-naming), or the refresh-order template (refresh-lifecycle).\n\nThe genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is HOW a type opts in + carries its prefix, HOW the three enabling routes map onto Rust's no-classpath reality, and WHETHER a config object is a bean: R1 = an attribute macro emitting a ConfigProperties trait-impl + a link-time descriptor (the literal @ConfigurationProperties + @ConfigurationPropertiesScan transcription — max intent parity, thin macro, structurally-enforced pure-projection, one descriptor feeds config-metadata, but inherits the full cross-crate DCE hazard with HIGHER stakes than components, generics-can't-register on the scan route, and lightly pre-judges a link-time substrate). R2 = explicit programmatic registration via a typed App builder (bevy/dill style — max predictability + reliability + wasm support + first-class third-party-type handling + generics-friendly + thinnest macro, but sacrifices the annotate-and-forget DX, makes 'scan' into list-crates-once boilerplate, and GAPS the auto-configuration story where a library wants to contribute a config type the app didn't name). R3 = config-properties as a first-class bean-definition role with a binder-backed instance-supplier (maximal charter #11 unification — reuses component-scanning/programmatic-registration/autowiring/bean-naming/conditions/lifecycle, makes config injectable as T/ObjectProvider<T>, articulates Spring's constructor-restriction rule cleanly as a construction-strategy seam, but is the MOST deferral-entangled — pre-judges the bean-model + type-erasure/registry + scope/lifetime keystones — and partly re-opens the inject-other-beans door Spring discourages, risking the 'config is inert data' intent). R1↔R2 differ on auto-discovery vs explicit composition; R1/R2↔R3 differ on side-table-projection vs config-is-a-bean.\n\nAll three: keep config-properties binding SYNCHRONOUS and non-blocking on a COLD early-refresh path (charter #4 — after property-source materialization, before consuming eager singletons, 'bound very early'; remote/async-backed config sources pre-snapshotted in a cold async BootstrapContext step shared with all the config neighbours); keep binding INERT (no expression evaluation — the deliberate split from @Value); enforce the pure-projection rule via a construction seam that hands the binder only the Environment read view, never the bean container; fail-fast ALL-OR-NOTHING with a rich, ideally AGGREGATED (every config-props type at once) BindValidationException-equivalent framed around the PROPERTY KEY + origin + matched-raw-key + candidates (charter #9); keep the Unbound (defaults/bind_or_create) vs Failed (config present but bad) distinction sharp (binder's three-state monad); keep the enabling-route / discovery seam ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (erased bind fn-pointer so native + future WASM-module config sources slot in identically); preserve a non-bean `binder::bind::<T>()` escape hatch so config objects stay testable/serializable outside the container; and keep macros THIN (charter #10 — the declaration macro emits only a trait impl + (R1) a descriptor + a forwarding binder call, all hand-writable; the explicit/builder route is plain typed Rust).\n\nNightly review (against rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md): nothing needs nightly — const descriptors + const TypeId::of (1.91) for the registry rows, distributed slices via linkme (stable, pinned ≥0.3.24, behind-flag) for R1's scan route, Any/downcast (stable) for the erased bound-value channel if config is stored type-erased, enums + fn-pointers + typed builders + derive-emitted const data are all stable, and the bind sweep is SYNCHRONOUS so no AFIT/RPITIT boxing tax on the descriptor/supplier. The cross-crate scan route (R1) shares the SAME link-time-registry/DCE substrate concern (linkme default 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath', selection/ordering by descriptor DATA never link order, force-link of opted-in crates, mandatory zero-contribution self-check / `leaf doctor` line) as component-scanning + auto-config + the binder/property-resolution handler discovery; the explicit route (R2, and R1's escape hatch) is Layer-0-safe and the universal/wasm fallback (Architecture D/C); whether config-properties scanning SHARES one substrate with component-scanning is flagged UNRESOLVED for Phase 2, consistent with Phase 1 staying implementation-agnostic. The sharpest Phase-2 tensions I surfaced but did NOT resolve: is-config-a-bean (the keystone, Q1), the scan discovery substrate + DCE-with-higher-stakes (Q2), structural-vs-lint enforcement of pure-projection (Q3), the bind-method model deferred to the binder (Q4), aggregated-vs-fail-first diagnostics (Q5), the metadata/codegen boundary incl. the v4 cross-module @ConfigurationPropertiesSource case (Q6), the auto-configuration-vs-explicit-route gap (Q7), and the config-refresh atomic-swap concurrency story (Q8). Naming ('ConfigProperties', 'ConfigPropsDescriptor', 'BindLeniency', 'ConfigBindError', 'InstanceSupplier::ConfigBind', 'config_properties_with/_if/_scan!') is Phase-1 placeholder. I wrote no files.\n\nRelevant grounded source paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (1553-1624 the dedicated @ConfigurationProperties section — prefix/kebab-canonical 1555/1565, leniency flags 1565, config-is-data-not-code/no-SpEL/discourage-injecting-beans 1567/1593, two binding modes + empty-@DefaultValue + public-field-removal 1569-1583, three enabling routes + constructor-restriction + derived bean name 1585-1593, the Binder/Bindable/BindResult/BindHandler 1595-1606, collections-replaced-not-merged + conversion + @ConfigurationPropertiesBinding-static 1608-1612, @Validated + BindValidationException + configurationPropertiesValidator 1614-1616, config-metadata + v4 @ConfigurationPropertiesSource 1618-1624; plus 1329 @Profile placement on config-props, 1535 relaxed-binding equivalence); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md (invariants §2 esp. DX#1/overhead#2/async-first§2.3/reactive§2.4/no-global-locks§2.5/stable§2.8/rich-diagnostics§2.9/thin-macros§2.10/unification§2.11; deferred keystones §3 esp. metadata-codegen-boundary/type-erasure-registry/scope-lifetime/cross-crate; topology §6); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (Layer 0 unreferenced-crate 149, Layer A rustc-reachability 139, Layer B --gc-sections 143, silent-DCE self-check mandate 152, generics-can't-register 153, ordering-unspecified 154, register-descriptors-not-live-objects 155, four Architectures A/B/C/D 277-331, role-separation 233, binary-sees-whole-graph 260, two-source duality / scope-discovery 362); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (const TypeId::of 1.91 line 16, Any+downcast line 17, linkme behind-flag line 30, no-nightly-needed line 76, async Drop absence as a design constraint line 86 — relevant to config-refresh shutdown/swap).

## Binder API  `[binder]`

This feature is the PROGRAMMATIC BINDING ENGINE that projects a tree of externalized configuration (the ordered, first-source-wins ConfigurationPropertySource stack) onto a strongly-typed target rooted at a kebab-case prefix — the machinery `config-properties` (`@ConfigurationProperties`) uses internally, exposed as a standalone API. Spring's intent (docs §"The Binder API" + §"Collections, conversion, and validation" + §"Two binding modes") has SIX load-bearing parts to replicate as INTENT, not mechanism:\n\n(1) **A `Bindable<T>` target descriptor** — carries the target TYPE plus binding metadata: the constructors `of`, `ofInstance` (existing value), `listOf`/`setOf`/`mapOf` (container shapes), and builder modifiers `withAnnotations`, `withExistingValue`, `withSuppliedValue`, `withBindMethod`, `withBindRestrictions`. It is the self-describing 'what am I binding onto, and how' handed to `bind(prefix, bindable)`. In Rust, with no runtime reflection, the divergent question is HOW a target describes its own tree-shape (its fields/params, their names, their nested types) to the binder.\n\n(2) **Bind-method selection (the `BindMethod` enum: JAVA_BEAN vs VALUE_OBJECT).** JavaBean/setter binding (default): no-arg construct, then set each property (supports in-place mutation of pre-initialized collections/nested POJOs). Value-object/constructor binding (immutable, records): bind every constructor PARAMETER from config and construct once; `@DefaultValue` supplies param defaults, an EMPTY `@DefaultValue` on a nested param forces a non-null nested instance. THE hard rule: **an existing or supplied value forces JAVA_BEAN** (you cannot constructor-bind onto an instance that already exists). leaf must replicate this two-mode dispatch and the forcing rule.\n\n(3) **`BindResult<T>` — a result MONAD.** `isBound`/`get`/`orElse`/`map`, plus `bindOrCreate` (bind, else synthesize a default instance). It cleanly distinguishes 'nothing in config matched this prefix' (UNBOUND — not an error) from 'config matched but coercion/validation failed' (a hard FAILURE). leaf's natural shape is a three-state outcome (bound / unbound / failed), NOT a bare `Result` that conflates unbound with error.\n\n(4) **`BindHandler` lifecycle hook** — `onStart`/`onSuccess`/`onFailure`/`onFinish` per bound element, the SAME machinery `@ConfigurationProperties` uses internally (e.g. `ValidationBindHandler` runs JSR-303 on each bound object). It is an observer/interceptor/validator chain threaded through the recursive descent. This is explicitly the SAME family as property-resolution's flagged `ResolveHandler` (charter #11 unification candidate).\n\n(5) **Collections/maps are REPLACED, not deep-merged across sources.** A `List`/`Set`/`Map` comes entirely from the SINGLE highest-precedence source that defines it (no appending from a lower source); scalars follow normal precedence. Lists bind via `[index]` (files) / comma-split scalars; maps bind child keys directly under the prefix; nested objects descend one prefix segment per level. This 'one source owns the whole collection' rule is a binder invariant distinct from the stack's per-scalar first-source-wins.\n\n(6) **Conversion + fail-fast validation seams.** Each leaf value is coerced via the `type-conversion` neighbour (Duration/Period/DataSize suffixes, case-insensitive enums); validation (JSR-303 analogue) runs on each bound object and FAILS FAST at startup with a rich aggregated error rather than a deferred NPE. The two leniency flags: `ignoreUnknownFields` (default true — stray keys ignored) and `ignoreInvalidFields` (default false — coercion failure throws).\n\nDESIGN INTENT (the why): replace scattered, stringly-typed `@Value` reads with ONE cohesive, validated, documented config OBJECT that is a pure projection of the Environment, bound very early, fails fast, and is trivially testable/serializable. Config is DATA bound to a type — deliberately inert (no SpEL in binding, unlike `@Value`).\n\nSCOPE BOUNDARY (what THIS feature owns vs neighbours): `property-sources` owns the ordered stack + first-source-wins + never-blend; `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` placeholder walk + strict/lenient + the read interface; `relaxed-binding` owns canonical-key identity + per-transport name forms + the list/map index conventions + the bracket-escape; `type-conversion` owns string→T coercion; `config-properties` owns the prefix-rooted typed-target DECLARATION + the enabling routes + leniency-flag policy; `config-metadata` owns compile-time discoverable property metadata; `validation` owns the constraint engine. THIS feature owns ONLY: the `Bindable` target-shape DESCRIPTOR contract, the recursive TREE-DESCENT that maps property names to target slots, the bind-METHOD selection (constructor vs setter) + the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule, the collection/map REPLACEMENT (one-source-owns) rule, the `BindResult` three-state MONAD, the `BindHandler` observer/validator chain, and the orchestration of conversion+validation at each node. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: HOW a typed target self-describes its tree-shape WITHOUT runtime reflection (a derived trait emitting a static schema vs per-field closures vs a serde-Deserializer-shaped pull bridge), HOW bind-method dispatch is represented (an enum on a node-walker vs two trait impls vs a single visitor), and WHERE the monad+handler policy is carried so it shares maximal machinery with property-resolution's ResolveHandler.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Derived BindTarget schema + a recursive value-walker (the literal Binder/Bindable transcription)
Model the binder as the most direct Rust transcription of Spring's `Binder` + `Bindable`. A target type implements (via `#[derive(BindTarget)]`) a trait that yields a STATIC, reflection-free SCHEMA describing its tree-shape; a hand-written recursive `Binder` walks that schema against the resolved source stack, descending one prefix segment per level, and assembles the typed value.

```rust
pub trait BindTarget: Sized {
    const SCHEMA: &'static NodeSchema;   // const, fully describes fields/params, names, nested kinds
    fn bind(node: &mut BindCursor<'_>) -> BindOutcome<Self>;   // emitted: reads each slot, recurses
}
pub enum NodeSchema {
    Scalar,                                              // a leaf coerced via type-conversion
    Object { method: BindMethod, fields: &'static [Field] },
    List(&'static NodeSchema), Set(&'static NodeSchema), Map(&'static NodeSchema),
}
pub struct Field { canonical: &'static str /*kebab*/, schema: &'static NodeSchema, default: Option<DefaultValue>, has_setter: bool }
pub enum BindMethod { JavaBean, ValueObject }

pub struct Bindable<T: BindTarget> { existing: Option<T>, supplied: Option<Box<dyn FnOnce()->T>>, method_override: Option<BindMethod>, restrictions: BindRestrictions, _t: PhantomData<T> }
impl<T: BindTarget> Bindable<T> {
    pub fn of() -> Self;  pub fn of_instance(v: T) -> Self;            // existing forces JavaBean
    pub fn with_bind_method(self, m: BindMethod) -> Self; /* ... */
}
pub struct Binder<'s> { resolver: &'s dyn PropertyResolver, conv: &'s ConversionService, handler: &'s dyn BindHandler }
impl<'s> Binder<'s> {
    pub fn bind<T: BindTarget>(&self, prefix: &str, b: Bindable<T>) -> BindResult<T>;
    pub fn bind_or_create<T: BindTarget + Default>(&self, prefix: &str, b: Bindable<T>) -> T;
}
pub enum BindResult<T> { Bound(T), Unbound, Failed(BindError) }   // three-state monad: is_bound/get/or_else/map
```
The `derive(BindTarget)` macro emits ONLY: a `const SCHEMA` data literal (field canonical names derived snake→kebab via relaxed-binding's rule, nested schemas referenced by `<FieldTy as BindTarget>::SCHEMA`), and a thin `bind` fn that calls hand-writable cursor APIs (`cursor.scalar::<T>()`, `cursor.descend(field)`, `cursor.list_of::<E>()`). The walker selects BindMethod from `SCHEMA` (override > existing-value-forces-JavaBean > derived default), descends one segment per object level building the child prefix as a `ConfigPropertyName` (relaxed-binding), and for each leaf asks `resolver.get_property(child_key)` then coerces via `type-conversion`. **Collection replacement**: at a List/Map node the walker finds the SINGLE highest-precedence source that defines ANY indexed child under the node prefix and binds the whole collection from THAT source only (never appending across sources) — a query the resolver/relaxed layer must answer ('which source owns this collection root'). **BindHandler** is invoked `on_start`/`on_success`/`on_failure`/`on_finish` at every node; the stock `ValidationBindHandler` runs `validation` on each completed object. The macro is thin: all logic (descent, method selection, replacement, monad) is hand-writable runtime code in `leaf-core`.

**Pros:** Most literal intent parity: `Bindable<T>` with its constructors/builders, the `BindMethod` enum, the `BindResult` monad, and the `BindHandler` onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish are a line-for-line transcription — a Spring developer recognizes the exact API and mental model (charter #1 DX, #2 intent-shape).; The `const SCHEMA` is a reflection-FREE, fully-static description of the target tree — no runtime type introspection (which Rust lacks), computed once at compile time, embeddable as a `const`/`static` (aligns with const TypeId/const-eval baseline); the walker reads pure data, no per-bind allocation for the schema itself (charter #5).; ONE owner for tree-descent + method-selection + collection-replacement (the walker), so the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule, the snake→kebab name derivation (delegated to relaxed-binding), and the one-source-owns-collection rule live in a single legible place rather than scattered (charter #11 unification within the feature).; Thin macro (charter #10): `derive(BindTarget)` emits only a data literal + a cursor-calling `bind` fn — every line is hand-writable against the public cursor API; `cargo expand` is legible; the programmatic escape hatch (hand-implement `BindTarget`) exists at every level.; `BindHandler` is deliberately the SAME observer shape as property-resolution's flagged `ResolveHandler` (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish), directly advancing the charter #11 unification candidate; validation slots in as a stock handler, not a special case (matching Spring's `ValidationBindHandler`).

**Cons:** The `const SCHEMA` must encode nested target schemas by reference (`<FieldTy as BindTarget>::SCHEMA`), which works for a static tree but is awkward for RECURSIVE config types (a type containing `Vec<Self>` or a cyclic nesting) — a const self-reference needs a function-pointer or lazy indirection, an ergonomic wrinkle Spring's runtime reflection never hit.; Two bind-methods (JavaBean in-place mutation vs value-object construct-from-params) demand two distinct emitted code paths in the `bind` fn — JavaBean needs `Default`+setters (mutating an instance), value-object needs all params resolved before a single construct call; the macro must generate BOTH shapes and the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule means a value-object type bound onto an existing instance must FALL BACK to field-wise mutation, which an immutable type may not support — a real representational tension (Rust has no universal setter).; The walker re-walks the full schema on every `bind` call with no memoization; for a hot re-bind (a refreshable config object re-bound on change) the descent + per-leaf relaxed lookup repeats — acceptable on the cold startup path, but no amortization for any future config-refresh hot path.; Collection-replacement ('which single source owns this collection root') requires a capability the resolver/relaxed layer must expose (enumerate indexed children per source, pick the highest-precedence source defining any) — a non-trivial query that couples this feature to whether sources are enumerable (relaxed-binding's R3 index gives it cheaply; R1/R2 candidate-probing makes it harder), a cross-feature dependency that must be pinned.; `BindMethod` derivation from a Rust type is heuristic: Spring infers value-object from 'a single non-private non-@Autowired constructor (records get it free)'; Rust has no canonical 'JavaBean' (no universal getter/setter convention), so leaf must DEFINE the convention (e.g. a struct with `Default` + public fields = JavaBean; a type with a `#[constructor_binding]`-marked `new` = value-object), a convention this feature must invent rather than transcribe.

**Mechanisms considered:** `#[derive(BindTarget)]` emitting a `const SCHEMA: &'static NodeSchema` data literal + a thin cursor-calling `bind` fn (thin macro, all logic in leaf-core); a hand-written recursive `Binder` walker that descends one prefix segment per object level, building child keys as relaxed-binding `ConfigPropertyName`s; `BindResult<T>` as a three-state enum (Bound/Unbound/Failed) with monad ops (is_bound/get/or_else/map) + `bind_or_create` via a `Default` bound; `BindMethod` enum selection: override > existing-value-forces-JavaBean > derived-from-type-shape default; `BindHandler` trait (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish) shaped identically to property-resolution's ResolveHandler (charter #11), with a stock ValidationBindHandler; collection-replacement via a 'which source owns this collection root' query delegated to the relaxed/source layer (enumerable-source dependent); stable-only: const data, enums, `Box<dyn FnOnce>` for supplied values, object-safe `BindHandler`, `PhantomData`; synchronous walk so no async-trait machinery on the binder core

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The `Binder`, `Bindable`, `BindResult`, `BindMethod`, `BindTarget`, `NodeSchema`, and `BindHandler` are kernel types in `leaf-core`, named by absolute path. The CORE binder needs NO cross-crate registration — it is a pure consumer of a target's `const SCHEMA` (emitted at the target's own crate by `derive(BindTarget)`, using fully-qualified `::leaf_core::...` paths per proc-macro hygiene) plus the resolver/conversion seams it borrows. Cross-crate enters ONLY through the `derive(BindTarget)` macro (each config type in any downstream crate emits its OWN schema locally — NO link-time registry needed, because the binder is invoked WITH a concrete `T` whose schema is reached via the trait, exactly like serde's Deserialize: no discovery, just a per-type derived impl) and through one OPTIONAL extension point carrying the static-link-registry-plus-optional-dynamic-directory duality as CANDIDATES (not decisions): pluggable `BindHandler`s or custom per-type binders (a third-party type's bespoke binding logic, or a cross-cutting handler like a metrics/audit observer). IF leaf ever auto-discovers handlers across crates, they would be `const HandlerDescriptor { priority, applies_to, ctor_fn }` in a `linkme` distributed-slice (default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned set (the WASM-module 'classpath'), with DCE guardrails (const descriptors, runtime ordering by priority DATA never link order, force-link of opted-in crates, a zero-contribution self-check). CRITICAL difference from component-scanning: a config type does NOT need link-time discovery — it is bound by NAME at a known call site (`bind::<MyProps>(...)`), so the binder is largely cross-crate-INERT; only the optional handler/custom-binder extension touches the discovery substrate, shared (as a Phase-2 question) with property-resolution's ResolveHandler discovery. Generics caveat: a generic config type `Foo<T>` has no single `const SCHEMA` until monomorphized — fine here because binding always names a concrete `T` at the call site (no registration of the generic needed), unlike a discovered component.

**T2 — execution context:** Binding runs on a COLD path by default — it is bootstrap-time work (binding `@ConfigurationProperties`-equivalent objects during container refresh, 'bound very early' per Spring intent). The recursive walk + per-leaf `resolver.get_property` + `type-conversion` coercion are pure SYNCHRONOUS CPU over already-materialized strings; the binder MUST NOT `.await` or block (charter #4 — and the walk is synchronous so it carries no async-trait/RPITIT boxing tax on the binder core). Any source whose backing is remote/async must have been snapshotted into the stack during a cold async pre-step BEFORE the binder runs (BootstrapContext discipline, inherited from property-sources/property-resolution). Errors are rich, aggregated, synchronous values: `BindError` carries the full causal chain — prefix, the property name being bound, the target field/param, the raw value found + its origin, the conversion/validation failure, and CANDIDATES (charter #9), and ideally aggregates ALL failures in a startup-validation pass (fail with every bad field at once, not first-fail). The UNBOUND state is `BindResult::Unbound` (absence — NOT an error; falls through to `orElse`/`bindOrCreate`), kept DISTINCT from `Failed` (config present but bad). No cancellation concern on the synchronous walk (bounded CPU by schema size × source count); any async pre-materialization is a separate cold step with its own cancellation. The produced typed `T` is owned (moved out of `BindResult`), `Send + Sync` if its fields are, so a bound config object crosses `.await`/threads freely as a singleton; the `Binder` itself borrows the resolver for the bind call's duration, so the stack's cross-task reachability stays the `environment` neighbour's concern. A future config-refresh re-bind is a cold, cancellable background task — never a hot-path operation; an atomic-swap of the new bound object is a Phase-2 concurrency call (flagged, not decided).

#### R2 — Serde-Deserializer-shaped pull bridge: bind by driving the target's Deserialize over a config-tree data model
Invert R1's push-walker into a serde-style PULL model: treat the config source stack as a `Deserializer` data-format and let the TARGET drive binding through the standard `serde::Deserialize` machinery (or a leaf-native `FromConfig` mirror of it). The binder becomes a `ConfigDeserializer` adapter over the resolved, relaxed, origin-tracked stack; the target's derived `Deserialize` impl pulls fields by name; relaxed-binding canonicalizes each requested key; type-conversion is wired in as the scalar deserialization step.

```rust
pub struct ConfigDeserializer<'s> { prefix: ConfigPropertyName, resolver: &'s dyn PropertyResolver, conv: &'s ConversionService, handler: &'s dyn BindHandler, origin: OriginCtx }
impl<'de, 's> serde::Deserializer<'de> for &mut ConfigDeserializer<'s> {
    fn deserialize_struct(self, name, fields, visitor) -> Result<V, BindError> { /* for each field: canonicalize prefix+field, recurse a child deserializer, drive visitor */ }
    fn deserialize_seq(...) /* list: find the one owning source, replace-not-merge */ 
    fn deserialize_map(...) /* map: child keys under prefix, env lowercase-name rule */
    fn deserialize_str/.../bool(...) -> coerce via type-conversion from the resolved raw value
}
// Public API stays Spring-shaped:
pub fn bind<T: DeserializeOwned>(prefix: &str, env: &Environment) -> BindResult<T>;
```
The big win: a config type is just `#[derive(Deserialize)]` (or `#[derive(FromConfig)]`) — ZERO bespoke binder schema, full reuse of serde's mature, battle-tested derive (field renaming via `#[serde(rename)]`, defaults via `#[serde(default)]`, flattening, enum representations), and the ENTIRE Rust ecosystem's existing config structs bind for free. The `BindMethod` distinction mostly DISSOLVES: serde's derive already constructs the value from its fields (value-object-like) and handles defaults; there is no JavaBean in-place mutation because serde always constructs. `BindResult` wraps serde's `Result` into the three-state monad (a serde 'missing field' at the root → Unbound; a present-but-bad field → Failed). The `BindHandler` is harder to thread (serde gives no per-node onSuccess hook natively), so leaf either (a) layers handler callbacks at the `ConfigDeserializer`'s struct/field entry points, or (b) accepts a thinner handler surface than R1. `@DefaultValue`/empty-default maps to `#[serde(default)]`/`#[serde(default = "...")]`; relaxed-binding canonicalizes each `deserialize_struct` field key before lookup; collection-replacement is enforced inside `deserialize_seq`/`deserialize_map` (pick the one owning source, never merge).

**Pros:** MASSIVE DX win and ecosystem reuse (charter #1): a config type is plain `#[derive(Deserialize)]` — no leaf-specific derive to learn, every existing serde config struct in the Rust ecosystem binds for free, and serde's mature features (rename, default, flatten, untagged enums, skip) come along — the most idiomatic-Rust realization of 'config is data bound to a type'.; ZERO bespoke schema/macro maintenance for the common case: leaf writes ONE `Deserializer` adapter, not a `BindTarget` derive + walker; serde's derive (the most-tested derive in Rust) does the tree-shape description, defaults, and construction — dramatically less leaf-owned codegen (charter #10 in spirit: the 'macro' is serde's, already hand-writable-equivalent).; The `BindMethod` JavaBean-vs-value-object dichotomy largely DISSOLVES — serde always constructs from fields with defaults, which is exactly the value-object/record path Spring prefers for immutable config; no need to invent a Rust 'JavaBean setter' convention (R1's awkward con), and no existing-value-forces-JavaBean special case because there is no in-place-mutation mode (binding always produces a fresh value).; Relaxed-binding and type-conversion slot in at precisely the serde extension points (`deserialize_struct` field keys → canonicalize; scalar `deserialize_*` → coerce), a clean composition; origin-tracking threads through the deserializer context so a coercion error still reports file+line + matched raw key.; Async-free, synchronous, allocation-conscious: serde's pull model visits exactly the fields the type declares (no speculative full-schema walk), and the `Cow`/borrowed-value discipline of serde keeps scalar binding allocation-light on the hot leaf path (charter #4/#5).

**Cons:** Serde's data model is a poor fit for the binder's CORE invariants: (a) collection-REPLACEMENT-not-merge across sources is invisible to serde (serde sees one logical document, not a precedence stack) — leaf must enforce 'one source owns the collection' INSIDE `deserialize_seq`/`deserialize_map` against the stack, fighting serde's single-document assumption; (b) relaxed-binding's MANY syntactic forms per key (env four-candidate, list `_0_`/`[index]`, bracket-escape) must all be reconciled behind a serde field-name lookup, which serde never anticipated — a leaky, intricate adapter.; The `BindHandler` (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish per node) — the EXPLICIT 'same machinery @ConfigurationProperties uses internally' Spring intent and a charter #11 unification anchor with property-resolution's ResolveHandler — has NO native serde seam; leaf can only approximate it at the deserializer's struct/field boundaries, yielding a THINNER, less faithful handler than R1, and weakening the unification story.; Diagnostics regress: serde's `Error` is a flat string-ish trait designed for parse errors, not the rich, aggregated, candidate-listing `BindError` the charter (#9) wants; capturing 'which field, which target param, what was expected, what raw value + origin, all failures at once' through serde's `Visitor`/`Error` plumbing is awkward and tends toward first-failure-aborts rather than a full startup-validation aggregate.; Couples leaf's config-binding identity to `serde` (a non-leaf dependency on a core path) — a `FromConfig` mirror avoids the hard dependency but then RE-INTRODUCES the bespoke derive R2 was meant to eliminate, collapsing back toward R1; and Spring's deliberate 'binding is INERT (no SpEL/expression)' is easy to violate if a serde format-ish thinks values are richer than raw strings.; `config-metadata` (compile-time discoverable property surface) is harder to emit from serde's derive (which leaf doesn't own) than from a leaf-owned `BindTarget` derive that could co-emit metadata — a real loss for the self-documenting-config story (charter #1, and the config-metadata neighbour).

**Mechanisms considered:** a `serde::Deserializer` adapter (`ConfigDeserializer`) over the resolved/relaxed/origin-tracked stack, driving the target's standard `#[derive(Deserialize)]`; OR a leaf-native `FromConfig`/`Deserializer`-mirror trait (avoids the hard serde dependency but reintroduces a bespoke derive); relaxed-binding canonicalization injected at `deserialize_struct` field-key lookup; type-conversion injected at scalar `deserialize_*`; collection-replacement enforced inside `deserialize_seq`/`deserialize_map` (pick the one owning source) — fighting serde's single-document model; `@DefaultValue`/empty-default mapped to `#[serde(default)]`/`#[serde(default="...")]`; BindResult wrapping serde's Result into Bound/Unbound/Failed; approximate BindHandler callbacks at the deserializer's struct/field entry points (thinner than R1's per-node handler); stable-only: serde derive, object-safe handler, `Cow`; synchronous deserialization (no async on the bind path)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Even MORE cross-crate-inert than R1 on the target side: a config type binds via its own crate's `#[derive(Deserialize)]` (serde's derive, fully-qualified paths, no leaf macro at all) — NO leaf registration, NO discovery, the binder is invoked by NAME with a concrete `T: DeserializeOwned` at a known call site. This is the cleanest cross-crate story (serde's derive already solves the per-type-impl-in-arbitrary-crate problem the way leaf wants). The `ConfigDeserializer` adapter lives in `leaf-core`. Cross-crate touches only the OPTIONAL extension points: custom scalar converters (delegated to the `type-conversion` neighbour's registry, which carries its OWN discovery question) and optional `BindHandler`s — IF auto-discovered, same `linkme`-slice-default-plus-optional-dynamic-directory duality + DCE guardrails as R1, selection by priority DATA. A subtlety: because the binder rides serde, a third-party config type from ANY crate that already derives `Deserialize` binds with zero leaf awareness — maximal reach with zero registration, but it also means leaf cannot easily emit `config-metadata` for types it never sees a leaf-derive on (the metadata-generation gap noted in cons). No generic-registration hazard (binding names a concrete `T` at the call site; serde monomorphizes per instantiation).

**T2 — execution context:** Same cold-path bootstrap execution as R1: deserialization-driven binding is synchronous CPU over an already-materialized, snapshotted stack; the `Deserializer` impl MUST NOT `.await`/block (charter #4) — any remote/async source is pre-snapshotted in a cold async BootstrapContext step before binding (inherited discipline). Serde's pull model is bounded synchronous recursion (by the target's declared shape), no cancellation concern. Errors propagate through serde's `Error`/`Result` — synchronous values, but with the diagnostic-richness regression noted (mapping serde's flat error into the charter's aggregated `BindError` is the lossy seam); the Unbound-vs-Failed distinction is reconstructed at the top by inspecting whether the root prefix matched anything. The produced `T` is owned + `Send+Sync` if its fields are, crossing `.await`/threads freely as a singleton. The `ConfigDeserializer` borrows the resolver/stack for the call's duration (cross-task reachability = environment's concern). A config-refresh re-bind is again a cold, cancellable background task; the BindHandler/observer callbacks, where leaf can install them at struct/field boundaries, are synchronous non-blocking observers (never an await point), consistent with property-resolution's ResolveHandler contract.

#### R3 — Layered StringValueResolver-style binder pipeline: a DataObjectBinder chain + per-node BindHandler policy (the binder-grade extensible engine, unified with property-resolution)
Model binding as a small COMPOSABLE ENGINE that DELIBERATELY shares its substrate with property-resolution's flagged R3 (the ResolutionContext + handler-chain design): a `BindContext` carrying the resolver/conversion/origin seams, an ordered chain of `DataObjectBinder`s (Spring's actual internal abstraction — a `ValueObjectBinder` and a `JavaBeanBinder` are the two stock links, mirroring Spring's literal `Binder` internals), and a `BindHandler` chain that observes/customizes/validates each node — so the binder and the resolver share ONE handler family and ONE context-threading discipline (charter #11).

```rust
pub trait DataObjectBinder {   // tries to bind ONE object node; first-binder-wins, like first-source-wins
    fn bind<T>(&self, name: &ConfigPropertyName, target: &Bindable<T>, cx: &BindContext) -> Option<BindOutcome<T>>;
}
// chain: [ValueObjectBinder (constructor/record), JavaBeanBinder (default+setters/mutate), <user binders>]
pub trait BindHandler {   // SAME shape as property-resolution's ResolveHandler (charter #11)
    fn on_start(&self, name: &ConfigPropertyName, target: &BindableMeta) -> ControlFlow {..}
    fn on_success(&self, name: &ConfigPropertyName, result: &BoundValue) -> BoundValue {..}  // may replace/transform
    fn on_failure(&self, name: &ConfigPropertyName, err: BindError) -> Result<BoundValue, BindError> {..}  // may recover
    fn on_finish(&self, name: &ConfigPropertyName, ctx: &BindContext) {..}
}
pub struct BindContext<'s> { resolver:&'s dyn PropertyResolver, conv:&'s ConversionService, binders:&'s [Box<dyn DataObjectBinder>], handler:&'s dyn BindHandler, depth_guard: DepthGuard }
```
The orchestrator descends the property tree; at each OBJECT node it tries the `DataObjectBinder` chain in order (ValueObject first if the target shape/override allows, else JavaBean), with the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule enforced as a CHAIN-FILTER (an existing value removes ValueObjectBinder from contention). Each LEAF goes through resolver+conversion. Each node fires the `BindHandler` chain: `on_start` (skip/proceed — the leniency `ignoreUnknownFields` is a handler decision), `on_success` (transform — e.g. the `ValidationBindHandler` validates the completed object here), `on_failure` (recover or rethrow — the `ignoreInvalidFields` leniency lives here), `on_finish`. The `BindResult` three-state monad wraps the outcome. **Strict/lenient and validation are PLUGGABLE handlers**, exactly as in property-resolution's R3 — and crucially the SAME `ResolveHandler`/`BindHandler` family, so a unified diagnostics/validation pass can observe BOTH placeholder resolution AND binding in one startup-validation sweep. Collection-replacement is a stock concern of the orchestrator (one owning source). This is the heaviest realization but the one that most directly delivers Spring's 'BindHandler is the SAME machinery @ConfigurationProperties uses internally' and the charter #11 unification with property-resolution.
