**Pros:** Most faithful to the DEEP Spring intent that `BindHandler` IS the internal machinery (`ValidationBindHandler` etc.) — strict/lenient (`ignoreUnknownFields`/`ignoreInvalidFields`), validation, audit, and a 'collect ALL bind failures and report once' startup-validation pass all become PLUGGABLE handlers rather than hard-coded forks (charter #9 richest aggregated diagnostic; charter #1 DX of a single fail-fast report).; Maximally advances charter #11 unification: the `BindHandler` is the SAME family as property-resolution's flagged `ResolveHandler` (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish), so the binder and the resolver share ONE handler substrate, ONE context-threading discipline, and ONE diagnostics/validation-pass mechanism — the strongest signal toward a unified Phase-2 toolkit.; The `DataObjectBinder` chain is a clean, EXTENSIBLE home for bind-method dispatch: ValueObjectBinder and JavaBeanBinder are stock links (transcribing Spring's literal internals), and a third-party type with bespoke binding (a builder-pattern type, a newtype, a foreign type leaf can't derive on) ships its OWN binder link — origin-agnostic by construction (charter #6), where R1/R2 would need a hand-impl or are stuck.; first-binder-wins in the chain mirrors first-source-wins in the stack and first-resolver-wins in property-resolution's R3 — ONE consistent precedence mental model across all three features (charter #1 DX), and the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule expressed cleanly as a chain filter rather than a special case.; The handler observing every node is the natural, hot-path-free instrumentation point for `origin-tracking`/`condition-report`-style diagnostics ('this field bound to X from source Y via raw key Z') and for `config-metadata` cross-checks — a second pass is never needed.

**Cons:** By FAR the most machinery (binder chain + handler chain + context + depth guard) for a feature whose 95% case is 'bind this struct from this prefix' — a real over-engineering risk in direct tension with charter #2/#5 (don't build mechanism for its own sake); the simple `bind::<MyProps>()` call pays the abstraction tax even when no custom binder/handler is installed.; `Box<dyn DataObjectBinder>` chain + `&dyn BindHandler` introduce dynamic dispatch + heap allocation on a path R1 (a monomorphic walker) and R2 (serde's static dispatch) keep lighter; the binder is mostly a COLD-path so the overhead is tolerable, but it must be justified purely by the extensibility/unification win, not raw speed.; Binding a typed `T` through a `dyn DataObjectBinder` chain is GENERICS-vs-dyn awkward: `fn bind<T>(...)` is generic but the chain is `dyn`, so either the chain dispatches via a type-erased seam (TypeId + downcast, or a per-type registered binder shim) or the generic flows in some other way — a real representational friction (Rust's monomorphization vs the dyn chain) that Spring's erased JVM generics never faced.; Coupling the binder's handler+chain shape to property-resolution's R3 PRE-BIASES a Phase-2 unification that is properly Phase 2's call — adopting this shared substrate in Phase 1 risks distorting the meta-architecture signal (charter operating rule: Phase 1 stays implementation-agnostic); presented here strictly as a CANDIDATE shape, explicitly deferred.; The chain's cross-crate discovery (user `DataObjectBinder`s / `BindHandler`s) makes this the realization MOST exposed to the link-time-registration + DCE hazard — the very complexity R1/R2 mostly sidestep by binding a named concrete `T` with no discovery; a silently-dropped custom binder would make a whole config type bind wrong with NO error.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `DataObjectBinder` chain (first-binder-wins) with stock `ValueObjectBinder` (constructor/record) + `JavaBeanBinder` (Default+setters/mutate) links — transcribing Spring's literal Binder internals; a `BindHandler` chain shaped IDENTICALLY to property-resolution's ResolveHandler (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish) for charter #11 unification; strict/lenient (`ignoreUnknownFields`/`ignoreInvalidFields`) + validation + a collect-all-failures startup-validation pass expressed as stock handler impls; existing-value-forces-JavaBean enforced as a chain FILTER (existing value removes ValueObjectBinder from contention); type-erasure seam (TypeId + downcast, or per-type registered binder shim) to flow a generic `T` through a `dyn DataObjectBinder` chain; optional cross-crate discovery of custom binders/handlers via `linkme` slice (default 'classpath') + optional dynamic directory-scanned set (WASM 'classpath'), order by priority DATA, DCE guardrails + zero-contribution self-check; stable-only: object-safe traits, `Box<dyn>`, `Any`/downcast for the type-erasure seam, `ControlFlow`; synchronous binding (no async on the binder/handler path)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Kernel-resident core (`Binder`, `Bindable`, `BindResult`, `DataObjectBinder`, `BindHandler`, `BindContext` in `leaf-core`). This is the MOST cross-crate-exposed realization: both the `DataObjectBinder` chain and the `BindHandler` chain are EXPLICIT extension points across crates. A custom binder (for a foreign/builder/newtype config type) or a cross-cutting handler (audit, metrics, a centralized validation pass) is CONTRIBUTED from arbitrary crates and inherits the full static-link-registry-vs-build-codegen duality as a CANDIDATE: a default `linkme` distributed-slice of `const BinderDescriptor { priority, applies_to: TypeId|predicate, ctor_fn }` / `const HandlerDescriptor {..}` (the default 'classpath') PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned set (the WASM-module 'classpath'). DCE guardrails are CRITICAL (a silently-dropped custom binder binds a config type WRONG with no error): const descriptors, runtime SELECTION + ordering by priority/applies-to DATA never link/section order, force-link of opted-in crates, and a zero-contribution self-check warning when an expected binder/handler crate registered nothing. The stock ValueObjectBinder + JavaBeanBinder ship IN leaf-core and are NOT discovered (always present), keeping the common case inert; the discovery substrate is exercised only by third-party extensions. CRITICALLY this SHARES the same handler/discovery-substrate question as property-resolution's ResolveHandler and component-scanning — flagged as a Phase-2 unification KEYSTONE, not decided here. The generic-T-through-dyn-chain friction means a generic config type still needs a concrete per-instantiation binder shim if it routes through the dyn chain (the standard generics-cannot-be-registered constraint), though the common named-`T` call site avoids it.

**T2 — execution context:** All binding runs on the COLD bootstrap path (container refresh / 'bound very early'); the `DataObjectBinder::bind`, the per-leaf resolver+conversion, and the `BindHandler` callbacks are SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking CPU (charter #4) — none may `.await`/block; a custom binder backed by remote data is FORBIDDEN to fetch in `bind()` (must be pre-materialized in a cold async BootstrapContext step before joining the chain, the shared discipline). The handler chain's callbacks are synchronous observers/transformers (never await points), enabling a 'collect every bind failure and fail ONCE with the full list' startup-validation pass (charter #9 richest aggregated diagnostic) rather than first-fail-abort. A `DepthGuard` caps pathological recursive-config nesting (a robustness decision Spring's JVM recursion never bounded explicitly). Errors are synchronous rich `BindError` values carrying the full causal chain (prefix, field/param, raw value + origin via origin-tracking, candidates); Unbound stays a distinct `BindResult::Unbound` (not an error). No cancellation on the synchronous walk (bounded CPU); any async pre-materialization of a custom binder's backing is a separate cold step with its own cancellation. The chain (`Box<dyn DataObjectBinder>`) + handler are `Send+Sync` when their members are, so a `BindContext` can cross `.await`/threads as long as the borrowed resolver/stack outlives it (reachability = environment's concern). The produced `T` is owned + `Send+Sync` if its fields are; a config-refresh re-bind is a cold cancellable background task with a Phase-2 atomic-swap concurrency story (flagged). The `dyn`-dispatch chain is the one place indirection enters this (cold) path — justified by extensibility/unification, kept off the steady-state hot path entirely since binding is a startup concern.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `Binder` leans on JVM runtime REFLECTION: given `Bindable.of(MyProps.class)` it introspects fields/constructors/generic types at runtime to discover the tree-shape to bind. Rust has NO runtime reflection — the target's tree-shape must be described WITHOUT it, via a derived `const SCHEMA` (R1), the target's serde `Deserialize` impl (R2), or a per-type binder (R3). This is the deepest clash: faithful 'hand the binder a type and it figures out the shape' must be replaced by a compile-time-emitted self-description, and generic/recursive config types (a runtime triviality on the JVM) become a const-self-reference / monomorphization wrinkle in Rust.
- Spring's `BindMethod` (JAVA_BEAN vs VALUE_OBJECT) rests on JVM conventions Rust lacks: 'JavaBean' = no-arg construct + getters/setters + IN-PLACE mutation; 'value-object' = a single non-private non-@Autowired constructor (records get it free). Rust has NO universal setter/getter convention and NO uniform 'mutate an existing instance field-by-field' — an immutable struct simply cannot be JavaBean-bound. leaf must either INVENT a JavaBean convention (Default + public/`&mut` fields) or LEAN value-object-only (R2's serde-always-constructs dissolves the distinction). The existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule is especially awkward: Rust cannot field-mutate an arbitrary existing `T` without a leaf-defined setter seam.
- Spring's `BindResult<T>` monad blurs into Java's nullable/Optional idioms; Rust forces a SHARP three-state distinction that Java muddied: UNBOUND (nothing under the prefix — ordinary absence, falls through to orElse/bindOrCreate) vs FAILED (config present but coercion/validation failed — a hard error) vs BOUND. A naive `Result<Option<T>, E>` or `Option<Result<T,E>>` would conflate these or read awkwardly; leaf wants a purpose-built three-variant enum, and must NOT collapse Unbound into Err (swallowing the 'use default' path) nor into Ok(None) ambiguously.
- Spring's collection-REPLACEMENT-not-merge rule ('the whole List/Map comes from the single highest-precedence source defining it') is computed against a live, enumerable property-source stack on the JVM. In Rust this requires a 'which single source OWNS this collection root' query that depends on whether sources are ENUMERABLE (relaxed-binding's R3 index answers cheaply; its R1/R2 candidate-probing makes it hard) — and the rule fights serde's single-document model (R2) which has no notion of a precedence stack at all. The invariant is easy to state, non-trivial to enforce origin-agnostically across enumerable and non-enumerable sources.
- Spring's `BindHandler` (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish) is dynamically composed/wired on the JVM and is THE internal machinery (`ValidationBindHandler`). Rust has no classpath: cross-crate-contributed handlers/custom binders (R3's extension points) must be discovered via link-time registration (DCE-hazardous, silent-empty failure) or build-codegen, with ORDER from descriptor DATA not link order — and a silently-dropped handler would skip validation/audit with NO error. This is the same silent-DCE hazard component-scanning faces, here with config-correctness AND validation-bypass stakes, arguing for ONE shared discovery+handler substrate with property-resolution's ResolveHandler (a Phase-2 keystone, not this feature's call).
- Spring's binder + `ValidationBindHandler` FAIL FAST but typically surface failures one object at a time through exceptions. Rust's charter #9 wants the RICHEST diagnostic: ideally a startup-validation pass that AGGREGATES every bad field/coercion/constraint across the whole bind and reports them ALL at once with full context (prefix, field, raw value, origin, candidates). Serde's flat `Error` (R2) actively resists this (first-failure-aborts, thin error type); a handler-chain (R3) enables it but adds machinery. Whether to aggregate-and-report-once vs fail-on-first is an intent-richness decision with a Rust-specific aggregation cost Spring's exception model never optimized for.
- Spring binds onto MUTABLE bean instances (JavaBean mode) and re-binds freely; Rust's ownership/immutability and the async-first hot-path discipline push toward 'bind produces a fresh owned value, swapped atomically' rather than 'mutate the live config object in place.' A config-REFRESH (re-bind on file change) cannot mutate a shared `&T` config singleton without a lock or atomic swap (charter #5 — no global locks); the refresh/staleness/atomic-swap model is a Rust-specific concurrency concern (shared with relaxed-binding R3's index-invalidation and property-resolution) that Spring's GC'd mutable beans never forced.
- Spring deliberately keeps binding INERT (no SpEL, unlike @Value) — config is data, not code. In Rust this is mostly free (binding is pure data projection), but R2's serde route risks a subtle clash: a serde data-format mindset can tempt richer-than-raw-string value interpretation, and the boundary with property-resolution's `${...}` placeholder walk (which DOES run before binding) must be pinned — binding consumes ALREADY-placeholder-resolved raw values, never re-interprets them. The clean 'placeholders resolved upstream, binding is inert' layering must be explicit, where Spring's fused environment blurred it.

### Interactions
- **config-properties** — PRIMARY CONSUMER / inverse-of-dependency. config-properties (`@ConfigurationProperties`) is the DECLARATIVE front-end whose typed-target declaration, prefix-rooting, enabling routes (EnableConfigurationProperties/scan/Component analogues), and the two leniency flags (ignoreUnknownFields default-true, ignoreInvalidFields default-false) are all IMPLEMENTED by invoking THIS binder internally — exactly Spring's 'the machinery @ConfigurationProperties uses.' config-properties owns the annotation/derive surface + leniency policy + the 'config object is a pure projection, no other beans injected' rule; THIS feature owns the actual bind(prefix, Bindable) engine, bind-method dispatch, the result monad, and the handler chain it drives. The leniency flags map onto BindHandler decisions (ignoreUnknownFields = on_start skip-unknown; ignoreInvalidFields = on_failure recover-vs-rethrow).
- **property-resolution** — HARD DEPENDENCY + deep machinery-sharing CANDIDATE. The binder resolves every LEAF property value THROUGH property-resolution's read interface — so `${...}` placeholder expansion, strict/lenient, and the first-source-wins walk all happen at each leaf BEFORE the binder coerces/assembles (binding consumes already-resolved raw values; binding is INERT, no re-interpretation). CRUCIALLY, R3 deliberately shapes its `BindHandler` (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish) IDENTICALLY to property-resolution's flagged `ResolveHandler` to advance charter #11 unification — whether the two features SHARE one handler/context substrate (and one startup-validation diagnostics pass observing both placeholder resolution AND binding) is a Phase-2 keystone surfaced here, NOT decided. The binder is the downstream consumer; property-resolution is the read path it sits on.
- **relaxed-binding** — HARD DEPENDENCY — the binder's tree-descent IS where relaxed binding earns its keep. Every child key the binder forms (prefix + field-name, descending one segment per object level) is a canonical kebab `ConfigPropertyName` matched across camel/snake/UPPER_SNAKE/env forms via relaxed-binding; the list (`servers[0]`/`MY_SERVERS_0`) and map (env-lowercase-name, `[bracket-escape]` literal key) index conventions are consumed directly by the binder's seq/map descent. relaxed-binding's `Segment` model (Named/Indexed/MapKey) is the natural representation the binder walks; its R3 reverse index gives the binder 'all keys under this prefix' cheaply (needed for collection-replacement + ignoreUnknownFields). FLAGGED tension (shared with relaxed-binding's openNotes): the bracket-escape `[key-with-dashes]` ownership spans relaxed-binding (normalization), THIS binder (map-key binding), and property-resolution — exactly ONE owner must be pinned, or a literal map key with dashes round-trips wrong. The snake_case-Rust-field → kebab-canonical derivation rule (defined by relaxed-binding) is what the binder's field-name lookup relies on.
- **type-conversion** — DOWNSTREAM seam, invoked per leaf. After the binder resolves a leaf to a single raw winning string (one source, never blended, placeholder-expanded), it coerces to the target field/param type via type-conversion (Duration/Period/DataSize suffixes, case-insensitive enums, comma-split collections). THIS feature owns the tree-descent + 'which raw value goes to which slot'; type-conversion owns string→T. A coercion failure becomes a `BindError` carrying raw value + target type + origin + the field path (charter #9). Custom converters (Spring's `@ConfigurationPropertiesBinding`) are a type-conversion-registry concern that the binder merely consults — the binder does not own converter discovery. Spring's 'collection element coercion' (env `MY_SERVERS_0..N` → `Vec<T>`) is a binder-assembles-the-vec + type-conversion-coerces-each-element split.
- **validation** — DOWNSTREAM seam, invoked via the handler chain. Spring's `ValidationBindHandler` (JSR-303 on each bound object, fail-fast at startup with an aggregated error) is the canonical BindHandler — so validation plugs into THIS feature's handler chain as a stock `on_success` step that validates a completed object node, with failures aggregated into the BindResult/startup-validation pass (charter #9). THIS feature owns the handler hook + the descent that decides WHEN an object is complete-and-validatable; validation owns the constraint engine + the constraint vocabulary. The docs note validation is 'reused by config-properties binding' — confirming validation is a binder-driven handler, not a separate pass.
- **origin-tracking** — COMPLEMENTARY — every BindError and every bound leaf carries provenance. When binding fails (bad coercion/constraint), the rich diagnostic reports the matched RAW key + source/file+line (origin-tracking) alongside the canonical property and target field path. relaxed-binding's subtlety threads through: the canonical key the user authored (`my.app.item-price`) may differ from the raw key that matched (`MY_APP_ITEMPRICE` env), and the binder's error should report BOTH. The binder's handler chain (R3) is the natural hook to record the full provenance per bound node; origin-tracking owns the provenance representation, the binder feeds it the bind-path context (which target field, at which prefix-depth) that origin-tracking alone lacks.
- **config-metadata** — DISCOVERABILITY producer-side coupling. The same target description the binder consumes (R1's `const SCHEMA` / the target's fields + canonical names + defaults + nested kinds) is exactly the data config-metadata emits at compile time (groups/properties/descriptions/hints powering IDE autocompletion). A leaf-OWNED BindTarget derive (R1/R3) can CO-EMIT config-metadata from the same field walk; R2's serde-derive route (which leaf does not own) makes metadata emission harder (a noted con). The canonical kebab form is the form metadata advertises (the relaxed-binding asymmetric-placeholder lesson). THIS feature defines the bindable-target shape; config-metadata owns the metadata emission/format — but they want to share ONE source of truth for the target's field set.
- **environment** — UPSTREAM handle/reachability owner. `Binder.get(environment)` in Spring — the binder is constructed FROM the environment (which exposes the resolver + the source stack). environment owns the read/mutate seam, who-can-reach the resolver/stack, and the handle shape (borrowed vs Arc-rooted) + lifetime across `.await`/threads; the binder borrows that read view for the bind call's duration. The binder is a least-privilege CONSUMER of environment's read side (it never mutates sources). environment decides where the binder is reachable from and how the borrowed stack crosses execution contexts; the binder does not make that call.
- **type-conversion** — (See above — the per-leaf coercion seam.) Listed once; the binder orchestrates conversion at each leaf node but owns none of the coercion logic.
- **post-processor-spi / refresh-lifecycle** — BOOTSTRAP-PHASE coupling. In Spring, config binding runs 'very early' during context refresh (the BFPP-tier / definition-editing phase, before most beans exist) so config objects are bound before consumers need them — Spring even warns custom converter `@Bean`s must be `static` to avoid 'not eligible for all BeanPostProcessors' since binding precedes full BPP registration. leaf's analogue: the binder runs in a defined early refresh step (post property-source materialization, pre eager-singleton instantiation). refresh-lifecycle owns the fixed-order template + WHEN binding runs; THIS feature provides the binding the early step performs. Flagged: the exact ordering of binding vs converter-bean availability is a refresh-lifecycle sequencing concern the binder depends on.
- **deferral-primitives** — INTERACTION via bind-or-create + optional/default semantics. Spring's `bindOrCreate` (synthesize a default instance when nothing bound) and `@DefaultValue` (incl. the empty-default-forces-non-null-nested-instance rule) are the binder's deferral/optionality story for config objects — analogous to deferral-primitives' 0..1 / lazy / optional access made explicit in the type. THIS feature owns the bind-result three-state monad (Bound/Unbound/Failed) and bind_or_create; the Unbound state composing with a `Default` bound is the binder's local optionality, distinct from deferral-primitives' container-level ObjectProvider model — flagged as a related-but-separate concern (config optionality lives in BindResult, not in the injection-point deferral types).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- HOW does a typed target self-describe its tree-shape WITHOUT runtime reflection — a leaf-owned `#[derive(BindTarget)]` emitting a `const SCHEMA` (R1), riding the target's `serde::Deserialize` via a config-Deserializer adapter (R2), or a per-type `DataObjectBinder` in a chain (R3)? This is THE keystone representation question for the feature: it dictates the derive/metadata boundary (can config-metadata co-emit from the same source of truth?), the serde-dependency question, the generic/recursive-config-type story, and how much codegen leaf owns. Couples to the §3 metadata/codegen-boundary deferred decision and biases config-metadata. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- Does the binder SHARE a handler/observer + context substrate with property-resolution (R3's `BindHandler` ≡ the flagged `ResolveHandler`) and a discovery substrate with component-scanning/auto-config for any custom binders/handlers — or stay a self-contained named-`T` walk (R1/R2)? This is the charter #11 unification KEYSTONE; adopting R3's shared shape in Phase 1 would pre-bias the meta-architecture. Spans property-resolution, validation, the unified-diagnostics model, and the cross-crate-composition substrate. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- Which bind-METHOD model does leaf adopt, given Rust has no JavaBean setter/in-place-mutation convention? Faithfully replicate both JAVA_BEAN (invent a Default+setter convention) and VALUE_OBJECT (R1/R3), or lean value-object-only because serde-always-constructs dissolves the distinction (R2)? And how is the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule honored when Rust cannot field-mutate an arbitrary existing `T`? A cross-cutting modeling call spanning config-properties (which declares the target) and this feature; needs ONE convention.
- Is binding diagnostics fail-on-FIRST or an AGGREGATED startup-validation pass that collects EVERY bad field/coercion/constraint across the whole bind and reports them ALL at once (charter #9 richest diagnostic)? This cross-cuts validation (where constraint failures arise), the unified diagnostics/error model (§3), and property-resolution (a shared validation-pass observing both placeholder resolution AND binding). Spring fails fast per-exception; leaf must decide the aggregation policy framework-wide, not per-bind. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- Who OWNS the bracket-escape `[key-with-dashes]` semantics (literal map key, normalization disabled) — relaxed-binding (name normalization), THIS binder (map-key binding/assembly), or property-resolution (a bracketed key inside `${...}`)? The escape spans three features; Rust's explicit ownership forces exactly one owner or a literal map key with dashes/dots round-trips wrong. A cross-cutting boundary question (also flagged by relaxed-binding), NOT this feature's unilateral call.
- How is collection-REPLACEMENT-not-merge ('the whole List/Map comes from the single highest-precedence source defining it') computed origin-agnostically across BOTH enumerable sources (where 'which source owns this collection root' is a cheap index query) and non-enumerable sources (where it requires candidate-probing)? This couples the binder's seq/map descent to relaxed-binding's chosen representation (R1 value-type vs R2 mappers vs R3 index) and to property-sources' enumerability contract. A correctness invariant with no clean single mechanism; UNRESOLVED.
- For config-REFRESH (re-bind on source change), how is a freshly-bound config object atomically SWAPPED for the live one without a hot-path lock (charter #5), and does that align with whatever config-refresh story leaf adopts? Binding produces a fresh owned value (Rust can't mutate a shared `&T` singleton in place); the swap/staleness model spans environment, property-sources, relaxed-binding's R3 index-invalidation, and any future config-refresh feature. A Phase-2 concurrency call, NOT this feature's.
- Where does the async pre-materialization pipeline live for a remote/async-backed source or a custom binder whose backing is async, given the binder's walk + `DataObjectBinder::bind` + handler callbacks MUST be synchronous non-blocking? This is the SAME BootstrapContext-analogue (async fetch → snapshot → sync bind) that property-sources, property-resolution, relaxed-binding, and environment already flagged — must align framework-wide, not be re-invented here. UNRESOLVED.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated the Binder API strictly as the BINDING ENGINE that sits ON TOP OF the upstream property model (property-resolution's read path + relaxed-binding's key identity, both handed to me as completed designs and built on concretely, not reinvented) and BELOW config-properties (its declarative front-end). This feature owns ONLY: the `Bindable<T>` target-shape descriptor contract; the recursive TREE-DESCENT mapping property names to target slots (one prefix segment per object level); bind-METHOD selection (value-object/constructor vs JavaBean/setter) + the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule; the collection/map REPLACEMENT-not-merge ('one source owns the whole collection') invariant; the `BindResult` three-state MONAD (Bound/Unbound/Failed); the `BindHandler` observer/validator chain (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish); and the orchestration of conversion+validation at each node. I deliberately did NOT redesign the stack/ordering/never-blend (property-sources), the `${...}` walk + strict/lenient + read interface (property-resolution), canonical-key identity + per-transport forms + index conventions + bracket-escape (relaxed-binding), string→T coercion + converter registry (type-conversion), the typed-target DECLARATION + enabling routes + leniency-flag policy (config-properties), compile-time metadata emission (config-metadata), the constraint engine (validation), provenance internals (origin-tracking), or the refresh-order template (refresh-lifecycle).\n\nThe genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is HOW a typed target self-describes its tree-shape WITHOUT runtime reflection, HOW bind-method dispatch is represented, and WHERE the monad+handler policy lives: R1 = a leaf-owned `#[derive(BindTarget)]` emitting a `const SCHEMA` + a hand-written recursive walker (max intent fidelity — Bindable/BindMethod/BindResult/BindHandler transcribed line-for-line, thin macro, one owner for descent+method-selection+replacement, lets config-metadata co-emit from the same schema; but must invent a Rust JavaBean convention, awkward for recursive const-self-reference, and the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule is hard when Rust can't field-mutate an arbitrary existing T); R2 = a serde-`Deserializer` pull bridge driving the target's `#[derive(Deserialize)]` (MASSIVE DX + ecosystem reuse, zero bespoke schema, the BindMethod dichotomy largely DISSOLVES since serde always constructs, cleanest cross-crate story; but serde's single-document model FIGHTS collection-replacement-not-merge + relaxed-binding's many-forms, the BindHandler unification anchor has no native serde seam, diagnostics regress to serde's flat first-fail Error, and config-metadata is hard to emit from a derive leaf doesn't own); R3 = a `DataObjectBinder` chain (stock ValueObjectBinder + JavaBeanBinder, transcribing Spring's literal internals) + a `BindHandler` chain shaped IDENTICALLY to property-resolution's flagged ResolveHandler (most faithful to 'BindHandler IS the internal machinery', strict/lenient/validation/aggregated-validation-pass all pluggable handlers, maximally advances charter #11 unification, extensible per-type binders for foreign types; but by far the most machinery for a 95%-case 'bind this struct', dyn-dispatch + the generic-T-through-dyn-chain friction, and most exposed to the cross-crate DCE hazard + pre-biases a Phase-2 unification).\n\nAll three: keep binding SYNCHRONOUS and non-blocking on a COLD bootstrap path (charter #4 — the walk/coercion/handler callbacks are pure CPU over already-materialized, placeholder-resolved raw strings; any remote/async source or custom binder must be pre-snapshotted in a cold async BootstrapContext step before binding — the same pipeline property-sources/property-resolution/relaxed-binding/environment all flagged); keep binding INERT (consume already-resolved raw values, never re-interpret — Spring's deliberate no-SpEL-in-binding); preserve the upstream invariants UNTOUCHED (first-source-wins + never-blend per scalar inherited from property-sources; the binder ADDS only the one-source-owns-the-whole-collection rule for List/Set/Map); encode Unbound (absence, falls to orElse/bindOrCreate) vs Failed (config present but bad) vs Bound as DISTINCT states, never collapsing Unbound into an error; surface rich diagnostics (a `BindError` carrying prefix + target field/param path + raw value + matched raw key + origin + candidates, ideally aggregated into a startup-validation pass per charter #9); keep the source/binder seams ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (native, file, or future WASM-module source bind identically; a generic config type binds by naming a concrete T at the call site — NO link-time discovery of the config type itself, unlike component-scanning); and keep macros THIN (charter #10 — at most a `derive(BindTarget)` emitting a const data literal + a cursor-calling fn, all logic hand-writable in leaf-core; R2 borrows serde's already-hand-writable-equivalent derive).\n\nNightly review (against rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md): nothing needs nightly — `const SCHEMA` data literals (const-eval baseline + const TypeId 1.91 if a node embeds a type key), enums/`Box<[T]>` for the schema, object-safe `BindHandler`/`DataObjectBinder`, `Any`/downcast (R3's type-erasure seam, stable since 1.0/1.29) + trait upcasting (1.86) if a binder needs supertrait coercion, `BindResult` as a plain enum, `Cow`/`PhantomData`, serde derive (R2) are all stable; the binder walk is SYNCHRONOUS so no AFIT/RPITIT boxing tax on the binder core (the dyn-incompatibility-of-async-traits constraint never bites because binding doesn't await). The cross-crate touchpoints (optional custom `BindHandler`/`DataObjectBinder` for third-party types or cross-cutting concerns) are OPT-IN — the core binder is cross-crate-INERT because it binds a named concrete T at a known call site (no discovery), and the stock binders ship in leaf-core — and where present they share the SAME link-time-registry/DCE substrate concern (linkme default 'classpath' + optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath', ordering/selection by priority/applies-to DATA never link order, zero-contribution self-check) as component-scanning and as property-resolution's ResolveHandler discovery; whether the binder SHARES one handler/discovery substrate with property-resolution + the discovery features is flagged UNRESOLVED for Phase 2, consistent with Phase 1 staying implementation-agnostic. The sharpest Phase-2-flavored tensions I surfaced but did NOT resolve: the target-self-description representation (the keystone — derive-schema vs serde vs binder-chain), the BindHandler/ResolveHandler unification + shared discovery substrate, the bind-method model given no Rust JavaBean convention (and the existing-value-forces-JavaBean rule), the aggregated-vs-fail-first diagnostics policy, the bracket-escape ownership across three features, and the config-refresh atomic-swap concurrency story.

## Configuration Metadata Generation  `[config-metadata]`

This feature is the SELF-DOCUMENTING METADATA EMISSION layer — Spring Boot's `spring-boot-configuration-processor` analogue (docs §"Configuration metadata generation", lines 1618-1624) that emits, AT COMPILE TIME and at ZERO RUNTIME COST, a structured, tool-readable description of every configuration property the application accepts: GROUPS (the prefix-rooted config types), PROPERTIES (canonical kebab-case name, type, description-from-doc-comment, default value, deprecation status), and HINTS (enumerated/suggested values, provider references). The driving intent (docs line 1622): make configuration "a discoverable, self-documenting API surface" answering "what properties does this app even accept?" — powering IDE autocompletion, generated docs, and upgrade tooling (Spring's `properties-migrator` reads the JSON to detect renamed keys), WITHOUT reflection and WITHOUT runtime cost.\n\nIt is deliberately NOT the binding engine (`binder`), NOT the declaration front-end (`config-properties`, its UPSTREAM dependency — it CONSUMES the same prefix-rooted typed-target declaration), NOT the key-identity layer (`relaxed-binding`, whose canonical-kebab form is the form metadata MUST advertise), NOT the validation engine (`validation`, whose constraints metadata may surface as hints). It is the PASSIVE, build-time PROJECTION of the config declaration into a tooling artifact.\n\nSpring's mechanics to replicate as INTENT (not mechanism): (1) COMPILE-TIME emission from the same `@ConfigurationProperties` declaration that drives binding — one source of truth, no duplicate declaration; (2) the EMITTED CONTENT taxonomy — groups + properties (name/type/description/defaultValue/deprecation) + hints; (3) DESCRIPTION sourced from documentation comments (Javadoc → Rust doc comments `///`); (4) a HAND-AUTHORED OVERRIDE/SUPPLEMENT channel (Spring's `additional-spring-configuration-metadata.json` + its `ignored.properties` section) for things the processor cannot infer — collection/map defaults, descriptions for externally-bound keys, intentionally-ignored keys; (5) the v4 CROSS-MODULE case (`@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` + per-type output location `META-INF/spring/configuration-metadata/<fqn>.json`) — full metadata for REUSABLE config types in a SEPARATE crate even when the consuming crate cannot see their source; (6) ZERO RUNTIME COST / NO REFLECTION — metadata is a build artifact, never loaded by the running app.\n\nSCOPE BOUNDARY (what THIS feature owns vs neighbours): `config-properties` owns the prefix-rooted declaration surface + the three enabling routes + leniency policy; THIS feature owns ONLY the EMISSION of the tooling artifact from that declaration — the artifact FORMAT (a leaf-native equivalent of the JSON), the SOURCE-OF-TRUTH coupling to the config declaration (one macro/codegen pass produces both binding artifacts and metadata, or metadata rides alongside), the DOC-COMMENT→description capture, the DEFAULT/deprecation/hint capture, the hand-authored OVERRIDE/IGNORE channel, the CROSS-MODULE/cross-crate metadata story (the genuinely hard Rust axis), and the DELIVERY of the artifact to tooling (where it lives, how an IDE/CLI finds it). `relaxed-binding` owns the canonical-kebab key identity the metadata advertises; `binder` owns the BindTarget tree schema (field set/types/defaults) which metadata READS; `type-conversion` owns the type coercion metadata might reference; `validation` owns constraints a hint might surface. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: there is no annotation processor and no classpath; a proc-macro sees ONLY its own invocation (cross-crate doc line 89) so it can emit metadata for the DECLARING crate's types but CANNOT aggregate across crates or see a reusable type defined elsewhere — so the v4 cross-module case and the whole-workspace "what does this app accept" rollup force either a build.rs/CLI codegen pass (sqlx model) over the resolved graph, a per-type metadata file convention each crate emits, or a link-time descriptor the runtime/tooling reads. This squarely engages the DEFERRED metadata/codegen-boundary keystone (charter §3) — surfaced, NOT resolved.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Proc-macro co-emission: the same #[config_properties] declaration emits a const MetadataDescriptor alongside the binding artifacts (single source of truth, per-crate)
Fold metadata emission INTO the config-properties declaration macro (config-properties R1's `#[config_properties(prefix=...)]` + `#[derive(BindTarget)]`), so ONE proc-macro expansion produces BOTH the binding artifacts AND a `const ConfigMetadata` describing the accepted surface. The macro, while it already has the struct's fields/types/defaults/doc-comments as tokens in front of it, additionally emits a const metadata tree: group (prefix + type name + type-level `///` doc), and per-field a property row (canonical-kebab name via the relaxed-binding derivation rule, Rust type rendered to a metadata type string, the field's `///` doc as description, the `#[config(default=...)]` value, a `#[deprecated]`/`#[config(deprecated=...)]` flag, and any `#[config(hint(...))]` enumerated values).

```rust
#[config_properties(prefix = "my.app")]
#[derive(BindTarget)]
pub struct AppProperties {
    /// Human-facing display name shown in the UI banner.
    name: String,                               // -> property my.app.name : String, desc from ///
    /// Roles granted by default to anonymous users.
    #[config(default = "GUEST")]
    #[config(hint(values("GUEST", "USER", "ADMIN")))]
    default_role: String,                       // -> default "GUEST", hint 3 values
    #[deprecated = "use my.app.tls instead"]
    legacy_ssl: bool,                           // -> deprecation { replacement: "my.app.tls" }
}
// emitted (hand-writable) — metadata as DATA, zero runtime cost:
impl ConfigMetadataSource for AppProperties {
    const METADATA: ConfigGroup = ConfigGroup {
        prefix: "my.app", type_name: "my_crate::AppProperties",
        description: "Top-level application settings.",      // type-level ///
        properties: &[
            Property { name: "my.app.name", ty: "String", description: Some("Human-facing display name shown in the UI banner."), default: None, deprecation: None, origin: decl_site!() },
            Property { name: "my.app.default-role", ty: "String", description: Some("Roles granted by default to anonymous users."), default: Some("GUEST"), deprecation: None, hints: &[Hint::Value("GUEST"), Hint::Value("USER"), Hint::Value("ADMIN")], origin: decl_site!() },
            Property { name: "my.app.legacy-ssl", ty: "bool", description: None, default: None, deprecation: Some(Deprecation { replacement: Some("my.app.tls"), reason: None }), origin: decl_site!() },
        ],
    };
}
```
DELIVERY to tooling has two candidate sub-paths kept open: (i) the const `METADATA` is registered into a link-time descriptor slice (the same substrate config-properties R1's scan route uses) so a `leaf metadata dump` CLI run against the FINAL BINARY can walk all linked `ConfigGroup`s and serialize the whole-app artifact (canonical JSON / leaf-native format) — the binary is the only place the whole graph is visible (cross-crate doc line 260); OR (ii) a thin `build.rs` in each crate calls a `leaf-codegen` helper that re-derives the same metadata and writes a per-crate `OUT_DIR`/target file an IDE plugin reads (closer to Spring's per-jar `META-INF` file). The HAND-AUTHORED override/ignore channel (Spring's `additional-...json`) is a checked-in `leaf-config-metadata.toml`/json the delivery step MERGES over the generated tree (supplying collection/map defaults the macro can't infer, descriptions for externally-bound keys, an `ignored` list). The doc-comment capture is the Javadoc analogue: the proc-macro reads `#[doc]` attributes (which `///` desugars to) directly from its token input — fully stable, no nightly. Declaration-site provenance uses `proc_macro::Span` file/line (stable 1.88) so the metadata says WHERE a property is declared.

**Pros:** Strongest single-source-of-truth (charter #11): the EXACT declaration that drives binding (config-properties) drives metadata, in ONE macro expansion — a field rename, a new field, a changed default, a new doc-comment automatically and atomically updates both binding and metadata; impossible to drift. Directly transcribes Spring's 'same @ConfigurationProperties powers both the binder and the processor.'; Doc-comment → description is a clean, idiomatic, ZERO-nightly transcription of Javadoc → description (docs line 1620): `///` desugars to `#[doc]` attributes the proc-macro already has in its token stream, so the natural Rust documentation a developer writes anyway becomes the config docs — Spring-grade DX (charter #1) with no extra ceremony.; Thin macro (charter #10): the emission is pure `const` DATA (a `ConfigGroup` tree of plain structs/enums + `&'static str`) — every line hand-writable, `cargo expand` shows the literal metadata, and the override channel + a programmatic `ConfigGroup { .. }` constructor are the escape hatches; no logic hidden in the macro.; ZERO runtime cost / no reflection (Spring intent, docs line 1622; charter #2): metadata is `const` data; on the link-time delivery sub-path it occupies a section the running app never reads (and which DCE can even drop with no functional harm — uniquely, a dropped metadata descriptor degrades only TOOLING, never app behavior, INVERTING config-properties' high-stakes-DCE concern); on the build.rs sub-path it is a build artifact entirely outside the binary.; Origin-agnostic delivery: the const `ConfigGroup` is a uniform data shape independent of how the type is constructed, so a future WASM-module-sourced config type could contribute the SAME metadata shape — native and dynamic config sources self-document identically; metadata is just data about an accepted surface, not about a construction mechanism.; Provenance for free (charter #9 rich diagnostics): `proc_macro::Span` (stable 1.88) embeds declaration file/line into each property row, so tooling (and a `leaf doctor` 'unknown property' warning) can point a user at the exact `///`-documented field — the same provenance origin-tracking uses for bind failures, here serving discoverability.

**Cons:** CANNOT see across crates (the decisive limit, cross-crate doc line 89): a proc-macro sees only its own invocation, so this realization emits metadata ONLY for config types DECLARED in the macro's own crate. The v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` cross-module case — full metadata for a reusable config type defined in crate A but only bound/referenced in crate B that cannot see A's source/doc-comments — is UNSERVED by the proc-macro alone; A must emit its OWN metadata (fine if A is a leaf-aware crate) but a truly foreign type leaf cannot annotate has no doc-comments to read, so its metadata must come from the hand-authored override channel — a real gap vs Spring's processor that can read a dependency's source.; Whole-app rollup needs a SECOND mechanism: producing 'what does the WHOLE app accept' (the headline intent) requires aggregating every crate's per-invocation metadata — which the proc-macro cannot do, forcing either the link-time slice walk (inherits DCE/force-link concerns, though metadata-DCE is harmless to the app) or a build.rs/CLI pass at the binary. So R1 is really 'per-crate co-emission + a separate aggregation/delivery step' — the macro alone is incomplete for the tooling artifact.; Pre-judges (lightly) toward proc-macro-emitted metadata, which is exactly the DEFERRED metadata/codegen-boundary keystone (charter §3): co-emitting in the proc-macro biases that signal toward 'macro emits metadata' over 'build.rs/CLI generates it from the resolved graph' — must stay a CANDIDATE alongside R2/R3, not a decision.; Rust-type → metadata-type-string rendering is a convention the macro must INVENT (Spring reads JVM type signatures): `Duration`, `Vec<String>`, `HashMap<String,Foo>`, an enum's variant set — how each renders into a stable, tool-friendly type string (and how an enum's variants become hints) is non-trivial and couples to type-conversion's coercion vocabulary; getting it wrong gives tooling a misleading surface.; Collection/map defaults can't be auto-detected (Spring says so explicitly, docs line 1620): the macro sees the field type but not a meaningful runtime default for a `Vec`/`HashMap`, so those MUST be documented via the override channel — meaning the 'single source of truth' is not total; some metadata always lives in the hand-authored supplement, a split R1 must own gracefully.; Doc-comment capture is shallow: the proc-macro gets the raw `///` text but has no Markdown/structure model, no `@param`-style structured tags (Java's Javadoc has more structure than a Rust doc comment exposes to a macro), and `Span::source_text()`/byte_range nuances mean rich extraction beyond the plain doc string is limited on stable — descriptions will be plain text, acceptable but less structured than some IDE tooling expects.

**Mechanisms considered:** co-emission inside the `#[config_properties]` proc-macro (config-properties R1's declaration macro) of a `const ConfigGroup`/`impl ConfigMetadataSource` alongside the binding artifacts — one expansion, two outputs; `#[doc]`-attribute reading in the proc-macro to capture `///` doc comments as property descriptions (Javadoc analogue), fully stable; `proc_macro::Span` file/line (stable 1.88) for per-property declaration-site provenance; a `#[config(hint(values(...)))]` / `#[config(default=...)]` / `#[deprecated]` attribute vocabulary the macro lifts into metadata rows; link-time descriptor slice (linkme) of `ConfigGroup`s + a `leaf metadata dump` CLI walking the FINAL BINARY for the whole-app rollup — a CANDIDATE delivery path; per-crate `build.rs` calling a `leaf-codegen` helper to write a metadata file into `OUT_DIR`/target (closer to Spring's per-jar META-INF) — an alternative delivery CANDIDATE; a hand-authored checked-in `leaf-config-metadata` override/supplement/ignore file merged over the generated tree (Spring's `additional-...json` + `ignored.properties` analogue); a programmatic `ConfigGroup { .. }` builder as the escape hatch for foreign/dynamic types the macro can't annotate; stable-only: const data, &'static str, enums, fn-free metadata (no async, no runtime); linkme behind-flag for the rollup CANDIDATE

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the CRUX and the hardest part of the feature, because the headline intent ('what does the WHOLE APP accept') is inherently whole-graph, while a proc-macro is inherently single-invocation (cross-crate doc line 89 — 'no API to enumerate other items, other crates'). R1's proc-macro co-emission is honest about this: it produces correct, doc-sourced metadata for config types DECLARED in the emitting crate, but CANNOT produce metadata for a config type defined in a sibling/dependency crate it cannot see — directly the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` cross-module problem. Two CANDIDATE aggregation/delivery substrates carry the duality: (i) a link-time `linkme` slice of `const ConfigGroup` descriptors (the static 'classpath') walked by a `leaf metadata dump` CLI at the FINAL BINARY (the only whole-graph vantage, cross-crate doc line 260), OR (ii) a build.rs/CLI codegen pass (sqlx model, Architecture C) that walks the resolved graph and gathers each crate's per-type metadata file. UNIQUELY among discovery features, the DCE hazard is BENIGN here: a dropped metadata descriptor degrades only IDE autocompletion/docs, never running-app behavior — so R1 does NOT need the high-stakes force-link + zero-contribution self-check config-properties' scan route demands; a `leaf metadata --check` (sqlx-`prepare --check` analogue) can still warn when a crate contributed zero metadata, but a miss is a tooling gap, not a misconfiguration. Generics-can't-register (cross-crate doc line 153) applies to the link-time path but is moot for metadata: a generic config type has no single accepted prefix anyway, so it is documented per concrete instantiation via the programmatic/override channel. Proc-macro hygiene: the emitted `ConfigGroup` references `::leaf_core::metadata::...` via absolute paths; `leaf-macros` (proc-macro=true) emits only the data, `leaf-core` hosts the `ConfigGroup` types. SHARES the metadata/codegen-boundary keystone with the binder's BindTarget schema and config-metadata's whole purpose — flagged Phase-2, not decided. The override/ignore channel and the rollup live at the binary/app crate (role separation, cross-crate doc line 233).

**T2 — execution context:** Almost entirely a BUILD-TIME / OUT-OF-RUNTIME feature — the cleanest T2 in the config family. The proc-macro expansion runs at COMPILE TIME of the declaring crate (host target, no async, no runtime, must not block on I/O — it only reads its own token stream + Span info). The whole-app rollup (the CLI/build.rs delivery) runs at BUILD TIME of the binary crate, also synchronous and outside any async runtime — it serializes `const` data to a file; idempotent/deterministic (cross-crate doc OUT_DIR hygiene). CRUCIALLY there is ZERO RUNTIME execution context for the core intent: the running application NEVER reads config-metadata (Spring intent, docs line 1622 — 'no runtime cost or reflection'); the artifact is consumed by EXTERNAL tooling (IDE, docs generator, migrator) entirely off the app's execution path. On the link-time-slice delivery sub-path the `const ConfigGroup`s occupy a section the app never touches and which may even be DCE'd harmlessly (no cancellation, no errors-at-runtime to propagate — a dropped descriptor is a silent tooling gap, caught by `leaf metadata --check` in CI, not a runtime fault). NO blocking, NO cancellation, NO hot path — this feature is reactive/event-free by nature. The ONLY runtime adjacency: IF a future 'list accepted properties at runtime for an admin endpoint' capability is wanted (a possible Actuator-style consumer), the same `const` metadata could be optionally retained and read on a COLD diagnostic path — but that is opt-in and out of Phase-1 scope; the default is build-artifact-only, charter #2 zero overhead by construction.

#### R2 — build.rs / `cargo leaf metadata` codegen pass over the resolved graph (sqlx model): out-of-band whole-workspace artifact, decoupled from the binding macro
Invert R1's macro-coupling: metadata is produced by an OUT-OF-BAND build step (a `build.rs` in the binary crate, or a `cargo leaf metadata` CLI — the sqlx `cargo sqlx prepare` analogue) that walks the resolved dependency graph (`cargo metadata`) and a per-crate metadata-source convention, then EMITS a single canonical whole-app artifact (the `spring-configuration-metadata.json` equivalent) — checked in and `--check`-able in CI. The config declaration macro's only job is to leave a small, machine-readable BREADCRUMB the pass can find: each `#[config_properties]` type emits a per-crate metadata fragment (a tiny generated `OUT_DIR` file, or a `const ConfigGroup` the pass reads via a generated `leaf_config_metadata()` fn the crate exports) — analogous to Spring's per-jar `META-INF/.../<fqn>.json` (the v4 per-type location). The codegen pass then UNIONS every participating crate's fragments + the hand-authored override/ignore supplement into one artifact.

```text
# binary-crate build.rs (or `cargo leaf metadata`):
#   1. cargo metadata -> resolved graph of crates the app actually depends on
#   2. for each leaf-aware crate, read its exported config-metadata fragment
#      (a `pub fn __leaf_config_metadata() -> &'static [ConfigGroup]` convention,
#       or a per-crate target/.../leaf-config-metadata/<fqn>.json file)
#   3. merge + the checked-in `additional` override/ignore supplement
#   4. emit  ./config-metadata.json  (canonical, kebab keys, groups+properties+hints)
#      and optionally `--check` it against the committed copy (fail CI if stale)
```
The v4 CROSS-MODULE case is served FIRST-CLASS: a reusable config type in a separate crate A emits its own per-type fragment when A is compiled; the pass at binary B picks up A's fragment from the resolved graph WITHOUT B seeing A's source (exactly Spring's `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` motivation). For a TRULY foreign type leaf cannot annotate, the supplement supplies it. The doc-comment description is captured by a SMALL proc-macro/derive in A's crate that records `///` into A's fragment (the macro is still the only thing that can read doc-comments at A's compile time) — so R2 is a HYBRID: a thin per-crate recorder + an out-of-band aggregator. The artifact location/format is a leaf convention (a `config-metadata.json` at the workspace root, or the per-type `target/.../<fqn>.json` Spring-v4 layout) an IDE plugin / docs generator reads.

**Pros:** FULLY serves the whole-app rollup AND the v4 cross-module case (the two things R1 cannot do alone): the pass sees the RESOLVED GRAPH at the binary (cross-crate doc line 260, the only whole-graph vantage), so 'what does this app accept' is answered deterministically over exactly the crates the app depends on — and a reusable config type in a separate jar/crate gets full metadata at the consumer even when its source is invisible, the precise v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` intent (docs line 1624).; Most reliable + portable delivery (cross-crate doc Architecture C): pure build-time codegen, NO link-time tricks, NO DCE exposure, fully platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded — the artifact is a checked-in file, not a linker section that can vanish. The `--check` mode (sqlx `prepare --check`) makes CI fail when metadata drifts from source, turning the silent-staleness risk into a loud, deterministic gate (charter #9).; Deterministic, inspectable, debuggable: the generated `config-metadata.json` is a plain file a human/IDE/tool reads directly — maximal tooling interop and reproducibility, and it composes cleanly with Spring's existing ecosystem expectation (the same JSON shape the migrator + IDEs already understand), easing 'feels like Spring' adoption.; Decouples metadata-emission timing from the binding macro: metadata can be regenerated/inspected WITHOUT recompiling the whole app (a `cargo leaf metadata` invocation), and the metadata pass can do richer cross-property analysis (detect prefix collisions, near-duplicate keys, undocumented properties across the WHOLE app) that a per-invocation proc-macro structurally cannot — a whole-graph lint surface.; Honors role separation (cross-crate doc line 233): contribution crates only DECLARE their config + emit a passive fragment (no global side effect); the binary/app crate OWNS the aggregation — clean ownership, no transitive dependency silently changing the artifact, and the override/ignore supplement is owned at the app where the whole surface is known.; Zero runtime cost is structural (charter #2): the artifact never enters the binary at all (it is a sibling build output), so unlike R1's optional link-time slice there is no section in the binary, no question of retaining-vs-DCE — the running app is provably untouched by metadata.

**Cons:** Requires a BUILD STEP / CLI ('less magic', cross-crate doc Architecture C tradeoff): users must run `cargo leaf metadata` (or accept a build.rs that does it), and keep the checked-in artifact fresh — more ceremony than Spring's transparent annotation-processor that 'just runs' during `javac`. The DX is good (deterministic, CI-checkable) but not the zero-config feel of Spring's processor (charter #1 cost).; STILL needs a per-crate proc-macro/derive to capture doc-comments (only a macro at A's compile time can read A's `///`): so R2 is not purely out-of-band — it is a hybrid (thin recorder macro + aggregator pass), and the recorder macro re-introduces the metadata/codegen split this realization tried to cleanly separate, plus a fragment-file/exported-fn convention each crate must honor.; The per-crate fragment convention is a contract integration-crate authors must follow (emit `__leaf_config_metadata()` or a fragment file) — more burden on library authors than Spring's automatic processor, and a crate that forgets it contributes no metadata silently (caught by `--check` only if the app KNOWS to expect it), an honest-but-manual opt-in per crate.; build.rs cannot see SIBLING/downstream crates and `cargo metadata` enumerates DECLARED deps, not a true classpath (cross-crate doc line 357, 317): the pass documents what the app DEPENDS ON, which is correct for 'what THIS app accepts', but it cannot discover a config type in a crate the binary doesn't reference — consistent with scoped discovery (good) but means 'metadata' is dependency-graph-scoped, not globally-scoped.; Two artifacts to keep coherent (the generated fragments + the merged whole-app file) and a merge/override precedence to define (generated vs hand-authored supplement vs ignore-list ordering) — a small but real coherence surface R1's in-place co-emission sidesteps for the single-crate case.; Pre-judges (lightly) toward build-time codegen on the DEFERRED metadata/codegen-boundary keystone (charter §3) — presenting the sqlx-style pass as THE mechanism biases that Phase-2 signal toward codegen over proc-macro co-emission; must stay a CANDIDATE.; OUT_DIR/codegen determinism + idempotence is required (cross-crate doc line 52, 317): the pass must produce byte-stable output for `--check` to be meaningful, and `cargo metadata` resolution differs between `-p` and `--workspace` (cross-crate doc line 209) so the artifact's scope must be documented as binary-specific.

**Mechanisms considered:** an out-of-band `build.rs` (binary crate) or `cargo leaf metadata` CLI walking `cargo metadata` resolved graph (sqlx `prepare` model, cross-crate Architecture C); a thin per-crate recorder proc-macro/derive that captures `///` doc-comments + field/type/default/hint into a per-crate metadata FRAGMENT (the only way to read doc-comments at the declaring crate's compile time); per-crate fragment delivery: either an exported `pub fn __leaf_config_metadata() -> &'static [ConfigGroup]` convention OR a per-type file `target/.../leaf-config-metadata/<fqn>.json` (Spring v4 per-type location analogue); a `--check` mode (sqlx `prepare --check`) failing CI when the committed artifact is stale — the loud anti-staleness gate; a canonical whole-app `config-metadata.json` (Spring `spring-configuration-metadata.json` shape) as the delivered artifact + the hand-authored override/ignore supplement merged in; whole-graph metadata lints (prefix collisions, undocumented properties, near-duplicate keys) the aggregator can run that a per-invocation macro cannot; stable-only: build.rs codegen, cargo_metadata crate, serde-serialized const data; no nightly, no link tricks, wasm/embedded-safe (Architecture C is the portable path)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This realization is BUILT for the cross-crate reality and is the most T1-complete: the aggregation runs at the FINAL BINARY (cross-crate doc line 260, the only whole-graph vantage) over the RESOLVED dependency graph via `cargo metadata`, so it answers 'what does THIS app accept' deterministically and serves the v4 cross-module `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` case first-class (a reusable config type's metadata fragment travels with its crate and is picked up at the consumer without source visibility — cross-crate doc line 89's proc-macro limit is sidestepped because the FRAGMENT, not the source, crosses the boundary). It is the sqlx/Architecture-C 'build-time analysis → checked-in artifact → consumed' pattern, the cross-crate doc's recommended PORTABLE path (line 232, 315) — NO DCE exposure (the artifact is a sibling file, not a linker section), NO force-link discipline needed, full wasm/embedded support. The honest limit (cross-crate doc line 357, 317): build.rs/`cargo metadata` cannot scan a true classpath — it enumerates DECLARED dependencies, so a config type in an unreferenced crate is invisible (correct per scope-discovery, cross-crate doc line 362). The residual proc-macro dependency (doc-comment capture must happen at the declaring crate's compile time) means R2 is a HYBRID — a thin recorder macro per crate + the aggregator at the binary — so it does NOT escape the metadata/codegen-boundary keystone, it lands it firmly on the codegen side while still needing a macro breadcrumb. The `--check` gate (sqlx `prepare --check`) is the cross-crate doc's recommended self-check (line 235) against silently-lost contributions, here lower-stakes because a miss only degrades tooling. SHARES the metadata/codegen-boundary + the cross-crate-substrate keystones with the binder, config-properties' scan route, and component-scanning — flagged Phase-2, resolved toward the codegen end here as a CANDIDATE. Role separation (cross-crate doc line 233): crates declare + emit fragments; the binary owns aggregation + override.

**T2 — execution context:** Purely BUILD-TIME, entirely off the application's runtime — the cleanest possible T2. The per-crate recorder macro runs at COMPILE TIME of each declaring crate (host, synchronous, reads tokens + `///` + Span, no I/O blocking beyond writing its OUT_DIR fragment). The aggregator (build.rs or `cargo leaf metadata`) runs at BUILD TIME of the binary crate as an ordinary host executable (cross-crate doc line 46): synchronous, NO async runtime, may do bounded file I/O (read fragments, read `cargo metadata` output, read the override supplement, write the canonical artifact) — blocking file I/O is fine here because it is a build tool, NOT the async-first runtime (charter #4 applies to the framework's execution paths, not its build tooling). Determinism/idempotence required for `--check` (cross-crate doc line 52). There is ZERO RUNTIME execution context: the artifact is a sibling build output the RUNNING APP never reads (Spring intent, docs line 1622) — so no async context, no cancellation, no error propagation into the app, no hot/cold path question at all; metadata generation cannot fail the app's bring-up (it can only fail the BUILD/CI via `--check` or a malformed declaration, which is the correct, earliest-legible failure point — charter #9). The only execution the running binary ever does related to this feature is NONE by default. (If a runtime 'list accepted properties' admin endpoint is ever wanted, it would be a separate opt-in feature loading the artifact or a retained const table on a COLD diagnostic path — out of Phase-1 scope.)

#### R3 — Reflection-trait + link-time descriptor registry: config types implement a queryable ConfigSchema trait, runtime/tooling reads a metadata catalog (the synthesized-reflection model)
Treat config-metadata as the framework's ANSWER to Rust's missing reflection (nightly doc line 449: 'leaf must synthesize reflection at build time'): every config-properties type implements a `ConfigSchema` reflection trait exposing its accepted-surface metadata as DATA, and these schemas are collected into a link-time descriptor catalog the RUNTIME (or a tool linked against the binary) can QUERY — making config-metadata a first-class, in-program, reflectable catalog rather than only an out-of-band file. This unifies metadata with the SAME descriptor substrate config-properties' scan route + component-scanning use (charter #11): one descriptor carries BOTH the bind fn-pointer (config-properties) AND the schema (config-metadata).

```rust
// the config-properties descriptor GROWS a schema field (one descriptor, two consumers):
pub struct ConfigPropsDescriptor {
    type_id: TypeId, prefix: &'static str,
    bind: fn(&Environment, &dyn BindHandler) -> Box<dyn Any>,   // config-properties owns this
    schema: &'static ConfigGroup,                              // config-metadata owns THIS
    origin: DeclSite,
}
#[distributed_slice(leaf_core::CONFIG_PROPS)]
static __APP: ConfigPropsDescriptor = ConfigPropsDescriptor {
    type_id: TypeId::of::<AppProperties>(), prefix: "my.app",
    bind: |e, h| Box::new(leaf_core::bind::<AppProperties>(e, h)),
    schema: &AppProperties::SCHEMA,    // the metadata tree, co-emitted by the SAME macro
    origin: decl_site!(),
};
// a tool / admin endpoint / docs-gen queries the catalog:
for d in leaf::config_metadata::catalog() {        // walks the linked descriptor slice
    println!("{}: {} properties", d.schema.prefix, d.schema.properties.len());
}
let json = leaf::config_metadata::to_canonical_json();   // serialize whole-app surface
```
The DELIVERY is dual: (i) a `leaf metadata` CLI or a `cargo` xtask links a tiny harness against the binary's descriptor catalog and serializes the whole-app artifact (the JSON Spring tooling expects) — whole-graph at the binary (cross-crate doc line 260); (ii) the SAME catalog is optionally readable at runtime on a COLD diagnostic path (an Actuator-style `/config-metadata` or `leaf doctor` 'these are the properties you can set, here's an unknown one you set' check) — config-metadata becomes a live self-description, not just an IDE file. The doc-comment → description capture is still done by the declaration proc-macro (only it sees `///`) emitting `AppProperties::SCHEMA`. The override/ignore supplement merges at serialization time. The v4 cross-module case: a reusable type in crate A emits its OWN `ConfigSchema` + descriptor (force-linked when A participates); a truly foreign type uses the programmatic descriptor + override.

**Pros:** Maximal charter #11 unification: ONE descriptor in ONE link-time slice carries BOTH config-properties' bind fn-pointer AND config-metadata's schema — the scan route's discovery substrate, config-properties' registration, and config-metadata's catalog become the SAME machinery; a config type that is bindable is automatically self-documenting from the same row, no parallel pipeline.; Directly realizes the nightly doc's 'synthesized reflection' thesis (line 449, 497): config-metadata becomes leaf's reflection answer for config — a queryable, in-program catalog of the accepted surface — which is strictly more capable than an out-of-band file: it enables a RUNTIME 'what can I configure / you set an unknown key' diagnostic (an Actuator-style endpoint, a `leaf doctor` unknown-property warning) that R1/R2's build-artifact-only model cannot serve without re-loading a file.; Single source of truth like R1 (the same macro co-emits bind + schema) AND whole-app rollup like R2 (the catalog is walked at the binary) — R3 combines R1's atomic-with-binding coherence with R2's whole-graph completeness via the shared descriptor, without a separate aggregation contract.; Origin-agnostic by construction: the descriptor's schema field is uniform data independent of construction, so a dynamic/WASM-module config source contributes the SAME schema row to the SAME catalog — native + dynamic config self-document through one catalog (the cross-crate two-source duality, as a CANDIDATE), which neither a per-crate file (R2) nor a pure proc-macro (R1) expresses as cleanly.; Rich runtime diagnostics (charter #9): because the schema is in-program, a startup or admin-path check can cross-reference SET property keys against the catalog and emit 'unknown property my.app.naem — did you mean my.app.name? (declared at src/config.rs:12)' using the schema + Span provenance — a Spring-grade DX touch (Spring's relaxed-binding + metadata powers exactly this IDE/startup hint).; Reuses config-properties' EXISTING descriptor/slice (if config-properties R1 or R3 is chosen): no new substrate — config-metadata is a FIELD on a descriptor that already exists, the thinnest possible addition (charter #2/#11), and the macro that already emits the descriptor just fills one more const field.

**Cons:** TIGHTLY COUPLES config-metadata to the link-time descriptor substrate AND to config-properties' realization choice — exactly the DEFERRED cross-crate-composition + metadata/codegen + type-erasure keystones (charter §3): R3 only works cleanly if config-properties is ALSO descriptor-based (its R1/R3), and it pre-judges that the metadata catalog rides the runtime-linked slice — the most architecturally presumptuous realization, must stay strictly a CANDIDATE.; Puts metadata INTO the running binary (the catalog is linked in) — VIOLATING Spring's 'no runtime cost' intent (docs line 1622) at least for binary SIZE: the `const ConfigGroup` schemas occupy space in the shipped binary even though the default use is build-time tooling. R1's optional slice and R2's sibling-file keep metadata out of the running app; R3 deliberately keeps it IN for the runtime-query capability — a real overhead tradeoff (charter #2) accepted only IF the runtime catalog is wanted.; Re-introduces the FULL DCE hazard with the runtime-query capability raising the stakes: if the catalog is meant to be queried at runtime (the differentiator), a DCE-dropped schema descriptor now produces a WRONG runtime answer ('this property doesn't exist' when it does), not just a tooling gap — so R3 inherits config-properties' force-link + zero-contribution self-check obligations (cross-crate doc line 152, 168), unlike R1/R2 where metadata-DCE is benign.; The runtime-query capability is arguably SCOPE CREEP beyond Spring's config-metadata intent (which is purely compile-time, IDE/docs-facing, docs line 1622): Spring does NOT expose config-metadata at runtime — making it runtime-reflectable is a leaf INVENTION (defensible as 'Rust's reflection answer' but a divergence from the parity target that must be justified, not assumed).; Couples config-metadata's correctness to whatever the type-erasure/registry substrate becomes (the descriptor lives in the same slice as type-erased beans/config) — entangling a TOOLING feature with a deep keystone, the inverse of good layering; a TOOLING artifact should not gate on the bean-storage substrate.; Heaviest binary + heaviest entanglement for a feature whose 80% use case (IDE autocompletion) is served by R1/R2's build-time file at zero binary cost — R3's extra power (runtime catalog) is the rarer need, so paying its costs by default is poorly amortized unless the runtime capability is a first-class requirement.

**Mechanisms considered:** a `ConfigSchema` reflection trait (`const SCHEMA: ConfigGroup`) every config-properties type implements — the synthesized-reflection model (nightly doc line 449); GROWING config-properties' existing `ConfigPropsDescriptor` with a `schema: &'static ConfigGroup` field — one descriptor, two consumers (bind + metadata), maximal unification; link-time `linkme` slice as the shared discovery+metadata catalog (the static 'classpath'); + optional dynamic/WASM-module schema source feeding the same catalog (the dynamic 'classpath') — a CANDIDATE; a `leaf::config_metadata::catalog()` / `to_canonical_json()` runtime+tool API walking the descriptor slice at the binary (whole-graph vantage); a runtime COLD-path diagnostic: cross-reference set keys vs catalog, emit 'unknown property + did-you-mean + declaration site' (Span provenance) — an Actuator/`leaf doctor` analogue; the declaration proc-macro still co-emits `SCHEMA` (only it reads `///`); override/ignore supplement merged at serialization; force-link + zero-contribution self-check REQUIRED for the runtime-query path (DCE here gives wrong answers, not just tooling gaps); stable-only: const ConfigGroup data, const TypeId::of (1.91), linkme behind-flag, Any-free schema (pure data); no nightly

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** R3's cross-crate behavior is INHERITED from the link-time descriptor substrate it shares with config-properties' scan route + component-scanning (charter #11 unification) — and that is both its strength and its entanglement. The default is a `linkme` slice of descriptors each carrying a `schema: &'static ConfigGroup` (the static 'classpath'), with an optional dynamic/WASM-module schema source feeding the SAME catalog (the dynamic 'classpath') — both origin-agnostic. The whole-app rollup is the catalog walk at the FINAL BINARY (cross-crate doc line 260). The DECISIVE T1 difference from R1/R2: because R3's differentiator is RUNTIME query, the DCE hazard becomes STAKEFUL again (cross-crate doc line 135, 152) — a dropped schema descriptor means the runtime catalog reports a real property as 'unknown', actively misleading, so R3 MUST inherit the force-link discipline (`use crate as _;`, cross-crate doc line 168) + the zero-contribution self-check + the toolchain guardrails (Rust ≥1.89 / `-z nostart-stop-gc`, cross-crate doc line 169) that R1/R2 could relax. Generics-can't-register (line 153) and proc-macro absolute-path hygiene (line 90) apply as for any descriptor. The v4 cross-module case is served (crate A force-emits its own schema descriptor) but ONLY if A participates in the link graph — weaker than R2's `cargo metadata` pass which sees DECLARED deps regardless of link reachability. R3 thus FOLDS config-metadata into the cross-crate-composition + type-erasure/registry keystones (a TOOLING feature gating on deep substrate decisions), the most entangled position — flagged Phase-2, NOT decided. SHARES the substrate question with config-properties, component-scanning, auto-configuration, the binder.

**T2 — execution context:** R3 is the ONLY realization with a genuine RUNTIME execution context, by design. Build-time portion (proc-macro co-emits SCHEMA; CLI/xtask serializes the artifact) matches R1/R2: synchronous, host, no async, no blocking concern. The DIVERGENCE: R3's catalog is LINKED INTO the running binary, enabling a COLD-PATH runtime capability — `leaf::config_metadata::catalog()` / a `leaf doctor` unknown-property check / an Actuator-style `/config-metadata` endpoint. Per charter #4, any such read is a COLD path (startup self-check or an explicit admin/diagnostic request — never a hot path, never per-request steady-state), and it is a pure SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking read of `const` data already in memory (walk the slice, compare TypeIds/keys, serialize) — no `.await`, no I/O, no allocation beyond the serialization buffer, so no cancellation concern and no blocking risk (charter #4/#5). If a runtime unknown-property check runs at startup, it composes with config-properties' early-refresh bind step (refresh-lifecycle) and can AGGREGATE 'unknown property' warnings alongside config bind/validation diagnostics into the same startup report (charter #9) — but it is advisory (a warning, since `ignore_unknown_fields` defaults true), NOT a fail-fast (distinguishing it from config-properties' bind failures). The catalog is `const`/`'static`, trivially `Send + Sync`, crosses `.await`/threads freely (concurrency-contract). There is NO write path, NO mutation, NO lock — purely read-only static data. The accepted cost vs R1/R2: the schema occupies binary space at runtime even when only build-time tooling consumes it (charter #2 overhead tradeoff), justified ONLY if the runtime-query capability is a requirement.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's config-metadata is produced by an ANNOTATION PROCESSOR (`spring-boot-configuration-processor`) that runs during `javac`, reads the `@ConfigurationProperties` source INCLUDING Javadoc, and can even read a DEPENDENCY's source to document a reusable type (the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` case). Rust has NO annotation processor and NO whole-program compile-time view: a proc-macro sees ONLY its own invocation's tokens (cross-crate doc line 89) — it can document the DECLARING crate's types but CANNOT see a config type defined in another crate, and a `build.rs` sees only its own crate's files + `cargo metadata` (declared deps, not a classpath, cross-crate doc line 357). So the single thing Spring's processor does transparently — 'document every config property in the whole app, including reusable types from other jars, from their source' — must be SPLIT in leaf between a per-crate doc-comment-capturing macro and a whole-graph aggregation pass at the binary; there is no single mechanism that does both.
- Spring sources property DESCRIPTIONS from Javadoc on the field/record-component. Rust's analogue is the `///` doc comment (desugaring to `#[doc="..."]`), which a proc-macro CAN read from its token input — a clean intent transcription. BUT: doc comments are unstructured plain text/Markdown with no `@param`-style tags, `Span::source_text()`/`byte_range()` richness is partly nightly (nightly doc line 555), and a build.rs canNOT read doc comments at all (they are not in `cargo metadata`) — so description capture is FORCED through a proc-macro at the declaring crate's compile time even in an otherwise-codegen approach, and the captured description is shallower than Javadoc's structured form. The 'documentation IS the config docs' DX is achievable but less structured than the JVM's.
- Spring's metadata is a runtime-irrelevant build artifact (`META-INF/...json` in the jar, never loaded by the app — docs line 1622 'no runtime cost or reflection'). Rust offers THREE divergent homes for that artifact, each with a different cost profile that Spring never had to choose between: (a) a proc-macro-emitted `const` (lives in the binary unless DCE'd); (b) a build.rs/CLI-emitted sibling FILE (outside the binary, sqlx model); (c) a link-time descriptor catalog deliberately kept in the binary for runtime query. Spring's JVM put it in the jar's META-INF for free; Rust forces a binary-size-vs-portability-vs-runtime-capability tradeoff that lands squarely on the DEFERRED metadata/codegen-boundary keystone (charter §3).
- Spring's metadata advertises the CANONICAL property name and reads JVM type signatures for the `type` field. In Rust, the canonical kebab name must be DERIVED from the snake_case field via relaxed-binding's convention (a leaf invention, not a transcription), and the Rust TYPE must be RENDERED to a stable, tool-friendly type string by leaf — `Duration`, `Vec<String>`, `HashMap<String,Foo>`, an enum's variant set — a vocabulary that couples to type-conversion and that Spring got from reflective type signatures for free. A field RENAME silently changes the advertised key unless the metadata is regenerated, and the type-string rendering is a convention with no canonical Rust answer.
