- Spring auto-detects `defaultValue` from initializers but explicitly CANNOT for collections/maps (docs line 1620), pushing those to the hand-authored `additional-...json`. In Rust, a proc-macro sees a `#[config(default=...)]` literal but NOT a meaningful default for a `Vec`/`HashMap` field type (and `Default::default()` is opaque at macro time — it is a trait call, not a readable value), so the SAME collection/map-default gap exists, AND the hand-authored override channel (Spring's `additional-...json` + `ignored.properties`) must be reinvented as a checked-in leaf supplement with a defined merge/precedence over the generated tree — a coherence surface Spring's processor + single JSON file handled by convention.
- Spring's config-metadata is INHERENTLY whole-classpath ('what does this app accept' is a query over every jar's META-INF). Rust has no classpath: the whole-app rollup must be synthesized at the FINAL BINARY (the only whole-graph vantage, cross-crate doc line 260) via either a link-time descriptor walk (DCE-exposed, cross-crate doc line 135) or a `cargo metadata` codegen pass (declared-deps-scoped). UNIQUELY, the DCE hazard that is high-stakes for component/config-properties discovery is BENIGN here for the build-artifact use (a dropped metadata descriptor degrades only IDE/docs, never app behavior) — but becomes stakeful AGAIN if the catalog is made runtime-queryable (R3), inverting the usual DCE calculus and making 'is metadata in the binary?' a load-bearing question Spring never faced.
- Spring keeps config-metadata strictly COMPILE-TIME / IDE-facing. Rust's missing reflection (nightly doc line 449 — 'no runtime reflection; synthesize at build time') TEMPTS leaf to make the metadata catalog runtime-reflectable (R3) as the framework's reflection answer, enabling runtime 'unknown property' diagnostics Spring's relaxed-binding+metadata powers in the IDE. This is a capability EXPANSION beyond the parity target — defensible (it serves the same 'discoverable surface' intent at runtime) but a divergence that trades binary size + DCE-stakes for a capability Spring delivers only in tooling; whether leaf should exceed Spring's compile-time-only scope is a genuine design question Rust's reflection gap raises and the JVM never posed.

### Interactions
- **config-properties** — HARD DEPENDENCY and the UPSTREAM declaration this feature projects. config-properties owns the prefix-rooted typed-target declaration (the `#[config_properties(prefix=...)]` surface + the three enabling routes + leniency policy); THIS feature is its SELF-DOCUMENTING SEAM — Spring's 'the same target declaration powers compile-time config-metadata emission' (config-properties intent part 7). The genuinely divergent axis is whether ONE macro co-emits both binding artifacts AND metadata (R1/R3 — single source of truth, atomic coherence) or a separate codegen pass reads a per-crate fragment the declaration leaves (R2). config-properties owns WHAT is declared (prefix, fields, defaults, bind-mode); this feature owns the EMISSION of the accepted-surface artifact from that declaration. The 'config is data' philosophy config-properties instills is exactly why metadata is a clean projection — there are no expressions to document, just an inert tree.
- **relaxed-binding** — HARD DEPENDENCY (transitively, for key identity). The metadata MUST advertise the CANONICAL kebab-case property name (Spring's metadata uses the canonical form), and that name is DERIVED from the Rust snake_case field via relaxed-binding's `first_name`→`first-name` rule. So this feature consumes relaxed-binding's field-name→canonical-key derivation to render each property's `name`; relaxed-binding owns the canonical-key identity + per-transport equivalence. The metadata advertises the canonical form precisely so tooling/IDE autocompletion suggests the one form a developer should write (the relaxed-binding asymmetric-placeholder lesson — advertise canonical, accept many).
- **binder** — UPSTREAM schema source (the tree shape this feature reads). The binder's `BindTarget` derive (binder R1) already captures the config type's tree schema — field set, nested structure, types, defaults — as const data for binding; this feature READS that same schema to populate property rows, rather than re-deriving the tree independently (charter #11 — one schema, two consumers: bind + document). binder owns the tree-descent + BindTarget schema representation; this feature owns rendering that schema into the tooling-facing metadata format (canonical names, type strings, descriptions, hints). The bind-method (JavaBean vs value-object) is binder's concern and largely invisible to metadata, which documents the accepted KEYS regardless of construction mode.
- **type-conversion** — COMPLEMENTARY (the type vocabulary metadata advertises). The `type` field of each property and the rendering of `Duration`/`DataSize`/enum-variant hints reflect what type-conversion can coerce a string INTO — so the metadata's type strings + value hints should align with type-conversion's coercion vocabulary (an enum's accepted variant names become value hints; a `Duration`'s accepted suffixes inform the hint/description). type-conversion owns string→T coercion; this feature owns advertising, in tool-readable form, what types/values are accepted — ideally sourcing enum-variant hints from the same place type-conversion knows them, not a parallel list.
- **validation** — COMPLEMENTARY producer-side (constraints as hints/docs). A `#[validated]` config type's constraints (min/max/pattern/enumerated) are exactly the kind of accepted-value information a HINT or description should surface — Spring's metadata can carry such hints. So this feature MAY read validation's constraint metadata to enrich a property's hints ('must be >= 1', 'one of: A|B|C'), making the accepted surface more discoverable. validation owns the constraint engine + constraint metadata; this feature owns optionally projecting those constraints into the tooling artifact as hints/descriptions — a one-directional read, never invoking validation.
- **config-data** — COMPLEMENTARY (tooling consumes metadata against config files). config-data loads application/profile config files; an IDE or `leaf doctor` uses THIS feature's emitted metadata to validate/autocomplete those files ('this key in application.toml is unknown / deprecated / has these accepted values'). config-data owns file loading + precedence; this feature owns the metadata that tells tooling what those files MAY legitimately contain — the two compose at the tooling layer (metadata describes the schema; config-data provides the instances tooling checks against it).
- **origin-tracking** — COMPLEMENTARY (provenance in metadata + diagnostics). This feature embeds DECLARATION-site provenance (the Rust source file/line where a property is declared, via `proc_macro::Span`, stable 1.88) into each property row — the mirror of origin-tracking's VALUE-site provenance (where a value came from). Together they let tooling say 'property my.app.timeout (declared at src/config.rs:12) — you set it from application.yaml:8 to an invalid value'. origin-tracking owns the loaded-value provenance representation; this feature owns the DECLARATION-site provenance in the metadata, the static half of the same diagnostic story.
- **component-scanning** — CANDIDATE-SHARED discovery/aggregation substrate. The whole-app metadata rollup ('what does this app accept') is a whole-graph discovery problem the SAME way component-scanning discovers beans — and R3 explicitly proposes the metadata catalog ride the SAME link-time descriptor slice config-properties' scan route + component-scanning use (charter #11). Whether metadata aggregation rides that one substrate, a `cargo metadata` codegen pass (R2), or a parallel slice is a flagged Phase-2 keystone, NOT decided here. component-scanning owns the discovery primitive; this feature owns the metadata-specific content (schema rows) on whatever descriptor/aggregation mechanism is chosen — with the unique note that a DCE miss here is benign (tooling-only) unless metadata is made runtime-queryable.
- **auto-configuration** — CONSUMER + CONTRIBUTOR (library config types must self-document). Auto-config crates ship their own config-properties types (the 'libraries carry @EnableConfigurationProperties' story); for the app's metadata to be COMPLETE, those library config types must contribute metadata too — exactly the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` cross-module case (document a reusable type from another crate). This is where R1's proc-macro-only model has a gap (it documents only the declaring crate) and R2's `cargo metadata` pass / R3's force-linked descriptor shine (they gather library-contributed metadata at the binary). auto-configuration owns the opinionated-defaults registration; this feature owns ensuring those auto-config-shipped config types appear in the app's accepted-surface artifact.
- **value-injection** — SIBLING + scope contrast. `@Value`-style per-field externalized values (value-injection) are NOT part of config-metadata's documented surface in Spring — metadata documents `@ConfigurationProperties` GROUPS, not scattered `@Value` keys (which are expression-bearing and ad hoc). This feature inherits that boundary: it documents the cohesive, inert, prefix-rooted config-properties surface, NOT individual value-injection points. The contrast reinforces config-properties' 'cohesive documented config object replaces scattered @Value' intent — only the cohesive form is self-documenting; the scattered form is not (a reason to prefer config-properties).
- **profiles** — COMPLEMENTARY (profile-conditional config in metadata). Profile-gated config-properties types (active only under a named profile) are still part of the accepted surface tooling should document — metadata may note that certain properties apply under specific profiles (Spring's metadata can carry such grouping). profiles owns the activation grammar + conditional gating; this feature owns documenting the full accepted surface including profile-conditional groups, so 'what CAN this app accept under profile X' is discoverable — the metadata is a superset describing all declared properties regardless of which profile activates them.
- **conditions** — COMPLEMENTARY (conditional config types still documented). Like profiles, a `@Conditional`-gated config-properties type contributes to the documented surface even if not always active — metadata describes what is DECLARED/ACCEPTED, orthogonal to whether a condition activates it at runtime. conditions owns the pure-predicate gating; this feature documents the declared surface unconditionally (tooling wants to know about a property even if it only applies when a condition holds), keeping metadata a complete catalog of declarations rather than a runtime-active subset.
- **startup-instrumentation** — ANALOGOUS pattern (the tooling-facing-artifact, no-runtime-cost-by-default sibling). startup-instrumentation records a tool-friendly taxonomy of startup steps that is no-op by default (opt-in recording, zero overhead otherwise); config-metadata is its compile-time analogue — a tool-friendly description of the config surface that costs the running app nothing by default (build artifact, or DCE-able section, or opt-in runtime catalog in R3). Both embody charter #2 (zero cost unless opted in) + the 'documentation-as-metadata for tooling' stance (Spring's role-hint design intent, docs line 616). No data dependency; a shared design philosophy worth aligning the diagnostics taxonomy with.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- WHERE does the metadata/codegen boundary fall for config-metadata — proc-macro CO-EMISSION (R1, single source of truth atomic with binding, but blind across crates), out-of-band build.rs/`cargo leaf metadata` CODEGEN over the resolved graph (R2, whole-graph + v4 cross-module + portable, but a build step + still needs a doc-comment-capturing macro), or a link-time REFLECTION CATALOG in the binary (R3, runtime-queryable + maximal unification, but binary cost + DCE-stakeful + scope-creep)? This IS the deferred metadata/codegen-boundary keystone (charter §3) instantiated for config — and it cross-cuts the binder's BindTarget-schema source of truth and config-properties' declaration macro. Deliberately UNRESOLVED.
- How is the v4 CROSS-MODULE / cross-crate metadata case (`@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` — full metadata for a reusable config type defined in crate A but bound/consumed in crate B that cannot see A's source) served, given a proc-macro sees only its own crate (cross-crate doc line 89)? Candidates: a per-crate metadata FRAGMENT each crate emits + a binary aggregation pass (R2); a force-linked descriptor catalog (R3); or accept the gap and require the override channel for foreign types (R1). This shares the cross-crate-composition keystone with component-scanning, auto-config, config-properties' scan route, and the binder's handler discovery — adopting one substrate biases the meta-architecture. UNRESOLVED.
- Should config-metadata be RUNTIME-QUERYABLE (R3 — a live catalog enabling Actuator-style `/config-metadata` + a startup 'unknown property, did-you-mean' diagnostic, leaf's answer to Rust's missing reflection per nightly doc line 449) or strictly a COMPILE-TIME build artifact (R1/R2 — Spring's actual intent, docs line 1622 'no runtime cost or reflection')? Runtime query is a capability EXPANSION beyond the parity target that trades binary size + re-stakes DCE (a dropped descriptor gives wrong runtime answers) for richer runtime diagnostics. Whether leaf exceeds Spring's compile-time-only scope here is a genuine call entangled with the diagnostics model (charter §3) and the type-erasure/registry substrate. UNRESOLVED.
- WHERE does the emitted artifact LIVE and how does tooling find it — a `const` in the binary (DCE-able, R1), a sibling checked-in `config-metadata.json` (sqlx model, R2), a per-type `target/.../<fqn>.json` (Spring v4 per-type-location analogue), and/or a runtime catalog (R3)? And is there a `--check`-able committed artifact (sqlx `prepare --check`) gating CI against metadata drift? This is both a DX question (how does an IDE plugin / docs generator discover leaf metadata) and a binary-cost question (charter #2), and it depends on the metadata/codegen-boundary resolution. UNRESOLVED.
- How does the HAND-AUTHORED override/supplement/ignore channel (Spring's `additional-spring-configuration-metadata.json` + its `ignored.properties` section) work in leaf — its FORMAT, its merge PRECEDENCE over generated metadata, and its OWNERSHIP location (per-crate vs app-root)? It is mandatory for collection/map defaults (un-inferable, docs line 1620), descriptions for externally-bound/foreign keys, and intentionally-ignored keys — so 'single source of truth' is never total; the split between generated and hand-authored metadata must be defined coherently. Cross-cuts config-properties (foreign-type documentation) and the artifact-location question. UNRESOLVED.
- What is the leaf convention for rendering a RUST TYPE into a stable, tool-friendly metadata `type` string, and for deriving HINTS from types (enum variants → value hints, `Duration`/`DataSize` suffixes, collection element types)? Spring read JVM type signatures for free; leaf must INVENT this rendering, and it couples to type-conversion's coercion vocabulary (the hints should match what conversion accepts) and validation's constraints (constraints as hints). Whether the type-string + hint vocabulary is owned by config-metadata, type-conversion, or shared is a cross-feature consistency question. UNRESOLVED.
- Should config-metadata aggregation SHARE one substrate with the whole family of whole-graph discovery problems (component-scanning, config-properties' scan route, auto-configuration, the binder/property-resolution handler discovery) — the charter #11 unification goal — or stay a parallel/independent path given its UNIQUE property that DCE misses are benign (tooling-only) for the compile-time use? The benign-DCE asymmetry means metadata could ride a CHEAPER, force-link-free substrate than the other discovery features need — but a shared substrate is the unification north-star. Whether metadata's lower stakes justify (or contraindicate) sharing is a Phase-2 substrate call. UNRESOLVED.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I designed the config-metadata feature (the metadata EMISSION layer) — NOT config-properties, which was handed to me as the already-designed UPSTREAM dependency (the prefix-rooted declaration front-end). I built ON config-properties concretely: this feature is its 'self-documenting seam' (config-properties intent part 7), projecting the SAME declaration that drives binding into a tooling-facing artifact. This feature owns ONLY: the metadata artifact FORMAT (the `spring-configuration-metadata.json` analogue — groups + properties{name/type/description/default/deprecation} + hints), the SOURCE-OF-TRUTH coupling to the config declaration, the doc-comment(`///`)→description capture, the default/deprecation/hint capture, the hand-authored OVERRIDE/IGNORE channel (Spring's `additional-...json`), the v4 cross-module story (the genuinely hard Rust axis), and the DELIVERY of the artifact to tooling. I deliberately did NOT redesign: the declaration surface / three enabling routes / leniency policy (config-properties), the bind engine / BindTarget schema (binder), canonical-key identity + snake→kebab derivation (relaxed-binding), string→T coercion (type-conversion), the constraint engine (validation), file loading/precedence (config-data), or value provenance (origin-tracking).\n\nThe genuinely divergent Rust axis for THIS feature is the metadata/codegen BOUNDARY (a charter §3 deferred keystone) + the no-classpath cross-crate reality: Spring's annotation processor transparently documents the WHOLE app (including reusable types from other jars, from their source) during `javac`; Rust has no such whole-program processor — a proc-macro sees only its own invocation (cross-crate doc line 89), a build.rs sees only its own crate + declared deps (line 357). So the three realizations diverge precisely on how to bridge that gap. R1 = proc-macro CO-EMISSION (the same `#[config_properties]` macro emits a `const ConfigGroup` alongside binding artifacts — strongest single-source-of-truth, cleanest doc-comment capture, thinnest macro, zero runtime cost, UNIQUELY benign DCE since a dropped metadata descriptor harms only tooling not the app; BUT blind across crates, so the whole-app rollup + v4 cross-module case need a second mechanism). R2 = out-of-band build.rs/`cargo leaf metadata` CODEGEN over the resolved graph (sqlx model — FULLY serves the whole-app rollup + v4 cross-module + `--check`-able CI gate + portable incl. wasm; BUT a build step, and STILL needs a thin per-crate macro to capture `///` doc-comments, so it is a hybrid recorder+aggregator). R3 = link-time REFLECTION CATALOG (grow config-properties' descriptor with a `schema` field, query it at runtime — maximal charter #11 unification + enables runtime 'unknown property' diagnostics as leaf's reflection answer per nightly doc line 449; BUT puts metadata in the binary violating Spring's no-runtime-cost intent, re-stakes DCE since a miss gives WRONG runtime answers, and is scope-creep beyond Spring's compile-time-only metadata). R1↔R2 differ on macro-coupled-vs-out-of-band; R1/R2↔R3 differ on build-artifact-only-vs-runtime-queryable.\n\nAll three: source descriptions from `///` doc comments (the Javadoc analogue, read via `#[doc]` attributes — stable, no nightly); advertise the CANONICAL kebab key (relaxed-binding) as the form tooling suggests; embed declaration-site provenance via `proc_macro::Span` file/line (stable 1.88, nightly doc line 555); keep metadata ZERO runtime cost by default (Spring intent docs line 1622); provide a hand-authored override/ignore supplement for un-inferable collection/map defaults + foreign-key descriptions + ignored keys (docs line 1620); keep macros THIN (charter #10 — emit only `const` ConfigGroup data, hand-writable, plus a programmatic `ConfigGroup{..}` builder escape hatch for foreign/dynamic types); keep the schema shape ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a dynamic/WASM-module config source self-documents identically); and serve the v4 cross-module case + whole-app rollup at the FINAL BINARY (the only whole-graph vantage, cross-crate doc line 260).\n\nNightly review (against rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md): NOTHING needs nightly — `proc_macro::Span` file/line/source_text is stable 1.88 (line 555; note byte_range/join/parent remain nightly, avoided); `#[doc]`-attribute reading is plain token inspection; `const ConfigGroup` data + const TypeId::of (1.91, line 16) for the catalog rows; linkme (behind-flag, line 30) for R1's optional rollup slice + R3's catalog; build.rs codegen + cargo_metadata (stable) for R2; serde for serialization. The metadata schema is pure DATA with no async, no fn-pointers required, no trait dispatch — the simplest T2 in the config family (build-time only, except R3's opt-in cold-path runtime read). UNIQUE among discovery features: the DCE hazard (cross-crate doc line 135) is BENIGN for the compile-time use (a dropped metadata descriptor degrades only IDE/docs, never app behavior — INVERTING config-properties' high-stakes DCE), so R1/R2 can RELAX the force-link + zero-contribution self-check that config-properties' scan route demands; only R3's runtime-query path re-stakes it (a miss gives wrong answers). The sharpest Phase-2 tensions I surfaced but did NOT resolve: the metadata/codegen boundary (Q1, the keystone), the cross-crate/v4-cross-module substrate (Q2), runtime-queryable-vs-compile-time-only (Q3, a parity-scope call), artifact location + `--check` gate (Q4), the override/ignore channel format+precedence+ownership (Q5), the rust-type→metadata-type-string + hint-derivation vocabulary (Q6), and whether metadata aggregation shares one substrate with the discovery family given its benign-DCE asymmetry (Q7). Naming ('ConfigMetadataSource', 'ConfigGroup', 'Property', 'Hint', 'Deprecation', 'config-metadata.json', '`cargo leaf metadata`', 'catalog()') is Phase-1 placeholder. I wrote no files.\n\nRelevant grounded source paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (1618-1624 the dedicated 'Configuration metadata generation' section — compile-time emission of groups/properties{name/type/description-from-Javadoc/defaultValue/deprecation}/hints 1620, the 'discoverable self-documenting API surface / no runtime cost or reflection' intent 1622, the `additional-spring-configuration-metadata.json` override + `ignored.properties` channel + collection/map-default gap 1620, the v4 `@ConfigurationPropertiesSource` cross-module case + per-type `META-INF/spring/configuration-metadata/<fqn>.json` location + properties-migrator-reads-the-JSON 1624; plus 616 the documentation-as-metadata/role-hint design stance, 1553-1624 the config-properties section it projects, 1535 relaxed-binding canonical form); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md (invariants §2 esp. DX#1/overhead#2/async-first§2.3 cold-vs-hot§2.4/no-global-locks§2.5/stable§2.8/rich-diagnostics§2.9/thin-macros§2.10/unification§2.11; deferred keystones §3 esp. metadata-codegen-boundary/cross-crate-composition/type-erasure-registry/diagnostics-model; T1/T2 §4; topology §6 incl. leaf-macros/leaf-codegen separation); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (proc-macro single-invocation-scope 89, absolute-path hygiene 90, leaf-macros/leaf-core split 91/353, build.rs-cannot-scan-siblings 357 + cargo-metadata-is-declared-deps-not-classpath 317, DCE three layers 135/146/149, register-const-descriptors 167, force-link discipline 168, generics-can't-register 153, binary-sees-whole-graph 260, role-separation 233, Architecture C sqlx build-time-codegen + `--check` 305-317/228/235, Architecture B linkme+force-link 291, scope-discovery-not-global 362, OUT_DIR determinism 52); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (proc_macro::Span file/line stable 1.88 line 22/84/555 incl. the byte_range/join nightly caveat, no-runtime-reflection synthesize-at-build-time 449/497, const TypeId::of 1.91 line 16/453, type_name diagnostic-only/emit-canonical-name-in-metadata 477, linkme behind-flag + cross-crate-discard caveat 30/365, no-nightly-needed 76).

## Command-line argument property source + ApplicationArguments parsing  `[extra-6]`

Spring's `CommandLinePropertySource` (Framework) plus Boot's `DefaultApplicationArguments`/`ApplicationArguments` is a DISTINCT property-source TYPE with its own PARSING GRAMMAR, sitting at a canonical near-top precedence rung and exposed as an injectable bean. The intent leaf must replicate (intent, NOT JVM mechanism) has five load-bearing parts:

(1) A PARSING GRAMMAR distinct from a generic Map backing. Spring's `SimpleCommandLineArgsParser` splits raw argv into (a) OPTION args — tokens beginning with `--`: `--key=value` (key+value), or bare `--flag` with NO `=` (an OPTION WITH EMPTY/absent value, a boolean-ish presence flag); and (b) NON-OPTION args — everything else (positionals; a lone `--` and single-dash `-x` are non-option in Spring's simple parser). A malformed `--=value` (empty option name) is rejected. This grammar is the whole reason this is a source TYPE, not just another map.

(2) REPEATED OPTIONS COLLAPSE TO A LIST. `--foo=a --foo=b` yields option `foo` with values `["a","b"]` (`getOptionValues` → list). As a flat property value the source joins them comma-separated (`getProperty("foo")` → `"a,b"`), composing with relaxed-binding list conventions and type-conversion comma-split. A present-but-empty bare flag resolves to an EMPTY string value (present, not absent) so it honors null-never-overrides (presence ≠ absence).

(3) NON-OPTION ARGS ARE A FIRST-CLASS, SEPARATE CHANNEL — NOT properties. Spring exposes them BOTH as `getNonOptionArgs()` AND, within the source, under a configurable synthetic key (`nonOptionArgs`, default) whose value is the comma-joined list — so positionals are addressable through the uniform resolver if needed while staying conceptually distinct.

(4) A CANONICAL NEAR-TOP PRECEDENCE RUNG, seeded VERY EARLY. In Boot's 15-rung ladder command-line args are rung 11 — above OS env, system props, JNDI/servlet, and `SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON`, below only test-scoped overrides. It is added in `configureEnvironment()` during `prepareEnvironment()` — before EnvironmentPostProcessors / config-data load — so `--spring.config.location=…` / `--spring.profiles.active=…` are visible to the config bootstrap (these early control keys ONLY work as env/system-prop/CLI args). Added as ONE named source so ordering mutation can target it by name. Disable-able (`setAddCommandLineProperties(false)`).

(5) `ApplicationArguments` IS AN INJECTABLE BEAN + the runner duality. The parsed handle is registered as a singleton (`springApplicationArguments`); it exposes `getSourceArgs()` (raw), `getOptionNames()`, `containsOption`, `getOptionValues(name)`, `getNonOptionArgs()`. Two runner shapes consume it: raw-args (`CommandLineRunner.run(String[])`) and parsed (`ApplicationRunner.run(ApplicationArguments)`), fired in one `@Order`-sorted stream after refresh, before ready.

SCOPE BOUNDARY: `property-sources` owns the ordered stack + first-source-wins + never-blend + the `PropertySource` trait shape (this source is one conformer); `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` walk + read interface; `relaxed-binding` owns canonical-key matching + list/map index conventions; `type-conversion` owns string→T (incl. comma-split→Vec); `config-data` owns the PRECEDENCE-ORDER POLICY (which rung) + early-control-key bootstrap; `origin-tracking` owns the `Origin` carrier (this source attaches a coarse CommandLine origin, no file/line); the bootstrap feature owns the run() pipeline + runner invocation. THIS feature owns ONLY: the argv→(options, non-options) PARSER + its grammar, the repeated-key→list + comma-join rule, the present-empty vs absent distinction, the `PropertySource` ADAPTER projecting parsed options (+ synthetic non-option key) onto the stack with a coarse origin, the canonical source name + disable lever, and the `ApplicationArguments` HANDLE type (accessor surface + raw/parsed runner-consumption shapes). It does NOT decide its ladder position (config-data policy) nor how it is seeded (bootstrap).

### Candidate realizations

#### Eager-parsed owned struct + thin PropertySource adapter (parse-once-at-bootstrap)
A plain stable-Rust value type, owned, parsed exactly once at the very start of the bootstrap pipeline.

```rust
pub struct ApplicationArguments {
    raw: Box<[String]>,
    options: BTreeMap<Box<str>, SmallVec<[Box<str>; 1]>>, // repeated→list
    non_option: Box<[String]>,
}
impl ApplicationArguments {
    pub fn parse(argv: impl IntoIterator<Item=String>) -> Result<Self, ArgParseError>;
    pub fn option_names(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item=&str>;
    pub fn contains_option(&self, name: &str) -> bool;
    pub fn option_values(&self, name: &str) -> &[Box<str>]; // []=absent; [""]=bare flag present
    pub fn non_option_args(&self) -> &[String];
    pub fn source_args(&self) -> &[String];
}
```
Grammar lives in `parse`: token `--xxx` (len>2) is an option; split on FIRST `=` → (name, Some); no `=` → (name, None) recorded as empty string; `--=` → `ArgParseError::EmptyOptionName{index,token}` (rich diagnostic); else (incl. lone `--`, `-x`) → non_option. Repeated names append.

A thin adapter implements the `property-sources` `PropertySource` trait by borrowing the parsed struct, named `"commandLineArgs"`:
```rust
struct CommandLineSource<'a> { name:&'static str, args:&'a ApplicationArguments, non_option_key:&'static str }
impl PropertySource for CommandLineSource<'_> {
  fn get(&self, key:&str)->Option<PropertyValue<'_>>{
    if key==self.non_option_key { return Some(joined(self.args.non_option_args(), Origin::CommandLine)); }
    match self.args.option_values(key){ []=>None, vs=>Some(joined_csv(vs, Origin::CommandLine)) }
  }
  fn key_names(&self)->impl Iterator<Item=&str>; // option names + synthetic key
}
```
First-source-wins/never-blend/null-never-overrides inherited verbatim: `[]`⇒None⇒fall-through; bare flag `Some("")`⇒present, never falls through. The struct is moved once into the registry as the `springApplicationArguments` singleton; adapter holds a shared ref/Arc into it (one small Arc, justified). The bootstrap (not this feature) calls `stack.add_first(name, source)` at the config-data-dictated rung.

**Pros:** Zero runtime polling/async/global state — parse is a pure synchronous fold over argv; fully stable-buildable (charter #7/#8).; Stack-friendly memory: one owned struct, adapter borrows it; at most ONE small Arc to share the handle between bean and source (charter #5).; Clean separation: the PARSER is a normal testable fn with no container coupling — heavy logic in normal crates, macros not involved (#10).; `option_values` returning a slice maps directly onto getOptionValues→list and composes with relaxed-binding/type-conversion comma-split with no special-casing.; present-empty (`[""]`) vs absent (`[]`) encoded structurally, so null-never-overrides is honored for free.

**Cons:** Two representations of the SAME data co-exist (typed accessors AND stringly property view) — a unification smell Phase 2 must reconcile even though shared backing helps.; Borrowing adapter needs the struct to outlive the stack; forces the Arc/`'static` lifetime decision (the deferred ownership keystone §3) — cannot be settled here.; Eager parse surfaces a malformed-arg error at the very first bootstrap step, before diagnostics/logging is up — error rendering must be self-contained.

**Mechanisms considered:** plain stable parser fn (no proc-macro, no codegen, no registry); runtime registry only insofar as the bootstrap inserts the named source into the property-sources stack; dyn dispatch via the PropertySource trait object the stack already stores

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** NONE of the cross-crate/link-time hazards apply to the parser or source: argv is a runtime input owned by the binary, not a contribution discovered across crates. Parser + `ApplicationArguments` live in a normal inward-pointing kernel crate; no linkme/inventory/build.rs, no DCE exposure, works on every target incl. wasm (embedder passes a Vec<String>). The only cross-crate touchpoint is registering `ApplicationArguments` as a resolvable bean (rides the container's normal singleton path, Phase-2-decided) and the runner traits being a discovery surface (owned by bootstrap/runner feature, not here). Because the source is seeded by a DIRECT bootstrap call (`stack.add_first`), there is NO silently-empty-registry failure mode — presence is guaranteed by a call, not by link survival.

**T2 — execution context:** Parsing runs SYNCHRONOUSLY on the bootstrap thread at the first pipeline step, before any executor exists — must NOT block (pure CPU over an in-memory slice, microseconds) and must NOT be async (no runtime yet), satisfying §2.3. No cancellation surface (completes or errors). Errors propagate as a typed `ArgParseError` up the bootstrap result chain to the handle-run-failure equivalent, carrying token+index. The source's `get()` runs on whatever context the resolver uses (hot read path): map lookup + cheap CSV join, never blocks/awaits, holds no lock (struct immutable after bootstrap → reads need no sync). The injectable bean is publish-once/read-many, honoring concurrency-contract safe-publication with no runtime lock.

#### Lazy enumerable source over retained raw argv (parse-on-demand, no eager materialization)
Keep ONLY the raw `Box<[String]>` argv plus the option-prefix policy; don't materialize the options map up front. The source + accessors compute lazily, caching behind a `OnceLock` so repeated reads are O(1).

```rust
pub struct ApplicationArguments { raw: Box<[String]>, parsed: OnceLock<Result<Parsed, ArgParseError>> }
struct Parsed { options: BTreeMap<Box<str>, Vec<Box<str>>>, non_option: Box<[String]> }
impl ApplicationArguments {
  fn parsed(&self)->Result<&Parsed,&ArgParseError>{ self.parsed.get_or_init(|| Parsed::from(&self.raw)).as_ref() }
  pub fn option_values(&self,n:&str)->&[Box<str>]{ self.parsed().map(|p| p.options.get(n).map(|v|v.as_slice()).unwrap_or(&[])).unwrap_or(&[]) }
}
```
The adapter is identical in shape to realization 1 but reads through `parsed()`. The grammar is the same; what differs is WHEN it runs (first access, not bootstrap step 1) and that the raw argv is the source of truth (the structured view is a derived cache). A parse error is stored as data in the `OnceLock`, surfaced to the first reader.

VARIANT: skip the map entirely — a pure on-demand SCANNER linear-scans `raw` per `get(key)`. argv is tiny (tens of tokens) so even un-cached scanning is cheap; this removes the cache allocation AND the second representation, at O(n)-per-lookup cost. `key_names()` scans once.

**Pros:** Defers the only fallible step (parsing) past bootstrap step 1, so the failure surfaces when the richest diagnostic context exists (after logging/error-rendering is up) — directly serves charter #9 ('as early as the richest diagnostic allows, not earlier').; Minimal eager footprint: just the raw argv slice; the structured map is built only if someone reads options structurally (some apps only use positionals or raw args).; The pure-scanner variant has a SINGLE source of truth (raw argv) — no dual representation, dissolving realization 1's main unification smell.; Still fully synchronous/stable; argv tiny enough that lazy/scan cost is negligible.

**Cons:** A deferred parse error means a malformed `--spring.config.location=` is not caught until config-data reads it — which IS early in practice (early-control-keys are read first) but the timing is now implicit/data-dependent, not guaranteed.; `OnceLock` introduces a one-time init race to reason about across the bootstrap→runtime thread hop — a (single, cold-path) synchronization point the charter wants justified.; The pure-scanner variant trades memory for repeated O(n) hot-path work — acceptable only because argv is tiny; a larger arg set would make it a poor default.; Lazy parsing makes origin/diagnostics slightly less direct — the 'where' is only known after parse.

**Mechanisms considered:** lazy OnceLock-cached parse (interior mutability, cold-path init); pure stateless per-lookup scanner over raw argv (no cache, single source of truth); no proc-macro / no codegen / no link-time registry — purely runtime data over an owned slice

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Identical cross-crate profile to realization 1 — runtime input, not a cross-crate contribution, so no linkme/inventory/build.rs/DCE concerns. Only internal delta is OnceLock vs eager field, invisible across crate boundaries. Type lives in a normal inward-pointing kernel crate; bean registration + runner discovery owned elsewhere. Works on every target incl. wasm/embedded since it never touches the link-time substrate. No force-link/Layer-0 exposure (source inserted by a direct bootstrap call, not by registration survival).

**T2 — execution context:** Parsing deferred to first structured access — for the early-control-keys path this is on the bootstrap thread during config-data resolution: still synchronous, non-blocking (CPU-only over a tiny slice), pre-executor. If the handle is shared to runtime/async beans before first parse, `OnceLock::get_or_init` may run on a worker thread; it stays non-blocking and panic-free (parse error stored as DATA, not panicked) so it is safe to call from any context incl. inside an async task without awaiting. No cancellation surface. Cached state is published-once via OnceLock, so post-init reads are lock-free and visibility-safe (concurrency-contract honored); the single init is the only synchronized event and lies on a cold path (charter #4 permits cold-path sync).

#### Configurable-grammar parser SPI + GNU-ish extensibility, Spring-simple grammar as the default impl
Spring deliberately ships a SIMPLE grammar and leaves room for richer parsers. Model the grammar as a small replaceable strategy so leaf offers the Spring-compatible default AND lets an app opt into a fuller GNU/clap-style grammar (short `-f`, `-fvalue`, `--flag value`, `--` terminator) WITHOUT changing the source-adapter or `ApplicationArguments` shape.

```rust
pub trait ArgGrammar { fn parse(&self, argv:&[String]) -> Result<ParsedArgs, ArgParseError>; } // pure, no IO/async
pub struct ParsedArgs { options: Vec<(Box<str>, Box<str>)>, non_option: Vec<Box<str>> } // dups preserved → folded to list
pub struct SimpleSpringGrammar; // canonical default; exactly Spring's SimpleCommandLineArgsParser
impl ArgGrammar for SimpleSpringGrammar { /* --key=value, bare --key→"", --=→err, else non-option */ }
```
`ApplicationArguments::parse_with(grammar, argv)` folds `ParsedArgs` (dups→list, comma-join for the flat view) into the SAME accessor surface as realizations 1/2. The adapter + handle are grammar-agnostic. Grammar choice is a bootstrap-time, runtime-selected lever (a field on the application builder), NOT a cargo feature — honoring the cross-crate doc's 'model a choice as runtime selection, never mutually-exclusive features'. A thin optional integration crate could supply a richer impl; the CORE never depends on it (charter #6).

**Pros:** Future-proofs the one place Spring is deliberately minimal: apps wanting POSIX/GNU conventions (a strong Rust expectation) get them without leaf reinventing clap, while the Spring-parity default stays out-of-the-box.; Keeps the source adapter + handle grammar-agnostic — one stable surface regardless of which parser ran, so downstream (relaxed-binding, runners) never sees the difference.; Grammar selection as RUNTIME strategy sidesteps the additive-feature/mutually-exclusive-feature trap (cross-crate doc §features).; Default `SimpleSpringGrammar` is a tiny zero-field type; if taken as a generic rather than a trait object, the common path pays nothing for the seam.

**Cons:** Adds an SPI surface that may be premature for a feature whose Spring analogue is intentionally fixed — risks gold-plating; divergence from 'one canonical grammar' could surprise parity expectations unless the default is loud + documented.; A `dyn ArgGrammar` adds one boxed indirection + possible heap alloc on a cold path (bootstrap) — negligible but contrary to 'avoid gratuitous boxing'; the generic form avoids it but complicates the builder type.; Differing grammars change the option/non-option split → change WHICH keys reach the near-top precedence rung — a subtle provenance hazard if an app swaps grammars and `--flag value` becomes a positional. Origin/diagnostics must record which grammar produced a value.; Two grammars = two truth tables for bare-flag-empty-value and the `--`-terminator rule — more to test and keep null-never-overrides consistent across.

**Mechanisms considered:** runtime strategy via `dyn ArgGrammar` trait object selected on the app builder; generic `parse_with::<G: ArgGrammar>` monomorphized (zero-cost default, no boxing); optional integration crate supplying a richer grammar impl (auto-discovered, never a core dep); explicitly NOT a cargo feature toggle (avoids mutually-exclusive-feature footgun)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Default grammar + SPI live in the normal kernel crate; same no-link-time-hazard profile as realizations 1/2 for parsing itself. The EXTENSIBILITY adds one genuine cross-crate question: if a richer grammar lives in an optional integration crate, how is its impl made available to the bootstrap? Two candidate shapes (NOT a decision): (a) EXPLICIT — the app constructs the grammar and hands it to the builder (`App::new().arg_grammar(ClapGrammar::new())`), zero discovery, max reliability, every target (the bevy/dill explicit-composition pattern); (b) DISCOVERED — the impl registers as a descriptor in the static link-time registry (linkme distributed-slice) like any pluggable, runtime selects highest-priority — inheriting ALL the DCE/Layer-0/force-link hazards (the crate must be path-referenced or its registration silently vanishes, yielding a surprising silent FALLBACK to the default grammar with no error). Since grammar choice is load-bearing for which keys reach the top rung, (a) is the safer default and (b) would need the self-check/expected-count guard the doc mandates. The injectable handle stays origin-agnostic per charter: the source provides dyn-shaped values regardless of whether a native or a future WASM-module-supplied grammar produced them.

**T2 — execution context:** `ArgGrammar::parse` is contractually SYNCHRONOUS, non-blocking, pure (no IO/async) — runs on the bootstrap thread before the executor exists, like realizations 1/2. A `dyn ArgGrammar` call is one virtual dispatch on a cold path; no awaiting/blocking/cancellation surface. Errors propagate as the same typed `ArgParseError` up the bootstrap chain. Once parsed, the result is immutable and the source's hot-path `get()` behaves like realization 1 (lock-free immutable read, safe publication). The grammar object is consumed/dropped after the single parse (or kept inert); it never participates in the async runtime, so there is no execution-context-propagation concern beyond the one-shot bootstrap call.

### Rust clashes
- No JVM `String[] args` magically threaded through the framework: in Rust the binary owns `std::env::args()`/`args_os()`, and a `#[leaf::main]`-style macro would have to capture argv and hand it in. The rust-native move is to collect argv at the top of (generated or hand-written) main and pass it explicitly to the bootstrap — there is no ambient global argv the framework can reach. And `args_os()` yields `OsString` (potentially non-UTF-8), which Spring's all-`String` model never confronts: leaf must decide lossy-UTF8 vs OsString-preserving early (a real grammar/typing question Spring never had).
- Spring's `CommandLinePropertySource` is one of many `PropertySource<T>` subtypes unified by erased generics + runtime polymorphism. In Rust the source is just one impl/dyn conformer of the property-sources trait — fine — but the DUAL exposure (typed `ApplicationArguments` accessors AND stringly property view over the SAME parsed data) has no single erased object backing both; leaf must either share an Arc/borrow between two views or accept two representations, touching the deferred ownership/erasure keystones.
- `ApplicationArguments` as an injectable bean assumes a GC'd shared singleton freely handed to any consumer. In Rust, sharing one immutable parsed handle across many beans/runners forces an explicit ownership choice (Arc<ApplicationArguments> vs &'static vs per-consumer clone) — the §3 scope/lifetime keystone — that Spring never surfaces.
- Spring seeds the source 'very early' in `configureEnvironment()` and lets EnvironmentPostProcessors later read `--spring.config.location` etc. The phasing assumes a mutable environment progressively built across listener callbacks. leaf's async-first explicit-execution-context discipline means this all happens synchronously before any executor/await exists — fine (parsing is cheap, sync) but the 'who mutates the stack and when' choreography is a bootstrap-ordering question leaf must make explicit, not emergent.
- The precedence RUNG (rung 11) is owned by config-data's precedence POLICY, but config-data's design explicitly scoped itself to file/configtree/env:/SAJ loaders and does NOT mention the command-line source — a genuine ownership gap: this feature provides the source + its canonical NAME, config-data must add the rung to its ordering table, and the bootstrap must perform the add_first/add_before(testSource) call. None of the three currently claims the seam; Phase 2/3 must assign it or the top-of-stack source stays orphaned (the very 'silently absent' problem flagged).
- Spring's grammar treats lone `--` and `-x` as non-option args, clashing with universal POSIX/GNU expectations Rust developers carry from clap (`--` as a terminator, `-x` as a short flag). Faithfully replicating Spring's intentionally-minimal grammar risks surprising rust-native users; diverging risks parity drift. An intent-vs-ergonomics tension Spring's JVM audience never felt.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — PROVIDER→OWNER. This feature contributes ONE concrete conformer of the `PropertySource` trait that property-sources defines; it relies entirely on that neighbour's first-source-wins, never-blend, null-never-overrides, and name-as-identity invariants. The source is enumerable (key_names() over option names + the synthetic non-option key). It does NOT decide its stack position — it only supplies the named source and expects placement via add_first/add_before.
- **config-data** — POLICY DEPENDENCY + ownership gap. config-data owns the full externalized-config precedence ladder and must add the command-line source at rung 11 (above SAJ/env/system-props, below test sources) as an ordering-mutation call. CRITICAL: the early-control-keys (spring.config.location/name/additional-location, spring.profiles.active) are read by config-data and must already see the command-line values — so this source MUST be seeded before config-data runs. config-data's current scope statement omits the command-line source; this interaction is the unclaimed seam.
- **property-resolution** — DOWNSTREAM CONSUMER of values. The resolver walks the stack and may hit this source first (highest non-test rung). A bare flag returning Some("") must be treated as a present value (not absent); the synthetic nonOptionArgs key is resolvable like any other. ${...} placeholders are not specially handled here — the source returns raw winning values and the resolver does the walk.
- **relaxed-binding** — CONSUMER of the list/flat-value rule. Repeated options exposed comma-joined (--foo=a --foo=b → "a,b") compose with relaxed-binding's list-index conventions and type-conversion's comma-split→Vec. The option NAME is matched via relaxed-binding's canonical-form equivalence (so --my-opt and a my.opt/myOpt lookup reconcile through the canonical key identity, not here).
- **type-conversion** — DOWNSTREAM. The comma-joined repeated-option value and the bare-flag empty-string value are coerced at the binding/injection point (empty string → bool-ish flag, CSV → Vec<T>). This feature only guarantees the string SHAPE; coercion semantics are the neighbour's.
- **origin-tracking** — PRODUCER of a coarse origin. Every value this source returns carries a coarse Origin::CommandLine (owning-source altitude); there is NO fine file/line origin (argv has no file). This honors origin-tracking's two-altitude model (coarse-only sources explicitly allowed) and rides the never-blend short-circuit so the winning value's origin is this source's, untouched.
- **bootstrap / SpringApplication-equivalent** — HOSTED-BY + early-seed. The bootstrap captures argv, calls this feature's parser at the first pipeline step, registers ApplicationArguments as the springApplicationArguments singleton, inserts the source into the stack (at config-data's dictated rung) during environment preparation, and exposes the setAddCommandLineProperties(false) disable lever. The bootstrap also owns runner discovery/ordering.
- **runtime-lifecycle / runners (ApplicationRunner & CommandLineRunner analogues)** — INJECTION TARGET. The parsed ApplicationArguments is injected into parsed-args runners; the raw &[String] into raw-args runners. Both runner kinds are collected and @Order-sorted into one stream by the bootstrap, fired after refresh and before ready. This feature provides the injectable handle + the two consumption shapes; the runner SPI/ordering is the bootstrap's.
- **profiles** — INDIRECT via property. --spring.profiles.active=dev,prod is just a command-line option value at the top precedence rung; profiles reads it through the environment like any other property. The CLI override beating a file is the canonical demonstration of the precedence ladder. No direct coupling beyond 'CLI is a high-precedence source for the activation property'.
- **deferral-primitives / autowiring-resolution** — BEAN RESOLUTION. ApplicationArguments is resolved as an ordinary singleton bean by type at injection points (and could be wrapped by ObjectProvider). It is a leaf-provided infrastructure bean, registered eagerly by the bootstrap, immutable after publication.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Who owns the precedence-RUNG seam? config-data scoped itself to file/configtree/env:/SAJ loaders and never claims the command-line rung; this feature provides the source + canonical name but not its position; the bootstrap performs the insertion. Phase 2/3 must assign one owner for 'command-line args land at rung 11, above SAJ/env, below test sources' or this top-of-stack source stays orphaned (the silently-absent problem).
- How is the DUAL representation unified? The typed ApplicationArguments accessor surface and the stringly PropertySource view project the SAME parsed data. Single shared backing (one Arc/borrow) or two representations? A concrete instance of the §3 type-erasure/registry and scope/ownership keystones — the answer must be consistent with whatever the property-sources stack stores.
- What is the ownership/lifetime of the injectable ApplicationArguments handle shared across beans, runners, and the property source? Arc<ApplicationArguments> vs &'static (leaked-once, valid for whole program) vs per-consumer clone — directly the deferred scope/lifetime/ownership keystone. The source adapter borrowing the handle vs owning an Arc ripples into the property-sources stack's storage model.
- Eager-at-bootstrap-step-1 vs lazy/deferred parse: where on the timeline does the (only) fallible step run so a malformed arg fails 'as early as the richest diagnostic allows' (charter #9) WITHOUT failing before the diagnostics/logging infrastructure that would render it well exists? Depends on the unified error/diagnostics model (§3) and bootstrap ordering.
- Should leaf ship ONLY the Spring-simple grammar (parity, minimal) or expose a pluggable ArgGrammar SPI for POSIX/GNU/clap-style parsing? If pluggable, is the alternate grammar supplied EXPLICITLY (bevy/dill style, reliable, every target) or DISCOVERED via the link-time registry (inheriting DCE/Layer-0/force-link hazards and the surprising silent-fallback-to-default failure mode)? Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition model and the 'scope discovery, don't make it global' guidance.
- argv as String (lossy UTF-8) vs OsString-preserving: Spring's all-String model never confronts non-UTF-8 argv. Does leaf's grammar operate on OsString (correct, but complicates the stringly property view property-sources expects) or lossy-String (simple, parity, but can corrupt a non-UTF-8 positional/value)? A cross-cutting typing decision touching property-sources' value model.
- Is the runner SPI (ApplicationRunner/CommandLineRunner analogues, one @Order-sorted stream) owned by THIS feature, by runtime-lifecycle, or by the bootstrap feature? The injectable handle is clearly ours; the runner discovery+ordering is ambiguous and overlaps the bootstrap pipeline design that does not yet exist as a catalogued Phase-1 feature.

### Notes
Grounding read: charter (all 11 invariants + §3 deferred keystones), the Spring bootstrap pipeline (prepareEnvironment/configureEnvironment/callRunners, lines 238-310), the PropertySource/first-wins section (1294-1308) including the explicit CommandLinePropertySource subtype mention (line 1296), the full 15-rung externalized-config precedence ladder (1417-1443, command-line = rung 11), and the cross-crate composition reference in full. The nightly doc was checked: argument parsing is purely synchronous stable-Rust work — NO nightly feature is relevant or needed (confirms charter #8's 'core fully stable-buildable').

Key finding for downstream phases: this feature is overwhelmingly a NORMAL-RUNTIME-DATA feature (a pure parser + a thin stack adapter + an injectable immutable handle) and is almost entirely INSULATED from the cross-crate/link-time hazards that dominate discovery-style features — argv is a runtime input the binary owns, not a cross-crate contribution. The ONE place T1 hazards re-enter is the OPTIONAL pluggable-grammar SPI (realization 3), and even there the explicit-composition path avoids them entirely. The genuinely hard, unresolved issues are all OWNERSHIP/SEAM questions (who owns the precedence rung; how the dual typed/stringly view shares one backing; the lifetime of the shared handle) which are instances of the §3 keystones and correctly belong to Phase 2/3 — surfaced as phase2Questions, not resolved.

The three realizations are deliberately divergent on the WHEN/HOW-of-parsing + grammar-extensibility axis (eager-owned vs lazy-cached/scanner vs pluggable-grammar-SPI), all sharing the same downstream contract (PropertySource adapter shape + ApplicationArguments accessor surface) so Phase 3 can mix-and-match (e.g. eager parse + simple-grammar-only as the conservative default, with the lazy-diagnostic-timing trick and the grammar SPI as opt-in refinements).

No files were created or modified; this is a design-only deliverable. No Phase-1 design directory yet exists under docs/design/ (checked) — the artifact is returned structurally per the workflow.

## ConfigurationPropertySource adapter layer (the relaxed/binder-facing view of the raw stack)  `[extra-7]`

This feature is the ADAPTER SEAM that the binder (and relaxed lookup) actually consume — NOT the raw stack and NOT the relaxed-name type. Spring interposes `ConfigurationPropertySources.attach()` to wrap the raw `MutablePropertySources` (string keys, per-scalar first-source-wins) into an ordered set of `SpringConfigurationPropertySource`s keyed by `ConfigurationPropertyName`. Each adapter wraps exactly one raw source and answers three questions the raw stack cannot: (1) RELAXED-KEYED LOOKUP — `get(ConfigurationPropertyName)` over a raw source whose native keys are in some transport syntax (dotted/UPPER_SNAKE/etc.), delegating identity to relaxed-binding; (2) the `ConfigurationPropertyState` TRI-STATE — `containsDescendantOf(name)` returns PRESENT / ABSENT / UNKNOWN, where UNKNOWN is the honest answer for a NON-ENUMERABLE source (one that can answer get(k) but cannot list its keys, e.g. a JNDI/random/lazy/remote/WASM-backed source); this tri-state is the documented correctness signal that the binder and relaxed-binding both flag as cross-feature, yet it is PRODUCED here. (3) ENUMERATION — for enumerable sources, iterate all `ConfigurationPropertyName`s (and thus "all keys under a prefix"), which powers map binding, unknown-field detection, and collection discovery. The adapter is also the concrete site of the binder's COLLECTION-REPLACEMENT rule ("which single source owns the whole collection"): because each adapter is one source and the set is ordered, the binder walks the ordered adapters and the first that reports PRESENT for the collection's name owns it entirely. Spring re-attaches the adapter set after environment type conversion (attach is idempotent and keyed by a sentinel source name). The load-bearing INTENT for leaf: a per-source, relaxed-keyed, tri-state-aware, optionally-enumerable VIEW, assembled into an ordered set that mirrors the raw stack's order, that is the ONLY surface the binder/relaxed walk touches — the raw resolver is never consumed directly. SCOPE BOUNDARY: `property-sources` owns the raw ordered stack + first-source-wins + never-blend + the origin-agnostic raw `PropertySource` trait; `relaxed-binding` owns the canonical `ConfigurationPropertyName` identity + UNIFORM-form equivalence + per-transport candidate-name rules + the bracket-escape; `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` placeholder walk + read interface; `binder` owns `Bindable`/tree-descent/`BindResult`/`BindHandler` and the collection-REPLACEMENT POLICY (this feature only gives it the mechanism to enforce it); `origin-tracking` owns the `Origin` carrier (this feature must propagate it unblended through the adapter). THIS feature owns ONLY: the per-source adapter trait (relaxed `get` + tri-state `contains_descendant_of` + optional `iter`), the ENUMERABLE-vs-NON-ENUMERABLE dichotomy and the UNKNOWN-state rule that flows from it, the ordered adapter-SET that mirrors the raw stack, the attach/re-attach idempotent lifecycle, and the contract that one adapter == one raw source (so collection-ownership and origin-tracing stay traceable to a single source).

### Candidate realizations

#### Eager normalized index per source (attach-time trie/map build)
At attach() time, for every ENUMERABLE raw source, eagerly walk its keys once and build a normalized index keyed by the relaxed UNIFORM form: `struct IndexedAdapter { raw: Arc<dyn PropertySource>, index: HashMap<NameHash, (RawKey, Origin)> , prefix_trie: Trie }`. `get(name) -> Option<PropertyValue>` hashes the canonical name's UNIFORM form and hits the map (O(1)); `contains_descendant_of(prefix) -> State` walks the prefix-trie and returns PRESENT/ABSENT with certainty. NON-ENUMERABLE sources get a different adapter `OnDemandAdapter { raw, mapper }` that has NO index: `get` asks relaxed-binding to expand the canonical name into candidate raw keys and probes `raw.get` for each (first hit wins, origin attached); `contains_descendant_of` returns UNKNOWN unconditionally (it cannot prove absence). The attach surface is `ConfigurationPropertySources::attach(stack) -> AdapterSet`, returning an ordered `Vec<Box<dyn ConfigurationPropertySource>>` parallel to the raw stack order. Re-attach diffs source names and rebuilds only changed/added enumerable indices. The binder's `iter_under(prefix)` fuses each adapter's enumeration in stack order, deduping by name (first-source-wins at the name level), so 'all keys under prefix' is a merged ordered iterator; collection-ownership falls out because the FIRST adapter reporting PRESENT for the collection name is the owner.

**Pros:** Hot read path is O(1) and the prefix-descendant query is certain (PRESENT/ABSENT) for the common enumerable case (env, maps, files) — UNKNOWN is confined to genuinely non-enumerable sources, matching Spring's behavior exactly.; Enumeration ('all keys under a prefix', unknown-field detection, map binding) is free — the index already holds every name; binder map/collection descent is a trie sub-walk.; Normalization cost is paid once at startup (a cold path per charter #4), not per get; steady-state binding is allocation-light and lock-free reads.; Origin rides inline in the index value, so the never-blend short-circuit and provenance survive untouched (charter-aligned with origin-tracking).

**Cons:** Eager index duplicates every enumerable key's normalized form in memory — heap cost proportional to total config size (tension with charter #5 memory discipline; mitigated by interning raw keys / storing handles not owned strings).; Re-attach after env conversion must invalidate/rebuild indices; if a raw source mutates AFTER attach without re-attach, the index goes stale (Spring sidesteps this by attach being late and sources being effectively frozen — leaf must make the freeze/rebuild contract explicit).; Two adapter shapes (indexed vs on-demand) is a branch the binder must not see — needs a uniform trait so the dichotomy is internal.; Building a trie/map for a huge configtree directory at startup adds measurable boot latency for very large config sets.

**Mechanisms considered:** Eager proc-macro/build.rs codegen of the index — REJECTED: config values are runtime data (env/files/secrets), unknowable at compile time; only the binding TARGET schema is static (that is binder's concern, not this adapter's).; Runtime HashMap<NameHash,..> + prefix trie built at attach.; linkme/inventory link-time registry — NOT used to hold values (runtime data); only potentially to register which raw-source ADAPTER FACTORIES exist (origin-agnostic, so a WASM source factory can self-register), but value indexing is pure runtime.; Trait-object adapter set (Box<dyn ConfigurationPropertySource>) for the ordered set so heterogeneous source kinds (native/file/env/WASM) erase uniformly.

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Almost entirely an in-crate, in-process concern: the adapter wraps a raw PropertySource value that already exists at runtime in the same crate as the environment — there is NO cross-crate aggregation of config VALUES (config is runtime data, not a link-time contribution). The only T1 surface is ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC source kinds: the adapter trait must erase to `dyn ConfigurationPropertySource` so a source produced by a dynamic layer (the directory-scanned WASM config-provider from the wasm-modules exploration) plugs in identically to a native MapSource — a WASM source naturally lands in the OnDemand/non-enumerable adapter (it can answer get over the boundary but may not cheaply enumerate), so it organically yields UNKNOWN, which is correct. If leaf ever wants to register adapter FACTORIES per raw-source-kind across crates, that is the standard linkme/inventory descriptor pattern (force-link + DCE caveats from the cross-crate doc apply) — but the values themselves never cross link-time. Keep the adapter trait + ConfigurationPropertyState enum in the kernel crate (leaf-core) so both binder and any source-providing integration crate depend on one copy (workspace version unification).

**T2 — execution context:** Index build runs at attach() — a COLD startup path (charter #4 permits non-reactive work here); it is synchronous CPU work over already-in-memory raw keys and must NOT block on IO (any file/network/WASM read that populated the raw source happened earlier in config-data loading, off this seam). Steady-state get/contains/iter are synchronous, lock-free, non-blocking, cheap — they are on the binder's HOT descent path and must never await. For a non-enumerable source whose get crosses a boundary (WASM/remote), the get is fenced behind the source's own async contract: the adapter trait's get stays sync over an already-resolved snapshot, OR (if a source is genuinely async) the async resolution is hoisted into the attach/snapshot step so the binder walk stays sync. Cancellation: binding is a bounded synchronous pass with no awaits, so cancellation is a non-issue on the read path; errors (a malformed raw key that won't normalize) surface as a rich diagnostic carrying the raw key + source name + origin, raised at attach (earliest richest context, charter #9) rather than mid-bind.

#### Lazy on-demand candidate-expansion adapter (no index; query-time mapping + memoized tri-state)
No eager index for ANY source. Every adapter is `LazyAdapter { raw: Arc<dyn PropertySource>, caps: SourceCaps }` where `SourceCaps` declares whether the raw source is enumerable (a capability bit the raw source self-reports). `get(name)`: ask relaxed-binding to lazily generate the ordered candidate raw keys for this name (the env four-candidate rule, dash-removal, bracket-escape, etc.), probe `raw.get(candidate)` for each, return the first hit with origin (a `Cow`-returning, allocation-minimal walk). `contains_descendant_of(prefix)`: if the source is non-enumerable -> UNKNOWN; if enumerable -> lazily ask the raw source `iter_keys()` (which enumerable sources provide) and short-circuit on the first key whose normalized form is a descendant -> PRESENT, else ABSENT. A small per-adapter memo cache (`OnceCell`/elsa-style append-only) caches the prefix->State answers computed during a binding pass so repeated descendant probes in one bind are O(1) the second time, but nothing is precomputed. The attach surface is the same ordered `AdapterSet`, but attach is now near-FREE (just wrapping, no walk); the work moves to first query.

**Pros:** Pay-for-what-you-bind: a 50k-key configtree costs nothing until the binder asks about a prefix it actually binds — startup stays fast, memory stays flat (strong charter #5 alignment; no duplicated normalized strings).; Re-attach is trivial and stale-proof: the adapter holds no snapshot, it reads through to the live raw source every time, so post-env-conversion re-attach is just re-wrapping (no index invalidation problem).; The candidate-expansion direction (canonical -> raw candidates) is exactly relaxed-binding's documented model (SystemEnvironmentPropertyMapper produces N candidates), so the adapter is a thin, faithful consumer rather than a reinvented index.; Non-enumerable sources are handled with zero special-casing — they simply lack the iter capability and return UNKNOWN; a WASM/remote source slots in with no extra code.

**Cons:** Enumeration ('all keys under prefix' for map binding / unknown-field detection) re-walks the raw source's keys per query unless memoized — repeated map binds or a big handler chain can re-scan; the memo cache reintroduces some of the memory the eager design tried to avoid.; contains_descendant_of for an enumerable source is O(keys) per uncached prefix (worst case), versus O(prefix-depth) with a trie — pushes cost onto the hot binder descent if the memo misses.; The lazy memo cache is per-binding-pass mutable state; making it lock-free/append-only (so it honors charter #5 no-global-locks) adds complexity, and cache invalidation across binds is a live question if the raw source can change.; More small allocations on the candidate-expansion path (one Vec/iterator of candidate names per get) unless carefully written as a lazy iterator + Cow.

**Mechanisms considered:** Pure runtime lazy mapper closures (source-side mappers that expand a canonical query into candidate concrete keys) — the relaxed-binding doc's 'source-side mappers' option.; OnceCell / elsa append-only memo for tri-state results (no RwLock; charter #5).; SourceCaps capability bit reported by the raw PropertySource trait (origin-agnostic: native/file/env set enumerable=true, WASM/remote/random set enumerable=false).; NO codegen, NO link-time anything — purely runtime, since the mapping is over runtime config keys.; Cow<str> + lazy candidate iterator to keep the get path allocation-light.

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same in-process character as realization A — config values are runtime data, no cross-crate value aggregation. The notable T1 win: because the adapter holds NO snapshot and reads through the raw source's reported `SourceCaps`, a dynamically-loaded source (WASM directory-scanned provider) added at runtime is handled with no rebuild — it just appears in the AdapterSet wrapping the new raw source, declares enumerable=false, and correctly yields UNKNOWN. The SourceCaps bit and the adapter trait live in leaf-core so any source-providing crate (native or a leaf-wasm integration crate) implements one shared contract. No linkme/inventory needed for values; if adapter-factory registration per source-kind is ever wanted it is the standard descriptor-in-distributed-slice pattern with the documented DCE/force-link caveats — but this realization deliberately keeps even that out by making the raw source self-describe its caps rather than registering a kind.

**T2 — execution context:** Attach is a trivial sync wrap (cold path, no work). All get/contains/iter are sync on the binder's hot descent. The memo writes happen inside the synchronous bind pass; with an append-only OnceCell-style structure there is no lock contention and no await, satisfying charter #4/#5. The genuinely async risk is a non-enumerable source whose get crosses an async boundary (WASM/remote): this realization must NOT make the adapter trait async (that would poison the whole binder descent into async and fight charter #2's no-bimodality at the wrong layer). Instead the contract is: a source that needs async to answer get must be resolved into a sync-readable snapshot during config-data loading / attach (the async is fenced there), so the steady-state adapter walk stays sync. Cancellation: none needed on the sync read path. Errors: a candidate that fails to map, or a source whose iter errors, produces a rich diagnostic naming the source + the canonical name + the attempted candidates (charter #9); raised lazily at the failing query, which still has full context because the canonical name and source identity are both in hand.

#### Pull-based cursor / Deserializer-shaped adapter the binder drives (no map, no candidate fan-out at this layer)
Invert control: rather than the adapter answering point queries, the adapter exposes a STREAMING CURSOR shaped like serde's pull model. `trait ConfigurationPropertySource { fn cursor(&self, prefix: &Name) -> Box<dyn PropertyCursor>; fn state(&self, prefix: &Name) -> ConfigurationPropertyState; }` where a `PropertyCursor` yields `(relative_segment, Entry)` events — Scalar(value, origin) | EnterMap | EnterSeq | Leaf — so the binder walks the cursor the same way serde walks a Deserializer, descending one prefix segment per nesting level. The adapter set is an ordered chain of cursors; the binder asks each in stack order and the FIRST cursor that produces entries under the prefix owns that subtree (collection-replacement falls out structurally — one cursor == one source == one owner of the whole collection). Relaxed identity is applied at the cursor's segment-emission point (each emitted segment is normalized to UNIFORM form). Non-enumerable sources expose a degenerate cursor that can only answer 'does a leaf at this exact name exist' (point-get) and report `state = UNKNOWN` for any descendant query; the binder then knows it may only bind scalars it can name explicitly from that source, never enumerate it. attach() builds the ordered cursor-factory set.

**Pros:** Maximal machinery-sharing (charter #11): the binder's tree-descent becomes a serde-Deserializer-shaped pull, so the adapter, the binder's descent, and potentially type-conversion all speak one streaming vocabulary — and a serde bridge to bind into arbitrary Deserialize targets becomes natural.; Collection-replacement and 'one source owns the whole collection' are STRUCTURAL, not a separate rule: a cursor delivers a whole subtree from one source; the binder never has to reconcile fragments across sources.; Enumeration vs point-get is expressed as cursor capability (a full cursor vs a degenerate point-only cursor), so the enumerable/non-enumerable dichotomy and the UNKNOWN state are first-class in the cursor's shape rather than a flag.; Streaming means the binder pulls only the subtree it is binding — good locality, no need to materialize 'all keys under prefix' as a collection.

**Cons:** Biggest conceptual distance from Spring's get(name)+containsDescendantOf(name) model — risks over-engineering the seam and complicating the relaxed-lookup path (which genuinely wants a point get(name), not a cursor) — relaxed-binding's placeholder lookup would need an awkward single-element cursor.; A pull cursor over a flat key/value source (env, properties) has to SYNTHESIZE the tree structure (group flat dotted keys into EnterMap/EnterSeq events) — that grouping is non-trivial and partly re-implements what a trie would give for free, possibly per-query.; First-source-wins at the NAME level across cursors is harder to express than in a keyed model: if source 1 owns `app.list` and source 2 has `app.scalar`, the binder must merge cursors at the object level while respecting per-collection single-ownership — more bookkeeping than 'probe adapters in order for a name'.; Statefulness of cursors (position, backtracking when the binder explores then abandons a branch) adds lifetime/borrow complexity in Rust; a Box<dyn Cursor> per descent is allocation per subtree.

**Mechanisms considered:** serde-Deserializer-shaped pull bridge (the binder design's flagged 'serde-Deserializer-shaped pull bridge' option) realized at the ADAPTER layer rather than the target layer.; Runtime cursor trait objects (Box<dyn PropertyCursor>) — heterogeneous source kinds erase uniformly; origin-agnostic so WASM/remote sources implement the degenerate point-cursor.; ConfigurationPropertyState as the cursor's self-reported capability (full vs degenerate) rather than a precomputed value.; Explicitly NOT codegen/link-time — the tree shape of CONFIG is runtime; only the TARGET tree shape is static and that belongs to binder, not here.

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** In-process like the others; values never cross link-time. The cursor trait being origin-agnostic is the key T1 property: a WASM directory-scanned config source implements the degenerate point-cursor + UNKNOWN state and slots into the ordered cursor set with zero binder awareness — WASM-ness stops at the cursor, exactly as the wasm-modules exploration says WASM-ness stops at the dyn-Trait proxy. Because a cursor can stream from a source that is itself backed by an async/boundary-crossing producer, the cursor abstraction is the natural place a future dynamic layer plugs in — but see T2 for the async fencing. The PropertyCursor + ConfigurationPropertySource + ConfigurationPropertyState types live in leaf-core (one shared copy, workspace-unified) so binder and any source crate agree. No distributed-slice needed for values; only an optional adapter-factory registry per source-kind would touch linkme/inventory with the usual DCE caveats.

**T2 — execution context:** Cursor pull happens on the binder's hot synchronous descent — so the cursor's next() must be sync and non-blocking. This is the realization most TEMPTED to go async (a cursor streaming from a remote/WASM source 'wants' to be a Stream), and that temptation is the main hazard: making PropertyCursor async would force the binder's entire tree-descent to be async and would smear awaits across the hot path (violates charter #4 reactive-hot-path and the no-bimodality intent). The discipline: the cursor is sync over a snapshot; any async/boundary-crossing producer is drained into a sync-readable buffer during attach/config-data (cold path) so the steady-state pull is sync. Cancellation is a non-issue on a sync bounded pull. Errors: a cursor that hits a malformed subtree yields an Err event carrying the source name + the path walked so far + origin (rich, charter #9), surfaced at the point of pull where the binder still has the full target-path context to render 'failed binding app.servers[2].port from <source> at <origin>'.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's `ConfigurationPropertyState.UNKNOWN` exists because the JVM has enumerable vs non-enumerable PropertySources and reflection-free enumeration is impossible for some (JNDI, system props proxies). In Rust the dichotomy is real too but SHARPER: a Rust raw source is enumerable iff it can implement an `iter_keys()`-style method — there is no runtime reflection to fall back on, so non-enumerability is a static capability fact, not a runtime surprise. Risk: tempting to think we can always enumerate (we control the sources), collapsing UNKNOWN away — but a dynamic/WASM/remote source genuinely cannot, so the tri-state MUST survive and be modeled as a real capability, not an afterthought.
- Spring's attach()/re-attach() relies on the GC'd, mutable `MutablePropertySources` being live-readable and the adapter holding a back-reference that always sees current sources. In Rust, an adapter that snapshots an index (realization A) can go stale vs the live stack; an adapter that reads through (B/C) needs the raw source to be cheaply re-readable. The mutation/freeze contract (when is the stack frozen relative to attach?) is implicit in Spring and must be made EXPLICIT in leaf — ownership/borrow rules force the question Spring never had to answer.
- Spring keys the adapter by `ConfigurationPropertyName` (a heap object with three precomputed string Forms). Idiomatic Rust resists eagerly materializing three owned strings per name (charter #5); the relaxed-binding neighbour already flagged 'not necessarily three eager strings'. The adapter must key on a cheap normalized HANDLE/hash, not a fat name object — but then equality/diagnostics need the original raw key recoverable, a tension between read-path cheapness and rich error context (charter #9).
- Spring's binder freely treats the adapter as a synchronous, infinitely-re-queryable map. leaf is async-first, and some origin-agnostic sources (WASM/remote) are async producers. The clash: the binder's tree-descent is a hot synchronous path that must NOT become async (charter #4), yet a source may need async to produce values. This forces an explicit FENCE — async resolution must be hoisted to a cold attach/config-data step into a sync-readable snapshot — that Spring never needed because the JVM just blocks the calling thread.
- Spring's 'attach a sentinel-named adapter source into the same MutablePropertySources so it is idempotent' trick re-uses the very stack it adapts as its own storage. In Rust this self-referential mutation is awkward (a source that wraps the stack, stored in the stack); leaf likely wants the AdapterSet as a SEPARATE ordered structure derived from the stack, not injected back into it — a cleaner ownership story but a divergence from Spring's mechanism that must be deliberate.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — CONSUMES (downstream of). This adapter wraps each raw `PropertySource` from property-sources' ordered first-source-wins stack; the adapter set mirrors stack ORDER so per-name first-source-wins is preserved at the adapter level.
