The never-blend + null-never-overrides invariants are inherited untouched — an adapter that reports ABSENT/falls through must not synthesize a value. property-sources owns the origin-agnostic raw source trait + the SourceCaps/enumerability capability the adapter reads; this feature must NOT re-decide ordering or blending.
- **relaxed-binding** — DELEGATES key-identity to. The adapter's relaxed `get(ConfigurationPropertyName)` and segment-normalization use relaxed-binding's UNIFORM-form equivalence + per-transport candidate-name rules (env four-candidate, dash-removal, bracket-escape, list/map index conventions). The adapter is the CONSUMER that applies those rules against a concrete raw source; relaxed-binding owns the rules, this feature owns the per-source application. The asymmetric-placeholder gotcha is honored because lookups always start from the canonical form at this seam.
- **binder** — IS-CONSUMED-BY (the binder's sole config surface). The binder walks the ordered adapter set, never the raw resolver. This feature PRODUCES the mechanism for the binder's collection-REPLACEMENT policy (first adapter reporting PRESENT for a collection name owns it) and the 'enumerate all keys under a prefix' query for map binding / unknown-field detection. The ConfigurationPropertyState tri-state directly gates the binder's descent (PRESENT->descend, ABSENT->skip, UNKNOWN->may only point-get named scalars, never enumerate). The binder owns the POLICY (what to do per state); this feature owns the SIGNAL.
- **property-resolution** — SIBLING / shares the relaxed lookup. property-resolution's `${...}` placeholder walk needs a relaxed point `get(canonical)` over the stack; this adapter's `get(name)` is a candidate surface for that lookup too (so placeholder resolution and binder resolution share one relaxed-lookup mechanism — charter #11 unification candidate). Open question whether the resolver consumes the adapter or a thinner relaxed-get primitive.
- **origin-tracking** — PROPAGATES. Every value the adapter returns carries its raw source's Origin unblended through the relaxed mapping (the relaxed normalization changes the KEY form, never the origin). The adapter must ensure the WINNING source's origin reaches the binder so binding/validation failures render 'property X from <source> at <file:line>'. One-adapter-per-source keeps origin traceable to a single source.
- **config-data** — ORDERED-AFTER (lifecycle). config-data loads/assembles the raw stack (files, configtree, env:, imports) and fixes precedence; the adapter attaches AFTER that assembly and RE-ATTACHES after environment type conversion (Spring's order). config-data also produces fine origins the adapter propagates. The async file/network IO config-data performs is fenced off BEFORE the synchronous adapter walk exists (the attach/snapshot boundary).
- **environment** — ATTACHED-VIA. The environment façade owns reachability and the mutate seam; attach()/re-attach() of the adapter set is an environment-bootstrap-phase operation (Spring runs it inside prepareEnvironment). The adapter set is the binder-facing projection of the environment's stack; environment owns WHO may attach/mutate, this feature owns the projection's shape.
- **config-properties** — INDIRECT-CONSUMER (via binder). @ConfigurationProperties drives the binder which drives this adapter; the leniency flags (ignoreUnknownFields) rely on this feature's ENUMERATION to detect stray keys — and crucially, unknown-field detection is only sound for ENUMERABLE sources (a non-enumerable/UNKNOWN source cannot report stray keys), a correctness subtlety this feature must surface to config-properties' policy.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Should leaf even have a distinct adapter layer, or does it COLLAPSE into binder + a relaxed-get primitive on property-sources? Spring needed the adapter because its raw PropertySource is string-keyed and its binder wanted a separate keyed view; if leaf's raw source trait can natively expose a relaxed get + enumerability + tri-state, the 'adapter' may be a thin trait the raw source implements directly rather than a wrapping object — a unification (charter #11) vs a clean-seam (charter altitude) tension Phase 2 must weigh.
- Where does the async FENCE live? Every realization concludes the steady-state adapter walk must be SYNC while some origin-agnostic sources (WASM/remote) are async producers. Is the canonical fence (a) config-data drains everything into a sync snapshot before attach, (b) the adapter holds a pre-resolved snapshot per source, or (c) a hybrid where non-enumerable async sources are point-resolved lazily but behind a sync-blocking-is-forbidden contract? This is the async-execution-model meta-decision (§3) hitting the config layer concretely.
- Is the relaxed-lookup mechanism shared between property-resolution's placeholder get and the binder's adapter get a SINGLE primitive (charter #11), or two? If single, does that primitive live on this adapter, on relaxed-binding, or on a new shared 'relaxed point-get over the ordered stack' kernel type? This decides whether the adapter is the home of ALL relaxed reads or just the binder's.
- Eager-index vs lazy vs cursor is a direct instance of the deferred 'compile-time vs runtime resolution' and memory/overhead axes — but for RUNTIME DATA (config values), so codegen is off the table; the real axis is startup-cost vs steady-state-cost vs memory, and whether the binder's descent shape (point-query vs pull-cursor) is unified with serde and with type-conversion. Phase 2's binder/serde-bridge decision should pick this jointly, not in isolation.
- What is the freeze/mutation contract for the raw stack relative to attach? Spring leans on live mutable sources + back-references; leaf's ownership model forces an explicit answer (snapshot-and-rebuild-on-reattach vs read-through-live). This couples to the scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (§3) — is the environment's stack effectively immutable after bootstrap, making a snapshotting adapter safe?
- Should the enumerability/UNKNOWN capability be a property of the RAW source (reported by property-sources) or DERIVED at the adapter? If the WASM/dynamic-source layer is to slot in origin-agnostically, the capability bit likely belongs on the raw source trait — but that pushes a binder-facing concern (enumerability) down into property-sources, a layering question for Phase 2/3.

### Notes
Grounding read: spring doc lines 256-262 (attach/re-attach in prepareEnvironment), 1525-1549 (origin-tracking + relaxed-binding internal model: ConfigurationPropertyName Forms + UNIFORM matching + env four-candidate rule), 1595-1614 (Binder over ConfigurationPropertySources + collection-replacement). The Spring source ref for ConfigurationPropertyName Form enum is cited at doc line 2891. Note: the prompt's framing ('attach/SpringConfigurationPropertySource/ConfigurationPropertyState PRESENT/ABSENT/UNKNOWN') is corroborated by the doc's relaxed-binding internal-model section and the prepareEnvironment ordering, though the doc does not name ConfigurationPropertyState explicitly — the tri-state is inferred from Spring's well-known containsDescendantOf contract and is consistent with the doc's enumerable/non-enumerable distinction. Capability envelope: this feature needs NO nightly (rust-nightly doc: Any+downcast, trait upcasting, RPITIT all stable; the adapter is plain runtime trait objects). Cross-crate doc: config VALUES are runtime data so the linkme/inventory DCE hazards do NOT apply to the values — they apply ONLY to an optional adapter-FACTORY-per-source-kind registry, which all three realizations treat as out-of-scope-here. WASM exploration (wasm-modules-for-leaf.md lines 55-59,77-78) directly supports the origin-agnostic stance: a directory-scanned WASM config source is a non-enumerable source that yields UNKNOWN and slots in behind the dyn adapter exactly as 'WASM-ness stops at the proxy'. No phase1 neighbour files exist on disk yet; neighbour intents were taken from the EXISTING DESIGNS array in the prompt. All three realizations converge on one hard requirement (the sync read-path fence for async sources) — flagged as the top phase2 question. Did NOT pick a winner per the implementation-agnostic guardrail.

## RandomValuePropertySource (random.*) — a non-enumerable computed source with its own grammar  `[extra-8]`

Spring's `RandomValuePropertySource` (docs §"RandomValuePropertySource and SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON", lines 1509-1518, plus precedence line 1422) is a SPECIAL, COMPUTED property source that answers ONLY the `random.*` namespace and produces a FRESH value on every read. It is the canonical concrete instance of the R3 "non-enumerable / on-demand" source the upstream `property-sources` design names abstractly. The load-bearing intent leaf must replicate (intent, NOT the JVM mechanism):

(1) A MINI-GRAMMAR over the key SUFFIX after `random.`: `value` → a random hex string (Spring derives it from random bytes); `int` → a random i32 over the full positive range; `long` → a random i64; `uuid` → a random UUID v4 string; `int(max)` → a non-negative int in [0, max) (max EXCLUSIVE); `int[min,max]` → an int in [min, max) (min inclusive, max EXCLUSIVE); the `(..)`/`[..]` range syntax also applies to `long`. The delimiters are `OPEN value(,max) CLOSE` — both `(N)` (bound) and `[M,N]` (range) forms, the comma separating min,max. There is NO file:line origin — only a COARSE source origin (charter via origin-tracking: random.* is explicitly listed as a coarse-only source).

(2) COMPUTE-PER-READ / NEVER-BLEND-FRESH semantics. Unlike a Map source (same value every read), this source RUNS A COMPUTATION per lookup; two reads of `${random.int}` yield two different ints. This stresses the never-blend invariant in the opposite direction: the source is honest that it has no stored value, so caching is semantically WRONG.

(3) PLACEHOLDER-ONLY ACCESS. It is consulted ONLY via the `${...}` placeholder walk (the `property-resolution` neighbour). It is NEVER bound directly by the binder/config-properties (you do not write `@ConfigurationProperties` over `random.*`), and it is NON-ENUMERABLE — it cannot list its keys (the suffix space is infinite), so it never participates in `property-names()`/iteration, env-dumps, or relaxed-binding's enumerate-and-match path. `contains_property("random.int")` must answer true WITHOUT computing/consuming a value.

(4) A FIXED PRECEDENCE RUNG. It sits at exactly one place: just ABOVE Config Data files and just BELOW OS env vars (precedence rung 4 of 15). `config-data` owns the act of PLACING it there (an ordering-mutation call on the stack); THIS feature owns only the rung's IDENTITY (named `random`) and the rule that it occupies one fixed rung.

SCOPE BOUNDARY: `property-sources` owns the `PropertySource` trait shape, the enumerable-vs-on-demand dichotomy, first-source-wins, never-blend, and name-as-identity; `property-resolution` owns the `${...}` walk that consults this source; `origin-tracking` owns the `Origin` type (this feature only ATTACHES the coarse origin); `config-data` owns WHERE the rung lands in the global precedence order; `relaxed-binding` owns canonicalization (and this source is exempt from enumerate-side relaxed matching); `environment` owns the façade. THIS feature owns ONLY: the `random.*` mini-grammar (parser + the int/long/value/uuid/`(max)`/`[min,max]` forms with max-exclusive semantics), the compute-per-read on-demand source implementation, the placeholder-only + non-enumerable contract, the coarse-origin attachment, the RNG execution-context discipline (where entropy comes from, that it never blocks the resolution path), and the rung's named identity. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: HOW the on-demand computed source is represented (a trait method returning a freshly-computed value vs a closure-backed dynamic source vs a registry of named generator fns), HOW the mini-grammar is parsed (eager char-scan vs a small nom-style parser vs a match on a pre-split suffix), and WHERE the RNG handle lives so the hot read path stays non-blocking and the source stays origin-agnostic (so a WASM/remote computed source could slot into the same on-demand seam later).

### Candidate realizations

#### On-demand source trait variant (the R3 second arm made concrete)
Make `random.*` the canonical implementor of the `property-sources` R3 dichotomy's SECOND arm. `property-sources` defines its source trait with two response modes; the enumerable arm has `property_names()` + `get(key)` returning a STORED `PropertyValue`, while the on-demand arm has only `get(key)` and reports `is_enumerable() -> false`. The trait method is intent-neutral: `fn get(&self, key: &ConfigPropertyName) -> Option<PropertyValue>` — for a Map it reads a slot, for `random` it COMPUTES. RandomValueSource is a unit-ish struct holding only an RNG handle; its `get` first checks the key starts with the `random.` prefix (else `None`, falling through per null-never-overrides), parses the suffix via a small hand-written scanner into a `RandomSpec` enum (`Value | Int | Long | Uuid | IntBounded(u64) | IntRange(i64,i64) | LongBounded | LongRange`), evaluates it against the RNG, and wraps the freshly-rendered string in a `PropertyValue { raw, origin: Origin::source("random") }` (coarse only — no file:line). `contains` returns `parse(suffix).is_ok()` WITHOUT drawing from the RNG. `property_names()` returns an empty iterator (non-enumerable), so env-dump/relaxed enumerate-side skip it entirely. The parser is a normal pub fn in the kernel crate (thin-macros invariant: nothing macro-only here — there is no macro at all; this is plain construction code the bootstrap calls). RNG: hold a `std::hash`-free dedicated generator — leaf depends on a small stable RNG crate (`rand`/`fastrand`) OR seeds a SplitMix64/PCG from `getrandom`/`RandomState` at source construction; the source owns its generator behind the minimal synchronization the chosen RNG needs (a per-read draw is cheap). Placeholder-only is enforced structurally: the binder/config-properties tree-descent walks `property_names()` (enumerable sources only) so a non-enumerable source is INVISIBLE to binding; only the `property-resolution` `${...}` walk calls `get` on every source including this one.

**Pros:** Most faithful to the upstream `property-sources` R3 intent: random.* becomes the *worked example* that proves the on-demand arm of the dichotomy, so the abstraction earns its keep instead of being hypothetical.; ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC by construction — the on-demand `get` returns `dyn`-able `PropertyValue` and assumes nothing about HOW it was computed, so a future WASM-module or remote-secrets computed source (`vault.*`) slots into the identical trait arm with zero new machinery.; Non-enumerable + placeholder-only fall out of the trait shape (`is_enumerable()->false`, empty `property_names()`) rather than needing a special-case guard at every call site — the binder simply never sees it.; Compute-per-read is the source's natural behaviour (each `get` runs the closure), so never-blend-fresh needs no caching-suppression flag; caching is structurally impossible.; Thin/no macro: the whole feature is hand-writable kernel code (parser fn + source struct), maximally testable and `cargo expand`-irrelevant.

**Cons:** Pushes a (small) shape decision back onto `property-sources` (it must commit to a two-arm trait or an `is_enumerable` discriminator) — a cross-feature coupling that Phase 2/3 must ratify.; Every `get` allocates a fresh `String` for the rendered value (hex/uuid) — minor heap churn on the read path; acceptable since placeholders are resolved at config-bind time, a cold path, not a steady-state hot path.; RNG state lives behind interior mutability (the generator must mutate to advance); needs a justified, fine-grained lock or a `Cell`/atomic-PCG to honour the no-global-locks invariant — a real but bounded concurrency-design point.; The `(max)`/`[min,max]` grammar lives in this source's parser; if a second computed source ever wants a similar bounded grammar it is not yet shared (acceptable — premature unification).

**Mechanisms considered:** runtime registry (the property-sources stack holds this as one `dyn Source` among many); dyn dispatch (the on-demand source is a `dyn` trait object so WASM/remote variants are interchangeable); hand-written recursive-descent / char-scan parser for the mini-grammar (no proc-macro, no codegen — grammar is fixed and tiny)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Zero cross-crate discovery concern in the common case: `random` is a CORE built-in source the bootstrap (`config-data`/`leaf-boot`) constructs and `add_*`-places at its fixed rung — it is NOT a user contribution, so no linkme/inventory/DCE hazard applies to it. The only cross-crate surface is the SHAPE of the on-demand trait arm living in the kernel crate (`leaf-core`) so that an optional dynamic computed source (a WASM module exporting a `compute(key)->value` world, per the wasm-modules exploration) can implement the SAME arm from a sibling crate. That dynamic case DOES inherit the link-time-registration / directory-scan duality of the discovery story (static built-in `random` always present; an optional directory-scanned WASM computed-source layer additive on top), but `random` itself is on the static, always-linked side and needs no registration at all.

**T2 — execution context:** The `get` computation runs SYNCHRONOUSLY on whatever execution context the placeholder walk runs in (config resolution — a COLD startup/bind path, charter §4-compliant: no hot-path polling). It must NEVER block: entropy is drawn from a generator SEEDED ONCE at source construction (the one place a `getrandom`-style syscall may occur, fenced to bootstrap), and per-read draws are pure arithmetic (PCG/SplitMix64) — no syscall, no `.await`, no lock contention on the resolution path. There is no cancellation surface (synchronous, instantaneous). Errors are confined to GRAMMAR errors (`random.int[5,2]` reversed range, `random.int(abc)` non-numeric) surfaced as a rich diagnostic up the `property-resolution` result chain naming the offending placeholder + the source `random` (charter §9); an RNG draw itself cannot fail.

#### Closure-backed dynamic computed-source (generator registry keyed by suffix verb)
Generalize the computed source into a tiny REGISTRY of named generator functions, of which `random` is the first (and only built-in) instance. A `ComputedSource { prefix: &'static str, generators: Map<Verb, GeneratorFn> }` where `GeneratorFn = fn(args: &RandomArgs, rng: &mut dyn RngCore) -> Result<String, GrammarError>`. The verbs `value/int/long/uuid` register their closures; the `(max)`/`[min,max]` argument shape is parsed by a shared `parse_args(suffix) -> (Verb, RandomArgs)` step before dispatch. `get(key)` strips the `random.` prefix, splits verb-vs-args, looks up the verb, and invokes its closure with a freshly-borrowed RNG; unknown verb → `None` (fall-through, never an error — preserves null-never-overrides). The source is constructed programmatically (`ComputedSource::random()` returns the preconfigured instance) and the generator map is the explicit escape hatch (charter §10): a user/integration can register an extra verb (`random.bytes`, `random.choice[...]`) on a custom computed source WITHOUT touching the kernel. This leans on a RUNTIME registry (the generator map) rather than the trait-arm shape — the source is enumerable-by-verb-not-by-value, still reporting `is_enumerable()->false` to the stack.

**Pros:** Extensible by data, not by new types: adding a verb is registering a closure, so the mini-grammar is open for ecosystem growth (the WASM/remote case becomes 'register a generator that calls out') while the kernel ships only `random`.; Keeps the on-demand `get` shape identical to realization A from the stack's perspective (non-enumerable, compute-per-read) — so it composes with whatever R3 trait `property-sources` settles on; the difference is purely INTERNAL dispatch (a map lookup vs a match).; The `RngCore`-by-`&mut dyn` seam decouples value computation from entropy source, so tests can inject a deterministic RNG (reproducible `${random.*}` in test fixtures) — a real DX win for testing config that uses random defaults.; Generator closures localize each verb's logic + its grammar-arg expectations, making per-verb diagnostics precise ('int expects an integer bound, got `abc`').

**Cons:** A registry of closures is heavier than a fixed `match` for a grammar that Spring froze years ago — risks over-engineering a closed, tiny grammar (YAGNI vs the four-verb reality); the extensibility may never be used.; Closures + a `Map` mean heap + indirection on construction and a dynamic dispatch per read; marginally worse than realization A's static parser, and the boxed-closure RNG `&mut dyn` adds a vtable hop per draw.; Opening the verb set invites users to put SIDE-EFFECTING or BLOCKING generators behind the placeholder seam (a generator that hits the network), violating the non-blocking-resolution discipline — the open registry must be policed (generators MUST be pure+non-blocking, enforced only by contract/docs, a weak guard).; Two ways to extend (new verb vs new whole source) creates a 'which do I use' DX ambiguity the simpler realizations avoid.

**Mechanisms considered:** runtime registry (a map of verb→generator-fn, the literal registry pattern); dyn dispatch (`&mut dyn RngCore` for entropy injection; `ComputedSource` as a `dyn Source`); closures as first-class generators (each verb is an `fn`/`Fn` value); hand-written arg-parser shared across verbs (`parse_args`), no codegen

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The generator-map is process-local runtime state populated by explicit programmatic registration at bootstrap — it does NOT use link-time collection, so it sidesteps the linkme/inventory DCE hazard entirely (the map is built by code the binary demonstrably runs). If leaf ever wanted ecosystem crates to contribute verbs cross-crate, THEN the map would need a link-time/inventory feed and would inherit the full DCE + 'crate must actually be linked' (`use crate as _`) hazard set + the static-registry-plus-optional-WASM-directory duality — but that is an explicit opt-in, not the default; the built-in `random` verbs are registered inline in the kernel and always present. The `GeneratorFn` ABI (a `fn` pointer + `RandomArgs`) is deliberately `const`-friendly and minimal so it COULD migrate to a linkme distributed-slice later without changing call sites.

**T2 — execution context:** Same cold-path, synchronous, must-never-block discipline as A: generators run inline on the placeholder-resolution context. The `&mut dyn RngCore` is borrowed per-read from an RNG the source owns (seeded once at construction — the only entropy syscall, fenced to bootstrap). The open-verb risk forces an EXPLICIT contract: a registered generator MUST be pure and non-blocking and MUST NOT `.await` or perform IO (the seam is synchronous `fn`, which structurally forbids `.await` but cannot forbid a blocking syscall — documented as a hard rule, charter §3). Cancellation: none (synchronous). Errors propagate as `Result<String, GrammarError>` from the generator, folded into the `property-resolution` diagnostic chain naming the placeholder and source; concurrency on the shared RNG handled by the same fine-grained-interior-mutability choice as A (no global lock).

#### Grammar-as-typed-key: parse-once into a RandomSpec, source is a pure evaluator
Split the feature cleanly into (1) a PARSER that turns a `random.*` placeholder key into a typed `RandomSpec` value-object and (2) a trivial SOURCE that is a pure evaluator of a `RandomSpec`. The placeholder engine (`property-resolution`), when it encounters a key beginning `random.`, hands the suffix to `RandomSpec::parse(suffix) -> Result<RandomSpec, GrammarError>` (a small recursive-descent/peg over `value | int | long | uuid | int '(' u64 ')' | int '[' i64 ',' i64 ']'`, with `[min,max)` max-exclusive enforced and `min<max` validated at parse). The source's `get(key)` simply does `RandomSpec::parse(strip_prefix(key)?).ok().map(|spec| spec.eval(&self.rng))`. `RandomSpec` is the OWNED, testable, origin-agnostic representation: the grammar is decoupled from both the source plumbing AND the RNG, so the parser is unit-tested in isolation, the evaluator is unit-tested with a seeded RNG, and `config-metadata`/diagnostics can describe the accepted forms by introspecting the `RandomSpec` variants. `eval` renders to a `String`; the source wraps it with `Origin::coarse("random")`. Non-enumerable + placeholder-only + fixed-rung identical to A. The distinctive move is making the GRAMMAR a first-class value type rather than buried inside `get`, which is the closest analogue to how `profiles` made its expression a parsed AST and `property-resolution` may parse placeholders to an AST — maximizing shared 'parse-to-typed-spec-then-evaluate' machinery across the config features (charter §11 unification candidate).

**Pros:** Cleanest separation of concerns: grammar (pure, total, testable) vs evaluation (RNG-dependent) vs source plumbing (stack integration) — three independently testable units, the strongest DX/diagnostics story (precise parse errors with the exact offending span).; The `RandomSpec` value-object is the natural place to attach a rich diagnostic and even a `config-metadata` hint ('random.* accepts: value, int, long, uuid, int(max), int[min,max]'), making the mini-grammar a discoverable, self-documenting surface rather than an opaque string convention.; Mirrors `profiles`' parse-to-AST and `property-resolution`'s placeholder-parse shape, so Phase 2/3 can unify on ONE 'tiny config sub-grammar → typed spec → evaluate' primitive across all three instead of three bespoke scanners (the unification the charter wants).; Parser is a pure `fn` with no RNG/IO/async — trivially `const`-evaluable-adjacent and fuzz-testable; evaluation with a seeded RNG gives reproducible tests.; Origin-agnostic + non-enumerable + placeholder-only inherited from the same source-arm as A; the parser/eval split adds zero coupling to the stack.

**Cons:** Parsing on EVERY `get` re-parses the same placeholder key each read (compute-per-read means no parse caching either) — wasteful versus realization A if the same `${random.int[..]}` is resolved repeatedly; mitigated because placeholder resolution is a cold bind-time path and the grammar is tiny, but it is real redundant work.; Risks the placeholder engine needing to KNOW about `random.` to pre-route (if parse is hoisted into the resolver) — a coupling that muddies the scope boundary (`property-resolution` should treat all sources uniformly via `get`, not special-case `random`); keeping parse inside the source's `get` avoids this but then the 'engine hands suffix to parser' framing weakens.; A standalone `RandomSpec` type is more API surface (a pub enum + parse + eval + error) than realizations A/B for a four-verb grammar — only pays off if the parse-to-spec primitive is genuinely shared in Phase 3.; Pushes a unification BET (shared sub-grammar primitive) that is properly a Phase 2 decision — Phase 1 must present it as a candidate, not assume it.

**Mechanisms considered:** hand-written recursive-descent / PEG parser producing a typed `RandomSpec` (no proc-macro, grammar fixed); value-object / typed-key representation (the spec is data, evaluated separately); dyn dispatch at the source seam (so the evaluator-source is interchangeable with other on-demand sources); seeded-RNG injection for deterministic tests (same as B)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Identical to A on the discovery axis: `random` is a built-in, always-linked core source — no link-time registration, no DCE concern. The `RandomSpec` type + parser live in the kernel crate (`leaf-core`) as ordinary pub items; if the parse-to-typed-spec primitive is unified in Phase 3 it would be a shared kernel utility consumed by `profiles`/`property-resolution`/this feature alike (one crate, no cross-crate magic). No proc-macro is involved, so the single-invocation/absolute-path proc-macro hazards do not apply. A future dynamic computed source still slots in at the SAME on-demand source arm (origin-agnostic), independent of whether it reuses `RandomSpec` or carries its own spec.

**T2 — execution context:** Cold-path, synchronous, non-blocking — same envelope as A and B. Parse runs inline (pure, total, no IO); eval draws from the source-owned, once-seeded RNG (the lone entropy syscall fenced to construction). No `.await`, no blocking, no cancellation surface on the read path. Errors are PARSE errors (`int[5,2]` → 'min must be < max', `int(0)` → 'bound must be > 0', non-numeric arg, unknown verb that looks like a typo) surfaced as rich diagnostics with the offending span up the `property-resolution` chain (charter §9), distinct from a clean fall-through (`None`) when the key simply is not a `random.*` key. RNG interior-mutability/concurrency handled with the same fine-grained, no-global-lock approach as A/B.

### Rust clashes
- Spring computes random bytes via JDK `SecureRandom`/`Random` always available on the classpath; Rust std has NO RNG. leaf must either depend on an external RNG crate (`rand`/`fastrand`/`getrandom`) — a core dependency the charter's 'minimal deps, std assumed' posture must sanction — or hand-roll a PCG/SplitMix64 seeded from `getrandom`. This is a genuine capability gap, not a mechanism choice: std gives `RandomState`/`DefaultHasher` (hash-flooding entropy, NOT a documented PRNG contract) which is unsuitable for advertised randomness. Phase 2 must decide the entropy dependency.
- Spring's source returns `Object` (an already-typed `Integer`/`Long`/`UUID`/byte-hex `String`) and relies on downstream conversion; leaf's stack is string-keyed/string-valued (`property-resolution` resolves to a raw string, `type-conversion` coerces at the injection point). So leaf must RENDER every random value to its canonical string form (uuid's hyphenated form, int's decimal, value's hex) inside the source, then let the normal string→T conversion run — the typed-at-source vs string-at-stack mismatch means leaf cannot mirror Spring's `Object`-returning shape and must pick the string rendering as the contract.
- Spring tolerates `random.*` being a quietly mutable global (a shared `Random` instance, GC-managed, no ownership concern). Rust forces an explicit OWNERSHIP + interior-mutability decision for the RNG state that advances per draw: a `&mut`/`Cell`/atomic-PCG behind the source, honouring the no-global-locks / minimal-Arc invariant. The 'just a static Random' JVM assumption has no free Rust analogue.
- Spring's `PropertySource` is a single interface where a computed source just overrides `getProperty`; Rust's stack design must commit UPFRONT to whether the source trait has a non-enumerable arm (`is_enumerable()/property_names()` returning empty) because the binder and relaxed-binding ENUMERATE sources — a JVM interface that lazily answers `containsProperty` has no enumerate-side cost, but in Rust the non-enumerable contract must be a structural property of the trait so binding never tries to iterate an infinite keyspace.
- Spring's placeholder helper and the source live in one runtime with reflection; leaf's placeholder-only access rule (never bound directly) must be ENFORCED structurally (only the `property-resolution` `${...}` walk calls `get`; the binder walks `property_names()` which is empty for this source) rather than by a runtime 'is this a bind context?' check — the enforcement moves from runtime convention to the type/trait shape, which is stricter but requires the dichotomy to exist first.
- Spring's 'sits at a fixed precedence rung' is a hard-coded position in Boot's `ConfigDataEnvironmentPostProcessor`; in Rust the rung is an ordering-mutation call owned by `config-data`, so 'fixed rung' becomes a convention this feature publishes (the name `random`) and `config-data` honours — there is no central post-processor that owns the whole order, so the rung's fixity depends on `config-data` correctly placing it relative to the (also-special) env-var and SAJ sources.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — PARENT/owns-the-shape. This feature is the canonical concrete implementor of property-sources' R3 'non-enumerable / on-demand' arm. It REQUIRES property-sources to commit to a source-trait shape that supports `get(key)` WITHOUT a backing store and reports non-enumerability (`is_enumerable()->false` / empty `property_names()`). It honours never-blend (returns one whole value, never merged) and null-never-overrides (a non-`random.*` key returns `None` and falls through). It must be addable at a specific position via the ordering-mutation vocabulary (`add_after`/`add_before` by name).
- **property-resolution** — PRIMARY CONSUMER / the only legitimate caller. The `${...}` placeholder walk is the ONLY path that invokes this source's `get`. `${random.uuid}` etc. resolve through the normal first-source-wins walk; recursion/defaults (`${random.int:0}`) compose normally (though a random key rarely needs a default). This feature relies on the resolver treating all sources uniformly (no special-casing `random`), and the resolver relies on this source's compute-per-read returning a fresh value each call. Grammar errors surface up the resolver's diagnostic chain.
- **origin-tracking** — PRODUCES coarse-only origin. Every value this source returns carries `Origin::source("random")` (the coarse `PropertySourceOrigin` analogue) and NEVER a fine file:line origin — origin-tracking explicitly lists random.* as a coarse-only source. This is the worked example of origin-tracking's 'fine origin is optional' altitude. Provenance rides the never-blend short-circuit unmodified.
- **config-data** — PLACED-BY. config-data owns the full externalized-config precedence order and is the producer that, during bootstrap, constructs `random` and inserts it at its fixed rung — just above Config Data files, just below OS env vars (rung 4 of 15). This feature publishes only the rung's named identity (`random`) + the rule that it occupies exactly one fixed rung; config-data executes the ordering-mutation call that realizes it. config-data's own intent doc LISTS random.* but assigns no design owner — this feature is that owner.
- **binder** — EXEMPT-FROM. The binder/config-properties NEVER bind directly over `random.*` (placeholder-only rule). Structurally the binder's tree-descent enumerates `property_names()`, which is empty for this non-enumerable source, so it is invisible to binding. The only way a bound config object gets a random value is indirectly: a placeholder `${random.*}` inside another (enumerable) source's value, resolved by property-resolution before/during binding.
- **relaxed-binding** — EXEMPT-on-enumerate-side. relaxed-binding's enumerate-and-match path (expand a canonical name into candidate forms, or normalize source keys) does NOT apply: this source is non-enumerable and its keyspace is the fixed `random.` namespace with a structured suffix, not relaxable identifiers. The placeholder key `${random.int}` is passed through to `get` as-is; the only canonicalization that matters is that the placeholder engine references the literal `random.` prefix (no kebab/camel variance on `random` itself).
- **type-conversion** — DOWNSTREAM. This source renders every computed value to a canonical STRING (decimal int/long, hyphenated uuid, hex value); the normal string→T coercion at the `@Value`/binding injection point (type-conversion neighbour) turns `${random.int}` into an `i32` field, `${random.long}` into `i64`, `${random.uuid}` into a `String`/`Uuid`. This feature owns the rendering; conversion owns the parse-back.
- **environment** — REACHED-THROUGH. The `random` source lives in the environment's owned property-source stack like any other; it is reachable wherever the environment is, but only the read/placeholder seam (PropertyResolver) ever surfaces its values. The mutate seam (ConfigurableEnvironment) is what config-data uses at bootstrap to place it.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- ENTROPY DEPENDENCY: does leaf's core take a direct dependency on an RNG crate (`rand`/`fastrand`/`getrandom`/`uuid`) for `random.*`, or hand-roll a seeded PCG/SplitMix64 over a single `getrandom` seed? This is a charter 'minimal deps' vs DX/correctness call, and it sets precedent for any other entropy need (e.g. id generation) across the framework.
- R3 TRAIT SHAPE: must `property-sources` commit to a two-arm source trait (enumerable vs on-demand) or a single trait with an `is_enumerable()`/empty-`property_names()` discriminator? This feature forces the decision because it is the FIRST non-enumerable source, and the binder/relaxed-binding enumerate-side behaviour depends on it. (Cross-cuts property-sources, binder, relaxed-binding.)
- SUB-GRAMMAR UNIFICATION: should the `random.*` mini-grammar parser, the `profiles` expression parser, and the `property-resolution` placeholder parser share ONE 'tiny config sub-grammar → typed spec → evaluate' primitive (realization C's bet), or stay three bespoke scanners? A genuine charter §11 unification candidate spanning three config features.
- RNG INTERIOR-MUTABILITY MODEL: per-read RNG advancement needs interior mutability honouring no-global-locks/minimal-Arc — is the answer an atomic PCG, a `Cell`-backed generator, a fine-grained per-source lock, or a per-resolution-context RNG handle threaded in? This intersects the broader execution-context/context-propagation model (does an RNG belong to the resolution context like a Locale, enabling deterministic seeding per request/test?).
- COMPUTED-SOURCE EXTENSIBILITY: is `random.*` a closed built-in (realization A), or the first instance of an OPEN computed-source/generator-verb family (realization B) that ecosystem crates can extend (`vault.*`, `random.bytes`)? If open, it inherits the full link-time-discovery + DCE + static-vs-WASM-directory duality and needs a policed 'generators must be pure+non-blocking' contract — a discovery-model and execution-discipline decision deferred to Phase 2.
- DETERMINISTIC-RANDOM FOR TESTS: should leaf expose a first-class way to seed `random.*` deterministically (so config fixtures using `${random.*}` are reproducible)? If yes, the RNG seed becomes part of the test/bootstrap configuration surface, touching the environment/bootstrap and context-propagation models.

### Notes
No per-feature Phase 1 design files exist on disk yet under docs/design/phase1/ (only docs/design/explorations/wasm-modules-for-leaf.md); the neighbouring designs (property-sources, property-resolution, origin-tracking, config-data, etc.) were provided to me only as the JSON catalog in the prompt, so I aligned to their stated scope boundaries and naming rather than to files. Key alignment confirmations: property-sources EXPLICITLY names the 'enumerable-vs-on-demand source dichotomy' as one of its divergent axes and lists random.* as a candidate non-enumerable source; origin-tracking EXPLICITLY lists 'random.*' as having ONLY a coarse origin (line: 'env vars, programmatic maps, random.* have only a coarse origin'); config-data's intent LISTS RandomValuePropertySource at its fixed precedence rung but assigns NO design owner — confirming this feature is the missing owner. Spring grounding read at lines 1415-1521 (precedence order + the random.* / SAJ section) and 1525-1529 (origin coarse/fine altitudes). I did NOT pick a meta-architecture: the three realizations span trait-arm (A), runtime-generator-registry (B), and parse-to-typed-spec (C) deliberately, leaving the R3 trait shape, entropy dependency, sub-grammar unification, RNG concurrency model, and computed-source extensibility as Phase 2 questions. All three realizations share the same non-enumerable + placeholder-only + coarse-origin + fixed-rung + non-blocking-cold-path contract; they diverge only on internal representation. Charter invariants honoured: no nightly needed (RNG + a hand-written parser are stable); thin/no macros (the feature is plain kernel code, no proc-macro); async-first/cold-path discipline (resolution is a cold path, RNG draw never blocks, entropy syscall fenced to bootstrap); origin-agnostic provider seam preserved so a WASM/remote computed source can slot into the same on-demand arm later."}

## SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON flattening loader  `[extra-9]`

Spring's `SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON` (SAJ) is a distinct format LOADER plus a fixed precedence rung, NOT the binder and NOT the config-data file engine. Spring intent (docs §"RandomValuePropertySource and SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON" line 1521, §precedence lines 1428-1429, §null-never-overrides line 1443) has FOUR load-bearing parts leaf must replicate as INTENT, not mechanism:

(1) THE FLATTENING ALGORITHM — the inverse of the binder's tree-descent. A JSON blob `{"my":{"name":"t"}}` becomes a FLAT map of dotted keys `my.name=t`; nested objects descend one dotted segment per level; arrays become indexed keys using the brackets convention `my.list[0]`, `my.list[1]` (NOT underscore-wrapped — that is the env-var convention `relaxed-binding` owns; SAJ produces the canonical file-style `[index]` form so the binder/relaxed lookup consumes it uniformly); scalars (string/number/bool) become string values; the empty object `{}` and empty array `[]` collapse to nothing (no key emitted). The result is an in-memory enumerable `PropertySource` of flat string keys with string values. This flatten walk is the genuinely new algorithm this feature owns — `config-data`'s .properties/.yaml loaders and the binder's descent are siblings, but none of them flattens a JSON tree into dotted/indexed keys.

(2) MULTI-TRANSPORT SOURCING with a fixed lookup order. The blob arrives from one of several transports: the `SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON` env var, the `spring.application.json` system property, a `--spring.application.json=...` command-line arg, or a JNDI attribute. Spring resolves the FIRST transport that supplies a non-blank blob (a small fixed search order), parses it ONCE, and contributes ONE property source. In leaf the JVM-specific transports (JNDI, system-properties-distinct-from-env) map to leaf-native equivalents or no-ops; the transport set must be ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC and extensible (a future WASM-module or platform-secret transport can supply the blob).

(3) A FIXED PRECEDENCE RUNG. The resulting source sits at exactly one rung (lines 1419-1433): above servlet/JNDI/system-props/OS-env, immediately BELOW command-line args. This feature does NOT own the global ordering policy (that is `config-data`'s precedence-order ownership and `property-sources`' ordering-mutation vocabulary) — it owns the CLAIM "SAJ belongs at this named rung relative to cmdline and the servlet/sysprop rungs," expressed as an `add_before(command-line-args, saj_source)` / `add_after(...)` request against the stack.

(4) JSON NULL IS ABSENT — never-overrides. A JSON `null` value (`{"my":{"name":null}}`) emits NO key for that path (the source returns `None`/absent for `my.name`), so it falls through to a lower-precedence source rather than masking it. This is the `property-sources` null-never-overrides invariant applied at FLATTEN TIME: the loader simply does not emit a key whose JSON value is null. Empty string is NOT null — `{"my":{"name":""}}` emits `my.name=""` (a present, winning value). This keeps "unset" and "set" distinguishable through the SAJ layer.

SCOPE BOUNDARY: `property-sources` owns the ordered named stack, the `PropertySource` source trait shape (`PropertyValue { raw, origin }`, name-as-identity, the add_first/add_before/add_after vocabulary), first-source-wins, and the never-blend + null-never-overrides invariants — SAJ is a PRODUCER of one conforming source and a CONSUMER of the ordering vocabulary. `config-data` owns the full externalized-config PRECEDENCE-ORDER POLICY and the early-control-key bootstrap; SAJ is one entry config-data places (or that registers itself into config-data's ordering plan) — the two designs must agree on who emits the `add_before` call. `relaxed-binding` owns key canonicalization (the flattened dotted keys are matched relaxed downstream — SAJ emits canonical dotted form + the `[index]` array convention, it does NOT itself canonicalize). `origin-tracking` owns the `Origin` type; SAJ attaches a coarse origin (the named SAJ source + which transport) plus an OPTIONAL fine origin (a JSON-pointer-style path `$.my.name` into the blob) to each flattened value. `binder`/`config-properties` consume the resolved value. THIS feature owns ONLY: the JSON-tree→flat-dotted/indexed-key flatten ALGORITHM, the null-as-absent + empty-collection-collapse rules, the multi-transport blob ACQUISITION (env/sysprop/cmdline/JNDI-analogue, origin-agnostic + extensible), the parse-once semantics, and the fixed-rung precedence CLAIM expressed as an ordering request. The genuinely divergent Rust axis: WHEN/WHERE the JSON is parsed and flattened (eager flatten-to-owned-map at bootstrap vs lazy parse-tree kept live with on-demand path lookup vs a serde-Deserializer-driven streaming flatten), HOW the multi-transport acquisition is modeled (a fixed ordered list of transport closures vs an origin-agnostic Transport trait vs config-data-driven), and WHERE the null-as-absent + array-index conventions live so they share the binder/relaxed-binding key vocabulary.

### Candidate realizations

#### Eager flatten-to-owned-MapPropertySource at bootstrap
At bootstrap, a single synchronous step acquires the blob from the first non-blank transport (in a fixed order), parses it once with serde_json into a serde_json::Value, and recursively flattens it into an owned BTreeMap<String, PropertyValue> wrapped as an ordinary enumerable MapPropertySource named `application-json`. The flatten is a depth-first walk: flatten(prefix, Value) — for Object recurse with prefix.child per entry; for Array recurse with prefix[i]; for a scalar insert prefix -> PropertyValue { raw: scalar.to_string(), origin }; for Null emit NOTHING (the never-override rule baked in at emit time); {}/[] emit nothing. Each value carries a fine origin = the JSON path ($.my.list[0]) + coarse origin = (source-name, transport-kind). The loader then asks the stack to add_before("commandLineArgs", source) (or add_first if cmdline is absent), claiming its fixed rung. API feel: let src = SajLoader::new().acquire_and_flatten()?; if let Some(src)=src { sources.add_before(CMDLINE, src); }. Pure data after construction — a snapshot. Mirrors Spring's JsonPropertySourceLoader/SpringApplicationJsonEnvironmentPostProcessor most directly: parse-once, flatten-once, contribute-once.

**Pros:** Simplest mental model and matches the property-sources enumerable source shape exactly — the result is an ordinary MapPropertySource indistinguishable downstream from a flattened .properties file; Parse-once is unambiguous; the blob is touched a single time and never re-read, so transient env/JNDI state can't cause inconsistent reads mid-run; null-as-absent and empty-collection-collapse are enforced structurally at emit time — a null path simply never becomes a key, so the never-override invariant is impossible to violate downstream; Cheap steady-state reads: a map lookup, zero JSON re-parsing on the hot read path (charter #4 — no work on hot path); Trivially testable and serializable: the flattened map is inspectable, dumpable for an /actuator/env analogue, fully synchronous, no async needed (charter #3 — clear execution context); Owns its memory as one contiguous map; no Arc/refcount churn, no live parse tree pinned (charter #5)

**Cons:** Eagerly materializes every key even if config-properties binds only a small prefix — wasted allocation for a huge blob (rare; SAJ blobs are typically small); String-ifies every scalar at flatten time, so number/bool JSON type info is lost into a raw string before the binder/type-conversion sees it (acceptable — matches Spring, which also stringifies; type recovery is type-conversion's job); Owned String keys + values mean one allocation per leaf value; for a very large blob this is more heap than a lazy parse-tree (mitigated: blobs are small by convention); Fine-origin JSON-path strings built eagerly even when never used in a diagnostic (mitigable: store a compact path-segment vector or recompute lazily — but that drifts toward realization B)

**Mechanisms considered:** serde_json::Value parse + recursive flatten into an owned MapPropertySource (no macros); No proc-macro and no build.rs — SAJ is pure runtime data, not a discovered extension point, so link-time registration does NOT apply to the flatten itself; linkme/inventory considered ONLY for registering the loader into config-data's loader set, then rejected for the loader-set in favor of an explicit ordered list owned by config-data (the loader set is small, fixed, core-owned — not an open extension point); Runtime evaluation of which transport supplied the blob (a fixed ordered scan), not compile-time

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** No cross-crate discovery problem for the flatten algorithm itself — it is core code in (likely) the same crate that owns config-data's loaders, invoked at bootstrap; no linkme/inventory, no DCE hazard, no classpath analogue needed. The loader is one entry in config-data's fixed, core-owned loader set (alongside .properties/.yaml/configtree/env:), so there is no open downstream extension point to register. T1 surfaces only for the multi-transport acquisition: the JNDI transport has no stable-Rust analogue and the OPTIONAL future WASM-module/platform-secret transport must be addable WITHOUT the core depending on it — so the transport list should be an ordered Vec of origin-agnostic transport handles the bootstrap layer (leaf-boot) populates, with integration crates contributing extra transports via the SAME link-time provider registry the rest of leaf uses (a transport is just another provider of dyn SajTransport). The core flatten never assumes native construction of the blob's bytes (origin-agnostic acquisition).

**T2 — execution context:** Runs in the synchronous bootstrap/cold path (charter #4 permits cold-path work). Env-var and system-property reads are non-blocking std calls; a JNDI-analogue or WASM-module transport COULD block or do IO — so acquisition is fenced: each transport returns its blob bytes, and any transport that must do IO is driven on the bootstrap executor with an explicit boundary (the synchronous flatten never awaits inside the stack-join). serde_json parse is synchronous CPU work bounded by blob size, on the bootstrap thread — never on a hot path. Errors (malformed JSON) fail bootstrap fast with a rich diagnostic naming the transport + byte offset + the offending JSON snippet (charter #9); cancellation is trivial since the whole step is synchronous and short. After bootstrap the source is immutable data — no execution-context concerns on the read path.

#### Lazy parse-tree source with on-demand path resolution
Acquire the blob once and parse it once into a serde_json::Value held INSIDE a custom SajPropertySource that implements the property-sources source trait directly — but DO NOT flatten eagerly. The source answers get(key) by splitting the dotted/indexed key into path segments (my.name -> [my,name]; my.list[0] -> [my,list,0]) and descending the live Value tree on demand, returning Some(PropertyValue) for a present scalar, None for a missing path OR a Null value (null-as-absent enforced at lookup time). For enumeration (the EnumerablePropertySource analogue the binder needs to discover keys under a prefix), it lazily walks the subtree under the queried prefix and yields flattened key names, memoizing the key set on first enumeration. Array indices are matched by parsing the [n] segment back to a usize index into a JSON array. API feel: struct SajPropertySource { root: serde_json::Value, name: Name, transport: TransportKind } with fn get(&self, key:&CanonicalKey)->Option<PropertyValue> doing the descent; the flatten is the INVERSE walk performed per-query instead of once up front.

**Pros:** Zero up-front flattening cost: a blob with thousands of keys of which the binder reads ten descends only the ten paths actually queried (charter #2/#5 — pay for what you use); Holds the JSON exactly once; no duplicated owned key strings — lowest memory for large blobs; Fine origin (the JSON path) is reconstructable on demand precisely when a diagnostic needs it, never paid for otherwise; null-as-absent falls out naturally: descending to a Null node returns None, identical to descending to a missing path — the never-override rule is a single branch in the descent; Most directly mirrors the binder's tree-descent (this loader IS the inverse walk run on demand), maximizing shared machinery with the binder's segment-splitting + array-index conventions (charter #11 unification)

**Cons:** Enumeration (binder needs 'all keys under prefix my.') forces a subtree walk anyway, so the lazy win evaporates for config-properties binding (the dominant consumer), which enumerates rather than point-queries — risk of re-walking unless memoized, and memoization re-introduces an owned key set (drifts back toward A); Each read re-splits the key into segments and re-descends — more work per read than A's flat-map lookup; on a warm read path this is repeated parsing of the same key string (charter #4 favors cheap hot-path reads); Keeping a live serde_json::Value pinned for the process lifetime is a long-lived heap structure with internal Box/Vec/Map nodes — more pointer-chasing and arguably more Arc-ish sharing if the source is shared across the hierarchy (charter #5 tension); Implementing the source trait by hand (vs reusing MapPropertySource) means SAJ carries bespoke lookup code that must independently honor every property-sources invariant (name-as-identity, never-blend) — more surface to get wrong than producing a plain map; array [n] segment parsing and the dotted-vs-bracket boundary must be re-decided here rather than reusing relaxed-binding's segment vocabulary — duplication risk unless explicitly delegated

**Mechanisms considered:** serde_json::Value kept live + on-demand recursive descent implementing the source trait directly; serde_json::RawValue borrowed tree to defer scalar parsing further (rejected as over-engineering for typically-small blobs); Memoized lazy enumeration (a once-cell key index built on first prefix enumeration) to bridge the point-query/enumerate gap; No macros, no link-time registration for the algorithm (same as A); transport acquisition identical to A

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same as realization A for discovery: the loader/source is core code, no cross-crate registry, no DCE. The added T1 consideration is the SOURCE TRAIT contract from property-sources — because this realization implements the trait by hand (not via the stock MapPropertySource), it hard-couples to the exact origin-agnostic trait shape property-sources defines, so it must stay an in-tree consumer that moves in lockstep with that trait (a downstream crate implementing a bespoke SAJ-like source would face the same coupling). Multi-transport acquisition T1 is identical to A (origin-agnostic transport list; JNDI/WASM transports added by leaf-boot/integration crates, not the core).

**T2 — execution context:** Acquisition + the single parse run synchronously on the bootstrap cold path, identical to A. The DIVERGENCE is that the read path now does real work (segment-split + tree descent) — this must be confirmed to stay off genuinely hot paths. config-properties binding happens at an early refresh step (cold path), so the enumerate-and-descend cost lands at startup, acceptable. But if @Value/${...} placeholder resolution against SAJ happens during steady-state request handling (a warm path), repeated descent violates charter #4's cheap-hot-path goal unless the memoized key index makes warm reads O(1) — so memoization is effectively mandatory, pushing this realization toward A's materialized map in practice. No async on the read path; the live Value is immutable after parse so it is freely shareable across threads without locks (charter #5).

#### Transport-trait + plan-then-apply contribution (origin-agnostic, config-data-integrated)
Model SAJ as TWO origin-agnostic seams that slot into config-data's loader/precedence framework rather than as a standalone bootstrap step. (1) A SajTransport trait — fn acquire(&self) -> Result<Option<BlobBytes>> with an associated transport-kind label — implemented for EnvVarTransport, SystemPropertyTransport, CommandLineTransport, and (in integration crates) JndiTransport/WasmModuleTransport. The bootstrap holds an ORDERED Vec<Box<dyn SajTransport>>; the first that yields Some non-blank blob wins (origin records WHICH transport). (2) A JsonFlattenLoader that implements config-data's generic ConfigDataLoader contract (the same trait .properties/.yaml/configtree/env: implement): given blob bytes it returns a LoadedDocument = (flat key/value pairs + fine origins + the requested precedence-rung TAG). Crucially the loader does NOT mutate the stack itself — it returns a CONTRIBUTION carrying a declarative rung tag (Rung::SajBelowCmdline), and config-data's single-pass assembler applies all contributions' rung tags to the property-sources stack in one ordering pass (plan-then-apply). The flatten algorithm underneath can be eager (A) or lazy (B) — this realization is orthogonal on that axis and focuses on the SEAM shape. API feel: impl ConfigDataLoader for JsonFlattenLoader { fn load(&self, blob: Blob) -> LoadedDocument { flatten_json(blob, Rung::SajBelowCmdline) } }; transports and loader registered into config-data's loader set the same way every other loader is.

**Pros:** Maximally unified with config-data (charter #11): SAJ becomes one more ConfigDataLoader + a rung tag, reusing the exact loader contract, origin-attachment seam, and single-pass assembler that .properties/.yaml/configtree/env: already use — no bespoke bootstrap path; Cleanly resolves the OWNERSHIP ambiguity flagged in the intent (who emits the add_before): NOBODY emits it imperatively — the loader DECLARES a rung tag and config-data's assembler owns all stack mutation in one place, so precedence stays a single deterministic policy (no scattered add_before calls); Origin-agnostic by construction: the SajTransport trait makes the blob's PROVENANCE a pluggable concern, so a WASM-module transport or a cloud-secret transport slots in as just another impl without the core knowing (the explicit origin-agnostic + WASM-slot-in requirement); Transports are testable in isolation (inject a fake transport returning a fixed blob); the loader is testable against bytes with no transport; plan-then-apply makes the whole precedence assembly auditable and deterministic — every contribution's rung is visible before any mutation, ideal for a rich 'why is this value X' diagnostic (charter #9); Leaves the flatten-strategy (eager A vs lazy B) as an internal implementation choice swappable later without changing the seam

**Cons:** Heaviest abstraction: a Transport trait + dyn dispatch + a generic ConfigDataLoader contract + a contribution/rung model is more machinery than a 20-line eager flatten — risk of over-engineering a small fixed feature (charter favors thin solutions; this must EARN the abstraction via reuse across the other loaders); Box<dyn SajTransport> introduces dyn dispatch + heap for the transport list (charter #5 tension) — defensible because acquisition is a one-shot cold-path call, but it is Box the simpler realizations avoid; Tightly couples SAJ's design to config-data's not-yet-finalized ConfigDataLoader contract and rung/contribution model — if those shift, SAJ moves; this realization can't be designed in isolation from config-data (a Phase 2/3 coordination dependency); The rung TAG vocabulary (Rung::SajBelowCmdline) must be a shared enum config-data owns, so SAJ doesn't independently name precedence rungs — correct for unification but means this feature owns LESS than the prompt's framing implies (it owns flatten + transports + the CLAIM, but the rung-enum lives in config-data); Indirection makes the simplest case (just an env var) traverse a trait-object + loader + assembler pipeline — more cognitive overhead for a reader chasing a single value's path

**Mechanisms considered:** A SajTransport trait (dyn-dispatched, origin-agnostic) for blob acquisition + a ConfigDataLoader trait impl for the flatten; Declarative rung-tag + plan-then-apply assembler owned by config-data (vs imperative add_before by the loader); linkme/inventory link-time registry for transports contributed by integration crates (the WASM-module transport is the canonical dynamic-source case) — as a CANDIDATE: a static link-time transport registry (the default 'classpath' of transports compiled in) PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module transport that itself supplies a blob; both feed the same ordered transport list; Runtime evaluation of transport order + which transport won (never compile-time); serde_json under the loader (eager or lazy flatten, deferred to the A/B axis)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This realization is where T1 bites hardest and is handled best. The SajTransport set is a genuine extension point: core compiles in env/sysprop/cmdline transports; integration crates (a hypothetical leaf-jndi, or the leaf-wasm module layer) contribute extra transports. The DUALITY applies directly: a STATIC link-time transport registry (linkme distributed-slice of transport descriptors — the default compiled-in 'classpath' of transports, zero runtime cost, but subject to the DCE/must-be-linked hazards — pin linkme>=0.3.24, require Rust>=1.89 for the #[used(linker)] default or inject -z nostart-stop-gc, force-link via the binary crate) is the common case; an OPTIONAL dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module transport (the runtime 'classpath' — scans ./modules/*.wasm, each may export a config-supplying capability) slots in as just another transport impl. Both are CANDIDATES, not a decision. The flatten loader itself, like A/B, is core code with no cross-crate discovery. The rung-enum and ConfigDataLoader contract are owned by config-data and shared, so SAJ emits fully-qualified references to them (proc-macro hygiene rules don't apply since there's no macro here — transport registration descriptors, if linkme is chosen, would be const data-only per the cross-crate doc's thin-descriptor guidance).

**T2 — execution context:** Transport acquisition is the only place that may BLOCK or do IO (JNDI lookup, WASM-module instantiation/scan, a cloud-secret fetch). So SajTransport::acquire is the explicit async/blocking boundary: it runs on the bootstrap (cold-path) executor; a transport needing IO either returns synchronously-acquired bytes or is awaited on the bootstrap executor BEFORE the synchronous flatten + stack-join begins — the property-sources stack is joined synchronously, never mid-await. The ordered first-non-blank scan short-circuits, so only as many transports as needed run. A blocking transport (JNDI-analogue) is offloaded to a dedicated pool with a bounded timeout; failure or timeout fails bootstrap with a rich diagnostic naming the transport (charter #9), and cancellation propagates by dropping the bootstrap future (each transport's acquire is cancellation-aware or short). The flatten (eager or lazy) and the plan-then-apply assembly are synchronous CPU work on the bootstrap thread. Post-bootstrap the contributed source is immutable, so read-path execution context matches A/B.

### Rust clashes
- No JNDI in Rust. Spring lists JNDI (java:comp/env) as both a SAJ transport AND its own precedence rung. Rust/std has no JNDI; the JVM 'naming context' has no native analogue. leaf must either drop the JNDI transport entirely (cleanest — it is a JVM-deployment artifact) or relocate it to an optional integration crate that provides a directory/secret-store transport. The fixed-rung precedence list also references servlet/JNDI rungs that will not exist in a core leaf app — so SAJ's 'sits just below cmdline, above JNDI/servlet/sysprops/env' becomes 'sits just below cmdline, above whatever lower rungs exist.' The relative claim (below cmdline) survives; the absolute neighbours partly evaporate.
- System properties vs env vars are nearly one-and-the-same in Rust. The JVM cleanly separates -Dspring.application.json=... (system property) from the SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON env var, and they occupy DIFFERENT precedence rungs. Rust has only process env vars + program args; there is no JVM system-property table. leaf must decide whether spring.application.json as a 'system property' transport maps to (a) a leaf-internal programmatic-properties layer, (b) just another env-var spelling, or (c) is dropped — and whether that collapses two Spring rungs into one. This is a transport-set mapping decision, not just a rename.
- Command-line argument parsing is not standardized in Rust. Spring's SpringApplication parses --spring.application.json=... from argv with its own CommandLinePropertySource conventions. Rust has no built-in --key=value argv parser, and apps commonly use clap/argh with their OWN conventions. leaf must own a minimal argv key=value parser for the cmdline transport (and for the cmdline RUNG generally), or risk colliding with the app's chosen arg parser — an ownership/conflict question that doesn't exist on the JVM.
- JSON null vs Rust Option vs empty-string is a tri-distinction Spring collapses deliberately. Spring maps JSON null -> absent, empty-string -> present-empty. Rust's natural serde model has Value::Null, Value::String(""), and a missing map key as THREE distinct states; leaf must collapse Null and missing-key to the SAME 'absent' (None) while keeping empty-string present — easy to get subtly wrong (e.g. serde default-field handling, or treating Null as Some("")). The never-override invariant depends on getting this exactly right at flatten/lookup time.
- No reflection / no runtime classpath for the transport extension point. Spring discovers SAJ handling via its EnvironmentPostProcessor machinery loaded from spring.factories on the classpath. leaf has no classpath; if SAJ transports are an extension point (realization C), discovery must be synthesized via link-time registration with its DCE/must-be-linked hazards, OR kept as an explicit core-owned fixed list (realizations A/B). The cross-crate doc is explicit: a registration-only transport crate the binary never references contributes nothing — so an integration-crate transport must be force-linked. This is a real clash only if SAJ transports are made open/pluggable; the fixed core transport set sidesteps it.
- Number/bool/JSON-type information is erased to strings at flatten time. The JVM happily stringifies everything for the property model and recovers types later via binding. Rust's serde gives leaf the actual typed JSON scalar (i64/f64/bool) at flatten time — it is tempting to preserve the type, but the property-sources stack is stringly-typed (raw: String) by the property-sources contract, and type recovery is type-conversion's job at the binding seam. leaf must resist preserving JSON types into the source (which would break the uniform raw-string source shape) — a mild impedance where Rust offers MORE than the model wants.

### Interactions
- **property-sources** — PRODUCES one conforming source + CONSUMES the ordering vocabulary. SAJ emits a single named enumerable PropertySource (PropertyValue { raw, origin }, name-as-identity) and asks the stack to place it via add_before(cmdline,...)/add_first. SAJ must honor never-blend + null-never-overrides — it enforces null-never-overrides at flatten/lookup time by not emitting null-valued keys. Open coordination: does SAJ call add_before imperatively (realizations A/B) or declare a rung tag the assembler applies (realization C)?
- **config-data** — PRECEDENCE-ORDER + LOADER-SET coordination — the central interaction. config-data owns the full externalized-config precedence-order policy and the loader set (.properties/.yaml/configtree/env:); the intent explicitly notes config-data lists SAJ only in its recap and does NOT own the JSON-flatten loader. This feature SUPPLIES that loader. The two designs MUST agree on: (a) whether SAJ is a ConfigDataLoader impl inside config-data's framework (realization C) or a separate bootstrap step (A/B); (b) WHO owns the rung tag/enum naming the SAJ rung; (c) ordering vs config-data's early-control-key bootstrap (SAJ is NOT an early-control-key source — control keys like spring.config.location only work via env/sysprop/cmdline, so a control key INSIDE the SAJ blob must be IGNORED, matching Spring's 'too late' rule — needs explicit confirmation).
- **relaxed-binding** — EMITS canonical-form keys that relaxed-binding then matches downstream. SAJ produces dotted keys (my.name) and the FILE-style [index] array convention (my.list[0]) — deliberately NOT the env-var underscore convention relaxed-binding owns for env sources. SAJ does NOT itself canonicalize; it must emit keys in the form relaxed-binding's UNIFORM matching consumes uniformly. Open question: does SAJ emit kebab-case, or preserve the JSON key's case and let relaxed-binding normalize? (Spring preserves JSON keys and normalizes at match time.)
- **origin-tracking** — PRODUCES fine origins. SAJ attaches a coarse origin (source-name + which transport supplied the blob) and an OPTIONAL fine origin (a JSON-pointer/path $.my.list[0] into the blob) to each flattened value, using origin-tracking's Origin type. This powers 'property X came from SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON, path $.my.name' diagnostics. The fine origin is path-based, not file+line (the blob has no lines), so SAJ exercises the coarse-origin + optional-fine-origin altitude split origin-tracking defines.
- **property-resolution** — DOWNSTREAM consumer reads through SAJ via first-source-wins. ${...} placeholder resolution and required/typed reads walk the stack and may resolve a key from the SAJ source; SAJ's null-as-absent ensures a null JSON value falls through to a lower source rather than resolving to an empty/null placeholder value. No direct coupling beyond conforming to the source trait.
- **binder / config-properties** — DOWNSTREAM consumer + ALGORITHMIC MIRROR. config-properties binding enumerates keys under a prefix from the stack, including SAJ keys; the binder's tree-descent is the INVERSE of SAJ's flatten — same dotted/indexed segment vocabulary and array [index] convention. Strong unification candidate (charter #11): SAJ's flatten and the binder's descent should SHARE the segment/index conventions rather than each defining their own. Realization B makes this mirror explicit (flatten = descent run on demand).
- **leaf-boot / bootstrap layer** — OWNS invocation + transport population. The SpringApplication-equivalent bootstrap is where SAJ acquisition runs (cold path), where the transport list is populated (env/sysprop/cmdline by default), and where integration crates' extra transports (JNDI-analogue, WASM-module) are wired in. The core never depends on those integration crates (charter #6); leaf-boot composes them.
- **leaf-wasm module layer (optional, future)** — CANDIDATE dynamic transport source. Per the origin-agnostic requirement, a WASM-module or directory-scanned transport could supply the SAJ blob (the dynamic 'classpath' duality). SAJ's transport seam must be origin-agnostic so this slots in later WITHOUT the core assuming native acquisition — explicitly a candidate, not a decision.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- OWNERSHIP OF PRECEDENCE-RUNG EMISSION: Does a loader (SAJ) imperatively call add_before on the property-sources stack, or DECLARE a rung tag that a config-data plan-then-apply assembler applies in one pass? This is a cross-cutting decision affecting EVERY config-data loader, not just SAJ — it determines whether precedence is one centralized deterministic policy or scattered imperative mutations. (Surfaced by realizations A/B vs C.)
- TRANSPORT EXTENSION POINT — open or closed? Is the SAJ blob-acquisition transport set a FIXED core-owned list (env/sysprop/cmdline) or an OPEN extension point integration crates contribute to via link-time registration (with the DCE/must-be-linked hazards + the static-vs-dynamic-WASM duality)? This is the same static-link-time-registry-plus-optional-dynamic-directory-scan question every leaf SPI/discovery feature faces — should be resolved uniformly across all of them, not per-feature.
- FLATTEN/DESCENT SEGMENT VOCABULARY UNIFICATION: SAJ's flatten (tree->dotted/indexed keys) is the exact inverse of the binder's descent (keys->tree) and shares the array [index] convention with relaxed-binding's index rules. Should there be ONE shared canonical key-segment + array-index primitive that SAJ-flatten, binder-descent, and relaxed-binding all consume, rather than three independent implementations? (charter #11 unification candidate spanning four features.)
- JVM-TRANSPORT MAPPING POLICY: How do the JVM-only transports/rungs (JNDI, system-properties-distinct-from-env, servlet) map into leaf's model — dropped, collapsed into env, or relocated to optional integration crates? This affects the absolute precedence-rung neighbours of SAJ and is a broader 'which JVM property rungs survive into leaf' question config-data must answer holistically.
- NULL/ABSENCE/EMPTY MODELING ACROSS THE WHOLE STACK: SAJ collapses JSON-null + missing-key to 'absent' while keeping empty-string 'present'. Is there a single leaf-wide absence model (Option<PropertyValue> where None is the only fall-through) that EVERY source produces uniformly, so null-never-overrides is enforced once at the trait level rather than re-implemented per loader? (property-sources owns the invariant; the question is whether enforcement is centralized.)
- COMMAND-LINE ARG OWNERSHIP: leaf needs a minimal argv --key=value parser for BOTH the cmdline transport and the cmdline precedence RUNG, but apps use clap/argh with their own conventions. Who owns argv parsing, and how does leaf's cmdline source avoid conflicting with the application's arg parser? (A bootstrap-layer question broader than SAJ.)

### Notes
Grounding read: charter (all 11 invariants + §3 deferred keystones), the Spring SAJ section (lines 1419-1443 precedence + null-never-overrides; 1509-1521 SAJ flatten), cross-crate composition doc (linkme/inventory, DCE three-layer hazard, must-be-linked Layer 0, the static-link-registry + optional-dynamic-WASM-classpath duality), nightly-tradeoffs (core fully stable; serde_json stable; const-eval baseline not load-bearing here since SAJ is runtime data), and the wasm-modules exploration (the dynamic directory-scanned 'classpath' as an optional transport source).

KEY FRAMING: SAJ is fundamentally simpler than its sibling config-data loaders — it is a single small blob, parsed once, flattened once, at one fixed rung. The genuine design tension is NOT the flatten algorithm (a ~20-line recursive walk under any realization) but (1) the seam/ownership boundary with config-data (who owns precedence emission + the loader contract), and (2) the multi-transport acquisition's origin-agnosticism + extension-point question. Realizations A and B diverge on the FLATTEN strategy (eager-map vs lazy-tree); realization C is ORTHOGONAL — it diverges on the SEAM shape (transport-trait + config-data-loader contract + plan-then-apply) and could wrap either A or B underneath. I kept C distinct because the seam decision is the higher-leverage one for Phase 2/3 unification.

LIKELY PHASE 3 DIRECTION (not a decision): eager flatten (A) for the cheap-hot-path read + impossible-to-violate-null-rule wins, expressed through config-data's loader contract + plan-then-apply rung tags (C's seam), with the transport set fixed-and-core-owned by default plus an origin-agnostic trait so an optional integration-crate/WASM transport can slot in. That blend honors charter #4 (cheap reads), #5 (owned map, minimal dyn), #11 (unified with config-data + binder segment vocab), and the origin-agnostic/WASM-slot-in requirement — but the seam-ownership and transport-openness questions are genuinely Phase 2's, so I did not pick.

NOT OWNED BY THIS FEATURE (re-confirmed against the catalog to avoid scope creep): the global precedence-order policy + early-control-key bootstrap (config-data), the stack/trait/never-blend/null-never-overrides INVARIANT definitions (property-sources), key canonicalization + UNIFORM matching + env-var conventions (relaxed-binding), the Origin TYPE (origin-tracking), the ${...} walk (property-resolution), and string->T coercion (type-conversion). This feature owns ONLY the flatten algorithm, null-as-absent/empty-collapse rules, multi-transport acquisition, parse-once, and the fixed-rung CLAIM.

## @PropertySource-equivalent: refresh-time declarative source contribution from config classes  `[extra-10]`

Spring's `@PropertySource` on a `@Configuration` class is the SEPARATE, LATER, CONFIG-CLASS-DRIVEN way to add a property source — distinct in PHASE and in PRECEDENCE-RUNG from Boot's Config Data file loading. `ConfigurationClassPostProcessor` reads the annotation while parsing config classes during context REFRESH (the `invokeBeanFactoryPostProcessors` step) and pushes the loaded source onto the bottom of the stack — at rung 2 of 15 in Boot's precedence order (doc lines 1419-1420), just above `setDefaultProperties` and BELOW the Config Data files it superficially resembles. Five load-bearing intents leaf must replicate AS INTENT, not mechanism (doc lines 1439-1441):\n\n(1) DECLARATIVE, CONFIG-CLASS-TIED CONTRIBUTION. The location-to-load is declared as an attribute ON a configuration item, NOT as a standalone bootstrap loader. It rides config-class parsing — so it is gated by the SAME conditions/profiles that gate the config class itself (an excluded config class contributes no source), and it can only be discovered once config-class parsing has begun.\n\n(2) REFRESH-PHASE TIMING — and the famous \"too late\" gotcha. Because the source is added during refresh (config-class parsing), it sits at the BOTTOM rung and is added AFTER the early bootstrap has already consumed logging config, framework-main settings, and the active-profile set. Setting `logging.level.*` / framework `main.*` / profile-activation keys via `@PropertySource` SILENTLY has no effect. leaf must replicate this ordering hazard FAITHFULLY (it is a real precedence-rung fact), but — per charter #9 — must NOT let it fail silently the way Spring does; leaf should detect a bootstrap-consumed key arriving on this low rung and emit a rich diagnostic.\n\n(3) BOTTOM-BUT-ONE PRECEDENCE. The contributed source lands just above the default-properties rung and below every Config Data file, env var, system prop, and CLI arg. It is the WEAKEST declarative source — a code-level fallback default that any external file or env var overrides. Multiple `@PropertySource`s among themselves order by declaration/processing order, all clustered at that one low rung.\n\n(4) `${...}` PLACEHOLDERS IN THE LOCATION + `@Repeatable`. The location string itself is placeholder-expanded against the already-built environment before loading (`${config.dir}/app.properties`), and the annotation is repeatable (many sources per config class). leaf must support both.\n\n(5) THE FORMAT/CAPABILITY LIMITATION. Spring's `@PropertySource` cannot load YAML or multi-document files (no `---` activation, no profile docs) — it is a thin `.properties`-only loader, deliberately less capable than Config Data.
