The IO-bearing wrinkle is the dynamic WASM directory scan (if WASM flavors must factor into deduction): that scan is real filesystem IO and MUST be fenced to a clearly-marked cold startup step (the wasm-modules exploration already constrains it to a single configured location, no recursion, no network), never on the hot path — and its result must join the synchronous flavor registry the deduction reads, so the async/sync boundary is crossed exactly once, explicitly, before deduction. Errors (deduced flavor unconstructible, override to an unregistered flavor, ambiguous deduction with multiple seeders claiming incompatible flavors) fail fast at boot with the full causal chain; cancellation = abort whole bootstrap. The actual transplant in the override case inherits the cold-path, owned-not-shared, non-blocking properties of realization 1/2.

### Rust clashes
- Spring's 'conversion' is class-hierarchy SUBTYPE swap (`StandardEnvironment` → `StandardServletEnvironment`) with reflective field copying; Rust has no subtype reflection and no way to 'reinterpret' an owned struct as a sibling type — so 're-typing' must become either (a) re-seeding ONE type's stack (no second type), or (b) an EXPLICIT total state-extraction/transplant (`into_parts`/`from_parts`). There is no in-place reinterpretation.
- The `environment` feature mandates exactly ONE owned environment built once; mid-bootstrap 'conversion' literally produces a SECOND instance and discards the first. In Rust that means the old environment is MOVED/consumed and any handle already shared (to an earlier EnvironmentPostProcessor) is invalidated — Spring's GC'd shared reference tolerates this; Rust ownership forces conversion to occur strictly before any `Arc`/handle sharing, narrowing the legal window to the bootstrap tail.
- Spring deduces the application type partly from runtime CLASSPATH presence (`WebApplicationType.deduce` loading SPI deducers); Rust has no classpath and link-time registration can SILENTLY drop a flavor's seeder (DCE / Layer-0 unreferenced-crate), so a deduced/overridden flavor can have NO registered seeder with no error — Spring's classpath query always sees a present class; leaf must add an explicit self-check or it silently runs the wrong flavor.
- Spring's flavor difference is encoded as distinct subclasses each FREE to add typed state (servlet context, etc.); a single-type leaf environment (realization 1) cannot hold per-flavor typed state without a downcast-y extension map, while a multi-type leaf environment (realization 2) reintroduces `Box<dyn>`/`Any`-downcast the charter's memory-discipline (#5) and least-privilege façade want to avoid — there is no free lunch that is both single-typed AND flavor-specifically-typed.
- Spring sets the final type via `spring.main.web-application-type` bound back from config THAT WAS LOADED against the early environment — a deliberate chicken-and-egg Spring resolves by using a plain environment for the early phase. leaf must prove that deployment FLAVOR affects only later default-source precedence and NOT config LOADING itself, or the 'load config then re-type' ordering is unsound (config could have been loaded against the wrong source seeding).

### Interactions
- **environment** — PARENT/anchor. This feature is a bootstrap-phase operation ON the single owned environment the `environment` façade defines. It must NOT widen the read/mutate seam: conversion is a MUTATE-side, bootstrap-only operation (never exposed to application beans through the `PropertyResolver` read view). The 'one owned environment' invariant is preserved by treating conversion as build-time re-seeding (realization 1) or a total transplant that yields one environment (realization 2), not as runtime multiplicity.
- **property-sources** — USES as the transplant primitive. The lossless source-stack migration IS the ordering-mutation vocabulary `property-sources` already owns (`add_first`/`add_before(name)`/`add_after`/`add_last`/`replace`/`remove`). Realization 1 reseeds by removing flavor-tagged sources and re-adding via this vocabulary; realization 2 surrenders/reconstructs the whole `PropertySources` via `EnvironmentParts`. The never-blend + name-as-identity + child-wins invariants must survive the transplant untouched — user/config sources keep their instances and order; only flavor-default sources move.
- **profiles** — PRESERVES. Active + default + include + group profile sets (the sealed `ActiveProfiles` the `profiles` feature owns) must transplant LOSSLESSLY into the re-typed/re-seeded environment — this is half of Spring's preserved state. Because flavor seeding is decided AFTER config-data loading (where `leaf.main.flavor` and profile activation are read), the profile sets are already final at conversion time and are simply carried, not recomputed.
- **config-data** — ORDERING DEPENDENCY + open question. Conversion runs at the TAIL of prepare-environment, AFTER config-data loading (so config can override the deduced flavor via `leaf.main.flavor`, the `bindToSpringApplication` analogue). The hard constraint inherited from Spring: a flavor must NOT change how config-data LOADS (else loading happened against the wrong source set) — only which DEFAULT sources sit at the bottom afterward. config-data's deterministic single-pass model must complete before conversion; conversion only mutates flavor-default precedence rungs, never re-runs the import-traversal.
- **relaxed-binding** — RE-ATTACH target. Spring's final step re-attaches `ConfigurationPropertySources` — the relaxed-binding adapter source that exposes the stack under canonical-key lookup. After any transplant the leaf equivalent (the relaxed-binding ConfigurationPropertySource adapter) must be re-attached/`replace`d so it wraps the NEW stack, or relaxed `get(canonical)` would consult a stale source view. This is the explicit 'and re-attach' in Spring's order.
- **origin-tracking** — USES (realization 1) + PRESERVES (all). Realization 1 uses a coarse origin marker to TAG flavor-seeded sources so re-seed removes exactly them. All realizations must preserve each surviving source's origin through the transplant untouched (provenance rides the move), so a post-conversion env-dump still attributes every value to its true source — and the conversion itself becomes diagnosable ('this source was re-seeded by flavor Reactive').
- **bootstrap (SpringApplication-equivalent / leaf-boot)** — OWNED-BY / ordering. This operation lives in the leaf-boot bootstrap pipeline's prepare-environment step (the `prepareEnvironment` analogue), sequenced exactly: deduce flavor → build/seed environment → run env-post-processors + config-data → bind-back `leaf.main.flavor` → CONVERT if mismatch → re-attach ConfigurationPropertySources → printBanner/createContext. The deploy-flavor deduction (servlet/reactive/WASM) and the `setFlavor` escape hatch are bootstrap-layer surface, not framework-core.
- **auto-configuration** — DOWNSTREAM CONSUMER. The deployment flavor that conversion finalizes is read by `@ConditionalOnWebApplication`-style conditions (the `condition-family` neighbour) to gate servlet-vs-reactive auto-config. So the flavor must be FINAL and queryable on the environment before any condition evaluation / refresh — reinforcing that conversion completes at the bootstrap tail, before the context refreshes.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- The cross-crate composition & tooling keystone (§3): how are deployment-flavor SEEDERS/FACTORIES (servlet/reactive/WASM-host) discovered — static linkme distributed slice (default 'classpath') vs inventory (for runtime-computed/trait-object factories) vs build-time codegen vs the dynamic directory-scanned WASM 'classpath' — and how is the DCE silent-vanish hazard defeated so a deduced flavor whose seeder didn't link fails LOUDLY rather than silently running Plain? (Decision deferred; this feature only needs SOME origin-agnostic flavor-provider registry.)
- The scope/lifetime/ownership keystone (§3): the environment is built once and held everywhere — does conversion (a consuming move / re-seed BEFORE sharing) constrain when the environment first becomes `Arc`-shared? If any bootstrap step needs a shared handle BEFORE flavor is final, realization 2's `into_parts(self)` consume-move is illegal and we're forced toward realization 1's in-place re-seed. The ownership model must fix the 'first share point' relative to flavor finalization.
- Single-typed vs multi-typed environment is itself a meta-decision touching the registry/type-erasure substrate (§3): does leaf want ONE environment type (realization 1, flavor = data) or N flavor backings behind a façade (realization 2, flavor = type)? This ripples into whether flavor-specific TYPED state (servlet-context analogue) is a first-class need or can be pushed entirely into the bean graph — Phase 2 should decide whether deployment flavor carries typed environment state at all, or is purely a default-source-seeding selector.
- Does deployment FLAVOR influence config-data LOADING, or only post-load default-source precedence? Spring guarantees the former is false (uses plain env for the early phase). If leaf's servlet/reactive/WASM flavors contribute config SOURCES that affect profile activation or import resolution, the 'load-then-convert' ordering is unsound and flavor must be pinned earlier — this interacts with the compile-vs-runtime resolution split (§3) and must be resolved before the bootstrap ordering is frozen.
- Timing of the dynamic WASM 'classpath' scan relative to flavor deduction: the wasm-modules exploration constrains the scan to a single configured location at startup, but if a WASM module can CONTRIBUTE a deployment flavor, the (IO-bearing, async-boundary-crossing) scan must complete before flavor deduction — pulling an async/IO step into the otherwise-synchronous pre-environment bootstrap window. Phase 2's async-execution & context-propagation model (§3) must place this scan and its sync/async boundary explicitly.

### Notes
Grounding read: charter (all 11 invariants), Spring design doc lines 244-323 (the run sequence, classpath-driven app-type deduction, ApplicationContext selection, the prepareEnvironment order incl. the literal 'convert the environment type if it does not match the deduced type; re-attach ConfigurationPropertySources' at line 258, bindToSpringApplication bind-back at 260, property-source reordering at 262) and lines 1307/1309/1315 (StandardEnvironment vs StandardServletEnvironment default-source seeding; never-blend; child-wins merge); cross-crate composition doc (linkme vs inventory vs build.rs, the three DCE layers + Layer-0 unreferenced-crate silent vanish, the explicit-vs-magic camps, the static+dynamic discovery duality); wasm-modules exploration (the dynamic directory-scanned loadable 'classpath' as the genuinely-new dynamic-discovery capability, scan bounded to one configured location). No prior Phase 1 design files exist for this area yet (docs/design/phase1/explorations is empty; only docs/design/explorations/wasm-modules-for-leaf.md present), so alignment is with the EXISTING DESIGNS supplied in the catalog (environment / property-sources / profiles / config-data / origin-tracking / relaxed-binding). All three realizations are implementation-agnostic and DIVERGENT: (1) flavor-as-data single-type re-seed, (2) typed-flavor multi-backing explicit transplant, (3) deduce-first control-flow that makes conversion the rare exception and DELEGATES the transplant to 1 or 2. The unified mechanism choice (single vs multi-typed env; provider-registry substrate) is explicitly left to Phase 2/3. Key honest tension surfaced repeatedly: Rust has no subtype reinterpretation, so 'conversion' is either re-seeding one type or an explicit total transplant — and the DCE silent-vanish risk means flavor deduction MUST be self-checked.

## Area coherence notes

- ENUMERABLE-FACET SHAPE IS SPECIFIED THREE TIMES WITH DIFFERENT MODELS. property-sources offers `as_enumerable` (R1 downcast) vs first-class `EnumerablePropertySource` sub-trait (R3); relaxed-binding needs key enumeration for canonicalization; binder needs 'all keys under a prefix' for collection-replacement + ignoreUnknownFields. All three describe the same enumerable capability but each picks its own representation. This must be ONE contract (likely the ConfigurationPropertySource adapter + a ContainsState PRESENT/ABSENT/UNKNOWN tri-state), or the three features will assume incompatible enumeration surfaces. Currently each design's R3 silently assumes a different shape.
- COLLECTION-REPLACEMENT ('one source owns the whole List/Map') HAS NO CONCRETE OWNED MECHANISM. binder states the invariant and flags it as unresolved across enumerable vs non-enumerable sources; property-sources only guarantees PER-SCALAR first-source-wins (never-blend at the key level), which does NOT by itself decide 'which single source owns this collection ROOT'. The collection-replacement rule is therefore a binder-level invariant that needs a property-sources/adapter contract ('is there any key under prefix X in source S') that no feature currently owns. This is an inter-feature gap dressed as a binder-only open question.
- THE include 'per-property-source, not list-merged' RULE STRADDLES THREE FEATURES WITH NO PINNED OWNER. profiles flags it (transport-vs-algebra boundary), property-sources flags it (consistent with never-blend, no cross-source list extension), and config-data harvests the levers. All three acknowledge it; none commits to where the per-source structure lives. If ProfileLevers must carry per-source provenance (leaking transport into the profile algebra), that decision has to be made jointly — right now each design defers to the others, risking a circular non-decision.
- STRICT-VS-LENIENT DEFAULT IS RAISED IDENTICALLY BY THREE FEATURES AND MUST BE ONE POLICY. property-resolution, value-injection, and (for ignoreInvalidFields) config-properties/binder each independently surface the lenient-foot-gun-vs-strict question and each says 'must be one framework-wide policy'. This is coherent as a deferral, but note the binder's leniency flags (ignoreUnknownFields/ignoreInvalidFields) and property-resolution's strict/lenient placeholder mode are DIFFERENT axes that both map onto the same BindHandler/ResolveHandler decisions — the designs should be explicit that these are two distinct knobs sharing one handler substrate, not one policy, to avoid conflating 'unresolved placeholder' with 'unknown/invalid bound field'.
- BRACKET-ESCAPE [key-with-dashes] OWNERSHIP IS FLAGGED BY relaxed-binding AND binder BUT DECLARED OUT-OF-SCOPE BY config-properties. Three features touch the literal-map-key escape (relaxed-binding normalization, binder map-key assembly, property-resolution bracketed key inside ${...}); relaxed-binding and binder both flag it; config-properties inherits-but-does-not-resolve. Rust forces exactly one owner or a literal dashed/dotted map key round-trips wrong. This is a genuine pending boundary decision, consistently acknowledged but unassigned.
- HANDLER-SUBSTRATE UNIFICATION (ResolveHandler == BindHandler) IS PROPOSED BY R3 OF BOTH property-resolution AND binder — COHERENT BUT DOUBLE-COUNTED. Both features shape their R3 observer chain (onStart/onSuccess/onFailure/onFinish) identically and BOTH defer 'do we share one substrate' to Phase 2 (charter #11). This is consistent, but the two designs should cross-reference that adopting R3 in ONE pre-commits the other; currently each treats it as its own independent open question, risking divergent handler signatures if decided separately.
- ORIGIN OF A PLACEHOLDER-EXPANDED / DERIVED VALUE IS UNDER-SPECIFIED ACROSS origin-tracking, property-resolution, AND value-injection. origin-tracking proposes Origin::Derived chaining; property-resolution asks whether an expanded value's origin is the outer key, a composite, or unrepresented; value-injection adds a COMPILE-TIME injection-site origin (proc_macro::Span) altitude with no Spring analogue. These three must agree on whether Origin is a single value or a composite/chain AND whether it spans runtime-file and compile-time-source altitudes — currently each sketches a different richness level (Derived chain vs composite vs single). The two-altitude (file:line vs source-span) unification is a real cross-feature design point, not just a representation choice.
- CONFIG-PROPERTIES-AS-A-BEAN (R3) RE-OPENS THE 'NO OTHER BEANS' RULE THAT THE SAME DESIGN WANTS TO ENFORCE STRUCTURALLY. config-properties simultaneously (a) proposes R3 making the config object a first-class bean with a binder-backed supplier and (b) wants to enforce 'pure projection / cannot inject other beans' by handing the construction seam only &Environment. These pull against each other: a first-class bean on the normal autowiring path is exactly where other-bean injection becomes possible. The design flags this, but it is an internal tension between two of its own realizations that must be resolved (role-gated supplier vs separate inert pipeline), not merely deferred.
- CONFIG-METADATA SOURCE-OF-TRUTH OVERLAPS THE BINDER'S BindTarget SCHEMA — POTENTIAL DUPLICATED MECHANISM. config-metadata (R1) co-emits from the same field walk the binder's BindTarget derive produces; binder's R1 also captures field set/types/defaults. Both want 'one schema, two consumers (bind + document)'. This is the intended unification, but the two designs must explicitly share ONE derive/const-schema or they will independently re-derive the type's tree shape (and diverge on canonical-name rendering, defaults capture, and nested-kind handling). Flagged by both but the shared artifact is not yet named.
